# Changelog

All notable changes to Agnosis are documented here.

Format: [Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/en/1.1.0/) —
Versioning: [Semantic Versioning](https://semver.org/spec/v2.0.0.html)

## [0.9.47] — 2026-07-22

### Fixed
- **A deliberately embedded other-language passage — e.g. a Latin quotation inside a Catalan poem — got translated right along with its surrounding text during native-language-to-primary translation, and from there propagated (already wrong) to every one of Lingua Forge's own fanned-out language versions too.** Live incident: a poem alternating Latin couplets with the artist's own Catalan rendering of each one came back with BOTH languages translated to English. `PRESERVE_EMBEDDED_OTHER_LANGUAGE_INSTRUCTION` (added 2026-07-21) was present in the prompt the whole time — the actual problem is that a single soft "translate this, but leave that part alone" instruction was never reliable for text interleaving two languages stanza by stanza, as opposed to one isolated quote. Its wording now explicitly names that alternating-couplet/stanza shape (not just "a quotation") and uses imperative "MUST" language, since the original wording's own framing was part of why the model didn't hold to it. A separate, structurally-stronger fix — detect other-language spans in a dedicated AI call, swap them for placeholder tokens, translate, then restore verbatim — was tried and reverted the same day: it added an extra AI call per protected field, silently breaking the exactly-one-AI-call-per-approval guarantee `translate_fields()` exists to provide (caught by three integration tests asserting exact call counts). The hardened instruction is the whole of the fix here; no structural placeholder mechanism is used, so translating a cross-language approval still costs exactly one AI call. (`includes/AI/SubmissionTranslator.php`)
  **Same day, additional hardening:** the hardened instruction above only reaches Agnosis's own translation call — Lingua Forge's own fan-out to every OTHER configured language has no equivalent mechanism available (LF exposes no hook to intercept source text before its own translation call, only an instruction-injection filter and a post-translation result filter), so it depends entirely on the model actually following the same in-prompt instruction. A new `Compat\LinguaForge::force_quality_translation_model()` narrows that gap by forcing LF's 'quality' AI tier and a lower (0.2) temperature for every Agnosis CPT's fan-out translation specifically, via LF's `linguaforge_translation_worker_config` filter, regardless of whatever tier Settings → Lingua Forge → Translation Limits is set to site-wide — a stronger, more literal-following model is measurably less likely to drift from an explicit instruction than a cheaper one. Uses LF's own `Config::model('quality')` rather than a hardcoded model string, since Agnosis has no way to know which AI provider LF is actually configured to call. (`includes/AI/SubmissionTranslator.php`, `includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`)
- **A pure@ text-only artwork's poster could end up completely broken — missing everywhere, not only on translated siblings — after being resent to a different endpoint with unchanged content.** Live incident: a "replace@" resend published with a valid poster; resending the identical content to `pure@` afterward left every version of the post pointing at an attachment whose file no longer existed on disk at all (confirmed directly in the hosting file manager). Root cause: `merge_gallery()`'s ordinary hash-based dedupe (reused across every submission lane, to avoid re-uploading a byte-identical image) reused the EXISTING poster's attachment id into the new gallery, since a resend with unchanged text renders an identical PNG — but the synthetic-poster stale-detection filter, added in 0.9.46, still scanned the FULL previous gallery without excluding ids also present in the new one, so that same id was simultaneously kept (as the current poster) and recorded as stale — and then hard-deleted, file included, by the cleanup step 0.9.46 added. Fixed by excluding any id also present in the new gallery (`array_diff()`) before computing what's safe to hard-delete. (`includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`)
- **No published artwork/biography/event image ever had an `alt` attribute, regardless of what accessibility description was actually stored for it.** `build_image_block()` — the one function that renders every `wp:image`/`wp:gallery` block that ends up in a post's own `post_content` — built its `<img>` tag by hand and simply never included an `alt` attribute at all, confirmed directly against a live post's raw block markup. This was true even where a real description already existed in `_wp_attachment_image_alt` (an AI-vision-generated one for artwork/photo@ submissions, or the artist's own subject line for pure@'s zero-AI lane) — none of it ever reached the actual page. Now reads the attachment's stored alt text and falls back to the artwork's own title (the same value `post_title` itself resolves to) when there is none. Two `Artist\ContentEditor` upload paths (on-site poster regeneration, on-site photo replacement) were separately hardcoding an empty alt text with "out of scope" comments — both now default to the post's title too, same as everywhere else. (`includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`, `includes/Artist/ContentEditor.php`)
- **A native-language artist's own medium category showed up in the WRONG language on their native-language sibling post — e.g. the English word "Poetry" on the Catalan version of a poem, instead of "Poesia".** Root cause: medium classification is always constrained to the site's fixed, PRIMARY-language controlled vocabulary, so `_agnosis_native_medium` actually holds a primary-language value (e.g. "Poetry") from the moment it's first classified, regardless of the artist's own language — not a genuinely native-language value the way excerpt/body/tags are. `Compat\LinguaForge::sync_native_sibling()` was copying that value onto the native sibling verbatim, with no translation step. Fixed by reusing `sync_taxonomy()` — the same trid-based, translate-once-and-cache mechanism every other configured language already uses to get its own correctly-translated medium term — instead of a raw copy. No new AI call per approval: the very first time a given (medium, language) pair is needed it's translated and cached/linked once, exactly like every other language; every subsequent post in that language and medium reuses the linked term for free. This also fixes a side effect on the shared medium filter, which never recognised a language bucket existed for the native-language term at all (the raw-copy path skipped the term-creation flow that flags a new term with its language). (`includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`)
- **Native-language-to-primary translation could pick the WRONG one of two co-present languages to preserve versus translate — e.g. translating an embedded Latin quotation while leaving the artist's own Catalan poem untouched, the exact opposite of the intended behavior.** `translate_fields()`'s prompt only ever named the TARGET language ("Translate the sections below to English") — it never stated what the SOURCE language actually was, leaving the model to guess which of two languages present was "the source's own dominant language" `PRESERVE_EMBEDDED_OTHER_LANGUAGE_INSTRUCTION` refers to. A classical-language quotation followed by a modern-language rendering is genuinely ambiguous read either way without that signal. Lingua Forge's own fan-out translation doesn't share this gap, since stating "translate FROM X TO Y" is intrinsic to what its own translation call already does. Fixed with a new optional `$source_lang_code` parameter on `translate_fields()`, passed through by `ReviewEndpoints::translate_native_content_to_primary()` from the artist's own declared native language — the prompt now states one concrete, actionable rule keyed to the real language pair ("translate text written in Catalan to English; leave anything not written in Catalan exactly as written") instead of two disconnected facts the model had to connect itself. (`includes/AI/SubmissionTranslator.php`, `includes/Publishing/ReviewEndpoints.php`)

### Changed
- **The model used for native-language-to-primary translation was pinned to the same cheap/fast model picked for one-word medium classification and contact-message moderation (`agnosis_openai_text_model`/`agnosis_anthropic_text_model`, defaulting to gpt-4o-mini/claude-haiku) — reasonable for classification, but this is the highest-stakes AI call the plugin makes: it produces every artwork/biography/event's actual published primary-language text, once per approval rather than once per email.** New, separate `agnosis_openai_translation_model` (default `gpt-4o`) and `agnosis_anthropic_translation_model` (default `claude-sonnet-5`) settings (Settings → AI Providers) now govern `SubmissionTranslator` alone; the existing text-model settings continue to govern only Pipeline's own classification/moderation calls. A stronger model here is also materially less likely to mishandle an embedded other-language passage, on top of general translation quality. (`includes/AI/SubmissionTranslator.php`, `includes/Admin/SettingsFields.php`)

## [0.9.46] — 2026-07-22

### Fixed
- **A pure@ (text-only — poetry, essays) submission's auto-generated poster image piled up a new copy in the gallery on every correction, instead of replacing the outdated one.** `TextPosterGenerator` renders a stand-in poster from the artist's own words whenever a pure@ submission arrives with no photo (see that class's own docblock) — since the poster is regenerated fresh from whatever text was just submitted, an artist correcting a typo via a replace@ resend already produced a corrected poster, but `merge_gallery()`'s ordinary hash-based dedupe never recognized it as "the same image, resent" (it's a different PNG on every regeneration), so it just accumulated alongside every earlier poster — and `pick_thumbnail_id()`'s gallery-order-first pick could still surface an OLD, pre-correction poster as the featured image even after a corrected one existed. Poster attachments now carry `_agnosis_is_text_poster` meta; `merge_gallery()` replaces the prior poster instead of appending the new one, the same one-image-at-a-time rule the existing `agnosis_biography` branch already applies to its own gallery. The replacement is staging-aware: a not-yet-approved update never touches the still-live post's current poster — the superseded attachment is deleted immediately for a direct (non-staged) update, or stashed as `_agnosis_stale_poster_ids` on the staging draft for `ReviewEndpoints::finalize_publish()` to delete only once it has actually overwritten the live post's own gallery. (`includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`, `includes/Publishing/ReviewEndpoints.php`)
  **Correction, same day:** the fix as originally shipped here still showed an old and a newly-corrected poster side by side — reported live on a real "Naevius" entry, screenshot showing both the typo'd and the corrected poster stacked in the same notification email. Root cause: `_agnosis_is_text_poster` is only ever set at the moment a poster is uploaded, so it only exists on a poster created AFTER this fix shipped — any poster already in a gallery from before was untagged, `merge_gallery()`'s tag-filtered drop never recognized it as a poster at all, and it was silently kept while the new, tagged one was added alongside it. Fixed properly: regenerating a poster now discards the ENTIRE existing gallery unconditionally (matching `agnosis_biography`'s own unconditional one-image rule) rather than trying to filter it by tag first. A new `PostCreator::is_text_poster_attachment()` (public, shared with `ContentEditor`) still uses the tag as a fast path but falls back to a filename check (`pure-poster-` prefix, the exact name `handle()` has always given the synthetic attachment) for anything predating the tag, backfilling it once found — this is also what decides whether a dropped id is safe to hard-delete outright versus just removed from display, so an untagged real photo from an earlier pure@ submission is never destroyed on a guess. `ContentEditor::maybe_regenerate_text_poster()`'s own trigger check had the identical tag-only blind spot and now goes through the same shared method. (`includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`, `includes/Artist/ContentEditor.php`)
- **Correcting a typo through the on-site text editor (`Artist\ContentEditor`) never touched a pure@ post's poster image at all — the featured image, gallery, and the image embedded in the post body itself all kept showing the OLD, uncorrected text indefinitely.** `ContentEditor::save_text()` now regenerates the poster from the post's current title/body whenever a title or content edit lands on a pure@ artwork whose gallery holds one (a pure@ post that shipped with a real photo instead is left untouched — there's no machine-made stand-in to regenerate), swaps it into the gallery and featured image across every Lingua Forge language sibling, and rewrites the `<img>`/`wp-image-{id}` markup already baked into each sibling's own `post_content` — necessary because the front-end's in-place editor resubmits the whole rendered `the_content()` HTML verbatim (`blocks/content-editor/frontend.js`'s `region.innerHTML`), old image markup included, on every content save. The superseded poster is deleted outright — unlike Phase 2's real-photo replacement, there's no "restore" concept for a machine-generated placeholder. (`includes/Artist/ContentEditor.php`)

## [0.9.45] — 2026-07-21

### Added
- **New on-demand dev tooling replaces the manual Loco Translate workflow.** `composer fill-loco-gaps` detects and fills the plural-form translation slots Loco Translate's own editor UI doesn't surface for locales needing more than two categories (Arabic's 6, Russian's 3) — used to close that exact gap for both this cycle. `composer translate-missing` goes further: AI-translates any remaining empty string in any locale in one pass — Anthropic (default, Haiku), OpenAI, or Gemini, selectable via `--provider=`, each needing its own API key (set as an environment variable, or entered at a hidden interactive prompt if left unset) — using a prompt that knows Agnosis's own domain vocabulary and house style (including the same gender-neutral-phrasing preference already used in the plugin's own AI translation prompts), with no download/upload round-trip against a live Loco instance. Both write directly into `languages/*.po`; both are on-demand, not run automatically on every version bump. Dev-only — neither ships in the plugin ZIP. (`dev/bin/fill-loco-gaps.php`, `dev/bin/translate-missing.php`, `dev/composer.json`, `CONTRIBUTING.md`)

### Changed
- **Six user-facing "no AI at all" strings describing the pure@ lane no longer matched what the lane actually does, once 0.9.44 added a deliberate medium-classification call for it.** Reworded to the accurate promise — pure@ content (the artist's own words and photograph) is never touched or rewritten by AI; AI is only ever used to classify the medium and a few tags, so the post stays findable. Touched: the Settings → Email field label/description, the artist admission-email subject-line legend and address list, the email footer's Pure entry, the `docs/guides/email-templates.md` mirror, and README.md's "AI opt-out lanes" bullet. (`includes/Admin/SettingsFields.php`, `includes/Artist/AdmissionNotification.php`, `includes/Core/EmailFooter.php`, `docs/guides/email-templates.md`, `README.md`)
- Added a "Publishing your own words, untouched" section to the in-site Artist Guide (and its `docs/guides/artist-guide.md` mirror) explaining the pure@ lane to artists directly — it was previously undocumented there entirely. (`includes/Core/Activator.php`, `docs/guides/artist-guide.md`)

### Fixed
- **A pure@ submission's one-and-only classification call computed a medium but discarded the tags already present in the same AI response, so every pure@ post published with zero tags — undiscoverable, and unamplified once federated out to the fediverse.** `Pipeline::classify_medium_from_image()`/`classify_medium_from_text()` now return both `medium` and `tags` from that same call — no second API call: the vision `describe()` call and the text-only `chat()` prompt were already generating tags, only `->medium` was ever read back out before this fix. `PostCreator::handle()` now writes both fields onto the pure@ result before `write_post_meta()` runs, the same as every other publishing lane. (`includes/AI/Pipeline.php`, `includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`)
- **`GENDER_NEUTRAL_INSTRUCTION` — added 2026-07-19 to prevent AI translations from defaulting a gender-unmarked term (e.g. "artist") to masculine or feminine — was never fed through to Lingua Forge's own translation pass, so every LF-side translation (the automatic fan-out to other configured languages, AND the post-list Retranslate/Sync buttons, queue, and backfill) silently lost the rule. Only `PRESERVE_EMBEDDED_OTHER_LANGUAGE_INSTRUCTION` was being forwarded through `Compat\LinguaForge::preserve_embedded_other_language_text()`, LF's one bridge into `linguaforge_translation_extra_instruction` (LF 2.6.6+) — an LF-retranslated biography could regress to exactly the masculine-default phrasing the original fix was meant to prevent.** `GENDER_NEUTRAL_INSTRUCTION` is now `public const` (same reason its sibling constant already was) and appended alongside it in the same callback, additive to whatever instruction (if any) another plugin already supplied on that filter. `PLAIN_STRING_VALUES_INSTRUCTION` remains private and is not forwarded — it governs Agnosis's own JSON-envelope response format, not LF's. (`includes/AI/SubmissionTranslator.php`, `includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`)

## [0.9.44] — 2026-07-21

### Added
- **Every chat-based AI call (submission translation, medium classification, contact-message moderation) had its response token ceiling hardcoded at 8192 — a site translating long text into several configured languages, or with a particularly long biography/description, had no way to raise it short of a code change.** A new `agnosis_ai_max_response_tokens` setting (Settings → AI Providers; default 8192, floor 1024) now governs that ceiling for `OpenAI::chat()`, `Anthropic::chat()`, and `WordPressAI::chat()` alike. Every existing caller's own prompt-length-based sizing is unchanged — only the ceiling itself moved from a literal to a site-level setting. Output tokens are billed as used, not reserved, so raising this costs nothing when the extra room isn't needed; the AI provider's own account/model limits still apply on top of whatever is set here. (`includes/Admin/SettingsFields.php`, `includes/AI/Providers/OpenAI.php`, `includes/AI/Providers/Anthropic.php`, `includes/AI/Providers/WordPressAI.php`)

### Fixed
- **The site's last-configured language never got an AI-translated artwork/event title — reported live as "our last language is never translated automatically."** Root cause: `SubmissionTranslator::translate_to_languages()`'s single JSON-envelope call (one translated title per configured target language, all in one AI response) sized its response token budget purely off the prompt's own length — a formula that barely changes with the number of target languages, even though the response has to contain a full translated copy per language. Once the budget ran out mid-JSON, whichever key the model was still writing — always the same, stably-ordered last language — came up short and was silently dropped by the existing "missing from the model's response" guard, with nothing surfaced beyond a Settings → Logs warning. `ProviderInterface::chat()` (and all three providers, plus `Pipeline::chat()`) gained an optional `$min_tokens` floor; `translate_to_languages()` now computes one scaled by both the number of target languages and the text length, so every language's translation actually fits in the one response, and shares the new `agnosis_ai_max_response_tokens` ceiling above with every other chat-based call. (`includes/AI/ProviderInterface.php`, `includes/AI/Pipeline.php`, `includes/AI/SubmissionTranslator.php`, `includes/AI/Providers/OpenAI.php`, `includes/AI/Providers/Anthropic.php`, `includes/AI/Providers/WordPressAI.php`)
- **Two WordPress.org Plugin Check findings on `Admin\MediumProposals` were false positives on already-safe code; a third was genuine.** `handle_approve()`/`handle_reject()`'s `$_GET['proposal']` was already fully unslashed, decoded, and sanitized (`sanitize_text_field( rawurldecode( wp_unslash( ... ) ) )`) — Plugin Check's static analysis just doesn't trace sanitization through the intermediate `rawurldecode()` call, so both are now explicitly ignored with a documented reason rather than left as unexplained warnings. The actual gap was the admin-notice renderer's `$_GET['agnosis_medium_proposal_error']`, read straight into `esc_html( rawurldecode( (string) $_GET[...] ) )` with no `wp_unslash()` at all — fixed to match the other two handlers' own unslash → decode → escape order. (`includes/Admin/MediumProposals.php`)
- **Medium taxonomy term auto-assignment had silently never worked at all for any AI-described artwork or photo submission — reported live as a gallery with no "Poetry" filter tab despite published poems, and confirmed to affect every submission type once checked.** Root cause: `AI\Pipeline::process_single()` (the image-description branch every artwork/photo@ submission runs through) and `process_video_single()`'s poster-frame branch both correctly computed `$description->medium` (the vision call's own JSON response, validated against the live `agnosis_medium` vocabulary) but never actually included it in the array `PostCreator::write_post_meta()` reads — the value existed, was correct, and simply never crossed the boundary between the two classes. Fixed by adding the missing `'medium' => $description->medium` key to both result arrays. Investigating further surfaced two related, independent gaps in the same feature, both closed in the same pass: `process_audio_single()` and the video branch's text-only fallback (`describe_video_from_context()`) each asked the AI to classify against their own invented, non-matching vocabulary ("sound", "music", "spoken word"... / "video", "animation", "documentary"...) instead of the live `agnosis_medium` terms, and neither ever read a `medium` value back out of the AI's response at all — both now prompt against `PromptConfig::medium_terms()` like every other branch, and carry the result through. Separately, the `pure@` lane (zero-AI-by-design) never classified a medium at all, since it makes no AI call of any kind — two new, narrowly-scoped methods (`Pipeline::classify_medium_from_image()`, reusing the same vision call the image branch uses; `classify_medium_from_text()`, a lightweight `chat()` call over up to 300 words) now make exactly one classification-only call per `pure@` submission (vision when the artist attached a real photo, text otherwise), the sole deliberate exception to that lane's "no AI at all" design. (`includes/AI/Pipeline.php`, `includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`)
- **An AI-proposed medium that doesn't match the live vocabulary used to be silently discarded in three separate places — the AI's answer simply vanished, with nothing telling an admin it ever happened, let alone what it was.** All three (`PostCreator::write_post_meta()`, and both of `ReviewEndpoints::finalize_publish()`'s re-check sites for the native-language pipeline) now record a non-matching value as `_agnosis_medium_proposal` post meta instead of dropping it. A new `Admin\MediumProposals` review queue surfaces these directly on the existing Artwork → Mediums screen (`edit-tags.php?taxonomy=agnosis_medium`) — grouped by distinct proposed value with a count and the actual submission title(s) it applies to (each linked to its edit screen, so an admin can sanity-check the proposal against the real submissions before acting on it) — with **Approve** (creates the term if it doesn't already exist, or reuses it; assigns it to every matching submission; clears the meta) and **Reject** (clears the meta only, without creating or assigning anything) actions. (`includes/Admin/MediumProposals.php`, `includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`, `includes/Publishing/ReviewEndpoints.php`, `includes/Core/Plugin.php`)

## [0.9.43] — 2026-07-21

### Fixed
- **Manually discarding a draft submission from the review screen sent the artist a completely wrong "photo quality too low, 0/10" email — for every post type, every reason, with or without a real photo involved.** Reported live: a discarded text-only poem (whose only "photo" was a synthetic poster image generated for the gallery) got the same "retake your photo" bounce as a genuine low-quality photo rejection. Root cause was `ReviewEndpoints::reject()` (the endpoint behind the artist's own "discard" action) firing the exact same `agnosis_submission_rejected` hook `PostCreator`'s automatic AI photo-quality gate uses — but with a hardcoded score of 0 and no issues, since a manual discard has no relationship to AI-detected photo quality at all. `Notification::on_submission_rejected()`'s listener for that hook is a photo-quality-specific template (score display, camera tips), so it fired unconditionally regardless of post type, whether a photo was even involved, or the artist's actual reason for discarding. Fixed with a new, separate `agnosis_submission_discarded` hook and a plain, honest `Notification::on_submission_discarded()` email ("your submission wasn't published — resend any time") — `agnosis_submission_rejected` is now reserved exclusively for the real, score-carrying AI quality-gate rejection it was originally built for. (`includes/Publishing/ReviewEndpoints.php`, `includes/Publishing/Notification.php`, `includes/Core/Plugin.php`)
- **A published post's line breaks could still vanish even after the 0.9.42 fix for this — because that fix only covered the initial draft's creation, and the artist's actual review-and-publish flow never goes through it.** Reported live: a poem's line breaks were lost again despite the earlier fix shipping. Root cause was that `ReviewEndpoints::save()` (the endpoint behind the "Publish this artwork?" web review form every submission is actually approved through) rebuilds `post_content` from scratch with its own hand-wrapped `'<!-- wp:paragraph --><p>' . wp_kses_post( $body ) . '</p><!-- /wp:paragraph -->'` — no `wpautop()` call at all, so single line breaks in the artist's own text never became `<br />` tags, regardless of what `PostCreator::build_post_content()` had produced at draft time. The identical pattern turned up in two more places: `ReviewEndpoints::translate_native_content_to_primary()` (the AI-translated body at cross-language approval) and `Compat\LinguaForge`'s native-language sibling-post builder. `PostCreator::paragraphs_to_blocks()` (the 0.9.42 fix's own helper) is now `public static` and shared across all four call sites, each routed through `wpautop()` before wrapping — so every path that ever assembles a post body from raw artist text now preserves line breaks identically. (`includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`, `includes/Publishing/ReviewEndpoints.php`, `includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`)

## [0.9.42] — 2026-07-21

### Added
- **Both of Agnosis's translation passes now instruct the AI to leave embedded other-language passages untranslated.** An artist's submission can deliberately mix languages — a Latin original quoted alongside the artist's own Catalan translation of it, an epigraph left in its source language — and a full-text translation pass was flattening that distinction, translating the quoted original along with everything else. A new shared, `public` `SubmissionTranslator::PRESERVE_EMBEDDED_OTHER_LANGUAGE_INSTRUCTION` constant is appended to all three of `SubmissionTranslator`'s own prompt-building paths (`call_translate()`, `translate_fields()`, `translate_to_languages()`) — Agnosis's pre-publish translation — telling the model to leave any passage that's deliberately in a different language from the source's own dominant language exactly as written, and only translate the surrounding text. Lingua Forge's own separate translation pass (which fans a published artwork/biography/event out to the site's other configured languages) had the identical gap; LF 2.6.6 added a `linguaforge_translation_extra_instruction` filter specifically for this, and `Compat\LinguaForge::preserve_embedded_other_language_text()` now feeds it the same shared constant — version-gated to LF >= 2.6.6, a no-op on an older LF install. Both passes read from one constant rather than risking two hand-copied sentences drifting apart. (`includes/AI/SubmissionTranslator.php`, `includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`)

### Fixed
- **A text-only ("pure@") submission with no attachment — poetry, an essay — was rejected outright with a "no usable photo/audio/video file" bounce, even though it contained valid text and pure-lane submissions never required one.** Root cause was in `Email\Parser`: webklex/php-imap's `Message::getStructure()` returns a `Structure` with a non-empty `parts` array even for a single-part, header-only message that hasn't actually had its body fetched yet — the existing `$needs_fetch = ( null === $structure || empty( $structure->parts ) )` check treated that as "already populated" and permanently skipped the real body fetch, so `text_body_len` came back 0 regardless of what the artist actually wrote. Root-caused via targeted diagnostic logging after a live test (confirmed `fetch attempted=no (structure already populated)`) rather than guessed at — an earlier hypothesis (a stale `pure@` Settings value) was ruled out first by checking the Inbox admin table's Endpoint column, which already correctly showed "Pure". Fixed with a new `structure_has_fetched_content()` helper that checks whether any part actually carries fetched `content`, not just whether `parts` is non-empty; applied identically to both `parse_imap_message()` and `parse_broadcast_body()`, which shared the same buggy heuristic. (`includes/Email/Parser.php`)
- **The poster image generated for a text-only submission with no photo now uses the artist's own body text to fill the frame, edge to edge, instead of stopping after the title.** `TextPosterGenerator::extract_lines()` previously had ambiguous priority between subject and body; it now always leads with the subject (if any) as the poster's first line, then fills the remaining line budget (`MAX_LINES`) with the body's own lines, preserving the artist's original line breaks rather than re-wrapping or truncating early. `PostCreator`'s pure-lane call site was simplified to hand the raw subject/description straight to `TextPosterGenerator::generate()`, which now owns this priority entirely rather than the caller pre-resolving it. (`includes/Publishing/TextPosterGenerator.php`, `includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`)
- **A published post's line breaks could silently vanish the first time it was opened in the block editor — reported live on a text-only poem, whose 5 lines collapsed into one run-on sentence.** `PostCreator::build_post_content()` was writing raw, unwrapped classic HTML (bare `<p>`/`<br>` tags from `wpautop()`, no `wp:paragraph` block-comment markers) into `post_content`. On agnosis-theme, a pure FSE block theme with no classic-editor fallback, that orphaned HTML is invisible to Gutenberg's block parser: the first time such a post opened in the editor, its block-recovery logic adopted the lone `<p>` as a `wp:paragraph` block by reconstructing it from its own rich-text model rather than preserving the original markup byte-for-byte — and that reconstruction doesn't round-trip a manually-inserted `<br />` the way a real Shift+Enter break would, silently dropping every line break. Diagnosed empirically before any fix: `wpautop()` itself was ruled out first (verified directly against a full WordPress core checkout, confirmed to correctly emit `<br />` for the exact poem text), then the actual stored block-editor markup was inspected, which showed the `<br>`-less, `wp:paragraph`-wrapped result — confirming Gutenberg's own auto-recovery, not `wpautop()`, was the culprit. Fixed with a new `paragraphs_to_blocks()` helper that wraps every `<p>...</p>` `wpautop()` produces in explicit `<!-- wp:paragraph -->`/`<!-- /wp:paragraph -->` markers before the post is ever created, so there's nothing left for the editor to "recover." Applied to both the artwork/pure body path and the biography/event body path — the latter also gained a `wpautop()` call it never had at all (previously ran through `wp_kses_post()` alone, with no paragraph or line-break structure whatsoever), for the same underlying reason. (`includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`)

## [0.9.41] — 2026-07-20

### Changed
- **The "Commerce" plan (a future donation/art-sale revenue layer with a configurable platform fee) is replaced with a simpler "Donations" plan: a no-fee way for visitors to support an artist directly, with marketplace/checkout functionality left to dedicated plugins.** The old plan's fee-percentage scaffolding (`agnosis_tx_fee_percent`, Settings → Commerce) never matched what actually got built — C-1 (closed 2026-07-19) already rejected the split-payment mechanism the fee implied, dropping `agnosis_transactions` outright rather than build it. The fee field itself was leftover scaffolding for that dropped plan and is now removed; Settings → Donations (renamed from Commerce) instead shows a plain status card explaining nothing is built yet. README.md and readme.txt's Commerce bullets, feature lists, and FAQ answer are reworded to match — no more promising a "configurable transaction fee" that was never going to ship. Neither this settings tab nor either doc claimed anything was live before, so no user-facing behavior changes for an operator who never touched that tab. **i18n structurally synced at close of this version:** `languages/agnosis.pot` and all 18 locale `.po` files now carry the new "Donations" msgid (replacing "Commerce," which is gone from source) plus the two new status-card strings, with the two dead fee-field strings removed; `.mo`/`.l10n.php` recompiled for every locale (`dev/bin/compile-pos.sh --check` clean). Actual translation of these three strings into the 17 non-English locales is still outstanding — they compile as untranslated (falling back to the English source text at runtime) until Ulises's usual Loco Translate pass fills them in. (`includes/Admin/Settings.php`, `includes/Admin/SettingsFields.php`, `includes/Core/Activator.php`, `README.md`, `readme.txt`, `languages/agnosis.pot`, `languages/agnosis-*.po`, `languages/agnosis-*.mo`, `languages/agnosis-*.l10n.php`)

### Fixed
- **The "Mediums" checklist on the Artworks Quick Edit panel (and the classic edit-screen "Categories"-style meta box, since `agnosis_medium` has no `meta_box_cb` override) mixed every language's translated copy of every medium into one list — reported live as 7 different-language "Watercolor" checkboxes shown at once, none of them the English one.** `agnosis_medium` stores every translated term as a sibling row in the same flat taxonomy, flagged with `Compat\LinguaForge::TRANSLATED_TERM_META`; core's `wp_terms_checklist()` (what both screens render through) does a plain, unfiltered `get_terms()`, so nothing was ever scoping it by language — `Admin\TaxonomyLanguageFilter` already solves the identical overcrowding problem for the Tags/Mediums term-LIST screens, but that filter is only registered on `load-edit-tags.php`, so it never reached a checklist rendered on an artwork's own edit/Quick Edit screen. Beyond the clutter, this was a real data-integrity risk: nothing stopped an editor from checking a wrong-language term directly onto a primary-language artwork, which `Compat\LinguaForge::sync_medium_assignment_to_siblings()`'s already-automatic propagation (fires on every save via the `set_object_terms` hook) would then push out to every translated sibling as if it were genuine primary vocabulary. **Correction, same day:** the fix as originally shipped here (`Admin\ArtworkMediumSync::filter_checklist_by_language()`, hooked to `wp_terms_checklist_args`) did not actually work — reported live, screenshot still showing all 7 languages. Verified against WordPress core's own source directly this time rather than assumption: (1) `wp_terms_checklist()` (`wp-admin/includes/template.php`) applies `wp_terms_checklist_args` but then only reads *walker*/*selected_cats*/*popular_cats*/*checked_ontop* off the result — the actual term list comes from a separate, hardcoded `get_terms( [ 'taxonomy' => $taxonomy, 'get' => 'all' ] )` call a few lines later that never sees anything that filter added; and (2) Quick Edit specifically can never be scoped by "the post's own language" at all, because `WP_Posts_List_Table::inline_edit()` renders the ENTIRE Quick Edit row — checklist included — ONCE per page load as a single hidden template shared by every row via JS, calling `wp_terms_checklist( 0, ... )` with a hardcoded post ID of 0; there is no per-row server round-trip to derive a language from. The real fix (`Admin\ArtworkMediumSync::register_edit_screen_scoping()` / `register_list_screen_scoping()`, hooked to `load-post.php`/`load-post-new.php`/`load-edit.php`) uses the lower-level `get_terms_args` filter instead — the same one `TaxonomyLanguageFilter` already uses successfully — and scopes the classic edit screen by that specific post's own language (a real `$post->ID` is available there), while Quick Edit is scoped by the Artworks list's own active language filter (Lingua Forge's `lf_lang_filter` dropdown/user-meta) instead, since every visible row genuinely is that language whenever it's set to one specific language; left unscoped when "All languages" is selected rather than guessing. (`includes/Admin/ArtworkMediumSync.php`, `includes/Core/Plugin.php`)

## [0.9.40] — 2026-07-19

### Added
- **The OpenAI/Anthropic API keys, the inbound-webhook HMAC secret, and both Cloudflare Turnstile keys can now optionally be set via `wp-config.php` constants instead of the database (P-4, `agnosis-audit/AUDIT-0.9.39.md` §3c).** Every one of these five secrets has always lived as a plain `wp_options` row — the WordPress-standard pattern, and not a real weakness on its own — but an operator who already keeps secrets in `wp-config.php` (an environment variable, a secrets manager writing PHP constants at deploy time) had no way to keep these ones there too. Defining any of `AGNOSIS_OPENAI_KEY`, `AGNOSIS_ANTHROPIC_KEY`, `AGNOSIS_WEBHOOK_SECRET`, `AGNOSIS_TURNSTILE_SITE_KEY`, or `AGNOSIS_TURNSTILE_SECRET_KEY` with a non-empty value now overrides the matching database option everywhere it's read — a new `Core\Secrets` class is the single place this precedence is decided, replacing what used to be eleven separate direct `get_option()` calls across five files with one call each through it, so "which value actually wins" only ever has one answer. Its matching Settings field switches to a locked, read-only "defined in wp-config.php" notice whenever its constant is set, rather than letting an operator type a new value into a database option that would then be silently ignored — `Admin\Settings::render_field()` does this generically off `Secrets::override_constant_name()`, not by special-casing five fields by name. An empty-string constant (`define('AGNOSIS_OPENAI_KEY', '')`) is deliberately treated as "not set," not as a lockout. Nothing changes for an operator who doesn't define any of these. Moving the actual `get_option()` calls into `Core\Secrets` broke 17 existing unit tests across `SubmissionTranslatorTest`, `WebhookSignatureTest`, and `WebhookReplayProtectionTest` — PHP resolves an unqualified function call by the *calling code's own* namespace, so once the call lived in `Agnosis\Core` it stopped reaching the `Agnosis\AI`/`Agnosis\Email` namespaces' own test-only `get_option()` overrides (`ai_namespace_stubs.php`/`email_namespace_stubs.php`) and silently fell through to the real global stub instead, which always returns empty. Fixed with a matching `Agnosis\Core` namespace stub (`tests/php/Unit/Core/Stubs/core_namespace_stubs.php`) that reads the exact same fixture properties (`SubmissionTranslatorTest::$options`, `WebhookSignatureTest::$options`) those tests already set, so none of the three existing test files needed to change at all. **That fix resolved the `SubmissionTranslatorTest` failures but a second PHPUnit run turned up 15 more, all in `WebhookSignatureTest`/`WebhookReplayProtectionTest`** — `SecretsTest`'s own `define()` calls on the five real constant names (`AGNOSIS_WEBHOOK_SECRET` etc.) were meant to be contained by `@runInSeparateProcess`/`@preserveGlobalState disabled`, but a constant defined there still leaked into whatever ran afterward in the same PHPUnit invocation: `Secrets::resolve()` checks a defined constant before any option, so a leaked `AGNOSIS_WEBHOOK_SECRET` silently overrode the secret those two suites' own fixtures were configuring, breaking their HMAC signature math in a way that had nothing to do with what they were actually testing. Rather than trust process isolation to behave a particular way in every environment, `Core\Secrets` gained a `set_constant_lookup_for_testing()` hook — a swappable `callable` that stands in for `defined()`/`constant()` — so `SecretsTest` no longer calls PHP's real `define()` on any of the five constant names at all; nothing it does can leak into another suite regardless of process isolation. (`includes/Core/Secrets.php`, `includes/Core/Turnstile.php`, `includes/AI/Pipeline.php`, `includes/AI/SubmissionTranslator.php`, `includes/Admin/Settings.php`, `includes/Admin/Dashboards/AiTestTools.php`, `includes/Email/Webhook.php`, `tests/php/Unit/Core/SecretsTest.php`, `tests/php/Unit/Core/Stubs/core_namespace_stubs.php`, `dev/bootstrap.php`)

### Fixed
- **`dev/coverage/` (90 MB of local PHPUnit coverage output, embedding this machine's own `/Users/tiger/...` filesystem paths) was tracked by git without being excluded by any `.gitignore` — flagged as a going-public blocker (H-1, `agnosis-audit/AUDIT-0.9.39.md` §6).** Coverage reports are `composer coverage`'s own reproducible output, not source, and had no reason to live in the repository at all — let alone one about to go public with a stranger's local machine path baked into every HTML report. Added `coverage/` to `dev/.gitignore` so it can't be re-added by accident. Untracking the already-committed copy, and folding its removal into the git-history decision (H-2, same audit), is a maintainer-run `git` operation outside this session's reach — no `git` commands are ever run against this repo from here. (`dev/.gitignore`)

## [0.9.39] — 2026-07-19

### Added
- **A new "Powered by Agnosis" page is created as a draft on activation, promoting the plugin itself rather than the running community.** Every existing managed page (About, Artist Guide, Join, My Submissions) speaks to that specific install's own artists and visitors; nothing pointed a curious visitor — someone who found the site and wondered what it runs on — toward Agnosis the project, or explained how to get it for their own site. The new page is an easy-reading condensation of README.md's opening sections (what Agnosis is, how the email-to-post-to-fediverse workflow works, who it's designed for) ending with a link to the GitHub repository for full documentation and installation instructions. Unlike every other managed page, it's created as a **draft**, not published — whether to publish it, and where (if anywhere) to link it from, is the site owner's call, not something activation should decide for them. `Activator::create_managed_page()`'s idempotency check was generalized alongside this (skip whenever the page still exists in any non-trashed status, not only 'publish') — needed so a page meant to stay in draft doesn't get a fresh duplicate created every time this runs, which is on every activation and again on every version upgrade (`create_managed_pages()` is deferred to `init` from `maybe_upgrade()`). This also means an admin who deliberately drafts one of the *other* managed pages will no longer have it silently duplicated on the next upgrade either. (`includes/Core/Activator.php`)

### Fixed
- **"Sync all translations" no longer runs as one unbounded request that can silently exhaust PHP's execution time on a large vocabulary.** On a vocabulary the size the live site has already demonstrated (746 tags × 17 languages), a cold-cache run could imply thousands of sequential AI calls inside a single admin-post request — long enough to hit `max_execution_time`, the gateway timeout, or the AI provider's rate limit, leaving the operator with a bare browser error and nothing telling them the button might just need clicking again. `Compat\LinguaForge::sync_all_terms_across_languages()` now stops cleanly after a 20-second time budget (`SYNC_ALL_TIME_BUDGET_SECONDS`) — the deadline is only ever checked between terms, never mid-term, so nothing is left half-synced across languages. The redirect notice (`TaxonomyLanguageFilter::maybe_render_sync_notice()`) now distinguishes a complete run ("N term(s) processed…") from a time-bounded one ("X of Y done… click again to continue"), and the button's confirm dialog no longer promises "this can take a moment" — it says plainly that a large vocabulary may take more than one click. The sync was already idempotent and resumable (every completed term persists before the next starts); this makes that resumability something the operator can actually see and rely on, instead of an accident they'd only discover by re-clicking a button that looked like it had failed. (`includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`, `includes/Admin/TaxonomyLanguageFilter.php`, `includes/Admin/LanguageAwareTermsListTable.php`)
- **A cross-language homograph collision no longer fails a term-sync language silently and forever, and every sync now reports a `failed` count instead of absorbing failures into "created"/"skipped."** Two languages can independently translate a term to the same (or accent-insensitively equal) word — "Fotografie" is both German and Dutch, "Fotografía"/"Fotografia" differ only by an accent AI output isn't guaranteed to keep across es/it/pt/ca — and `wp_insert_term()` rejects the second language's insert as a duplicate. The old handling was a bare `continue`: no trid link was ever created, so every future sync re-attempted the identical insert and re-failed identically, with nothing counting the loss — an operator reading "N terms processed, 0 created, 0 already up to date" couldn't tell that apart from "nothing to do." A new `Compat\LinguaForge::insert_translated_term()` resolves the collision instead of giving up on it: if the term already sitting on that name carries the SAME trid, it's a harmless lost race (e.g. two syncs running close together) and gets linked as normal; if it carries a different trid — or none, meaning it's an admin-curated primary term — it's never claimed, and the insert is retried once with an explicit language-suffixed slug (`fotografie-nl`), which `wp_insert_term()`'s own same-name/different-slug allowance lets through. Both this and the pre-existing "no AI provider / translation call failed" case now add the language to a new `failed` bucket, surfaced through both the per-term and sync-all admin notices — any non-zero `failed` count turns the notice into a warning instead of a silent success. (`includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`, `includes/Admin/TaxonomyLanguageFilter.php`)
- **Cleared all 90 wrong-match fuzzy translation entries across every one of the 18 `.po` language files (5 per language), and automated this clearing so it can never silently reaccumulate — the second time this exact problem has recurred (the first was 0.9.36, 252 entries, done by hand).** A prior `.po` regeneration had fuzzy-matched changed source strings (the artwork-copyright block's strings, the gallery-overview empty-state messages) to the closest existing translation, several of them wrong in a way that looked plausible on read (German `"No artwork matches this filter yet."` had matched to `"Keine Warteschlangenzeilen entsprechen diesem Filter."` — "queue rows," not artwork). Fuzzy entries are already skipped at `.mo`/`.l10n.php` compile time, so nothing wrong ever reached a live site, but the `.po` source itself kept looking translated when it wasn't. Policy going forward: a fuzzy match is never left in a `.po` — it's cleared back to a clean untranslated entry for a real retranslation pass in Loco Translate, never patched in place. `dev/bin/make-pot.sh` now runs a new `dev/bin/clear-fuzzy.awk` automatically right after its `msgmerge` step, so this can no longer reaccumulate silently between releases; `dev/bin/compile-pos.sh` additionally refuses to compile if it ever finds a fuzzy entry anyway (defense in depth for a hand-run `msgmerge` outside the script), and gained a `--check` mode that fails if any `.mo`/`.l10n.php` is older than its `.po` — the "stale `.mo`" half of this same audit finding — intended as a release-checklist / CI step. `languages/agnosis-*.l10n.php` regenerated in-sandbox against the now-clean `.po` content; `languages/agnosis-*.mo` still needs a real `msgfmt` recompile on a machine that has it (`bash dev/bin/compile-pos.sh`) before release — this sandbox has no `msgfmt` binary. (`dev/bin/make-pot.sh`, `dev/bin/compile-pos.sh`, `dev/bin/clear-fuzzy.awk`, `CONTRIBUTING.md`, `languages/agnosis-*.po`, `languages/agnosis-*.l10n.php`, 18 files each)
- **Three small taxonomy-screen polish fixes and one new escape hatch, all on the Tags/Mediums language filter added in 0.9.38.** A term whose translated-language flag names a language since removed from Lingua Forge's configuration was unreachable from any dropdown selection at all — excluded from the default view (it has the flag) and from every remaining configured language's view (the flag matches none of them). A new "All languages (unfiltered)" option at the bottom of the dropdown (`TaxonomyLanguageFilter::ALL_LANGUAGES_VALUE`) restores an escape hatch for exactly that term. Separately: the term search box on this screen submitted its own form without the current language selection, so searching while viewing a non-primary language's terms silently reset the view back to primary — a hidden field now carries the selection through a search submit. And the per-term "Sync translations" row action's redirect always landed back on page 1 of the term list, regardless of which page the operator was actually working through — it now carries the current `paged` value through both the row action's URL and its redirect, so syncing a term on page 3 of a long vocabulary keeps you on page 3. (`includes/Admin/TaxonomyLanguageFilter.php`, `includes/Admin/LanguageAwareTermsListTable.php`)
- **A remote fediverse account's own self-Delete is no longer stuck unactionable forever when its signing key can no longer be fetched — a known, accepted ecosystem gap now gets one narrow, safe corroboration path instead.** Mastodon fans out an account-delete *after* the account is already gone, so fetching the signer's public key to verify the Delete's HTTP Signature returns 410 Gone — cryptographic verification then becomes structurally impossible forever, not just temporarily, so the old behavior (reject and wait for the delivery-side 410/404 fast path to eventually stop retrying) left the stale `agnosis_followers` row itself in place permanently. `HttpSignature::fetch_public_key()` now carries the real remote HTTP status through its `WP_Error` (including through the 5-minute negative cache, so a retried request within that window doesn't lose the detail) instead of collapsing every failure reason into one generic message; `ActivityPub::verify_inbox_signature()` uses this to accept a Delete specifically when the key fetch failed with a live 410 AND the activity is a genuine self-delete (`object` resolves to the same actor as `actor`) AND the Signature header's own keyId belongs to that exact actor. This is corroboration, not a bypass: an attacker cannot forge a peer server's 410 response for a URL they don't control, so this only ever accepts a Delete for an actor whose own real endpoint has genuinely, verifiably stopped existing. (`includes/Network/HttpSignature.php`, `includes/Network/ActivityPub.php`)
- **Promoting an artwork (promote@) no longer shows a ✦ "Featured" mark or reorders anything on an artist's own subdomain gallery — it now only ever affects the shared main gallery, as intended.** `blocks/gallery-overview/render.php` is the single block behind both galleries — the sitewide portal (all artists) and, on an artist's own subdomain, that artist's personal one-artist gallery — and its "featured artwork first" query and ✦ badge previously ran unconditionally in both contexts. On the main gallery this is meaningful: an artist's per-artist slot budget can be smaller than their total published output, so pulling the featured piece first guarantees it survives that cut. On an artist's own subdomain the per-artist budget already equals the whole pool target — every one of that artist's works is included regardless — and the block's own day-seeded shuffle reorders the full pool afterward anyway, so the query had no visible ordering effect there at all; it only left a meaningless ✦ badge on a single-artist gallery where nothing is actually being chosen over anything else. Both the featured-first query and the badge are now skipped whenever `SubdomainRouter::is_artist_subdomain()` is true. The same wrong claim was corrected in both places it's written: `docs/guides/artist-guide.md` (the repo's contributor-facing copy) and `Activator::help_page_content()` (the actual "Asking to be featured" paragraph on the live Artist Guide page every install creates). (`blocks/gallery-overview/render.php`, `docs/guides/artist-guide.md`, `includes/Core/Activator.php`)
- **A medium (or tag) that failed to translate into a given language stayed missing from that language's sync forever, no matter how many times "Sync all translations" or the per-term "Sync translations" action was re-run — reported live: "Mixed Media" permanently absent from German, unchanged across repeated retries.** Root cause was two compounding bugs, both in the term-translation path. First, `Compat\LinguaForge::translated_term_name()` called `SubmissionTranslator::translate_text()` without the `$context` parameter that `Artist\BiographyTitle` already uses for this exact failure shape (2026-07-18, the "Meet the Artist" mis-gendering bug): a short, bare label with no surrounding sentence — exactly what every medium/tag term is — sometimes gets a non-scalar JSON value back from the AI model instead of a plain string, which every caller here already defends against defensively by falling back to the original, untranslated text (see `SubmissionTranslator::call_translate()`'s own docblock on the "Array — Cal Talaia" incident this pattern was first found from). A new `TERM_TRANSLATION_CONTEXT` now tells the model explicitly that this is a controlled-vocabulary label, not prose, reducing how often that fallback path triggers at all; all three JSON-envelope prompts in `SubmissionTranslator.php` also gained an explicit "each value must be a plain string" instruction, and previously-silent non-string/missing-field responses now log a warning instead of nothing — the admin notice's "check the AI provider configuration" was actively misleading for this cause, and Settings → Logs had nothing to show either. Second, and the actual reason retrying never helped: `translated_term_name()` only skipped writing to its translation cache when the AI result was an *empty string* — a same-as-source fallback is never empty, so every failure got cached as if it were a genuine translation, and every subsequent sync attempt hit that cache first and returned the poisoned value instantly, never calling the AI translator again. Fixed to also treat a same-as-source result as uncached; a one-time `LinguaForge::purge_self_referential_term_translations()` repair (mirroring `BiographyTitle::repair_array_titles()`'s existing 0.9.23 pattern) runs from `Activator::maybe_upgrade()` on this upgrade to clear any already-poisoned cache entries from before this fix — the next "Sync translations" click is what actually re-creates the missing term. (`includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`, `includes/AI/SubmissionTranslator.php`, `includes/Core/Activator.php`)
- **The fix directly above reduced how often a term fails to translate, but a live, larger-scale report made clear it wasn't enough on its own: a real AI provider still fails a real percentage of calls, and "Sync all translations" was consistently leaving a meaningful fraction of every language's vocabulary with no term at all — German 9/10, Italian 8/10, Dutch 8/10, Portuguese 6/10 on one reported run, "unacceptable" per the report, since an admin had no way to fix what didn't exist.** The trid system this class already maintains makes a different guarantee possible: a (term, language) pair is never left empty again. `Compat\LinguaForge::insert_fallback_translated_term()` is a new method that always creates a real, trid-linked term — using the primary term's own name verbatim as a placeholder — whenever AI translation isn't available or fails, tagged with a new `TERM_NEEDS_TRANSLATION_META` and given a visible "needs translation" note in its `description` field (rendered automatically by WP_Terms_List_Table's own Description column on the Tags/Mediums screens — no admin-UI code needed for that part). This can't reuse `insert_translated_term()`'s own collision handling: the source name always collides with the primary term itself (which carries the same trid), and that method's "same trid = lost race" resolution would wrongly reuse the primary term's own ID — silently tagging the primary vocabulary as its own translation. `insert_fallback_translated_term()` instead always forces a distinctly-slugged insert (`{name}-{lang}`), the same disambiguation the homograph-collision fix already uses. `sync_term_across_languages()`'s result gained a `needs_translation` bucket, separate from `created` (a genuine AI translation) and `failed` (now reserved for the rare case even the disambiguated insert itself couldn't complete); `sync_all_terms_across_languages()` and both admin notices (`TaxonomyLanguageFilter::maybe_render_sync_notice()`, per-term and sync-all) were updated to surface it with its own wording — "created as placeholders needing translation... edit them in this list" — instead of the misleading "check the AI provider configuration" text, which now only appears for a genuine hard failure. An admin can now always find and hand-correct every gap directly in the Tags/Mediums screen, exactly as requested — nothing is ever silently missing. (`includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`, `includes/Admin/TaxonomyLanguageFilter.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Compat/LinguaForgeTermSyncTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Admin/TaxonomyLanguageFilterTest.php`)
- **Found the actual reason the two fixes directly above still weren't enough, after a live report with screenshots showed German fully synced (10/10, with one honest placeholder) while Portuguese sat at 6/10 and Spanish at 9/10 — with "Sync all translations" reporting a clean "0 failed" run in every case.** Root cause was a bug in `insert_translated_term()`'s own collision handling from the §2b fix (0.9.39, above): a `term_exists` collision against a term already carrying the SAME trid was unconditionally treated as a harmless "lost race" and reused — correct only when the colliding term is ALREADY the same language's own translation (a genuine concurrent duplicate). It's wrong, and silently destructive, in two other same-trid cases this taxonomy hits constantly: (1) two DIFFERENT target languages in the same trid group translate to an identical or accent-equivalent word — "Arte Digital" and "Escultura" are byte-identical in Spanish and Portuguese, "Fotografía"/"Fotografia" differ only by an accent — so whichever language synced second collided with the FIRST language's own term, not a duplicate of itself; (2) the AI's "translation" happens to equal the primary term's own name verbatim (unremarkable between closely related languages), colliding with the primary term itself. In both cases the code reused the wrong term's ID, then tried to tag it `TRANSLATED_TERM_META = $lang` — which `add_term_meta( …, $unique = true )` silently refuses to do when that key already holds a DIFFERENT value, adding nothing and returning `false`, a return value nothing checked. The caller counted the language as `created` anyway: a full, silent no-op reported as success, on every single sync attempt, for every term whose translations happen to share vocabulary across two or more configured languages — which is the normal case for any set of Romance languages, or German/Dutch, and why this kept recurring across "several programming sessions" no prior fix actually reached. Two changes close it: `insert_translated_term()` now only reuses a same-trid collision when the existing term's language meta already matches the language being inserted — the primary-term case and the different-language case both now correctly fall through to the same disambiguated-slug retry a different-trid collision already used, so each language always gets its own real term; and `sync_term_across_languages()` now reads the term-meta back immediately after writing it and compares against what was actually intended, counting a mismatch as `failed` (with a `Logger::error()` entry) instead of trusting the write succeeded — closing this exact class of silent miscount for good, regardless of future cause. A fresh "Sync all translations" click after this ships will finally create the real missing terms (or honest placeholders) for every language still short, converging every configured language to full parity with the primary vocabulary. Also fixed alongside: the language-filter dropdown's own navigation script never cleared the previous sync notice's query args on a language switch, which is why three screenshots (German/Spanish/Portuguese) all showed the identical "10 term(s) processed…" text — that notice was stale, carried over from one earlier run, not a fresh (and wrongly clean) check of each language; switching languages now clears it. (`includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`, `includes/Admin/TaxonomyLanguageFilter.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Compat/LinguaForgeTermSyncTest.php`)

### Removed
- **The `agnosis_transactions` table is dropped, closing C-1 — the "build the donation slice or drop the table" decision carried unbuilt across thirteen consecutive audits (`agnosis-audit/AUDIT-0.9.38.md` §9).** Before building a donation feature, checked whether a free WordPress plugin already did the job well enough not to bother — it doesn't, because the actual requirement (collect a donation, retain a 7% platform fee, remit the rest to the specific artist) is a marketplace split-payment feature, not a donation box. Every free donation plugin surveyed (GiveWP, Charitable, WPForms Lite) pays out to a single site-wide destination account in its free tier; the one plugin built for split payouts (Split Pay for WooCommerce) gates multi-recipient routing behind its paid tier too. Doing this properly means a genuine Stripe Connect integration — real payment engineering, judged out of scope for 1.0.0 — so rather than leave an unused table (and its matching, fully-built-but-never-exercised privacy exporter/eraser) sitting dormant indefinitely, both are removed outright. `Core\Activator::maybe_upgrade()` carries a one-time `DROP TABLE IF EXISTS` migration for existing installs; `Core\Privacy.php`'s `agnosis-transactions` exporter/eraser pair (`export_transactions()`, `erase_transactions()`) is deleted along with it. Decision and rationale documented in the audit; revisit post-1.0.0 only if artist demand for donations actually materializes. (`includes/Core/Activator.php`, `includes/Core/Privacy.php`, `uninstall.php`)

## [0.9.38] — 2026-07-19

### Added
- **A language filter dropdown on the Tags and Mediums admin screens, plus an on-demand "Sync translations" action on Mediums, both addressing the same underlying UX problem: every AI-translated term lives in the same flat taxonomy as the admin-curated original, so an 18-language site had 746 tags and 38 mediums all mixed into one unfiltered list — impossible to find or manage the actual admin-curated vocabulary among hundreds of translated duplicates (reported live, with screenshots of both overcrowded screens).** The Tags (`post_tag`) and Mediums (`agnosis_medium`) list screens now show only the primary/admin-curated vocabulary by default (every AI-translated term — flagged with `Compat\LinguaForge::TRANSLATED_TERM_META` — is hidden), with a new dropdown to switch to any other configured language's translated terms one at a time. WordPress's own term list table has no equivalent to `restrict_manage_posts` (the hook post lists use for exactly this kind of filter) — no core hook fires anywhere a plugin could inject a dropdown — so this required swapping in a custom `WP_Terms_List_Table` subclass via the `wp_list_table_class_name` filter (added in WP 6.1 for precisely this kind of substitution) purely to override the one protected method (`extra_tablenav()`) that renders it; the actual term-scoping itself is a `get_terms_args` filter, registered only while genuinely on one of these two admin screens so it can never affect any other `get_terms()` call site (front-end filter pills, REST, nav menus). Separately, Mediums gained a "Sync translations" row action (shown only on primary-language terms, since there's nothing to sync from a translated one) that creates any missing translated term across every configured language on demand, via a new `Compat\LinguaForge::sync_term_across_languages()` — until now, a translated medium term only ever came into existence as a side effect of some artwork happening to be translated in that language, so a medium with no artwork yet published in, say, Japanese had no Japanese term at all, even if an admin wanted the full vocabulary ready ahead of time. A companion fix closes a related gap: editing an artwork's medium *after* it was first published previously left every already-translated sibling silently pointing at the old, stale translated term forever, since the existing AI-translation sync only ever ran at initial translation-creation time — a new `set_object_terms` hook now re-propagates a primary-language artwork's medium change onto its already-published siblings automatically. (`includes/Admin/LanguageAwareTermsListTable.php`, `includes/Admin/TaxonomyLanguageFilter.php`, `includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`, `includes/Core/Plugin.php`)
- **A "Sync all translations" bulk action for the Tags and Mediums screens.** The per-term "Sync translations" row action above only ever handles one term at a time — clicking through hundreds of primary terms to build out a new language from a cold start was never realistic. A "Sync all translations" button next to the language dropdown (`LanguageAwareTermsListTable::extra_tablenav()`) now walks every primary-language term in the current taxonomy and syncs each one in a single admin-post request (`TaxonomyLanguageFilter::sync_all_url()` / `handle_sync_all_terms()` → `Compat\LinguaForge::sync_all_terms_across_languages()`), reporting back how many terms were processed, how many translations were newly created, and how many were already up to date. The operation is idempotent and resumable — every completed term persists before the next starts, so re-clicking after a timeout picks up where it left off. (`includes/Admin/LanguageAwareTermsListTable.php`, `includes/Admin/TaxonomyLanguageFilter.php`, `includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`)
- **On-demand medium-translation sync for individual artworks and in bulk.** The automatic re-propagation added above (the new `set_object_terms` hook) only fires reactively when an artwork's medium is actually changed after publish — it does nothing for an artwork/sibling pair that was already out of sync before that hook existed, which was exactly the shape of a live Catalan-testing data-integrity incident. A new "Medium translations" meta box on the artwork edit screen pushes one artwork's current medium onto its already-translated siblings on demand, and a matching bulk action on the artwork list screen sweeps every artwork at once. All three triggers — automatic, one artwork, all artwork — now share the same underlying implementation (`Compat\LinguaForge::sync_medium_assignment_to_siblings()` / `sync_all_medium_assignments()`), so there's exactly one place any future fix to the propagation logic needs to apply. (`includes/Admin/ArtworkMediumSync.php`, `includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`)

### Fixed
- **Term-translation sync now links a term to its translations by a stable ID instead of matching names, closing a duplicate-term bug.** AI translation output isn't byte-stable — the same source term translated twice can come back with slightly different wording. Sync used to decide "does this translation already exist" with a name lookup (`get_term_by( 'name', … )`), so re-running sync after a re-translation created near-duplicate terms instead of recognizing the one that already existed. Every term that participates in sync now gets a `_agnosis_term_trid` (a v4 UUID shared by a primary term and every one of its translations, assigned on first use via `get_or_create_term_trid()`), and `find_term_by_trid()` / `find_primary_term_by_trid()` become the sole "does a translation exist" check across every sync path — never a name comparison again. The same trid link is now also used to reconcile a submitting artist's native-language tags against the primary vocabulary (`resolve_primary_tags()`): an established link is reused for free, and only a name match is attempted when no trid exists yet — deliberately never a fresh AI call there, to preserve the native-language pipeline's one-AI-call-per-approval guarantee (`NATIVE-LANGUAGE-PIPELINE.md` §7). (`includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`)
- **Terms auto-created while tagging a non-primary-language submission are now correctly flagged as translated, closing a data-integrity incident.** A term created as a side effect of AI-tagging an artwork (rather than through the dedicated translation sync above) never had its language recorded anywhere — 127 `post_tag` terms accumulated silently in the "primary language" bucket during Catalan testing, byte-for-byte indistinguishable from genuine primary-language terms. Every term creation is now tracked for the duration of the request (`track_newly_created_term()`, hooked to core's `created_term`) and cross-referenced, a few lines later in the same `wp_set_object_terms()` call, against the terms actually assigned to the post being saved (`flag_newly_created_terms_by_post_language()`, hooked to `set_object_terms`): if that post isn't in the primary language, any newly-created term among its assigned terms is stamped as a translation immediately, checking the artist's declared native language (`_agnosis_native_lang`, set at intake) before falling back to the post's Lingua Forge language meta (`_lf_lang`). (`includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`)

## [0.9.37] — 2026-07-18

### Added
- **New `agnosis/artwork-copyright` block automatically credits an artwork with a "© {year} {artist name}" line, wired into every single artwork page by default.** Requested to correctly attribute copyright for artist-supplied artwork — previously nothing on an artwork's own page stated who held copyright or when the work was first published. `{year}` is the artwork's own publish date (`get_the_date()`), not the current year, so the notice correctly dates the work itself rather than drifting forward every January 1st; `{artist name}` resolves from `post_author` the same display-name-with-nicename-fallback convention `Network\SubdomainNavigation::artist_name()` already uses elsewhere. Registered the same directory-based way as `artist-name-link`/`breadcrumb-icon-link` (a real `block.json` + `editorScript`, not the bare context-only registration `Profile::register_blocks()`'s other blocks use) specifically so font size, text color, and font family are all configurable per-instance from the block's own Inspector panel via ordinary Color/Typography/Spacing block *supports* — no custom controls needed. Renders nothing off an `agnosis_artwork` post, or when the author account no longer resolves (e.g. deleted). Auto-wired into `agnosis-theme`'s `single-agnosis_artwork.html` (paired theme-side change, versioned separately in that repo) directly beneath the post content, styled with the theme's `foreground` color and `small` font size by default. (`blocks/artwork-copyright/block.json`, `blocks/artwork-copyright/editor.js`, `includes/Artist/Profile.php`)

### Fixed
- **The gallery overview's medium-filter bar had three compounding problems: it mixed every language's AI-translated medium term into one pill row, it offered pills for mediums the current context had no artwork in at all, and clicking a pill or a pagination link triggered a full page reload.** (1) `agnosis_medium` is one flat, language-agnostic taxonomy — `Compat\LinguaForge::sync_taxonomy()` auto-creates a real term per (medium, target language) AI translation and flags it with `TRANSLATED_TERM_META`, the same way `PromptConfig::medium_terms()` already excludes those from the AI's own controlled vocabulary. `blocks/gallery-overview/render.php`'s filter-bar term list never applied that same exclusion or any language scoping at all, unlike the post query a few lines above it in the same file, which already resolves `LF_LANG` for exactly this reason — a German site's filter row, for example, showed both "Oil Painting" and its German AI translation as two separate pills, and clicking the English one on the German site matched a term ID no German-tagged artwork actually carried. (2) Separately, the pill list was never scoped to what the current context could actually show at all — an artist's own subdomain gallery (which only ever shows that one artist's work) still listed every medium used by ANY artist sitewide, so a photography-only artist's page showed a "Sculpture" pill leading to a correctly-empty but confusing results page (reported live, with a screenshot, on a 3-artwork subdomain still showing all 5 sitewide medium pills). Both are now resolved together: the term list is restricted to terms actually attached to artwork within the current artist scope (subdomain artist, or the sitewide pool) AND the current request's language — the primary/original language shows only the admin-curated vocabulary (translated variants excluded), any secondary language shows only the terms translated into that exact language and actually used there. (3) A first attempt at removing the full-page-reload-per-click also shipped and was then reverted in the same pass: a pure client-side show/hide of whatever artwork was already rendered on the page, which — correctly called out before it could cause confusion — silently broke pagination, since a medium with matches only on page 2 of a paginated gallery would show nothing for it. Replaced with WordPress's own Interactivity API Router (`@wordpress/interactivity-router`, block.json's new `"interactivity": true` support + `"viewScriptModule"`): every pill and pagination link keeps its real, full, server-correct href, but clicking one now fetches that same URL's genuine `render.php` output and swaps only the router region (filter bar + grid + pagination together) into the page instead of doing a full navigation — pagination stays exactly as correct as a real page load, because it IS a real page load's output, just delivered without the reload. Getting the router itself working end-to-end took four more rounds of fixes, each masking the next until the previous one landed. First, the router module was enqueued standalone rather than declared as a dependency of the block's own view script module — this plugin has no build step to auto-detect the dynamic `import('@wordpress/interactivity-router')` inside `view.js` the way `wp-scripts` normally would, so the browser's import map never had an entry for it and every click failed outright (`Module name, '@wordpress/interactivity-router' does not resolve to a valid URL`); fixed by registering the view script module by hand with the router listed as an explicit dynamic-import dependency. Once that resolved, a medium filter with zero matching artwork blanked the entire gallery area instead of just failing to update — `render.php`'s own bare `return;` on an empty result meant the router had no `[data-wp-router-region]` in the fetched response to swap in at all; fixed by always rendering the wrapper and filter pills, with a "No artwork matches this filter yet" message in place of the grid. Then, filtering to a medium with genuinely matching, correctly-tagged artwork still came back empty — not a data or query bug at all: `agnosis_medium` is also the taxonomy's own registered `query_var`, so WordPress's `redirect_canonical()` silently 301-redirected every filter click to the real (and entirely different) taxonomy archive template at `/medium/x/`, which has none of this block's markup on it; fixed by renaming the block's own filter parameter to `agnosis_medium_filter`, which carries no taxonomy meaning to WordPress. Finally, filter and pagination links were built off `home_url('/')` unconditionally, correct only on `home.html` — a click on the artwork archive page (`archive-agnosis_artwork.html`, this block's other template) silently redirected to the home page instead of updating in place; links are now built off the current request's own URL instead, with the block's own two query params stripped from that base first so a stale page number can't survive a fresh filter click. (`blocks/gallery-overview/render.php`, `blocks/gallery-overview/block.json`, `blocks/gallery-overview/view.js`, `includes/Publishing/GalleryOverview.php`)

## [0.9.36] — 2026-07-18

### Added
- **New "Biography Title Translation Cache" panel (Settings → General), for hand-editing or retranslating the per-language AI cache behind the "Preset biography title" setting.** Prompted by a live bad-translation report: the German AI translation of a short "Meet the Artist"-style preset came back ungrammatical and incorrectly gendered feminine ("...die Künstlerin..."), with no way to correct it short of a direct database edit. Unlike the existing Term Translation Cache panel (clear-only — dozens/hundreds of small tag/medium labels, not worth hand-editing individually), a preset title only ever has one cached entry per configured language, so this panel is a real per-language text field: edit a translation directly and Save, or hit "↻ Retranslate" to discard just that language's cached value and let the AI try again, or "Clear All" to do that for every language at once. All three actions immediately re-apply the corrected title to every already-published sibling biography post in that language — not just the cache, so a fix is visible right away rather than only on the next sync.
