New `Artist\BiographyTitle::cached_translations()`/`set_translation_override()`/`clear_translation()`/`clear_all_translations()` read/write the same `agnosis_biography_preset_title_translations` option `translated_preset_title()` already used, gated behind three new admin-post handlers on a new `Admin\Dashboards\BiographyTitleCache` class. (`includes/Artist/BiographyTitle.php`, `includes/Admin/Dashboards/BiographyTitleCache.php`, `includes/Admin/Settings.php`, `includes/Core/Plugin.php`)

### Changed
- **`AI\SubmissionTranslator`'s AI translation prompts now steer away from defaulting to a specific grammatical gender, and `translate_text()` can be given short framing context — the other half of the fix above, and applying more broadly than just this one setting.** Every JSON-envelope prompt this class builds (`call_translate()`, `translate_fields()`, `translate_to_languages()`) now includes a standing instruction to prefer gender-neutral phrasing for a generic term (e.g. "artist", "author") whose gender the source text doesn't specify, rather than picking one by default — the root cause of the German mistranslation above: many target languages (German, French, Spanish, ...) grammatically require some gender choice for such nouns that English leaves unmarked, and nothing in the prompt previously said what to do about it. Separately, `translate_text()` gained an optional `$context` parameter so a caller translating an unusually short, bare phrase — exactly the shape that also caused the AI to misread "Meet the Artist" as a past-tense phrase rather than an imperative heading — can tell the AI what kind of text it is; `BiographyTitle::translated_preset_title()` now passes context explaining the text is a short page heading, not prose. Both changes are prompt-only — no change to which provider/model is used or how responses are parsed. (`includes/AI/SubmissionTranslator.php`, `includes/Artist/BiographyTitle.php`)
- **Cleared all 252 fuzzy-marked translation entries across every one of the 18 `.po` language files (14 per language), to hand full retranslation to Loco Translate instead of leaving a wrong AI-guessed match in place.** These were new/changed English source strings (mostly from the two features above, plus a few older ones — `"DKIM record"`, `"Language Badge"`, the breadcrumb block's description/keyword) that a prior `.po` regeneration had fuzzy-matched to the closest existing translation — several of which were flatly wrong, not just approximate (e.g. German `"DKIM record"` matched to `"DMARC-Eintrag"`, a different DNS record entirely; `"[%1$s] Application awaiting your review: %2$s"` matched to an unrelated old vouch-reminder sentence). Fuzzy entries are already skipped at compile time (confirmed neither the wrong text nor the correct-by-coincidence text had reached any `.l10n.php`), so this is a source-only, translator-facing change: no behavior change to what any site currently shows. (`languages/agnosis-*.po`, 18 files)

### Fixed
- **PHPStan: `BiographyTitle::clear_all_translations()` passed an `array_keys()` result straight to `resync_live_titles( string $target_lang )`, which types as `int|string` (a numeric-string array key is auto-cast to `int` by PHP, something PHPStan can't rule out for a language-code array even though no real Lingua Forge code is ever purely numeric).** Caught by a lint pass on the panel above before it shipped; fixed with an explicit `(string)` cast at the one call site. (`includes/Artist/BiographyTitle.php`)

## [0.9.35] — 2026-07-18

### Added
- **New setting, "Admin approval only" (`agnosis_voting_disabled`, Settings → Community → Rules), lets a node turn off community voting entirely and make every admission and removal decision a direct admin call — a gallery or other curated context may want a human deciding who joins and who is asked to leave, not a community majority.** A single switch covers both voting systems at once: `Admission::record_vote()` — the one choke point already shared by the authenticated REST vouch route and the unauthenticated `VouchConfirm` email-link vote — refuses with a 403 while it's on, and `Departure::nominate()` refuses to start a brand-new nomination or advance one still gathering signatures ('nominating' status) the same way. Neither call site needed to be invented: `Admission::admin_admit()`/`admin_reject()` (Settings → Community → Pending Applications) and `Departure::admin_ban()`/`admin_delete()` (Settings → Community → Members) already existed as an admin bypass alongside voting — this setting just makes the community-vote path unavailable so admin action becomes the *only* path instead of an optional shortcut. `Admission::check_expired_applications()` (the daily auto-reject cron) also stops acting on pending applications while the setting is on — with no possible votes, applying the existing voting-window auto-reject would have silently rejected every application an admin hadn't gotten to yet; applications now simply wait for `admin_admit()`/`admin_reject()` instead. A removal request already `'open'` when the setting is switched on is deliberately left alone: artists can still cast a vote on it (`record_vote_on_request()`, reached via `cast_vote()`, the `RemovalVoteConfirm` email link, or `nominate()`'s own forward-to-vote branch for a request already open) and it resolves normally via the unchanged `check_expired_removal_votes()` cron — only *opening new* community votes is blocked, whether via fresh nominations reaching threshold or `Departure::admin_open_removal_vote()`'s own admin bypass (which now refuses outright, since its whole purpose — opening a community vote while skipping nominations — no longer applies once community voting is off). `AdmissionNotification::on_application_received()` skips the per-artist vote-blast email and the digest-mode `VoteDigest::send_daily()` cron entirely while the setting is on (nobody could act on either), sending the admin a single actionable "Application awaiting your review" email with a link straight to the Pending Applications dashboard instead of the previous FYI-only summary; the applicant's own acknowledgment email is reworded to not promise a community vote or a fixed deadline that no longer applies. Both admin dashboards (`AdmissionDashboard`, `MembersDashboard`) show a notice and adjust their own display while the setting is on — the vote-progress bar/column is replaced with "Awaiting admin review" text, and the "Open Vote" button is hidden (its handler was already guarded independently via `admin_open_removal_vote()`'s own refusal, so this is belt-and-suspenders, not the only protection). Off by default — existing installs see no behavior change until an admin opens this setting deliberately. (`includes/Admin/SettingsFields.php`, `includes/Artist/Admission.php`, `includes/Artist/Departure.php`, `includes/Artist/AdmissionNotification.php`, `includes/Artist/VoteDigest.php`, `includes/Admin/Dashboards/AdmissionDashboard.php`, `includes/Admin/Dashboards/MembersDashboard.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Artist/AdmissionVotingDisabledTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Artist/RemovalVotingDisabledTest.php`)

## [0.9.34] — 2026-07-17

### Fixed
- **The three hand-maintained lists of Agnosis's WP-Cron hooks had drifted out of sync — `uninstall.php` was missing `agnosis_vote_digest` and `agnosis_flush_permalinks` entirely, and `Activator::deactivate()` cleared none of the three single-event hooks (`agnosis_publish_submission`, `agnosis_dispatch_lf_translations`, `agnosis_flush_permalinks`) at all.** A pending single-event of any of those three survived deactivation and fired into the void; on uninstall, `agnosis_vote_digest` was only ever cleared in practice because WordPress deactivates a plugin before deleting it (an ordering the uninstall contract shouldn't have been leaning on by accident), and `agnosis_flush_permalinks` was cleared nowhere at all — an orphan cron entry from a submission approved shortly before uninstall would survive indefinitely. Fixed with a new `Activator::CRON_HOOKS` constant (all 13 hooks — 10 recurring + 3 single-event) as the plugin runtime's single source of truth; `deactivate()` now loops over it. `uninstall.php` deliberately loads none of the plugin's classes, so it keeps its own literal copy of the same 13-entry list rather than referencing the constant directly — a new `CronHookParityTest` (parses `uninstall.php`'s array via PHP's own tokenizer, never by including/executing the file) asserts the two stay in exact parity going forward. Also switched both `deactivate()` and `uninstall.php` from `wp_clear_scheduled_hook( $hook )` to `wp_unschedule_hook( $hook )`: the former only matches an event scheduled with the exact arguments passed (none, by default) — since `agnosis_publish_submission` is always scheduled with a queue id and `agnosis_dispatch_lf_translations` with a dispatch payload, simply adding them to the old-style list would still have silently left a real pending instance behind. New tests cover this directly (scheduling each arg-bearing hook with real arguments, then asserting `deactivate()` actually clears it). (`includes/Core/Activator.php`, `uninstall.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Core/ActivatorTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Core/CronHookParityTest.php`)
- **The self-hosted update manifest (`docs/agnosis-update-manifest.php`) was eleven versions stale — still describing 0.9.22 while the plugin shipped as far as 0.9.33.** Any second install checking for updates against the live copy of this file would have seen nothing new since 0.9.22. Updated `$version`/`$download_url`/`$last_updated`/`$changelog` to 0.9.34 (trimmed to the two most recent releases, per the file's own stated convention), and cleared the stale `$sha256` back to the safe empty default until `dev/bin/build-zip.sh` fills it in for the real 0.9.34 ZIP. `dev/bin/build-zip.sh` already automated the `$sha256` field; the rest was still hand-edited by design (documented in the file's own header) but had simply stopped happening — added an explicit rule to `CONTRIBUTING.md`'s changelog/readme conventions section so this file gets the same "update on every version bump" treatment as `CHANGELOG.md` and `readme.txt`, rather than silently drifting again. (`docs/agnosis-update-manifest.php`, `CONTRIBUTING.md`)
- **The fediverse followers collection (`ActivityPub::followers()`) published each follower's delivery-plumbing *inbox URL* as its `orderedItems` entry, instead of the follower's *actor ID* — the field AS2/ActivityPub actually specifies there.** A consumer that dereferences a followers-list item (Mastodon's own follower-list rendering, a crawler, another node doing follower-graph work) expects a resolvable actor document; an inbox URL only answers signed POSTs, so nothing crashed (`totalItems` still drove the count correctly) but the collection wasn't spec-conformant, and for shared-inbox followers it incidentally exposed which server-wide endpoint each one delivers through. Fixed by selecting `actor_id` instead of `inbox_url` from `agnosis_followers` in the one public-facing branch that renders this collection; every delivery code path (`broadcast()`, the retry queue, node-scale broadcast) is untouched and still correctly reads `inbox_url` internally for actually delivering activities. (`includes/Network/ActivityPub.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Network/ActivityPubTest.php`)
- **A remote fediverse account self-deleting left its stale follower record behind forever, and every future broadcast kept POSTing to the now-dead inbox until the retry queue's full multi-day backoff finally exhausted — noisily, and only after the fact.** `ActivityPub::inbox()` handled `Follow`/`Like`/`Announce`/`Undo` but silently ignored `Delete`, the activity Mastodon (and other fediverse software) fans out when an account is removed. A verified `Delete` whose object resolves to the signing actor itself (a genuine self-account-delete — Mastodon sends this as an AS2 Tombstone, both that shape and a bare actor-URL string are handled) now removes every stored follower row for that actor, across every local owner it had followed (the node and/or any number of artists) — a Delete means the remote actor no longer exists at all, unlike an Undo's single-target unfollow. `Move` (account migration) is deliberately left unhandled, per an explicit decision recorded directly in the source: a follower relationship built on a migrated account simply lapses rather than transferring, an acceptable gap at gallery scale. Separately, a delivery that fails with a definitive `410 Gone` or `404 Not Found` — a confirmed-dead inbox, not a transient hiccup — now records straight to the retry queue's terminal `failed` state instead of working through its full ~4-day backoff first, on both the first live delivery attempt and the retry-queue processor. (`includes/Network/ActivityPub.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Network/ActivityPubTest.php`)
- **An email submission with no `text/plain` part — HTML-only mail from some webmail "rich text" modes, several mobile mail clients, and most marketing/newsletter composers an artist might paste from — silently lost its description text.** `Parser::parse_imap_message()` previously read only `getTextBody()`; a photo attachment still published correctly, but a text-only HTML submission (a poem, a biography written with no attachment) dead-ended at the "nothing usable" rejection as if the message were genuinely empty. Fixed with a new fallback: when the plain-text body is empty and an HTML body isn't, the HTML is converted to text (`<script>`/`<style>` blocks stripped entirely — real HTML mail does carry them — paragraph/line breaks converted to real newlines, tags stripped, and HTML entities decoded so `&#8217;` reaches the published post as an apostrophe, not literal entity text) before feeding the exact same reply/forward-extraction and rejection-gate logic a genuine plain-text body already goes through. A real `text/plain` part, when present, is always preferred — the fallback only ever engages when it's genuinely absent. (`includes/Email/Parser.php`, `tests/php/Unit/Email/ParserTest.php`, `tests/php/Unit/Email/FakeParserImapMessage.php`)
- **PHPStan: `Settings::field_definitions()`'s delegate (added this same version by the Settings.php refactor below) called `SettingsFields::all()` with static syntax against a method that was still declared as a plain instance method.** Caught by a `composer analyse` run before it could ship: `Static call to instance method Agnosis\Admin\SettingsFields::all().` `all()` has no instance state — it's pure data plus calls to its own already-`private static` `sanitize_color()` helper — so the correct fix is declaring it `static` to match how it's actually called, not adding an unnecessary `new SettingsFields()`. (`includes/Admin/SettingsFields.php`)

### Changed
- **Hygiene pass (audit §4d, AUDIT-1.0.0.md).** British spellings in comments/docblocks (`behaviour`→`behavior`, `colour`→`color`, plus `customisable`/`recognised` caught in the same sweep) Americanized across all 18 files the audit identified — the deliberate `'colour cast'` dual-spelling matcher key in `Notification.php` (matches either spelling in AI-generated quality-issue text) and its adjacent section-heading comment were left untouched by design, same for the `$level_colours` variable name in `Settings.php` (an identifier, not a comment — outside this finding's stated "comments/docblocks" scope). `WordPressAI.php`'s one unlabeled `@phpstan-ignore-next-line` (of thirteen in `includes/`, the only one with no rationale) now carries the same documented-reasoning style as the other twelve. `readme.txt`'s Installation section gained a first step noting Lingua Forge must be installed and active before Agnosis will activate (`Requires Plugins` resolves only against locally-installed slugs, so a fresh install hitting this needs to know the order). Of the finding's remaining two items: deferred-test debt was initially left as a recorded, no-action observation here, then corrected and actually closed this same version — see the entry two below. `Settings.php`'s size was likewise initially left as "confirmed accurate, no action needed" here, then actually refactored this same version once asked to propose a plan for it — see the entry directly below. (`includes/AI/Providers/WordPressAI.php`, `includes/Email/Inbox.php`, `includes/Email/IntakeGates.php`, `includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`, `includes/Core/EmailBranding.php`, `includes/Newsletter/PopoverBlock.php`, `includes/Publishing/Notification.php`, `includes/Core/Plugin.php`, `includes/Publishing/TextPosterGenerator.php`, `includes/AI/PromptConfig.php`, `includes/Core/Debug.php`, `includes/Core/LoginBranding.php`, `includes/Core/EmailFooter.php`, `includes/Network/SubdomainNavigation.php`, `includes/Artist/Profile.php`, `includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`, `includes/Artist/AdmissionNotification.php`, `includes/Publishing/EmbedPolicy.php`, `readme.txt`)
- **`Settings.php`'s size (audit §4d, AUDIT-1.0.0.md) — a 3,347-line god class (22 `admin_post_*` actions + 1 AJAX handler, 10 tabs' rendering, sanitizers, test-send handlers) split into 9 focused classes, none over ~230 lines.** Not a defect on its own — every handler was already correctly guarded and internally consistent — but the size was exactly where the audit flagged the next structural refactor would pay off if the plugin gains contributors; asked to propose a plan for it, then asked to execute the full plan this same pass rather than leave it recorded-only. `Admin\SettingsFields::all()` now holds the ~1,000-line field-definitions data table verbatim (plus the `sanitize_color()` helper its closures call) — `Settings::field_definitions()` stays as a one-line delegating wrapper, kept by name and visibility rather than removed outright, since `EmailBrandingColorFieldsTest`/`SettingsResettableFieldsTest` both reach it via `ReflectionMethod` and there's no benefit to churning that test surface for a rename. Eight self-contained render-method-plus-its-own-handler(s) clusters — each already had zero cross-references to any sibling cluster — moved to a new `Admin\Dashboards` sub-namespace, one class apiece: `AdmissionDashboard`, `MembersDashboard`, `NewsletterDashboard`, `InvitationCard`, `DeliverabilityCard`, `BrandingTestForm`, `LogsTab` (render + `handle_clear_logs()` only — the Logs tab's other two handlers, `handle_clear_debug_files()`/`handle_clear_term_translations_cache()`, stay on `Settings` since their render methods live on the General tab as shared framework content, not the Logs tab), and `AiTestTools`. `Core\Plugin::register_services()` rewires all 15 moved `admin_post_agnosis_*`/`wp_ajax_agnosis_test_ai` hook registrations from `$settings` to a `new` instance of the appropriate `Dashboards` class — same hook names throughout, so no behavior change for anything already wired against them. Five integration test files that reached into `Settings` for one of these moved methods (directly, or via `ReflectionMethod` for a private one) were updated to instantiate the new owning class instead: `AiProviderPingTest`, `SettingsInitiateRemovalVoteTest`, `DeliverabilityTest`, `SettingsRetryFailedNewsletterTest`, `SettingsNewsletterLocaleTest`. `Settings.php` itself is now 876 lines — `register_menu()`/`register_settings()`/`enqueue_assets()`/`render_page()`/the tab-switching and field-rendering machinery/the four inline JS/CSS builders/the two Logs-tab handlers that stayed — everything that's genuinely still one cohesive settings-page concern, not a stray leftover. (`includes/Admin/Settings.php`, `includes/Admin/SettingsFields.php`, `includes/Admin/Dashboards/AdmissionDashboard.php`, `includes/Admin/Dashboards/MembersDashboard.php`, `includes/Admin/Dashboards/NewsletterDashboard.php`, `includes/Admin/Dashboards/InvitationCard.php`, `includes/Admin/Dashboards/DeliverabilityCard.php`, `includes/Admin/Dashboards/BrandingTestForm.php`, `includes/Admin/Dashboards/LogsTab.php`, `includes/Admin/Dashboards/AiTestTools.php`, `includes/Core/Plugin.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Admin/AiProviderPingTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Admin/SettingsInitiateRemovalVoteTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Admin/DeliverabilityTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Admin/SettingsRetryFailedNewsletterTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Admin/SettingsNewsletterLocaleTest.php`)
- **Deferred-test debt (audit §4d, AUDIT-1.0.0.md) — actually closed, not just re-recorded.** The hygiene-pass entry above originally treated this item's own "None blocks 1.0.0" framing as license to leave it alone; corrected on review — closing a finding means fixing it, not re-confirming an audit's own softening language as a reason not to. Three previously-hand-verified-only or explicitly-deferred pieces of coverage now have real tests. (1) **Queue-claiming** (0.9.30's claim-then-read fix, §2c — PHPUnit coverage was "deliberately deferred this pass, by request" per that entry): every existing test for `Newsletter\QueueProcessor::process()` and `ActivityPub::process_delivery_retry_queue()` only exercised normal, non-overlapping single-call behavior, which passes trivially whether or not the claim mechanism actually prevents double-processing. New tests simulate a genuinely concurrent second tick directly — seeding a row already `'claimed'` by a token the call under test never issued — and prove: a live claim is never re-claimed or stolen; `reset_stale_claims()`/`reset_stale_delivery_claims()` recovers a claim abandoned past the 30-minute threshold but leaves a fresh one untouched; and `QueueProcessor::maybe_complete_issue()` doesn't mark an issue `'sent'` while a sibling row from another tick's still-outstanding claim remains `'claimed'`. (2) **Per-sender branding-accent wiring** (AUDIT-0.9.29.md §2a's test-coverage note, still open two audits later): nothing asserted that a *configured* Settings → Branding accent color actually reaches a rendered email per sender class — the Settings surface was tested, `Core\EmailTemplate` was tested in isolation, and the wiring claim itself ("every email") went untested, the exact pattern the note flagged. A new `EmailBrandingAccentWiringTest` configures one distinctive, non-default accent and asserts it survives into the real, captured send path of all 8 sender classes that read it (`Newsletter\Mailer`, `Newsletter\Subscription`, `Artist\AdmissionNotification`, `Artist\CommunityBroadcast`, `Artist\VoteDigest`, `Artist\DepartureNotification`, `Artist\Invitation`, `Publishing\Notification`). (3) **`EmailBranding` luminance sweep** (0.9.29's WCAG contrast fix, §2b — hand-verified only): a new `EmailBrandingLuminanceSweepTest` data-provider sweeps a representative range of configured header backgrounds — including the exact grayscale value pair the luminance formula's own 0.5 threshold falls between (`#bbbbbb`/`#bcbcbc`, independently computed from the same formula, not guessed) — against both `header_subtitle_color()` directly and `header_html()`'s embedded wordmark color, plus the malformed-input fallback path. AUDIT-1.0.0.md's priority-matrix `Status` column and §4d's own resolution note both updated to reflect the corrected count. (`tests/php/Integration/Newsletter/QueueProcessorTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Network/ActivityPubTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Core/EmailBrandingAccentWiringTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Core/EmailBrandingLuminanceSweepTest.php`)

## [0.9.33] — 2026-07-17

### Added
- **The artist breadcrumb now shows the artist's native language as a two-letter code, alongside the existing biography/events/contact icons, with the language's own native name (e.g. "Deutsch", "Español" — not translated into the visitor's own page language) as the hover tooltip.** New `type: 'language'` variant on the `agnosis/breadcrumb-icon-link` block, rendered as a plain-text badge rather than a link (there's nowhere for it to go). Sourced from the WP `locale` user meta already set on the artist's account at admission time (`Admission::iso_to_wp_locale()`, from the language they picked on the join form) — no new field, no schema change; an artist with no locale on file (admitted before 0.9.22, or an account created outside the join flow) shows no badge at all rather than a misleading default. The native-language display name comes from `AI\SubmissionTranslator::language_names()`, backed by Lingua Forge's `linguaforge_language_label()`, which already renders a language's name in its own script regardless of what language the visitor is currently browsing in. `agnosis-theme`'s `parts/header.html`/`header-pages.html` both got the new badge appended after the contact icon, in the same icon-links group (theme-side change, versioned separately in that repo). (`includes/Network/SubdomainNavigation.php`, `blocks/breadcrumb-icon-link/block.json`, `blocks/breadcrumb-icon-link/editor.js`, `blocks/breadcrumb-icon-link/frontend.css`)

### Fixed
- **Artists confirming a join application weren't realizing the email link's landing page still needed a second, manual click — the first few applicants got stuck there.** The confirm interstitial (`Artist\AdmissionConfirm::render_confirm()`) now auto-submits its confirm form via a small inline `<script>` the moment the page loads, so a real visitor doesn't have to click anything. This doesn't reopen the reason the two-step flow existed in the first place: corporate mail-security scanners prefetch links in incoming email to scan them, and a prefetch alone must never confirm an application (security audit §3a/§4a — see the class's own docblock). The server side is unchanged — it still only acts on a POST carrying a valid single-use token, and is still blind to a bare GET; scanners that prefetch links generally don't execute JavaScript, so only an actual browser triggers the auto-submit. The original "Confirm my application" button is kept as a `<noscript>` fallback for the rare visitor without JS. Scoped to the artist join flow only — `VouchConfirm` (community vote invites) and the newsletter's `SubscriptionConfirm`, which share the same prefetch-safe two-step pattern, were deliberately left untouched. (`includes/Artist/AdmissionConfirm.php`)

## [0.9.32] — 2026-07-16

### Added
- **The Deliverability card (Settings → Email) now also checks for a DKIM record and whether the sending domain is listed on Spamhaus's Domain Block List** — prompted by a real case: FluentSMTP reported a confirmation email as sent, but it was silently dropped by Spamhaus flagging a newly-registered domain as a possible spam source, something the existing SPF/DMARC-only card had no way to surface. New `Deliverability::dbl_check()` queries `{domain}.dbl.spamhaus.org` for an A record (the standard DNSBL convention) and, when listed, surfaces Spamhaus's own TXT explanation record alongside a red "LISTED" badge; a `127.255.255.x` response (Spamhaus's documented error/rate-limit range) is treated as `unavailable` rather than a false positive. New `Deliverability::dkim_check()` is necessarily best-effort — unlike SPF's bare domain or DMARC's fixed `_dmarc.` subdomain, a DKIM record's location depends on a selector chosen by whichever service actually signs outbound mail, which the plugin has no way to know for certain — so it tries a curated list of common provider selectors (`dkim_selectors()`, filterable via `agnosis_deliverability_dkim_selectors` for a site that knows its own) and only counts a match that actually looks like DKIM (`v=DKIM1` or a `p=` key field, not just any TXT record at that name). Both checks are transient-cached for an hour: DKIM's selector guessing can issue up to ~20 sequential DNS queries per identity, and Spamhaus's public DNSBL mirror has its own fair-use rate policy, so neither should re-query on every admin page load the way the existing uncached SPF/DMARC checks do. The admin UI clearly marks a DKIM "not found" as amber/inconclusive rather than red/failed, with an explicit note that this check cannot prove DKIM is absent — only that it isn't under one of the guessed names. (`includes/Admin/Deliverability.php`, `includes/Admin/Settings.php`)

## [0.9.31] — 2026-07-16

### Fixed
- **A newly approved submission's own page — and every Lingua Forge-translated sibling of it — could 404 until an admin manually resaved Settings → Permalinks.** WordPress only matches incoming requests against whatever rewrite rules are cached in the `rewrite_rules` option; neither Agnosis's own CPT registration nor Lingua Forge's language-prefixed CPT/taxonomy rules (`add_rewrite_rule()`, run fresh on every request) retroactively update that cached option — only an explicit `flush_rewrite_rules()` call does. New `Core\RewriteFlush` schedules exactly one debounced flush (a WP-Cron single event, deduplicated via `wp_next_scheduled()` the same way `Compat\LinguaForge::schedule_fanout()` already debounces its own translation dispatch) at two points: `Publishing\ReviewEndpoints::finalize_publish()` calls it once a submission is approved and its primary-language post (plus native-language sibling, when the artist writes in a different language) exists; a new `Compat\LinguaForge::mark_fanout_progress()` — hooked on `linguaforge_translation_complete` alongside this class's existing listeners — tracks which of a post's dispatched target languages (`request_translations()`'s own `$languages` list, recorded in a new `PENDING_FANOUT_META` post meta) are still outstanding, and calls it again once the last one finishes translating. Neither call site flushes synchronously on the request that triggered it — a burst of approvals, or one submission fanning out to a dozen languages, still collapses into a single flush. (`includes/Core/RewriteFlush.php`, `includes/Core/Plugin.php`, `includes/Publishing/ReviewEndpoints.php`, `includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`)

## [0.9.30] — 2026-07-15

### Added
- **A dedicated Settings → Branding tab, inserted right after General, now holds the three email-branding fields that were on General ("Email logo", "Email header background", "Email accent color" — relabeled "Email logo", "Header background", "Accent color" now that the tab name itself supplies the "email" context) plus five new controls: `agnosis_email_width` (card width in px, 320–800, default 600), `agnosis_email_body_bg` (the page/letterbox background around the card, default `#f5f5f5`), `agnosis_email_card_bg` (the card's own background, default `#ffffff`), `agnosis_email_text_color`/`agnosis_email_text_size` (primary body text, default `#222222`/16px), and `agnosis_email_text_secondary_color`/`agnosis_email_text_secondary_size` (the footer tagline and other muted text, default `#bbbbbb`/14px — the value already used by most of the plugin's email footers; the one file with a divergent `#999`/15px, `Publishing\Notification`, is now normalized to match). Every field keeps the same sanitize-fallback shape the original two color fields established (`sanitize_hex_color()`/clamped-range on save, re-validated again at read time in `EmailTemplate`'s own getters) so a stored value that predates validation can never break an email. All eight defaults reproduce the plugin's original hardcoded look exactly, so an existing install sees no visual change until an operator opens the new tab. (`includes/Admin/Settings.php`)
- **`Core\EmailTemplate` gained matching getters for all five new settings** (`width()`, `body_bg()`, `card_bg()`, `text_color()`/`text_size()`, `text_secondary_color()`/`text_secondary_size()`), and `render()` — the shared shell already used by `AdmissionNotification`, `CommunityBroadcast`, `CommunityCapNotification`, and `DepartureNotification` — now builds its card, page background, and text styling entirely from these getters instead of the previous hardcoded `#f5f5f5`/`#ffffff`/`600`/`#222`/`#bbb` literals. `EmailBranding::header_html()`'s logo backing panel, previously a literal `552` (`600 − 24 − 24`, the card width minus its own header padding), now derives that width from `EmailTemplate::width() − 48` so a resized card and its logo panel stay in sync. (`includes/Core/EmailTemplate.php`, `includes/Core/EmailBranding.php`)
- **Branding tab amplified with 5 more controls — footer background, divider/border color, button text color, notice-box background, and footer label color — closing the gap between "the shell is configurable" and "the template is configurable."** Everything the two entries above wired up covered the shell's own header/body/footer rows; it left roughly 35 more hardcoded `#f9f9f9`/`#eee` literals untouched across every `build_*_body()` method — the shaded quote/summary boxes (bio/statement quotes, "did you mean" suggestions, tip lists, application summaries) and thin divider lines (above the work-addresses footer card, around the newsletter's "view online" banner) that appear throughout actual email content, not just the shared shell. New settings: `agnosis_email_footer_bg` (footer strip background, independent of the card background so the footer can be set off visually), `agnosis_email_border_color` (every thin divider), `agnosis_email_button_text_color` (CTA button text, for operators pairing a light accent), `agnosis_email_notice_bg` (every shaded info/quote box), and `agnosis_email_footer_label_color` (the bold "Artwork:"/"Biography:" labels in the work-addresses card). All ~35 sites across `Publishing\Notification` (all 8 methods), `Artist\AdmissionNotification`, `Artist\DepartureNotification`, `Artist\CommunityCapNotification`, `Artist\VoteDigest`, `Artist\CommunityBroadcast`, `Newsletter\Mailer`'s "view online" banner, and `Core\EmailFooter` now read the matching getter instead of a literal. In passing, also caught and fixed a second contrast bug of the same shape as AUDIT-0.9.29.md §2b: `Newsletter\Mailer`'s newsletter-heading subtitle and `Artist\Invitation`'s "You're invited" subtitle both hardcoded `color:#ece9ff` under the header wordmark — invisible against a light "Header background" pick, same failure as the wordmark itself before §2b. New `EmailBranding::header_subtitle_color()` derives this from the same luminance check `header_text_color()` already does, rather than adding a raw color field that could reintroduce the bug. Deliberately left alone: `EmailTemplate::DANGER` and the logo's white backing panel (both already documented as intentionally fixed, not oversights — see `EmailTemplate`'s class docblock), and `Newsletter\Archive`'s paginated issue-list page (a standalone front-end page never routed through `EmailTemplate`, out of scope for "the template"). All new fields default to the plugin's exact original hardcoded values, so an existing install sees no visual change. (`includes/Admin/Settings.php`, `includes/Core/EmailTemplate.php`, `includes/Core/EmailBranding.php`, `includes/Core/EmailFooter.php`, `includes/Newsletter/Mailer.php`, `includes/Artist/Invitation.php`, `includes/Publishing/Notification.php`, `includes/Artist/AdmissionNotification.php`, `includes/Artist/DepartureNotification.php`, `includes/Artist/CommunityCapNotification.php`, `includes/Artist/VoteDigest.php`, `includes/Artist/CommunityBroadcast.php`)
- **AUDIT-0.9.29.md §2d: a "Send test email" card on Settings → Branding.** The color/logo/width fields saved blind — an operator's first real look at how they combine was whatever email happened to go out next, not guaranteed to exercise every field (the work-addresses footer card, for instance, only appears on artist-facing mail). A new card below the Branding fields (same one-click "send to an address" pattern as the newsletter/invitation/deliverability test-send buttons already on other tabs) sends one representative `EmailTemplate::render()` body — header with a subtitle, a body paragraph, a button, and the footer card when configured — so a single test exercises every Branding field together, built from whatever is currently saved. Diagnostic only: no subscriber, queue, or setting is touched. (`includes/Admin/Settings.php`, `includes/Core/Plugin.php`)

### Fixed
- **The header background and accent color settings added in 0.9.29 only ever reached 4 of the 10 classes that send outgoing HTML email.** `AdmissionNotification`, `CommunityBroadcast`, `CommunityCapNotification`, and `DepartureNotification` call the shared `EmailTemplate::render()` and so picked up both settings correctly. The other 6 — `Publishing\Notification` (8 separate `build_*_body()` methods: not-found, promotion-success, removal confirmation, removal-choice, review, no-attachment, reply-rejected, rejection), `Newsletter\Mailer`, `Newsletter\Subscription`, `Artist\Invitation`, and `Artist\VoteDigest` — hand-roll their own copy of the same HTML shell and had independently assigned `$header_bg = '#0d0d12'` / `$accent = '#7c6af7'` as PHP literals, completely bypassing `EmailTemplate::header_bg()`/`accent()`. Changing either setting silently did nothing for the majority of the plugin's outgoing mail — this is the bug behind the original "email branding settings aren't respected" report. All 10 classes now call `EmailTemplate::header_bg()`/`accent()` directly (destructive-action buttons keep using `EmailTemplate::DANGER`, unchanged and still not configurable — see that constant's docblock), and their hand-rolled shells were further updated to read the five new width/background/text settings above from the same getters, so every outgoing email — not just the four already on the shared shell — now honors the full Branding tab. One further bypass of the same kind was found and fixed in passing: `Newsletter\Mailer`'s "View it online" link used a literal `#7c6af7` instead of the accent setting. (`includes/Publishing/Notification.php`, `includes/Newsletter/Mailer.php`, `includes/Newsletter/Subscription.php`, `includes/Artist/Invitation.php`, `includes/Artist/VoteDigest.php`)
- **Checked the fix above against AUDIT-0.9.29.md §2a (filed against the same bug this same 0.9.30 cycle set out to close — a coincidence of timing, not the audit responding to this release) and found two things it caught that the first pass missed.** (1) `Publishing\Notification::build_removal_email()` and `::build_removal_choice_email()` never assigned a `$header_bg` variable at all — their header `<td>` had `background:#0d0d12` typed directly into the markup, so the variable-based fix above had nothing to replace there; both now call `EmailTemplate::header_bg()` inline, same as every other header cell in the file. (2) `Core\EmailFooter::html()` — the "work emails" reference card that `Publishing\Notification`, `AdmissionNotification`, `DepartureNotification`, and `CommunityCapNotification` all append below the main body as `$footer_extra_html` — hardcoded its own `color:#7c6af7` on every mailto link, independent of the accent setting entirely. This was the audit's sharpest catch: because `EmailFooter::html()` renders *inside* the same email as a correctly-accented button, a rebranded install was sending single emails carrying two different accent colors at once — the operator's choice on the button, the original purple in the footer underneath it. Now reads `EmailTemplate::accent()`, closing the gap for all four classes that use it at once. The audit's third item, `Core\CommunityMailer`'s "HTML path," turned out to be a naming shorthand for the classes that call its `html_headers()` (Content-Type only, no markup) — those are `Publishing\Notification`, `Artist\Invitation`, and `Artist\VoteDigest`, already covered by the fix above; `CommunityMailer.php` itself holds no color literals. (`includes/Publishing/Notification.php`, `includes/Core/EmailFooter.php`, `includes/Core/EmailTemplate.php`)
- **AUDIT-0.9.29.md §2b: a light "Header background" (Settings → Branding) made the header wordmark invisible.** `EmailBranding::header_html()`'s text-fallback (what every fresh install renders — the uploaded-logo path was already fine) hardcoded `color:#fff` regardless of what background it was sitting on; nothing constrains the new color field to dark, and plenty of art sites are light-themed, so a white-on-white header was one plausible Settings choice away on every single outgoing email, including the admission-confirmation email new applicants must click to join. New private `EmailBranding::header_text_color()` computes the WCAG relative luminance of `EmailTemplate::header_bg()` and switches to `#0d0d12` (the same near-black used as the header's own dark default) once the background reads as light (luminance ≥ 0.5), self-healing with no operator education needed — exactly the audit's own suggested fix, chosen over its alternative (a Settings-side contrast warning) because it needs no follow-up action from the operator. The default `#0d0d12` background (luminance ≈ 0.006) keeps rendering white text, so an existing install sees no change. A malformed/unsanitized background — shouldn't happen, since `EmailTemplate::header_bg()` already re-validates with `sanitize_hex_color()` — falls back to white, the original always-on default, rather than guessing. (`includes/Core/EmailBranding.php`)
- **AUDIT-0.9.29.md §2a, proper tier: the five classes still hand-rolling their own copy of the branded shell now render through `EmailTemplate` directly, retiring the last of the duplicated DOCTYPE/table markup the two fixes above only patched the colors of.** A new `EmailTemplate::card()` returns the shell minus doctype/head/body — the same two nested `<table>`s `render()` already built, now factored out as a reusable fragment — plus two new optional parameters, `$header_extra_html` (extra markup inside the header cell, under the wordmark) and `$notice_row_html` (a full extra `<tr>` between the header and body rows), both threaded through `render()` too. `Publishing\Notification`'s all 8 `build_*_body()` methods, `Newsletter\Subscription::send_confirmation_email()`, `Artist\Invitation::build_body()` (`$header_extra_html` for its "You're invited" line), and `Artist\VoteDigest::build_body()` now call `EmailTemplate::render()` directly instead of assembling their own copy of the shell around a `$body_html` fragment. `Newsletter\Mailer` needed both: a new private `build_parts()` computes the shared body/footer/header/notice content once, `build_email()` passes it to `render()` for the sent message and `build_body()` passes the same parts to `card()` for `Newsletter\Archive`'s doctype-less "view online" page — so the sent email and the archived copy can no longer drift apart. Zero hand-rolled shell markup remains anywhere in the plugin outside `EmailTemplate.php` itself. A final sweep for any remaining literal `#7c6af7`/`#0d0d12` across `includes/` — to make sure this pass didn't stop at the shell and miss the same bug elsewhere — caught four more: `Publishing\Notification`'s `build_not_found_email()`, `build_promotion_success_email()`, `build_removal_email()`, and `build_removal_choice_email()` each hardcoded `border-left:3px solid #7c6af7` on an info/suggestion callout box, independent of that method's own (correctly-accented) button — the same "mixed accents within one email" bug the audit's sharpest catch (`EmailFooter`) already described, just not fully swept the first time. All four now read a `$brand_accent = EmailTemplate::accent()` local. Everything else the sweep found — `EmailTemplate`'s own default constants, `Settings`' own default values, wp-admin dashboard chrome (nav tabs, icons), and the front-end confirmation pages (`SubscriptionConfirm`, `VouchConfirm`, `AdmissionConfirm`, `RemovalVoteConfirm`, `ReviewConfirm`, `NotificationPreferences`, `Newsletter\Archive`) — is correctly out of scope: none of those are among the ~30 outgoing HTML *email sends* this finding was scoped to. No visual change on a default/unconfigured install: every getter this shell reads already falls back to the plugin's original hardcoded defaults. (`includes/Core/EmailTemplate.php`, `includes/Publishing/Notification.php`, `includes/Newsletter/Mailer.php`, `includes/Newsletter/Subscription.php`, `includes/Artist/Invitation.php`, `includes/Artist/VoteDigest.php`)
- **AUDIT-0.9.29.md §2c: neither the newsletter send queue nor the ActivityPub delivery retry queue claimed its rows before working them — two overlapping cron ticks (real system cron firing `wp-cron.php` while a slow SMTP conversation stretches the previous tick past 5 minutes) could both SELECT the same `'pending'` rows and each send/deliver them, double-mailing a recipient or double-POSTing an activity.** `Newsletter\QueueProcessor::process()` and `ActivityPub::process_delivery_retry_queue()` both now claim a batch atomically before reading it: a single `UPDATE … WHERE status = 'pending' [AND next_attempt_at <= …] ORDER BY id ASC LIMIT %d` tags the claimed rows with a per-run `claim_token` (a fresh `wp_generate_uuid4()` each call), then a `SELECT … WHERE claim_token = %s` reads back exactly and only those rows. InnoDB's row locking makes this race-free: the claim UPDATE's `status = 'pending'` condition is re-checked against the live, committed value as each row's lock is acquired, so a second overlapping claim simply finds an already-claimed row ineligible and skips it — no row can ever be claimed twice. Both `agnosis_newsletter_queue` and `agnosis_ap_delivery_queue` gained a `claim_token VARCHAR(36)` + `claimed_at DATETIME` column pair and a new `'claimed'` status value (schema-guarded in `Activator::maybe_upgrade()` for existing installs, same `SHOW COLUMNS`/`MODIFY COLUMN` pattern already used throughout this method). A stale-claim sweep — `reset_stale_claims()` / `reset_stale_delivery_claims()`, run at the top of every tick — resets any row stuck `'claimed'` past 30 minutes back to `'pending'`, so a PHP process that dies mid-batch (execution-time limit, host OOM kill) can't strand its claimed rows forever; the 30-minute threshold matches `Email\Inbox::force_reprocess()`'s existing stuck-`'processing'` reset for the intake queue rather than inventing a second convention. One related bug caught while implementing: `QueueProcessor::maybe_complete_issue()` (which decides an issue is fully sent) counted only `status = 'pending'` rows — with rows now spending a moment as `'claimed'`, it could mark an issue `'sent'` while a *different*, still-in-flight overlapping tick's claimed rows for that same issue hadn't finished yet; now counts `status IN ('pending','claimed')`. PHPUnit coverage deliberately deferred this pass, by request. No behavior change for a normal, non-overlapping tick. (`includes/Core/Activator.php`, `includes/Newsletter/QueueProcessor.php`, `includes/Network/ActivityPub.php`)
- **AUDIT-0.9.29.md §2d, the two remaining notes.** Both were already "checked and fine" calls in the finding itself, re-affirmed rather than changed: plaintext-and-SQL-equality subscriber tokens (256-bit single-purpose random values; a DB reader already has the emails anyway) and `Mailer::sender_header()`'s unsanitized from-name (`manage_options`-gated, and `wp_mail()`/PHPMailer encode the display name regardless). Separately, `EmailTemplate.php`'s doc comments used British spelling ("colour" ×6 at the time of the finding) — by the time this was picked up the count had grown to roughly 25, since this same 0.9.30 cycle's own shell-migration and branding-amplification passes added new docblocks written using the file's own then-current spelling instead of the project's standing American-English convention. All instances now read `color`/`colors`/`colored`; `Mailer.php` had none left to fix (already clean from its own rewrite earlier this cycle). (`includes/Core/EmailTemplate.php`)
- **AUDIT-0.9.29.md G-3: nine carried `phpcs` nits in `blocks/gallery-overview/render.php`, unresolved across three prior audit cycles.** `composer qa`'s green result never actually contradicted this finding — `dev/phpcs.xml`'s `<file>` scope only ever declared `agnosis.php`, `includes/`, and `tests/php/`; `blocks/` was never scanned by the local QA gate at all, so it couldn't have caught or cleared this file either way. `blocks/` is now added to that scope, so `composer qa` covers it going forward. The nine nits themselves: `phpcbf` mechanically fixed four (a missing trailing comma on a multi-line array's last item, one `<?php` tag with code on the same line as the opening tag, and two off-by-one-tab indentation slips). The remaining five were manual — one multi-line array's closing bracket wasn't on its own line at the expected column (restructured to the standard one-item-per-line array shape), and four instances of `Squiz.PHP.DisallowMultipleAssignments` in `$agnosis_artist_url_for`'s `return ( $cache[ $id ] = $value )` pattern (each split into a plain assignment followed by `return $value`, same cache-then-return behavior, no functional change). `php -l` and `phpcs` both clean on the file afterward. (`blocks/gallery-overview/render.php`, `dev/phpcs.xml`)
- **Follow-up to G-3: `composer qa` had three more blind spots beyond `blocks/`, none of them from the audit — found by checking what else `dev/phpcs.xml`, `dev/phpstan.neon`, and `dev/package.json`'s lint scripts actually cover versus what exists on disk.** (1) `uninstall.php` and `docs/agnosis-update-manifest.php` were outside `dev/phpcs.xml`'s `<file>` list the same way `blocks/` was; both added. `uninstall.php` came back clean; the manifest file was missing an `@package` tag, added. (2) `dev/phpstan.neon`'s `paths` only ever covered `agnosis.php` and `includes/` — `blocks/`, `tests/php/`, `uninstall.php`, and the docs manifest were entirely outside static analysis, not just style-checking; all four added to `paths`. Not verified by an actual run: `dev/vendor` requires PHP ≥8.2 and no PHP interpreter available in this environment could run it — worth a `composer run analyse` to confirm no new errors surface now that the scope is wider. (3) The largest gap: `dev/package.json`'s `lint:js`/`lint:css` scripts globbed against `../src/**/*.js` and `../src/**/*.css`, but no `src/` directory exists anywhere in this repo — every block's real JS/CSS lives directly under `blocks/*/` (`editor.js`, `frontend.js`, `frontend.css`, `editor.css`, 9 blocks). Because both scripts pass `--no-error-on-unmatched-pattern`, this never failed either — `composer qa` reported success having linted zero of those files, every time it's ever run. Repointed both globs at `../blocks/**/*`. Running the real tool against real files then surfaced genuine, previously invisible findings: `blocks/submissions/editor.js` had an unescaped apostrophe inside a single-quoted string (`artist's`) that broke the file's JS parse entirely — a real, shipped bug, not a lint nit, fixed by escaping it. Eight blocks' `edit: function ( props ) {...}` object-method pattern tripped `react-hooks/rules-of-hooks` (the anonymous function's inferred lowercase name looks like a plain function calling a hook, not a component) — each pulled out into a capitalized `var Edit = function (...) {...}` referenced as `edit: Edit`, the standard fix for this exact false-positive class; no behavior change. One genuinely unused variable (`wrap` in `blocks/join/frontend.js`) removed. One invalid JSDoc tag (`@package` with a value — meaningless/flagged in JS's JSDoc dialect, unlike PHPDoc) removed from `blocks/gallery-overview/editor.js`. On the CSS side, `dev/.stylelintrc.json` had a stale `"scss/at-rule-no-unknown": null` override targeting a rule the installed `@wordpress/stylelint-config` doesn't actually register (no `stylelint-scss` plugin loaded), which errored on every file instead of suppressing anything — removed. The base config's `selector-class-pattern` also didn't permit this codebase's own consistent BEM (`block__element`, `block--modifier`) class convention, used throughout every block; rather than rename the convention, added a BEM-permitting pattern override. Fourteen `currentColor` → `currentcolor` casing fixes applied via `stylelint --fix` (cosmetic, CSS keywords are case-insensitive). One real value change: `content-editor/frontend.css`'s `.agnosis-editable__pencil` used `line-height: 1.75em` where the project's own stylelint config only allows `px` for `line-height`; converted to the equivalent `28px` at the standard 16px base font-size (same computed value as the em version in the overwhelmingly common case, matching the width/height already set on the same element). `lint:js` and `lint:css` both clean afterward. (`dev/phpcs.xml`, `dev/phpstan.neon`, `dev/package.json`, `dev/.stylelintrc.json`, `docs/agnosis-update-manifest.php`, `blocks/submissions/editor.js`, `blocks/join/frontend.js`, `blocks/gallery-overview/editor.js`, `blocks/artist-breadcrumb/editor.js`, `blocks/artist-name-link/editor.js`, `blocks/breadcrumb-icon-link/editor.js`, `blocks/contact-form/editor.js`, `blocks/join/editor.js`, `blocks/newsletter-popover/editor.js`, `blocks/newsletter-signup/editor.js`, `blocks/content-editor/frontend.css`)
- **`wp i18n make-pot` warned that "Email: %s" carried 2 different translator comments.** `Artist\AdmissionNotification::build_admin_summary_body()` (applicant's own email, in the admin summary) and `Artist\ContactForm`'s visitor-forward email both used the identical `'Email: %s'` string under the same text domain, so the POT generator merged them into one entry — only one translator comment could survive, and it was wrong for whichever call site lost. Split via `_x()`/`esc_html_x()` with distinct contexts (`'application email'`, `'contact form reply-to email'`), which also removes a latent coupling bug: editing one call site's wording would previously have silently reworded the other, since they shared one msgid. Verified with a real `wp i18n make-pot` + `msgmerge` run: no warning, and both `.po` entries carried their existing translations straight through under the new contexts without going fuzzy. (`includes/Artist/AdmissionNotification.php`, `includes/Artist/ContactForm.php`, `languages/agnosis.pot`, `languages/agnosis-*.po`)
- **The same `make-pot` run surfaced 22 pre-existing fuzzy strings per locale (25 in en_US) — Branding-tab labels added earlier this cycle that `msgmerge` had guessed stale/mismatched translations for rather than leaving genuinely untranslated.** `msgfmt` already excludes fuzzy entries from compiled `.mo`/`.l10n.php` output by default, so this carried no user-facing effect, but the `.po` source was misleading about what's actually translated. Cleared via `msgattrib --clear-fuzzy --empty` across all 18 `languages/agnosis-*.po` files — strips the fuzzy flag and blanks the guessed `msgstr` rather than silently keeping a possibly-wrong translation, so these 22 strings now read as plainly untranslated and ready for a real translator pass. Recompiled `.mo`/`.l10n.php` for all 18 locales afterward; all succeeded. (`languages/agnosis-*.po`, `languages/agnosis-*.mo`, `languages/agnosis-*.l10n.php`)

### Changed
- **Minimum required PHP raised from 8.1 to 8.2.** Investigating why `composer qa` and this codebase's own bundled linter disagreed on `blocks/gallery-overview/render.php` (G-3, above) led to checking `dev/vendor`'s actual resolved dependency tree — and found that `webklex/php-imap`'s transitive dependencies (`illuminate/pagination` and its own `illuminate/collections`/`contracts`/`macroable`/`support`, plus `symfony/http-foundation`) had, at some past `composer update`, resolved to versions (Laravel 11.x's `illuminate/*` line, Symfony 7.x) that themselves require PHP ≥8.2 — silently, since `composer.json` only pins `webklex/php-imap`'s own version and never capped how new a transitive dependency it would accept. Composer's generated `vendor/composer/platform_check.php` — required unconditionally by `vendor/autoload.php`, which `agnosis.php` requires unconditionally on every plugin load, before the plugin's own graceful `agnosis_requirements_check()` version-gate function ever runs — enforces that floor with a hard `E_USER_ERROR`. In other words: this plugin's declared "Requires PHP: 8.1" was already inaccurate under the currently-locked dependencies; a real PHP 8.1 host would have fataled on activation instead of seeing the intended friendly admin notice. Rather than downgrade/pin the transitive dependencies back to 8.1-compatible versions, the decision was to raise the plugin's own declared floor to match what's already shipping — PHP 8.2 is widely available, and the plugin currently runs on one site the maintainer controls, so there's no compatibility cost to formalizing it. Updated everywhere the requirement is declared: `agnosis.php` (`Requires PHP:` header + `AGNOSIS_MIN_PHP` constant), `readme.txt`, `README.md`, `CONTRIBUTING.md`, both `composer.json` files (plugin root and `dev/`), `dev/phpcs.xml`'s `testVersion`, `dev/phpstan.neon`'s `phpVersion`, and `docs/agnosis-update-manifest.php`'s `requires_php` (read by the self-hosted updater and by any WP install checking update compatibility). No code changes — the codebase already only used syntax valid at 8.1+, which remains valid at 8.2+. (`agnosis.php`, `readme.txt`, `README.md`, `CONTRIBUTING.md`, `composer.json`, `dev/composer.json`, `dev/phpcs.xml`, `dev/phpstan.neon`, `docs/agnosis-update-manifest.php`)
- **Closing the loop on the previous entry's "not verified, worth a `composer run analyse`" caveat: it surfaced 4,550 findings on first real run, not zero.** Run for real (on a working PHP 8.2 CLI — the machine's own `/usr/local/bin/php` turned out to be a long-broken symlink to a `php@7.4` install missing a system library, unrelated to this session, worked around by pointing `PATH` at the working `php@8.2` Cellar install for these commands only), the widened `dev/phpstan.neon` scope from the G-3 follow-up above produced 4,550 errors, 4,544 of them in `tests/php/` alone. Root cause: `tests/php/Integration/`'s 130 files extend `WP_UnitTestCase` and use dozens of other WordPress test-suite classes that only exist at runtime (loaded by the WP core test suite, never by PHPStan) — with no stub package installed, PHPStan couldn't resolve any of it, and every unresolvable class cascaded into dozens of secondary "undefined method"/"undefined property" errors on top. This was never a real 4,550-defect codebase; it was 130 files hitting a missing dependency simultaneously, all at once, because `tests/php/` had never been in `phpstan.neon`'s `paths` before this session. **Fixed properly, not suppressed:** added `php-stubs/wordpress-tests-stubs` (a real dev dependency, `dev/composer.json`) and wired it into `phpstan.neon` via `scanFiles`, which alone dropped the count from 4,550 to 1,101 — the remaining errors, now genuinely visible for the first time, were checked file-by-file and split cleanly two ways. **Six were real, in shipped code, and got real fixes:** `blocks/gallery-overview/render.php` — `esc_attr()` fed a `wp_json_encode()` result typed `string|false` (cast to `string`; `json_encode` failing on this ASCII-only payload was never realistic, but the cast makes the guarantee explicit) — and a stray empty `<?php` block left dangling at the very end of the file after an earlier edit this session, which PHPStan correctly flagged as trailing-whitespace-after-code risk (removed, no behavior change, `render_callback`'s own `ob_start()`/`ob_get_clean()` wrapping is unaffected either way). `includes/Publishing/RemovalEndpoints.php` — a `?? 0` on an array key PHPStan can now *prove* always exists (because `tests/php/`'s own `lf_trash_cascade_stub.php` — now itself in scope — carries an accurate `@return array{trashed:int,skipped:int}` docblock PHPStan hadn't been able to see before), so the redundant coalesce was removed. `includes/AI/Providers/WordPressAI.php` (×2) and `includes/Admin/Settings.php` (×1) each had a stale `@phpstan-ignore-next-line` comment suppressing an error that no longer occurs — all three removed. A fourth stale ignore, same species, was in `tests/php/Integration/Network/SubdomainRouterIntegrationTest.php` — also removed directly rather than baselined, since PHPStan's own baseline generator refuses to baseline "unnecessary ignore" errors by design. **The other 1,099-plus, confined entirely to `tests/php/`, went into a new `dev/phpstan-baseline-tests.neon`** (included from `phpstan.neon`) rather than being hand-fixed: overwhelmingly one repeating shape — WordPress core's own stubs type functions like `wp_insert_post()`/`get_user_by()` as returning `int|WP_Error`/`WP_User|false`, and test code routinely uses the result as a bare `int`/`WP_User` after trusting a controlled test environment not to fail, which PHPStan can't see is safe the way a human reviewer or the test's own passing assertions can. Rewriting hundreds of individual test call sites with `is_wp_error()` guards to satisfy the analyzer would touch no real defect and carries real risk of introducing test bugs for zero safety benefit — a baseline is the standard, correct tool for exactly this situation: draw a hard line at today, keep the strict gate for all new code, and the debt stays visible and tracked in its own file rather than silently absent. Full `composer run qa` verified green end-to-end on the real environment afterward: `phpcs` clean, `phpstan` 0 errors, all 456 unit tests passing, `lint:js`/`lint:css` both clean. (`dev/composer.json`, `dev/phpstan.neon`, `dev/phpstan-baseline-tests.neon`, `blocks/gallery-overview/render.php`, `includes/Publishing/RemovalEndpoints.php`, `includes/AI/Providers/WordPressAI.php`, `includes/Admin/Settings.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Network/SubdomainRouterIntegrationTest.php`)
- **The baseline above still had two entries — `Imagick::addImage()`/`getImagesBlob()` in `tests/php/Unit/AI/MediaAdapterTest.php` — that only existed because the machine that generated it had a broken `imagick.so` (an architecture-mismatched build, unrelated to this session).** `dev/bootstrap.php` defines a fake `Imagick` stand-in class for machines without the real extension, and that fake never implemented those two methods — they're used only by a test helper's "real extension available" branch. On a machine where the real extension resolves, that fake never activates and the calls are valid, so the baseline entries came back stale ("Ignored error pattern... was not matched") the moment `composer run analyse` ran anywhere other than the machine that generated it — a baseline should never depend on which machine runs it. Fixed at the root, matching this test file's own stated goal of running identically on every machine: added minimal `addImage()`/`getImagesBlob()` implementations to the fake `Imagick` class (they're dead code at runtime — the real-extension branch that calls them is gated behind `extension_loaded('imagick')`, which is false whenever the fake is active — but PHPStan has no notion of that runtime guard and needs the methods to exist regardless), then removed the two now-unnecessary baseline entries. Verified with `composer run analyse` and `composer run qa` run again on the same broken-`imagick.so` machine that originally exposed the gap: both clean, zero unmatched-baseline warnings. (`dev/bootstrap.php`, `dev/phpstan-baseline-tests.neon`)
- **One more gap in the same PHP 8.1→8.2 raise: `composer build-zip` warned "the lock file is not up to date with the latest changes in composer.json."** The PHP-requirement raise above updated the plugin root's `composer.json` but only regenerated `dev/composer.lock` — the plugin root has its own separate `composer.lock` (the one `build-zip.sh`'s `composer install --no-dev` actually reads to populate the distributable `vendor/`), which was never touched. Confirmed it was the same stale-metadata shape as the earlier 4,550-error crisis, not a real dependency problem: the already-locked `illuminate/*` v11.51.0 and `symfony/http-foundation` v7.4.13 packages already require PHP ≥8.2, but the lock file's own recorded `platform.php` still read `>=8.1`. Fixed with `composer update --lock` at the plugin root — a metadata-only refresh; zero package versions changed. `composer validate` and `composer install --no-dev` (the exact step `build-zip.sh` runs) both verified clean afterward. (`composer.lock`)
- **AUDIT-0.9.27.md §4e / AUDIT-0.9.29.md's carried C-item, eleven-audit-old: the un-prefixed `webklex/php-imap` dependency tree (`illuminate/*`, `symfony/http-foundation`, `nesbot/carbon`) is the classic WordPress plugin-ecosystem collision — two plugins shipping different versions of the same package share one PHP namespace, and every CVE in that tree was Agnosis's to track regardless.** Decided in favor of prefixing (Strauss) over the audit's other option, replacing webklex with a leaner IMAP layer: webklex's `getAttachments()`/`getStructure()` MIME parsing is real, non-trivial functionality a replacement would have to reimplement, and webklex is pure-PHP with no `ext-imap` dependency — unaffected by PHP 8.4 unbundling `ext-imap` to PECL, a risk a lighter `ext-imap`-based replacement would have newly introduced instead of removing. Used `brianhenryie/strauss` (v0.28.1, via the officially-recommended `bin/strauss.phar` approach — the composer-dev-dependency alternative was tried first and hit a real self-collision bug: `symfony/console` [Strauss's own dependency] and webklex's tree both resolved to the same shared `vendor/symfony/deprecation-contracts`, so deleting it as part of webklex's tree broke Strauss's own second invocation). The full transitive tree (`webklex/php-imap`, `illuminate/{pagination,support,contracts,collections,macroable,conditionable}`, `symfony/http-foundation` + polyfills, `nesbot/carbon`, `doctrine/inflector`, `psr/{container,simple-cache,clock}`, `voku/portable-ascii`) is now prefixed to `Agnosis\Vendor\*` and copied to `vendor-prefixed/`, with the un-prefixed originals deleted from the shipped `vendor/` entirely. `includes/Email/{Inbox,Parser}.php`'s `Webklex\PHPIMAP\*` references were rewritten automatically via Strauss's call-site updater, widened to also cover `tests/php/` once `TestableInbox::query_messages()`'s method-override signature proved the rewrite had to be exact or PHP's own method-compatibility check would fatal. `dev/`'s test suite (which loads `includes/` directly) no longer needs its own `webklex/php-imap` dependency — `dev/bootstrap.php` now loads the plugin root's `vendor-prefixed/autoload.php` instead. Wired into the plugin root's `composer.json` via `post-install-cmd`/`post-update-cmd`, so the `composer install --no-dev` step `build-zip.sh` already runs self-bootstraps the whole pipeline (downloads the phar on first run) with no changes to `build-zip.sh` itself needed. Two build-tooling snags found and fixed along the way: Strauss's full-tree scan (now also covering `tests/php/`) exceeded Composer's default 300-second script timeout, requiring `Composer\Config::disableProcessTimeout` on both the plugin root's `prefix-namespaces` script and `dev/`'s `build-zip` script (two separate Composer processes); and Strauss's package deletion doesn't clean up Composer's separately-generated `vendor/bin/*` shims (found `vendor/bin/carbon` left dangling after `nesbot/carbon`'s own directory was deleted), added to `.distignore` alongside the phar and Strauss's dev-time `autoload_aliases.php` shim. Verified end-to-end: full `composer qa` clean (phpcs, phpstan, 456/456 unit tests, lint:js/lint:css) after the `dev/` bootstrap change, and a real `composer build-zip` run followed by unzipping and inspecting the actual archive — zero bare `Illuminate`/`Carbon`/`Symfony\Component\HttpFoundation` namespace declarations ship, 266 files correctly under the prefixed namespace, none of the excluded build artifacts present. (`composer.json`, `dev/composer.json`, `dev/bootstrap.php`, `.gitignore`, `.distignore`, `includes/Email/Inbox.php`, `includes/Email/Parser.php`, `tests/php/**` — call-site rewrite only, no logic changes)

## [0.9.29] — 2026-07-15

### Added
- **New `docs/guides/` folder — a plain `.md` reference for the plugin's largest blocks of user-facing prose (Artist Guide, About page, medium categories, join page copy, privacy policy + consent notices, and email templates), one file per topic plus an index `README.md`.** None of this text lived anywhere reviewable outside the PHP source that renders it; verified against the actual rendered output via a word-set-diff script before being added. (`docs/guides/README.md`, `docs/guides/artist-guide.md`, `docs/guides/about-page.md`, `docs/guides/medium-categories.md`, `docs/guides/join-page.md`, `docs/guides/privacy-policy-and-consent.md`, `docs/guides/email-templates.md`)
- **A shared `Core\EmailTemplate` class replaces roughly fifteen hand-rolled, duplicated copies of the same HTML email skeleton (DOCTYPE, 600px card, header/body/footer table rows) that had accumulated across the plugin's four notification classes.** `EmailTemplate::render( $lang, $body_html, $footer_extra_html = '' )` builds the full document; `EmailTemplate::button( $url, $label, $style = [] )` renders a consistently-styled call-to-action link. A fixed `EmailTemplate::DANGER` red (`#c0392b`) is available for destructive actions (reject, remove, vote-to-remove) and is deliberately **not** settings-configurable, so an operator can't accidentally make a destructive action visually indistinct from a routine one. (`includes/Core/EmailTemplate.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Core/EmailTemplateTest.php`)
- **Two new Settings → General fields — "Email header background" and "Email accent color" — let an operator restyle every outgoing HTML email to match their site's own branding**, via native `<input type="color">` fields with a "Reset to default" button. Both are read at send time by `EmailTemplate::header_bg()`/`accent()`, validated with `sanitize_hex_color()`, and fall back to the plugin's original hardcoded colors (`#0d0d12` header / `#7c6af7` accent) on an invalid or unset value — so an existing install sees zero visual change until an operator explicitly opts in. (`includes/Admin/Settings.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Admin/EmailBrandingColorFieldsTest.php`)

### Fixed
- **Investigated after being asked to "inform without coding first": several automated emails were still plain, unstyled text while the rest of the plugin's emails were already HTML.** `Artist\DepartureNotification` (all 8 email bodies — confirmation-requested, artist-left admin/artist notices, banned, reinstated, vote-opened/passed/failed) and `Artist\CommunityCapNotification` (all 3 — vote-opened/passed/failed) were plain text end to end; `Artist\AdmissionNotification` had 2 plain-text leftovers (the applicant/community expiry notices) plus an untranslated, raw-`sprintf()` admin summary email; `Artist\CommunityBroadcast` sent its "too long"/"empty" bounce notices as plain text and its per-recipient broadcast copy as `nl2br()`'d plain text. Root cause: a prior release's changelog entry overclaimed full HTML coverage, and that overclaim propagated into a stale docblock on `AdmissionNotification::build_vote_email_body()` ("the one remaining plain-text email") that this pass also corrected. All of the above are now built on the shared `Core\EmailTemplate` shell described above; `AdmissionNotification::send_admin_summary()` additionally gained real translatable strings in place of its raw `sprintf()` output. Every combined `\n\n`-joined plain-text paragraph was split into the same one-sentence-per-`__()` granularity every other HTML template in the plugin already uses, reusing existing msgids wherever the wording was unchanged. New/updated PHPUnit coverage across `AdmissionNotificationTest.php`, `DepartureNotificationTest.php` (previously covered only `on_artist_left()` — now also confirmation/ban/reinstatement/vote emails), a new `CommunityCapNotificationTest.php` (no dedicated mail-assertion coverage existed for this class before), and `CommunityBroadcastTest.php` verifies `Content-Type: text/html` and body content on every converted email. 38 new/changed translatable strings synced across `.pot` and all 18 `.po`/`.mo`/`.l10n.php` files (regenerated via a full `wp i18n make-pot`/`make-po`/`make-mo`/`make-php` pass rather than the usual surgical append, now that a `--skip-block-json --skip-js` flag combination was found that avoids this sandbox's network restriction to svn.wordpress.org for the PHP-string half of the scan; JS/block.json strings were left untouched by this pass to avoid losing existing entries no local fallback schema was available for). Two new Settings field descriptions were also caught using British spelling ("colour"/"coloured") and corrected to American English before syncing, per the plugin's established spelling convention. Deliberately out of scope for this pass: `Publishing\Notification.php`'s existing 8 HTML `wp_mail()` call sites (already styled, not "unstyled, plain" — the original complaint), and `ContactForm.php`/the AI-provider test-connection ping's separate plain-text usage (neither was flagged in the investigation this pass responded to). (`includes/Artist/AdmissionNotification.php`, `includes/Artist/DepartureNotification.php`, `includes/Artist/CommunityCapNotification.php`, `includes/Artist/CommunityBroadcast.php`, `includes/Admin/Settings.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Artist/AdmissionNotificationTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Artist/DepartureNotificationTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Artist/CommunityCapNotificationTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Artist/CommunityBroadcastTest.php`)

## [0.9.28]

### Security
- **Audit §3b (ninth audit): no keyId↔actor binding — any fediverse account holder with a valid key on any server could send a correctly-signed inbox request whose body claimed someone else's actor id, and `inbox()` would act on the claim.** `HttpSignature::verify()` proves the request was signed by the key at `keyId`, but nothing anywhere compared that identity to the `actor` field inside the activity JSON. Two concrete abuses: a **forged Follow** made `handle_follow()` fetch the victim's actor document and store the *victim's* inbox as a follower — every published artwork thereafter delivered to an inbox that never asked (spam vector, plus a plausible deliverability/reputation problem for the node); a **forged Undo** silently removed any real follower by claimed actor id (invisible denial of service on the social graph). New `HttpSignature::verify_actor_binding()` requires the keyId's base URL (fragment stripped) to exactly match the activity's actor id — accepting the AS2 embedded-object form (`actor.id`) as well as the plain string, falling back to the raw body when the Content-Type isn't a JSON media type, and rejecting with 401 (`ap_actor_mismatch`) on any mismatch or missing claim. Exact match was chosen over the audit's "same-origin at minimum" floor deliberately: every major implementation (Mastodon, Pleroma/Akkoma, GoToSocial, Pixelfed) mints keyId as `<actor>#main-key`, and same-origin-only would still allow same-server forgery between two accounts on one instance. `ActivityPub::verify_inbox_signature()` — the inbox route's permission callback — now chains the binding check after signature verification, so a forged activity is rejected before `inbox()` can mutate any state. New tests cover the binding matrix directly (match passes, forged string and forged embedded-object actor rejected as 401 `ap_actor_mismatch`, missing actor rejected, both the JSON-content-type and raw-body parse paths) and pin the wiring end-to-end through the permission callback with a request correctly signed by a fresh attacker key claiming a victim's actor. One new translatable string synced across `.pot` and all 18 `.po` files (placeholder msgstr; `.mo`/`.l10n.php` caches verified byte-identical on regeneration since untranslated entries aren't compiled, so they are deliberately untouched). (`includes/Network/HttpSignature.php`, `includes/Network/ActivityPub.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Network/HttpSignatureTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Network/ActivityPubTest.php`)
- **Audit §2d (ninth audit): `Node::register_peer()` accepted any unauthenticated request and wrote it straight into `agnosis_nodes`, with its own "TODO: verify the peer's signature before trusting" left unimplemented — an attacker could insert unlimited distinct-URL `pending` rows (table bloat, and a spam/decoy surface for any future pending-peer approval UI).** Closed with three independent controls. **Rate limit:** `RateLimiter::check( 'agnosis_node_register_peer', 5, 300 )` — 5 registrations per IP per 5 minutes — runs before any DB work. **Pending-row cap:** new `Node::enforce_pending_peer_cap()` keeps `agnosis_nodes` at or under 500 `status = 'pending'` rows, pruning the single oldest via `DELETE ... ORDER BY created_at ASC LIMIT n` — same bounded, oldest-first shape as `agnosis_ap_tombstones` (§3e); only counted against when the URL being registered is genuinely new, so a known peer re-announcing itself never triggers pruning. **The TODO itself:** new `HttpSignature::verify_with_key()` generalizes the existing HTTP-Signature verification machinery to check against a caller-supplied public key instead of one fetched from a remote actor document (the shared parsing/freshness/digest steps were extracted into `verify_preamble()`, the signature-decode/verify step into `verify_signature()` — `HttpSignature::verify()`'s own keyId-fetch behavior is unchanged). `register_peer()` now requires the request to be signed by the private key matching the `publicKey` it presents in the body — proof of possession of that exact key, closing the concrete abuse of registering an identity with a key the requester doesn't actually control. A missing `publicKey` is now also a 400. New `HttpSignatureTest.php` cases cover `verify_with_key()` in isolation (valid self-signed request, wrong-key rejection, missing signature, digest mismatch, zero outbound HTTP calls); new `NodeTest.php` covers the full `register_peer()` wiring, including the rate limit tripping on a sixth request and the pending-cap test seeding 500 rows via one bulk insert to confirm exactly the single oldest row is pruned on a 501st registration while re-registering a known URL prunes nothing. (`includes/Network/Node.php`, `includes/Network/HttpSignature.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Network/NodeTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Network/HttpSignatureTest.php`)

### Added
- **Audit §3e (ninth audit): deletions and edits never federated — the community removal machinery and the GDPR erasure layer both stopped at the site boundary while every follower's server kept the federated copy indefinitely, and `ContentEditor` corrections never reached followers at all.** `Plugin.php` wired exactly one federation trigger (`agnosis_post_published → broadcast()`); nothing fired on unpublish, trash, delete, or edit. Now the full artwork lifecycle federates. **Delete + Tombstone:** any transition out of `publish` (trash — which is where `RemovalEndpoints`' removal-vote flow lands — or unpublish) delivers `Delete { object: Tombstone { id, formerType: Note, deleted } }` to every follower via a new `transition_post_status` handler; `wp_delete_post()` force-deletes (Departure's path for a leaving or banned artist's works) never fire a status transition, so a `before_delete_post` handler covers them, with a status guard ensuring emptying the trash doesn't send a duplicate for an already-tombstoned object. Every tombstoned slug is recorded in a new bounded `agnosis_ap_tombstones` option (autoload=false, capped at 500 with oldest-first pruning — §3g's `agnosis_ap_followers` scale lesson applied from day one), and the §3c content-negotiation hook now serves **HTTP 410 + Tombstone JSON** at the object id thereafter, so any server that ever saw the object — not just followers — learns it's gone on re-fetch; browsers keep the theme's ordinary 404, and a restored/republished artwork clears its tombstone and dereferences again.
