The object id is resolved through a publish-status clone with the clean slug, so the Tombstone carries the exact id the Note federated under even though the post is already trashed (and possibly `__trashed`-suffixed) when the hook fires. **Update:** a meaningful edit of a published artwork — title/content/excerpt via `post_updated` (both sides must be `publish`, which also keeps `wp_trash_post()`'s internal update from double-firing next to the Delete), or a replaced photo via the `_thumbnail_id` meta hooks (`set_post_thumbnail()` fires neither `post_updated` nor any transition) — delivers `Update` with the refreshed Note, deduplicated per post per request since one editorial save can touch both the post row and the thumbnail. **Scope guard:** Lingua Forge language siblings never federate — `Create` only ever fired for the primary post, so Delete/Update/Tombstone mirror that scope via the same primary-language rule `PostCreator::primary_language_meta_query()` uses. All existing delivery machinery (§3a's signed, Digest-carrying, logged `deliver()`) is the transport; `broadcast()` now shares a `deliver_to_followers()` helper with the new paths. Eleven new integration tests drive the real lifecycle end-to-end through the Plugin.php wiring — wp_trash_post federates exactly one Delete with the pre-deletion object id, force delete federates, emptying trash doesn't duplicate, the Tombstone serves for AP consumers but not browsers, republish clears it, title edits federate the refreshed Note, non-content updates and draft edits don't federate, thumbnail changes do, and the sibling case stays silent including its tombstone. (`includes/Network/ActivityPub.php`, `includes/Core/Plugin.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Network/ActivityPubTest.php`)

### Added
- **Audit §3f (ninth audit): the ActivityPub Note undersold the artwork on four small, independent counts, plus one product decision the audit filed as "a call, not a defect."** Federated posts carried no alt text at all (the AI's own factual alt text was simply never sent — a described-nowhere image to fediverse screen-reader users), a hardcoded `image/jpeg` `mediaType` regardless of the real file type, no hashtags at all despite every artwork already carrying `post_tag`/`agnosis_medium` terms (Mastodon's primary discovery mechanism), and `content` flattened to a 50-word plain-text truncation of what is genuinely HTML-capable AP content — artists' AI-written descriptions arrived amputated mid-sentence. All four fixed directly: the featured image's `_wp_attachment_image_alt` becomes `name`; its real `get_post_mime_type()` becomes `mediaType`; a new `build_hashtags()` turns `post_tag` + `agnosis_medium` terms into an AS2 `tag` array of CamelCase hashtags (`#OilPainting`, not `#oilpainting` — the community-recommended, screen-reader-friendly form) with matching `#Name` strings appended to `content`, since Mastodon indexes hashtags from the content text itself rather than the `tag` array; and a new `build_note_content()` walks `parse_blocks()` to keep only the freeform HTML segments — the AI-written paragraphs `Publishing\PostCreator` inserts as raw HTML rather than a Gutenberg block — deliberately excluding the real gallery/image/video/audio/embed blocks around them (the image already travels separately via `attachment`), falling back to the old truncated summary only if no freeform text is found at all. **The `sensitive` decision:** rather than guess at content-moderation policy, asked directly — the answer was both of the audit's suggested levers, not just the minimum. An operator can now flag a whole `agnosis_medium` term as sensitive-by-default (new checkbox on its classic Edit Tags screen), and an artist can flag their own specific piece via a new `POST /agnosis/v1/content/{id}/sensitive` endpoint — boolean and language-neutral, so it propagates synchronously to every language sibling with no translation leg, the same shape the existing photo-replace endpoint already uses. Either lever is enough to set `sensitive: true` and a content-warning `summary` on the Note. Four new translatable strings synced across `.pot` and all 18 `.po` files. (`includes/Network/ActivityPub.php`, `includes/Artist/ContentEditor.php`, `includes/Artist/Profile.php`, `includes/Core/Plugin.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Network/ActivityPubTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Artist/ContentEditorTest.php`)

### Added
- **Audit §3g (ninth audit, hardening batch): four independent robustness gaps in the fediverse layer, none exploitable in a demonstrated way but each a real gap — asked directly on the two the audit itself filed as decisions rather than defects, and got the full build on both, not the minimum.** (i) `HttpSignature::verify()` didn't require `date` (or its `(created)` equivalent) or, on a POST, `digest` to actually appear in a signature's `headers` list — a signature legitimately covering only `(request-target) host` verified fine, silently defeating the freshness check (which only ran when a Date header happened to arrive) and the digest check (which only ran when `digest` happened to be listed). `verify_preamble()` now rejects either omission outright (401), mirroring Mastodon's own strictness for symmetry with what we send per §3a. (ii) `fetch_public_key()` cached success only, so a flood of requests bearing random or nonexistent keyIds forced one real outbound fetch per request (an amplification vector against this server's own outbound budget); it now also caches failures, in a separate transient, for 5 minutes. (iii) followers lived in one autoloaded `agnosis_ap_followers` option, rewritten wholesale on every Follow/Undo (a last-write-wins race under concurrency) and loaded into memory on every single page load regardless of whether the request touched federation — asked whether to fix this with the cheap `autoload => false` flip or build a dedicated table, the answer was the table: a new `agnosis_followers` table (`actor_id` UNIQUE, `inbox_url`) replaces it, upserted via `$wpdb->replace()` and row-deleted on Undo, with a one-time `Activator::migrate_followers_option()` carrying any existing option data across on upgrade. (iv) delivery was still fire-and-forget past §3a's logging fix — a failed delivery had exactly one trace of it ever happening (a Settings → Logs line) and was otherwise gone for good; asked whether to defer the "1.0-grade" cron retry queue the audit itself proposed, the answer was to build it now: a new `agnosis_ap_delivery_queue` table plus `ActivityPub::process_delivery_retry_queue()` (cron `agnosis_ap_retry_deliveries`, the same 5-minute tick as the email poll) retries a failed delivery on a backoff schedule spanning roughly 4 days before marking it permanently failed; `deliver()` was refactored so a live failure enqueues the exact signed payload rather than losing it. (`includes/Network/HttpSignature.php`, `includes/Network/ActivityPub.php`, `includes/Core/Activator.php`, `includes/Core/Plugin.php`, `uninstall.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Network/HttpSignatureTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Network/ActivityPubTest.php`)

### Added
- **Audit §3h (ninth audit): the last standards-conformance checklist, plus a roadmap-tier decision built ahead of schedule.** The checklist half: WebFinger now serves `application/jrd+json` (was riding `wp_send_json()`'s hardcoded `application/json`, which some strict fediverse implementations reject outright for the RFC 7033 endpoint) via a new `send_jrd_json()` helper, since `wp_send_json()` always overwrites any Content-Type a caller sets first; a new `/.well-known/nodeinfo` discovery document plus `GET /agnosis/v1/activitypub/nodeinfo` NodeInfo 2.0 document (software name/version, `activitypub` protocol, artist-role user count, artwork-post local count, open registration false) so instance-listing and health-check tools that walk NodeInfo before anything else stop treating the node as unidentifiable; and a `sharedInbox` entry on the node actor's `endpoints`, so followers deliver once per remote server rather than once per local actor once per-artist actors (below) exist. **The roadmap decision:** the audit filed the actor `type` (Service/Organization/Group) as a cosmetic confirm-and-move-on item — asked directly, the answer instead was to build the roadmap's own long-deferred per-artist actors feature now, in this session, rather than defer it to 1.0.0+. Every WordPress user with the `agnosis_artist` role is now a first-class ActivityPub actor (`type: Person`) in its own right: its own lazily-generated RSA keypair (usermeta, generated on first use), its own inbox/outbox/followers endpoints and WebFinger handle (`@{nicename}@{node-host}` — resolved on the node's own domain, not a per-artist subdomain, so discovery stays one hop), and its own signing identity for outbound deliveries, alongside the existing node-level actor (`type: Service`, unchanged) for node-wide announcements. Follower storage was re-keyed from a bare-`actor_id` uniqueness to `(owner_type, owner_id, actor_id)`, via an explicit idempotent index-swap migration (`dbDelta()` cannot itself swap a unique key), so the same remote follower can follow both the node and any number of individual artists without collision. A Follow/Undo's local target is resolved from the activity's own `object` field rather than the delivery URL, since `sharedInbox` means one inbox URL now legitimately serves many local actors. Artist-attributed posts deliver to the union of that artist's own followers and the node's followers (deduplicated by inbox), so existing node-level followers don't lose visibility into any artist's new work; each delivery is signed with the key belonging to the actor it's actually attributed to, matching this node's own §3b keyId↔actor binding enforcement rather than always signing as the node. `owner_for_post()` falls back to the node actor for any author who isn't (or is no longer) an `agnosis_artist` role holder, so the whole feature is additive with no migration required for existing content. One new translatable string synced across `.pot` and all 18 `.po` files. New tests (`ActivityPubTest.php`) cover per-artist actor document shape and 404 on a non-artist id, per-artist outbox/followers scoping, WebFinger resolution for the node, an artist, a non-artist user, and a wrong-host request, Follow/Undo owner resolution (including the node fallback), attribution + union delivery + inbox dedup, per-artist delivery signing, and the NodeInfo document shape; new tests (`ActivatorTest.php`) cover the followers-table migration adding the owner columns and swapping the unique key, the same remote actor following both the node and an artist post-migration, and migration idempotency. (`includes/Network/ActivityPub.php`, `includes/Core/Activator.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Network/ActivityPubTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Core/ActivatorTest.php`)

### Fixed
- **Audit §3c (ninth audit): artwork object ids weren't dereferenceable as ActivityStreams JSON — and on plain-permalink sites they were broken URLs outright.** `post_to_activity()` minted the Note's `id` as a hardcoded `home_url( '/art/' . $post->post_name )`: with plain permalinks the real page lives at `?agnosis_artwork=<slug>`, so every federated object carried an `id` that 404'd; even with pretty permalinks, fetching `/art/<slug>` returned the theme's HTML page regardless of the `Accept` header, while the AP spec expects an object's id to dereference to the object — Mastodon re-fetches objects by id to verify or refresh them (processing a boost of our post seen from a third server, or a user pasting the artwork URL into search), and those flows failed or degraded. Two-part fix, per the audit's own prescription: (i) the Note's `id` is now minted from `get_permalink()` — extracted into a new `post_to_note()` that `post_to_activity()` wraps — so `id` === `url` by construction in every permalink mode; (ii) a new `template_redirect` handler (`serve_artwork_activity_json()`, wired in `Plugin.php` — deliberately not inside `register_routes()`, which runs on `rest_api_init` and never fires for frontend requests) content-negotiates on the artwork permalink itself: a GET whose `Accept` names `application/activity+json` or `application/ld+json` receives the Note JSON with the proper `application/activity+json` Content-Type, everything else falls through to the theme untouched. The guard-and-build logic lives in a separate testable `singular_activity_json()` (null unless: artwork singular, ActivityPub enabled — the same operator lever that gates `broadcast()` — published, and an AS2 media type in `Accept`), with the emit-and-exit wrapper kept to four lines. This is also the hook §3e's Tombstone (HTTP 410) will extend, as the audit anticipated. New tests: `id` === `get_permalink()` and `id` === `url` under both plain and pretty permalinks (with preconditions pinning that each mode is actually in effect), Note served for Mastodon's real dereference `Accept` header and for bare `ld+json`, and declined for browser `Accept`, non-artwork singulars, and the disabled-lever case. (`includes/Network/ActivityPub.php`, `includes/Core/Plugin.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Network/ActivityPubTest.php`)
- **Audit §3a (ninth audit's headline finding): outbound ActivityPub deliveries could never pass Mastodon's signature requirements — `ActivityPub::deliver()` signed only `(request-target) host date` and never computed or sent a `Digest` header at all, while Mastodon (and Pixelfed, and most major implementations) rejects any inbox POST whose signature doesn't cover a Digest of the body.** The consequence chain was total and invisible: a Mastodon user's Follow arrived and verified fine (inbound verification was always solid), we stored the follower and sent `Accept` — which Mastodon rejected with a 401, leaving the follow "pending" on their side forever — and every subsequent `broadcast()` `Create` to that follower's inbox bounced the same way. Because delivery was fire-and-forget (`'blocking' => false`), nothing ever surfaced as an error anywhere: the feature demoed correctly from our side and failed completely on theirs. `deliver()` now computes `SHA-256=<base64>` of the exact request body, sends it as the `Digest` header on every delivery (signed or not), and extends both the signing string and the Signature header's `headers` list to `(request-target) host date digest`. Delivery is also no longer fire-and-forget — the request now blocks and any transport error or non-2xx response is logged (warning level, `activitypub` context) to Settings → Logs, naming the activity type, target inbox, status code, and response body, so the exact failure shape that hid this bug for years can't recur; the audit's §3g cron-driven retry queue remains a deliberate 1.0-scope follow-up. New integration tests pin the outbound signing composition precisely as the audit's test-coverage note requested: the Digest value matches the SHA-256 of the body actually sent, the signed-header list is exactly `(request-target) host date digest` (asserted as a literal), the emitted signature cryptographically verifies over a signing string reconstructed from the headers actually sent (a receiving server's view — this is the assertion that would have caught §3a), delivery is blocking, a 401 writes exactly one log entry naming the inbox, and a 2xx writes none. With this shipped, readme.txt's Mastodon FAQ answer ("follow `@agnosis@yoursite.com` and see new artworks in their feed") describes reality again (audit G-1's condition — ship §3a in the same release that next touches readme.txt — is met). (`includes/Network/ActivityPub.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Network/ActivityPubTest.php`)
- **Audit §2b (ninth audit): `agnosis_contact_messages` — the 15th table, added after `uninstall.php`'s drop list was written — survived plugin deletion, taking the header docblock's stale "14 custom tables" count down with it.** The table holds visitor names, email addresses, message bodies, and (inside the 30-day retention window) IP addresses — exactly the class of personal data `uninstall.php`'s own header promises to remove ("everything Agnosis creates that the operator would not expect to linger"). An operator deleting the plugin reasonably believed the GDPR story ended there; instead the highest-PII table was the one left behind. Added `'agnosis_contact_messages'` to the `$tables` drop list and corrected the docblock's count and enumerated list from fourteen tables to fifteen. (`uninstall.php`)
- **Audit §3d (ninth audit): the ActivityPub outbox root always returned `type: OrderedCollectionPage` with inline items — even when a spec-conformant consumer GETs the root expecting an `OrderedCollection` naming `first`, then walks `next` links from there.** Mastodon's profile-backfill and fedi crawler/archive-tool consumers do exactly that; against this outbox they instead saw a page of a collection that was never itself served, with page 2+ reachable only by guessing the `page` query param. A request with no `page` param now returns `{ type: 'OrderedCollection', totalItems, first: <outbox>?page=1 }` with no inline items; a request with `?page=N` keeps the existing page shape and adds `next` (while more items remain beyond this page) and `prev` (beyond page 1 — page 1 has none, since the root's own `first` is the entry point). (`includes/Network/ActivityPub.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Network/ActivityPubTest.php`)
- **Audit §2c (ninth audit): `uninstall.php` deleted only one (`_agnosis_newsletter_optout`) of the six `_agnosis_*` usermeta keys the plugin writes, leaving `_agnosis_bounce_count`, `_agnosis_bounce_last_at`, `_agnosis_broadcast_optout`, `_agnosis_contact_optout`, and `_agnosis_vote_email_mode` behind on plugin deletion.** None is sensitive on its own — a completeness/contract issue against the same file header's "everything Agnosis creates" promise. Step 6 now runs a single prefix-wide `DELETE FROM {$wpdb->usermeta} WHERE meta_key LIKE '\_agnosis\_%'` in place of the single-key delete, matching the pattern the options cleanup (step 2) already uses, so a future seventh key can't repeat this same gap. User accounts themselves remain untouched — only the plugin's own meta on those accounts goes. (`uninstall.php`)

### Changed
- **Audit G-1 (ninth audit, docs drift): three one-liners the eighth audit's own docs pass missed, plus a Mastodon FAQ line whose accuracy depended on §3a.** `README.md` line 24 still listed the medium taxonomy term as "Watercolour" against the actually-seeded American-spelling "Watercolor" — a doc-only drift, since the term itself was never wrong. `readme.txt` line 49's Settings tab list said "Behaviour" where `Settings.php:298` has always registered the tab as "Behavior". `README.md` line 35's Commerce bullet read as a shipped, present-tense feature ("configurable transaction fee on donations and art sales") when Commerce is still an unbuilt, planned layer (see the standing C-1 carry) — reworded to "Commerce (planned)" with wording matching readme.txt's own honest framing of the same gap. The fourth sub-item, the Mastodon FAQ's "follow and see new artworks in their feed" line, needed no separate fix: the audit's own stated condition — ship §3a in the same release that next touches readme.txt — was already met earlier in 0.9.28, so the FAQ was left as written, now true. Docs-only change; no PHP touched. (`README.md`, `readme.txt`)

## [0.9.27]

### Added
- **Audit §3c: reply-above-quote/forward extraction, resolving the product tension between the 0.9.22 "just hit reply to submit again" Reply-To feature and the 0.9.25 blanket reply/forward rejection.** Previously, any message `IntakeGates::is_reply_or_quote()` matched was rejected outright, full stop — including a message that genuinely carried the artist's own new comment or a fresh attachment above the quoted/forwarded portion, exactly the case the Reply-To feature invites. Chose option (c) from the audit's three alternatives (document the friction / drop Reply-To / extract-and-process): new `IntakeGates::extract_original_content()` strips every leading "Re:"/"Fwd:"/"Fw:" subject prefix (looped, so a doubly-stacked "Re: Fwd: My piece" fully unwraps) and "[Agnosis]" anywhere in what's left, and keeps only whatever body text comes before the EARLIEST quote/forward marker (a reply's "On … wrote:" line, either separator, or either forward marker — see the §3b fix just above). `Email\Parser::parse_imap_message()`/`parse_webhook_payload()` now run a detected reply/forward through extraction instead of rejecting immediately, and only fall through to the existing distinct `'looks_like_reply'` rejection (same email as before, its copy now explicitly saying extraction was tried and found nothing) when NOTHING survives — no original text, no attachment. A message extraction rescues is queued and processed exactly like any other genuine submission, tagged with a new `extracted_from_reply` flag Parser threads through the submission array. `PostCreator::create_post()` persists this as `_agnosis_extracted_from_reply` post meta (always written, so a later non-extracted resubmission correctly clears a stale flag), and `Notification::build_email()` shows a light, non-alarming note on the review email — "this looked like a reply or forward, we used what we found; a fresh email works best next time" — informational only, since the submission was fully processed either way. New/updated coverage: `IntakeGatesTest` (extraction algorithm, 13 cases including the earliest-of-multiple-markers case), `ParserTest` (end-to-end wiring for both transports, replacing the now-obsolete "always rejects" assertions), `WebhookReplyRejectionTest` (full pipeline — extraction rescues a message all the way to a queued row with the right extracted subject/description; genuinely-empty extraction still rejects and still fires the notification action), and `NotificationEmailTest` (the review-email note appears only when the meta is set). (`includes/Email/IntakeGates.php`, `includes/Email/Parser.php`, `includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`, `includes/Publishing/Notification.php`)

### Fixed
- **Audit §5c: the cheap/fast text-only model `OpenAI::chat()`/`Anthropic::chat()` use for translation and contact-message moderation was inlined as a literal (`gpt-4o-mini`, `claude-haiku-4-5-20251001`) at four call sites, with no operator lever at all — unlike the vision models (`agnosis_openai_description_model`, `agnosis_anthropic_model`), which have been configurable since they were introduced.** When a pinned model is eventually deprecated upstream, translation and moderation would break with no setting to change, only a plugin update. Added two new options, `agnosis_openai_text_model`/`agnosis_anthropic_text_model` (Settings → AI Providers), defaulting to the current values, and both providers now accept a `$text_model` constructor parameter that `chat()` sends instead of the old literal. Threaded the new options through both places these providers are constructed for chat()-driven work — `Pipeline::resolve_description_provider()` (used by `Pipeline::chat()`/`classify_text()`, i.e. contact-form moderation) and `SubmissionTranslator::from_settings()` (submission translation) — and through the Settings → AI Providers "Test connection" ping handlers, which previously pinged a hardcoded model that could silently diverge from whatever was actually configured for real use. This also becomes a spend lever: an operator can point translation/moderation at a cheaper model the day one exists, independent of the vision model used for artwork description. New tests cover the model default and override on both providers' `chat()` requests, the ping handlers sending the configured model, and `SubmissionTranslator::from_settings()` actually threading the option into the constructed provider (via Reflection, since it wraps the provider privately). Four new translatable strings synced across `.pot`, all 18 `.po` files, and every `.l10n.php` cache. (`includes/AI/Providers/OpenAI.php`, `includes/AI/Providers/Anthropic.php`, `includes/AI/Pipeline.php`, `includes/AI/SubmissionTranslator.php`, `includes/Admin/Settings.php`, `tests/php/Integration/AI/OpenAIChatTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/AI/AnthropicChatTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Admin/AiProviderPingTest.php`, `tests/php/Unit/AI/SubmissionTranslatorTest.php`)
- **Audit §2e: `Publishing\Notification`'s automated emails — most notably its "we couldn't process that" rejection notices — carried no RFC 3834 anti-loop headers, unlike `Artist\CommunityBroadcast`'s bulk sends, which already did.** The gap mattered most for `on_submission_looks_like_reply()`: it's an automatic response to an incoming email, sent to whatever address the artist mailed from — exactly the shape of message most likely to land in front of a vacation autoresponder, whose own reply would then itself look like a fresh reply/forward and get rejected again, generating another notice. Every one of this class's roughly eight `wp_mail()` call sites also duplicated the same two-line header array by hand, with no shared path between them. Added a new private `Notification::html_headers()` — the "shared send path" the finding's fix column asks for — carrying `Content-Type`, `From`, `Auto-Submitted: auto-generated`, and `X-Auto-Response-Suppress: All`, and switched every call site (`on_removal_requested()`, `on_removal_requested_multiple()`, `on_removal_target_not_found()`, `on_promotion_result()`, `on_post_drafted()`, `on_submission_rejected()`, `on_submission_no_attachment()`, `on_submission_looks_like_reply()`) to use it, `array_merge()`-ing in the per-post `Reply-To` where `on_post_drafted()` already needed one. Deliberately did not add `Precedence: bulk` (which `CommunityBroadcast` does send) — these are one-to-one emails to a single artist, not a bulk community send, so that header wouldn't be accurate. Also deliberately did not touch `Core\CommunityMailer`'s own shared `html_headers()`/`text_headers()`, used by several other classes (`AdmissionNotification`, `DepartureNotification`, `CommunityCapNotification`, `Invitation`) for one-off action mail where a human reply is the expected, wanted outcome — the same scoping decision the fourth audit's `CommunityBroadcast` fix already made, for the same reason. New tests confirm the shared helper's header list directly, that `Precedence: bulk` is absent, and that two representative send paths (`on_submission_rejected()`, plus `on_post_drafted()` specifically to prove its `array_merge()` with `Reply-To` didn't drop anything) actually carry the new headers end to end. (`includes/Publishing/Notification.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Publishing/NotificationEmailTest.php`)
- **Audit §2b: the admin "Open Vote" button on Settings → Community → Members always silently failed.** `Settings::handle_initiate_removal_vote()` resolved the target artist's WP user id with `SELECT user_id FROM wp_agnosis_applications WHERE id = %d`, but that table has never had a `user_id` column — the real column is `wp_user_id` (see `Core\Activator`'s `CREATE TABLE`). `$wpdb->get_var()` against a nonexistent column returns `null` (a recorded DB error, not a PHP exception), so the resolved user id was always `0` and the handler always took its "not found" branch — every click of "Open Vote" redirected with `vote_open_failed` and never actually opened a community removal vote, regardless of how valid the target application was. Fixed by querying `wp_user_id`, the column that has always existed. New `SettingsInitiateRemovalVoteTest` covers the handler end-to-end (auth/nonce gates, and — the actual regression — that a valid admitted application now resolves its subject and creates a real `open` removal request rather than always failing). (`includes/Admin/Settings.php`)
- **Audit §2c: `Admission::apply()`'s reapplication gates never checked for `status = 'banned'` at all.** A banned application row fell all the way through to the generic "every other case" branch, which silently re-parked the row as `unverified` with a fresh confirm token — overwriting the ban record outright and undermining the "banned artists keep their email specifically so the ban stays enforceable" retention policy documented alongside `Core\Privacy`'s DSAR eraser. In practice the earlier `get_user_by( 'email', $email )` check already blocks reapplication in the common case (`Departure::admin_ban()` only removes the `agnosis_artist` role, it doesn't delete the WP account), but that account can be deleted independently of Agnosis's own `Departure::admin_delete()` flow (e.g. a site admin using wp-admin's own Users screen), leaving a `banned` application row with no WP account behind it and nothing else to stop this path. Added an explicit `banned` block branch: the response is deliberately enumeration-neutral (identical `pending_confirmation` shape to a brand-new application, nothing actually created or modified, no email sent — a caller cannot distinguish "this address is banned" from "your application is being processed" by probing the endpoint). Also honors `banned_until` (the optional half of the fix): a lapsed temporary ban is now treated like any other resolved withdrawn/rejected/left row — falls through to the normal reapply path, subject to the same existing weekly per-email `RateLimiter::check_sender()` guard — rather than blocking forever or making the artist wait for `check_expired_bans()`'s next daily cron tick. A still-future or permanent (`banned_until IS NULL`) ban stays fully blocked. New `AdmissionBannedReapplicationTest` covers all four shapes: permanent ban blocked + enumeration-neutral response, future-dated ban blocked, lapsed ban allowed through (and clears the stale ban metadata), and the weekly reapply throttle applying to a second lapsed-ban reapplication. (`includes/Artist/Admission.php`)
- **Audit §3b: the 0.9.25 email-intake policy was always framed as rejecting "a reply or a forward," but nothing actually matched a forward as such — only Outlook forwards were caught, incidentally, because Outlook reuses its reply separator for forwards too.** A Gmail forward with no comment of the forwarder's own above the separator (no "Re:"/"Fwd:" subject, no "On … wrote:" attribution line) sailed straight through and could publish quoted third-party content — exactly what the policy exists to stop. `IntakeGates::is_reply_or_quote()` gained two new signals: the subject-prefix check now also matches "Fwd:"/"Fw:" (`/^\s*(re|fwd?|fw)\s*:/i`, was `/^\s*re\s*:/i`), and the body check now also matches Gmail's own forward separator ("---------- Forwarded message ---------", hyphen count tolerant) and Apple Mail/iOS Mail's "Begin forwarded message:" marker. The already-accepted false-positive policy (an artist genuinely titling a piece "Re: Something") now extends the same way to "Fwd: Something" — still recoverable via the existing rejection email. New tests in `IntakeGatesTest` cover both new subject prefixes and both new body patterns, plus a check that the bare word "forward" in ordinary prose doesn't false-positive. (`includes/Email/IntakeGates.php`)
- **Audit §5b: `OpenAI::chat()` and `Anthropic::chat()` both hardcoded `max_tokens => 1024` — enough for a short reply, but not for `SubmissionTranslator::translate_fields()`'s JSON-envelope batch translation of a long biography body.** Once translated content approached roughly 700 words, the response hit the cap mid-JSON, `json_decode()` failed, and the caller silently fell back to publishing the untranslated original — a real quality regression on a call that was still billed in full, since output tokens are charged as used, not as reserved. Worse, none of `SubmissionTranslator`'s three JSON-envelope call sites (`translate_fields()`, `translate_to_languages()`, `call_translate()`) logged anything at all when `json_decode()` failed, so this was invisible in Settings → Logs — it just looked like an ordinary unexplained translation gap. Both providers now size `max_tokens` from the prompt itself (`max(1024, min(8192, ceil(strlen($prompt) / 4 * 1.5)))` — floored at the old flat value, capped generously against a runaway prompt) instead of a flat cap. All three `SubmissionTranslator` decode-failure points now log a warning that distinguishes "looks truncated" (the response starts like the requested JSON object but never reaches its closing brace) from "malformed or unexpected shape" (the model didn't return JSON at all) — deliberately based on the response's own shape rather than the provider's `finish_reason`/`stop_reason`, since threading that through would have meant widening `ProviderInterface::chat()`'s return type everywhere it's called, including `Pipeline.php`'s six call sites and every test double, for a fix this scoped doesn't call for. New `OpenAIChatTest`/`AnthropicChatTest` cover the sizing floor, the raised ceiling for a long prompt, and the 8192 cap; new `SubmissionTranslatorTest` cases cover the truncated-response path through all three affected methods. (`includes/AI/Providers/OpenAI.php`, `includes/AI/Providers/Anthropic.php`, `includes/AI/SubmissionTranslator.php`)

### Docs
- **Audit §4e (interim): README's "Zero runtime dependencies — no Composer packages ship in the plugin zip" claim was false.** `composer.json` requires `webklex/php-imap`, and `dev/bin/build-zip.sh`/`.distignore` never excluded `vendor/`, so the distributable ZIP has always shipped webklex's full un-prefixed dependency tree (`illuminate/*`, `symfony/*`, `nesbot/carbon`, `doctrine/inflector`, `voku/portable-ascii`). The README bullet now names the actual shipped packages, confirms all are MIT-licensed (GPL-compatible, no legal issue), and states plainly that the tree is currently un-prefixed. The architectural decision the finding also raises — prefixing the tree via Strauss/PHP-Scoper, or replacing webklex with a slimmer IMAP layer — is a deliberate 1.0.0 call, not made in this release; this is docs-accuracy only. (`README.md`)
- **Audit §3d: the in-site Artist Guide (`Activator::help_page_content()`) predated the entire 0.9.25 email-intake policy — nothing in it warned artists that a reply/forward could be rejected, that Cc/Bcc are never read, or that only the first To: address routes a message.** An artist following the guide to the letter could still hit any of those three rejection lanes with no warning it existed. Added a new "How to email us" section right after the intro paragraph, covering all three rules in plain language — including that a reply/forward is rescued (not rejected) when the artist's own new text sits above the quoted part, per the §3c extraction fix just above, so the guide reflects current behavior rather than the older blanket-reject policy. While in there, also fixed a British-spelling leftover the 0.9.22 source-string sweep missed because seeded page content isn't in the i18n catalogs: "Colours, textures, composition" → "Colors, textures, composition," in both `about_page_content()` and `help_page_content()` (the audit's own finding text named only the About page instance at `Activator.php:848`; the identical phrase in the Artist Guide was found and fixed alongside it). Both pages are seeded once on first activation and never re-seeded on upgrade (`create_managed_page()` is idempotent), so this only affects fresh installs — an existing site's already-created pages are unaffected, same caveat as any other managed-page content change in this codebase. (`includes/Core/Activator.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Core/ActivatorTest.php`)
- **Audit §4b: the suggested Privacy Policy text named "Stability AI" as a possible processor — no such provider has ever existed in this codebase (`includes/AI/Providers/` has only `OpenAI.php`, `Anthropic.php`, and `WordPressAI.php`), and `agnosis_stability_api_key` was a dead option seeded on activation and read nowhere, already flagged as unreachable by the 0.9.20 audit.** README.md and readme.txt repeated the same false claim in their enhancement-step bullets. Conversely, `WordPressAI` — a real, working provider that delegates to WordPress core's own AI Client (WP 7.0+, credentials managed by the operator under Settings → Connectors, no key stored by Agnosis) — was entirely unmentioned in the privacy boilerplate. `Privacy::add_privacy_policy_content()` now names only the two real API-key providers (OpenAI, Anthropic) and adds a sentence covering the WordPress AI Client case, since whichever backend that connector routes to is also a processor. Dropped `agnosis_stability_api_key` from `Activator::seed_options()`'s defaults. README.md's provider-listing bullets (feature list and directory-structure line) now name WordPressAI instead of Stability; its and readme.txt's enhancement-specific bullets simply drop Stability, since WordPressAI's own `supports_enhancement()` returns `false` — it doesn't do image enhancement, so it isn't a substitute there. Translatable string change synced across `.pot`, all 18 `.po` `msgid`s/placeholder `msgstr`s (entry count re-verified unchanged at 1155/1154), and every `.l10n.php` cache regenerated via the bundled `wp-cli.phar i18n make-php`. (`includes/Core/Privacy.php`, `includes/Core/Activator.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Core/ActivatorTest.php`, `README.md`, `readme.txt`)

## [0.9.26]

### Fixed
- **The remove@ "we couldn't find that title" feedback email listed the artist's current titles once PER LANGUAGE SIBLING, not once per real work — on a multi-language site "Popcorn" could appear a dozen times in a row while genuinely distinct titles got crowded out of the list entirely (`gather_title_context()`'s `posts_per_page => 20` cap).** Artwork/event titles are never translated (the dual-title system keeps `post_title` byte-identical across the primary post, its native-language sibling, and every Lingua Forge machine-translated sibling — only the separately-stored display title differs), so every one of those siblings surfaced as its own "current title" row despite being the exact same work. `gather_title_context()` now applies the same `primary_language_meta_query()` scoping `find_post_by_subject()`/`find_posts_by_subject()` already used elsewhere in this file, collapsing back to one row per real work. (`includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`)
- **The remove@ "which one did you mean?" choice email could offer two options that were really the same underlying confusion — two rows of the SAME post type (e.g. two `agnosis_artwork` drafts) sharing an exact title, one of them not genuinely "real" content the artist would recognise — rather than only the legitimate case this email exists for: a title genuinely shared across an artwork AND an event.** `find_posts_by_subject()` now collapses to at most one match per post type (the first, per its own existing stable `orderby => 'type title'` ordering) before deciding whether to offer a choice at all — two same-type duplicates now silently resolve to the single-match path exactly as if the duplicate never existed, while a genuine artwork/event title collision still offers the choice as before. (`includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`)

## [0.9.25]

### Added
- **A remove@/promote@ management email that matches more than one post by subject (e.g. an artwork and an event sharing the same title) now gets a confirmation email listing every match, with its own individual "remove this one" link per item, instead of silently acting on (or failing on) just one of them.** `Publishing\PostCreator` gained `find_posts_by_subject()` (a plural counterpart to the existing single-match `find_post_by_subject()`), and `handle_removal_request()` now branches on how many posts match the request's subject: zero behaves as before (fires `agnosis_removal_target_not_found`), exactly one behaves as before (fires `agnosis_removal_requested`), and two or more mint an independent removal token per matched post and fire a new `agnosis_removal_requested_multiple` action instead. A new `Publishing\Notification::on_removal_requested_multiple()` + `build_removal_choice_email()` render one email with a card per match (post type label, title, its own confirm button) reusing the exact same per-post-id/token confirm URL scheme `Publishing\RemovalEndpoints::confirm()` already handles — that endpoint needed no changes at all, since it was already fully per-post/per-token. (`includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`, `includes/Publishing/Notification.php`, `includes/Core/Plugin.php`)
- **The IMAP inbox now rejects mail we were never actually addressed to.** A message whose To:/Cc: headers match none of this site's own configured addresses (every non-blank Settings → Email routing address — submit@/bio@/event@/replace@/remove@/promote@/photo@/pure@/goodbye@/community@ — plus the IMAP mailbox's own login address when it's a real email) never arrived via a genuine direct send to a known endpoint: it was BCC'd, or its true recipient was otherwise stripped before we ever saw it. Agnosis doesn't accept BCC submissions — such a message is now deleted from the mailbox outright by a new `Email\IntakeGates::is_recognized_recipient()` gate in `Inbox::process_messages()`, evaluated right after the existing bounce/DSN check: no queue row is created, it never touches the rest of the pipeline at all. Deliberately permissive when nothing is configured yet (an unconfigured or still-being-set-up site has nothing to validate against, so nothing is rejected in that state) and IMAP-only — the webhook transport has no equivalent ambiguity, since the provider's own routing rule already matched a configured address before our endpoint is invoked. (`includes/Email/IntakeGates.php`, `includes/Email/Inbox.php`)
- **Agnosis no longer accepts Cc: at all, and only the first/primary To: address counts for routing or recognition — a message reaching a management alias (or any other endpoint) only via Cc:, or via a secondary To: address, previously matched anyway; it no longer does.** This reverses the broader "match every To:/Cc: address" behavior from a prior release. `Email\IntakeGates::recipient_addresses()` (webhook) and `Inbox::message_recipient_addresses()` (IMAP) each now return at most one address — Mailgun's own already-disambiguated `recipient` field when present, otherwise only the first address in the raw `To:` header — and `Email\Parser`'s own recipient collection was simplified to match. Every downstream consumer (`in_array()`/`array_intersect()` checks in `Webhook::handle()`, `Inbox::process_messages()`, and `IntakeGates::is_recognized_recipient()`) needed no changes, since they already operated on an array that just never holds more than one address now. (`includes/Email/IntakeGates.php`, `includes/Email/Inbox.php`, `includes/Email/Parser.php`)
- **A message that looks like a reply or a forwarded email — carrying quoted content from an earlier message rather than original, curated material — is now detected and rejected on both transports, with the sender told why.** Agnosis's own outbound mail deliberately sets `Reply-To` back to the artist's intake address (so hitting "reply" starts a fresh submission) — but a mail client's default reply behavior quotes the whole original message and prefixes the subject with "Re:", neither of which should ever be published. A new `Email\IntakeGates::is_reply_or_quote()` matches any of: a subject starting with "Re:", a subject containing "[Agnosis]" (our own outbound notification prefix, distinct from the unrelated `[Biography]`/`[Event]`/`[Photo]`/`[Pure]` submission-routing indicators), a body containing an "On <date>, <name> <email> wrote:" quoted-reply attribution line, or an Outlook-style "-----Original Message-----" separator. `Email\Parser` gained a `last_rejection_reason()` signal so `Inbox::process_messages()` and `Webhook::handle()` can distinguish this from the older, generic "no attachments" null-return case; both now fire a new `agnosis_submission_looks_like_reply` action, handled by a new `Publishing\Notification::on_submission_looks_like_reply()` + email template (modeled directly on the existing "no photo found" rejection email) telling the sender to resend as a fresh, original message. Checked before attachment processing, deliberately — a reply carrying a genuine attachment is still rejected, since the policy is about original content, not whether a file happens to be attached. (`includes/Email/IntakeGates.php`, `includes/Email/Parser.php`, `includes/Email/Inbox.php`, `includes/Email/Webhook.php`, `includes/Publishing/Notification.php`, `includes/Core/Plugin.php`)

### Fixed
- **The "Inbox retention (days)" cleanup only ever deleted IMAP messages already flagged `\Seen` — a real, silent gap, since a whole class of mail this pipeline fully processes and records never gets its body fetched at all (the header-only "cheap gate" rejections — `auth_failed`/`unregistered_sender`/`not_admitted`/`throttled` — and the entire goodbye@ alias flow), and `\Seen` is only ever set as an incidental side effect of an actual body fetch, not something Agnosis manages deliberately.** Those messages were genuinely done with — each already has its own terminal `agnosis_queue` row — but sat in the physical mailbox indefinitely regardless of the configured retention window, exactly the overflow this setting exists to prevent. `Inbox::cleanup_imap()` now deletes by age alone (dropped the `->seen()` query constraint): every message this transport's own 5-minute poll scans (read or unread, no flag filter — see `query_messages()`) is either deleted outright (BCC/unrecognized-recipient) or fully captured into `agnosis_queue` well before it can reach the retention cutoff, so the physical IMAP copy serves no further purpose either way once that age is reached. (`includes/Email/Inbox.php`, `includes/Admin/Settings.php`)
- **A remove@ or promote@ request with no attachment and no body text — just a subject line naming the item to act on — was being silently dropped as "nothing usable," even though neither management command has ever needed an image, audio, or video attachment or any body text to work.** `Email\Parser::parse_imap_message()`'s final gate rejected any message with an empty `$attachments` array and an empty cleaned body, with no exemption for a message addressed to the configured remove@/promote@ management address — the same gate that correctly rejects a genuine artwork/biography/event submission missing its media. The gate now also passes a message through when its subject is non-empty and its recipient matches the configured `agnosis_email_remove` or `agnosis_email_promote` address, regardless of attachments or body. (`includes/Email/Parser.php`)
- **Any skipped inbox message — not just a remove@/promote@ one, and on both transports — showed a misleading "Artwork" endpoint label in the Inbox admin table, with no way to tell what the message actually was.** `Email\Inbox::mark_no_artwork()` (the single choke point every one of its seventeen call sites across `process_messages()`, `handle_goodbye_email()`, `handle_community_email()`, and `handle_bounce_dsn()` funnels through) and `Email\Webhook::mark_alias_event()` (its own equivalent choke point for goodbye@/community@ hits arriving via webhook) both only ever stashed the sender's address in the queue row's `raw_email` JSON, never the subject or recipient list, so `Publishing\PostCreator::resolve_endpoint_label()` (which reads that same JSON to power the Endpoint column) had nothing to recognise any skipped message by and silently guessed "Artwork" for every one of them, regardless of what the message actually was — an auth failure, an unregistered sender, a throttled sender, a missing attachment, a goodbye@/community@ alias hit, or an unresolved bounce DSN. On the webhook side specifically, the recipient list and subject were already computed locally in `Webhook::handle()` for the alias-routing checks themselves — they simply were never passed through to `mark_alias_event()`. Both methods now accept and persist an optional subject and recipient list, threaded through every call site that has them cheaply on hand (Inbox.php gained a new `message_subject()` helper alongside the existing `message_recipient_addresses()`, both defensive about the handful of lightweight test doubles that don't implement `getSubject()`/`getTo()`). `resolve_endpoint_label()` itself no longer guesses "Artwork" when a row carries no subject/recipient context at all — it now says "Unknown" plainly — and additionally recognises the goodbye@/community@ addresses as their own "Goodbye"/"Community" labels rather than falling through to the same default. "Artwork" is now only ever returned when a row's actual captured subject/recipient context genuinely resolves there, the same way `resolve_post_type()` itself would. Note: a row already skipped before this fix landed can't self-heal — the admin "Process"/"Force Reprocess" actions replay the already-stored (and already-stripped) `raw_email` rather than re-polling IMAP, so an artist affected by this needs to simply resend the message to get a fresh, correctly-labelled row. (`includes/Email/Inbox.php`, `includes/Email/Webhook.php`, `includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`, `includes/Admin/InboxPage.php`)
- **Follow-up to the fix directly above: a *rejected* goodbye@/community@ hit (non-artist sender, no active membership, throttled, auto-submitted) still showed the wrong Endpoint label — only the successful `goodbye_handled`/`community_handled` outcomes actually got it right.** `InboxPage::resolve_endpoint_label()` labels these rows "Goodbye"/"Community"/"Bounce" by matching `skip_reason`'s prefix, regardless of whether the outcome was a success or a rejection — but `mark_no_artwork()`/`mark_alias_event()` only ever stashed `skip_reason` for the handful of reasons recorded with a 'skipped' queue status (a genuine success), silently omitting it for every 'failed'-status member of the same alias family (`goodbye_non_artist`, `goodbye_no_membership`, `goodbye_throttled`, `community_non_artist`, `community_throttled`, `community_empty`, `community_auto_submitted`) — caught by a regression test expecting `skip_reason` on a throttled goodbye@ request. Both methods now also stash `skip_reason` whenever the reason itself is goodbye_/community_/bounce_-prefixed, regardless of status. (`includes/Email/Inbox.php`, `includes/Email/Webhook.php`)

## [0.9.24]

### Changed
- **An event's own title now uses the same dual-title system artwork titles have always had, instead of being machine-translated outright per language sibling.** Before this, `post_title` on an `agnosis_event` was translated per Lingua Forge sibling the same as any other content field — fine for ordinary text, but an event's title (an exhibition or show name — often effectively a proper noun in the artist's own language) could come back as an inconsistent or awkward literal translation. `Compat\LinguaForge::hold_artist_title()`/`build_title_translations()` (both previously gated `'agnosis_artwork' !== get_post_type(...)`) now gate on a shared `DUAL_TITLE_POST_TYPES = ['agnosis_artwork', 'agnosis_event']` constant instead: `post_title` stays byte-identical (the artist's own words) on every language version, and the AI-translated display title lives separately in `_agnosis_translated_title`/`_agnosis_title_i18n`, exactly as it already did for artwork. Biography is deliberately not included — its title has no "official own-language name" concept and keeps Lingua Forge's normal per-sibling translation. A new `agnosis/event-title` block (`Artist\Profile::render_event_title()`, mirroring `render_artwork_title()`) renders the original title as an `<h1>` with the translated version as a subtitle underneath when it differs, replacing the theme's plain `wp:post-title` on `single-agnosis_event.html`. `Artist\ContentEditor` gained a matching `'title' => 'post_title'` entry for `agnosis_event` in `EDITABLE_FIELDS` and `agnosis_event` joined `DUAL_TITLE_POST_TYPES`, so artists can now correct a published event's title from the front end the same way they already could for artwork — previously events had no title-editing affordance at all. (`includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`, `includes/Artist/Profile.php`, `includes/Artist/ContentEditor.php`, agnosis-theme `templates/single-agnosis_event.html`)

### Fixed
- **An artist's Events archive page could show every language's events mixed together instead of just the current language's.** `Artist\Profile::order_events_archive()` (sorts the archive by the event's own date meta rather than publish date) did `$q->set('meta_query', [...])` as a blind overwrite, silently discarding whatever `meta_query` Lingua Forge's own `QueryFilter::handle_pre_get_posts()` had already appended for the exact same `is_archive()` case — Agnosis's `pre_get_posts` registration runs after Lingua Forge's (a hard dependency, loaded first), so this callback always ran second and clobbered the language scoping outright on every request. It now merges the pre-existing `meta_query` as its own AND-ed group alongside the date-sort OR clause instead of replacing it, regardless of which callback happens to run first. (`includes/Artist/Profile.php`)
- **A featured image on an artwork, biography, or event page rendered uncropped (at its own natural aspect ratio) instead of the fixed crop every single-post template gives it — but only for the one viewer who could edit that post; everyone else always saw the correct crop.** Every CPT's single template sets a fixed `aspectRatio` on its `wp:post-featured-image` block (1:1 artwork, 3:4 biography, 16:9 event), which core enforces via `object-fit: cover` plus a `height: 100%` on the rendered `<img>` — a percentage height that only resolves against a parent with a *definite* height. `Artist\ContentEditor::decorate_thumbnail()` wraps that `<img>` in an `agnosis-editable--photo` `<div>` for an editable viewer only (a logged-out visitor gets the unwrapped core markup) — and that div had no explicit height, breaking the percentage chain the crop depends on, so the image fell back to its own natural aspect for exactly the artist/admin who'd be looking at it. `.agnosis-editable--photo` now sets `width: 100%; height: 100%` so it stays a transparent link in that chain. (`blocks/content-editor/frontend.css`)

## [0.9.23]

### Fixed
- **A biography's title could still show up as the literal word "Array" even after the 0.9.22 fix to `SubmissionTranslator::call_translate()`, because that fix only stopped a NEW bad translation from being produced — it did nothing for damage already done before it landed.** Two things survived the 0.9.22 release on any site that had already hit the bug: (1) a sibling post whose `post_title` had already been overwritten with the literal string "Array" (or "Array — Artist Name") by `BiographyTitle::translate_for_sibling()`, and (2) a corresponding "Array" entry already sitting in `BiographyTitle`'s own `PRESET_TITLE_TRANSLATIONS_OPTION` cache — which, being a cache *hit*, would keep serving that same bad value straight back out on every future sync without ever calling the now-fixed translator again. New `Artist\BiographyTitle::repair_array_titles()` purges any "Array" cache entries and re-translates + updates any `agnosis_biography` post still titled "Array" (via `linguaforge_get_lang()` to resolve each sibling's own language), run once from `Activator::maybe_upgrade()` on this upgrade. No-ops on a site with no preset title configured or nothing left to repair. (`includes/Artist/BiographyTitle.php`, `includes/Core/Activator.php`)

## [0.9.22]

### Added
- **The submission-review email ("Your submission is ready to review") now carries a `Reply-To` header pointing at the exact intake address the artist would use to submit more of the same kind of content — submit@/bio@/event@/photo@/pure@, per Settings → Email — instead of relying on whatever generic From identity the recipient's mail client would otherwise reply to.** New `Core\CommunityMailer::intake_address_for_post()`/`reply_to_header_for_post()` resolve the right address from the post type (`agnosis_biography` → the biography address, `agnosis_event` → the event address) or, for `agnosis_artwork`, from `_agnosis_intake_endpoint` (artwork/photo/pure — whichever lane the submission actually came in through); returns nothing (no header added) when that Settings field is left blank or holds an invalid address, so an unconfigured site behaves exactly as before. Wired into `Publishing\Notification::on_post_drafted()` — the moment an artist is actively engaged with submitting, and a natural point to want to send another one by just hitting reply. (`includes/Core/CommunityMailer.php`, `includes/Publishing/Notification.php`)
- **Two new default medium terms, Poetry and Essay, so the seeded `agnosis_medium` vocabulary covers written submissions, not just visual ones.** `PromptConfig::CANONICAL_MEDIUMS` grows from 8 to 10 entries; `Activator::seed_medium_terms()` inserts both the same idempotent way it does the existing eight, on any install that runs it again after this version. (`includes/AI/PromptConfig.php`)
- **A self-hosted updater — Agnosis isn't (yet) on WordPress.org, so until now a new release meant manually re-uploading the ZIP; wp-admin never showed an "Update available" badge or offered the one-click updater.** A new `Core\Updater`, modeled directly on the companion Lingua Forge plugin's own `Linguaforge_Updater`, hooks `pre_set_site_transient_update_plugins` to poll a small JSON manifest at `https://agnosis.art/wp-json/agnosis/v1/update` (cached 12h in a transient, purged on update-complete or "Check Again"), injects the standard `plugins_api` response for the "View version details" modal, and adds a "View details"/"Visit plugin site" row-meta link. As with Lingua Forge, package downloads are hardened: `upgrader_pre_download` pins the download host to an allowlist (`agnosis.art`, `github.com`, `objects.githubusercontent.com`, subdomains included) so a compromised or spoofed manifest can't redirect the update to an arbitrary server, and verifies the manifest's declared SHA-256 against the downloaded ZIP when present (skipped gracefully for a manifest that omits it). The manifest itself is a plain REST endpoint meant to be deployed as an mu-plugin on agnosis.art — template and deployment instructions in the new `docs/agnosis-update-manifest.php` (excluded from the distributable ZIP via `.distignore`, same as the rest of `docs/`). `dev/bin/build-zip.sh` now maintains the manifest's `$sha256` field itself, the same two-step lifecycle Lingua Forge's own build script uses: cleared to `''` at the start of every build (so a failed or superseded build never leaves a stale digest behind) and set to the freshly-built zip's real `sha256sum` once the build succeeds. (`includes/Core/Updater.php`, `includes/Core/Plugin.php`, `docs/agnosis-update-manifest.php`, `dev/bin/build-zip.sh`, `tests/php/Integration/Core/UpdaterTest.php`)

### Changed
- **The outbound sender identity for workflow/transactional mail (admission, vote, welcome, departure, invitation, submission-review) moved from Settings → Community → Rules to a new "Mail from:" field pair on Settings → Email, and its options were renamed `agnosis_community_from_name`/`agnosis_community_from_email` → `agnosis_mail_from_name`/`agnosis_mail_from_email`.** The old name lived on the "Community" tab and used the word "community" — easily confused with the separate, INBOUND `agnosis_email_community` ("Community announcement address") endpoint on Settings → Email, even though the two had never been related: one is who workflow mail appears to come *from*, the other is an address artists send *to*. `Core\CommunityMailer::sender_header()` now reads the renamed options; `Admin\Deliverability::identity_report()`'s row label changed from "Community (transactional)" to "Mail from (workflow)" for the same reason — including the translatable string itself, hand-synced into `languages/agnosis.pot` and all 18 locale `.po`/`.l10n.php` files (msgid changed, msgstr reset to the new English text for every locale as a placeholder since the old translation no longer applies to the new wording — re-translating that one label via Loco Translate is Ulises's own follow-up, same convention as every other translation-content task). A new `Core\Activator::migrate_mail_from_option()`, run from `maybe_upgrade()`, carries forward any value already configured under the old option names (including an intentionally-blank one) and then removes the old options, so an existing site's configured sender identity survives the upgrade untouched — no action needed on update. Caught by a live PHPUnit run: `DeliverabilityTest::test_identity_report_dedupes_identities_sharing_one_address()` still asserted the old "Community" label text — updated to assert "Mail from" instead. (`includes/Admin/Settings.php`, `includes/Core/CommunityMailer.php`, `includes/Core/Activator.php`, `includes/Admin/Deliverability.php`, `includes/Publishing/Notification.php`, `includes/Artist/AdmissionNotification.php`, `includes/Artist/CommunityBroadcast.php`, `languages/agnosis.pot`, `languages/agnosis-*.po`, `languages/agnosis-*.l10n.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Artist/CommunityBroadcastTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Admin/DeliverabilityTest.php`)
- **Lingua Forge is now a declared hard dependency, not an optional integration.** Given how much of the plugin now leans on it (the whole native-language pipeline, dual-title handling, translated-term sync, and more — thirteen files feature-detect its functions), `agnosis.php` adds a `Requires Plugins: lingua-forge` header (WordPress 6.5+'s Plugin Dependencies mechanism). WordPress core now refuses to install or activate Agnosis at all until Lingua Forge is installed and active — and, symmetrically, refuses to let an operator deactivate or delete Lingua Forge while Agnosis is still active. Since Lingua Forge isn't hosted on WordPress.org, WP's dependency UI can't offer a one-click "Install Now" for it — it still has to be installed manually — but the activation gate itself works independent of .org hosting. All of the existing `function_exists()`/`class_exists()` gating throughout the codebase stays as defense-in-depth regardless, per WordPress core's own guidance that Plugin Dependencies only enforces presence at install/activation time and isn't a substitute for runtime feature-detection. (`agnosis.php`, `includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`, `README.md`, `readme.txt`, `CONTRIBUTING.md`)

### Fixed
- **The plugin's own source strings mixed British and American spelling — not just the `en_US` translation layer — surfaced by `VouchConfirmTest` asserting the wrong one.** A first pass Americanized only `languages/agnosis-en_US.po`'s `msgstr` values ("favour"→"favor", "Behaviour"→"Behavior") while leaving the underlying PHP source (the actual `msgid`, and every other locale's `msgid`) still British. Fixed properly this time, at the source: `Behaviour`→`Behavior` (`Admin/Settings.php`, a Settings tab label, plus every code comment referencing that tab by name), `Analyses the artwork image…`→`Analyzes…` (`Admin/Settings.php`, an AI-provider description), `Vote in favour of this application?`/`You voted in favour…`→`favor` (`Artist/VouchConfirm.php`), `…a majority in favour.`→`favor` (`Artist/DepartureNotification.php`), `a strong colour cast… more accurate colours.`→`color`/`colors` (`Publishing/Notification.php`, a photo-quality email — already partly fixed in the prior pass), `Watercolour`→`Watercolor` (`AI/PromptConfig.php`'s medium list, plus five more British spellings in its AI prompt strings: colours, honour, Analyse, colour accuracy, flat colour, sRGB colour space), `analyse`→`analyze` (`AI/Providers/WordPressAI.php` failure messages), `summarise`→`summarize` (`Newsletter/Scheduler.php` log message), `flavour`→`flavor` (`AI/Pipeline.php` prompt string), and `randomised`→`randomized` (`blocks/gallery-overview/block.json`'s translatable `description` field). `languages/agnosis.pot` and all 18 locale `.po` files' `msgid` entries (verified via `polib`, entry counts unchanged at 1137) were hand-edited to match — no `wp i18n make-pot`/`msgmerge` regeneration, per instruction — and every locale's `.l10n.php` cache regenerated from the corrected `.po` source. `dev/bin/compile-pos.sh`'s `wp i18n make-php` invocation (previously passing an unsupported `--locale` flag that silently failed every single run) is also now fixed, so `composer compile-pos` produces correct output going forward; the `.mo` binaries (WP <6.5 fallback) still need regenerating via that command on a machine with `msgfmt` (unavailable in this sandbox). (`includes/Admin/Settings.php`, `includes/Artist/VouchConfirm.php`, `includes/Artist/DepartureNotification.php`, `includes/Publishing/Notification.php`, `includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`, `includes/Artist/ApplicationBiography.php`, `includes/Core/ImageSizes.php`, `includes/AI/PromptConfig.php`, `includes/AI/Providers/WordPressAI.php`, `includes/Newsletter/Scheduler.php`, `includes/AI/Pipeline.php`, `blocks/gallery-overview/block.json`, `languages/agnosis.pot`, `languages/agnosis-*.po`, `languages/agnosis-*.l10n.php`, `dev/bin/compile-pos.sh`, `tests/php/Integration/Artist/VouchConfirmTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Artist/ApplicationBiographyTest.php`, `tests/php/Unit/AI/PromptConfigTest.php`)
- **A biography's portfolio link and social-link URLs (and, for events, the location/date) still weren't reaching the artist's own native-language sibling post, despite three prior fix attempts targeting the meta-copy allowlist itself.** Those earlier fixes (adding the four keys to `Compat\LinguaForge::NEUTRAL_META_KEYS` and to `ReviewEndpoints::finalize_publish()`'s staged-update meta loop) were necessary but not sufficient — the actual bug was an order-of-operations gap in `ReviewConfirm`, one directory over. `handle_approve_submission()`'s two branches both call `rest_do_request()` — which runs `ReviewEndpoints::finalize_publish()`, which calls `LinguaForge::sync_native_sibling()` to copy the primary post's language-neutral meta onto its native-language sibling — and only *afterward* call `sync_extra_fields()`, which is what actually writes the approve form's portfolio/social-link URLs (or event location/date) onto the primary post. So `sync_native_sibling()` always copied whatever value the primary post held at the *start* of the request — one submission behind, or simply empty the first time a link was ever added — and nothing ever re-synced the sibling afterward. `sync_extra_fields()` now calls `LinguaForge::sync_native_sibling()` again once it's done writing, so the sibling picks up the value that was actually just submitted. Confirmed safe to call twice per request: the method is AI-free and idempotent (a plain meta/content refresh, not a fresh translation). (`includes/Publishing/ReviewConfirm.php`)
- **The portfolio link specifically still didn't appear on any sibling even with the fix above, because it's gated by a second, separate meta key that was never in the propagation allowlist at all.** `Artist\Profile::render_biography_social_links()` only shows the portfolio link when `_agnosis_biography_portfolio_embedded` (an EmbedPolicy moderation-approval flag, distinct from the URL itself) reads `'1'` on the post actually being viewed — and that key was missing from `Compat\LinguaForge::NEUTRAL_META_KEYS` entirely. So `_agnosis_biography_portfolio_url` was propagating correctly (per the fix above), but every sibling's own copy of the approval flag defaulted to empty, silently suppressing an already-approved link regardless of how correct its URL was. Added `_agnosis_biography_portfolio_embedded` to `NEUTRAL_META_KEYS`. (`includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`)
- **A biography title is normally machine-translated per language sibling, but Settings → General → "Preset biography title" showed the exact same untranslated text on every single language version once configured.** `Artist\BiographyTitle::apply_preset_title()` forces the preset onto every biography post's `post_title` via `wp_insert_post_data` — correct for the primary-language post, but that filter fires identically for Lingua Forge's own translated siblings and Agnosis's own native-language ones too, so the preset was never translated, unlike an artist's own (non-preset) title. New `translate_for_sibling()`, hooked on `linguaforge_translation_complete` (fires for both a genuine LF-AI-translated sibling and a native-language one), overwrites a sibling's initial (untranslated) preset title with a machine-translated version — cached per (preset text, language) to avoid re-spending an AI call on every resync — with the optional artist-name suffix appended afterward, never translated itself. Required a suppression flag around its own `wp_update_post()` call: that call re-fires `wp_insert_post_data`, which would otherwise let `apply_preset_title()` immediately stomp the translation back to the raw preset on the very same request. (`includes/Artist/BiographyTitle.php`)
- **The preset-title translation above surfaced a real, pre-existing bug: translating a single bare word (like a short preset title, with none of the surrounding-sentence context a normal biography title or body has) could publish the literal text "Array" as the translated result.** `SubmissionTranslator::call_translate()` blindly `(string)`-cast the AI's JSON `subject`/`description` fields without checking they were actually strings first — every OTHER method in this same file (`translate_fields()`, `translate_to_languages()`) already guards with `is_string()` before use, this one alone didn't. When the model's JSON response ever has one of those fields as a non-scalar (an array or nested object), PHP's array-to-string cast doesn't fail — it silently produces the literal string "Array", which then gets published as if it were a genuine translation (seen live: a Portuguese biography sibling titled "Array — Cal Talaia"). Now guarded with the same `is_string()` check the other two methods already use; a non-string response is treated as a failed field, so callers fall back to the original, untranslated text — never "Array". (`includes/AI/SubmissionTranslator.php`)

## [0.9.21]

### Added
- **A third contact-form rate-limit tier caps how many times the same visitor can message the same artist — surfaced during testing as a spam gap.** `ContactForm` previously only throttled by IP (5/min) and, globally, by sender email address (5/hour across every artist) — nothing stopped one visitor from repeatedly messaging one specific artist within either of those limits. A new `ContactForm::check_artist_limit()` adds a third tier scoped to (artist, visitor email), reusing `RateLimiter::check_sender()` with an action string keyed on `$artist_id`. Configurable via two new Settings → Email fields: "Per-artist contact limit" (`agnosis_contact_artist_limit`, default 2) and "Per-artist contact limit window (hours)" (`agnosis_contact_artist_limit_window_hours`, default 1). `$artist_id` is always the artist's WP user ID — the same one regardless of which LinguaForge-translated language version of their page the visitor is on — so this can't be sidestepped by switching languages. (`includes/Artist/ContactForm.php`, `includes/Admin/Settings.php`)
- **A new Settings → General "Preset biography title" field lets an operator force one fixed title across every biography page instead of each artist's own.** A biography's title today can be set from as many as five different places — an admission-derived first draft ("About {name}"), a bio@ email's subject line (on creation or any later resend), an artist's edit on the approve-confirm form, or a front-end edit to an already-published page — with no single call site an operator could override consistently. A new `Artist\BiographyTitle` hooks WordPress core's own `wp_insert_post_data` filter instead, the one point every one of those paths already converges through on every insert/update, and overrides `post_title` whenever `agnosis_biography_preset_title` (default: blank, meaning "use the artist's own title" exactly as before) is non-empty — including on a Lingua Forge translated sibling, shown as-is rather than machine-translated. A companion checkbox, "Include artist's name in preset title" (`agnosis_biography_preset_title_include_name`, default off), appends the post author's own WordPress display name (e.g. "Meet the Artist — Jane Doe"). (`includes/Artist/BiographyTitle.php`, `includes/Admin/Settings.php`, `includes/Core/Plugin.php`)

### Fixed
- **The contact form no longer just hides itself client-side after a successful submission — a visitor could trivially bring it back and keep spamming an artist.** `frontend.js` previously only set `form.hidden = true` in the DOM, a hide with no server-side backing (dev tools, bfcache, or reopening the popover could all bring it back). A successful POST now sets a short-lived `Set-Cookie` (`ContactForm::mark_contacted()`, same window as the per-artist limit above, set identically for a sent or a silently content-rejected message so it can't be used to infer moderation outcome), and `frontend.js` reloads the page shortly after showing the confirmation. `ContactFormBlock::render_block()` checks that cookie and renders a static "already contacted" notice in place of the form — a real server-rendered state, not a client-side suggestion. (`blocks/contact-form/frontend.js`, `includes/Artist/ContactForm.php`, `includes/Artist/ContactFormBlock.php`)
- **A biography/artwork/event resend with a new photo never updated the live post's featured image, and every Lingua Forge translated sibling silently kept showing the old one too.** `ReviewEndpoints::finalize_publish()`'s staged-update branch (any resend that merges into an already-published post — a biography singleton, a matched `replace@` artwork, a matched event resend) has always inserted the artist's new submission as a separate staging draft, correctly set THAT draft's `_thumbnail_id` (`PostCreator::write_post_meta()`), then copied an explicit allowlist of meta from the draft onto the live post before deleting the draft — but `_thumbnail_id` was never in that allowlist and no `set_post_thumbnail()` call existed anywhere in the method, so the live post's featured image was never actually touched. Lingua Forge's own sibling sync was already copying `_thumbnail_id` correctly; it was just faithfully re-propagating the live post's stale value. `finalize_publish()` now transfers the staging draft's thumbnail onto the live post (via `set_post_thumbnail()`, skipped when the update didn't include a new photo) before the existing Lingua Forge fan-out runs, so both the live post and every translated sibling now pick up the new photo. (`includes/Publishing/ReviewEndpoints.php`)
- **The three optional social links on a biography's approve form never reached a Lingua Forge translated sibling, and the separate portfolio-link field only reached one on first creation, not on a later correction.** `Compat\LinguaForge::NEUTRAL_META_KEYS` — the allowlist both the "born with" and post-translation meta-copy paths rely on for every translated sibling, and that `ReviewEndpoints::finalize_publish()`'s own staged-update meta-copy loop separately relies on for the live post itself — omitted `_agnosis_biography_social_url_1/2/3` entirely, and `finalize_publish()`'s loop additionally omitted them (though it already carried `_agnosis_biography_portfolio_url`). All three social-link keys are now in `NEUTRAL_META_KEYS` (propagating to siblings on both creation and re-translation) and in `finalize_publish()`'s copy list (surviving a staged update on the primary post itself). (`includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`, `includes/Publishing/ReviewEndpoints.php`)
- **The biography portfolio URL was appearing twice — once as a clickable social icon below the featured image, once again as a redundant embedded preview inside the post body.** The in-content `wp:embed` block predates the dedicated social-links display and was never removed once that display existed: `ApplicationBiography::build_content()` appended it when a biography was first auto-drafted from an admission application, and `ReviewConfirm::sync_portfolio_embed()` unconditionally rebuilt it into `post_content` on every single approve-form submission afterward, whether or not the URL had changed. Neither now touches `post_content` for this — the URL renders exactly once, via the existing `agnosis/biography-social-links` block. `sync_portfolio_embed()` still strips any leftover embed block from a biography saved before this fix, as a one-time cleanup the next time that biography is approved/edited. Moderation is unaffected: the social-links block was already reading the raw URL meta unconditionally, so as part of this fix it's now gated on the same `_agnosis_biography_portfolio_embedded` approval flag the old embed step used to enforce — a policy-rejected portfolio link still doesn't reach the page, it just no longer has two different code paths deciding that independently. (`includes/Artist/ApplicationBiography.php`, `includes/Publishing/ReviewConfirm.php`, `includes/Artist/Profile.php`)
- **An artist could receive a second "Approve & Publish / Edit before publishing / Discard" email for a submission they'd already approved (and that was already live), or already discarded — with no action on their part.** Any resend that merges into an already-published post (a biography update, a matched `replace@` artwork, a matched event resend) is drafted onto a temporary staging post, and `PostCreator::handle()` writes THAT staging post's ID onto the originating `agnosis_queue` row. Both `ReviewEndpoints::finalize_publish()` (on approve) and `ReviewEndpoints::reject()` (on discard) delete the staging post outright once they're done with it, but neither ever repointed that queue row — it was left permanently pointing at a post that no longer existed. `Inbox::is_already_queued()` treats a `'published'` row whose post has vanished as "post deleted — re-run," resetting it to `pending`: an admin's "heal the queue" action does this unconditionally for every such row, and a mailbox-migration-triggered UIDVALIDITY rescan can do it automatically. Either replayed the ORIGINAL submission through the pipeline, minting a brand new staging draft and re-firing the review email — for content already approved and live, or explicitly discarded. Both methods now repoint the queue row (via a newly-public `PostCreator::mark()`) at a post that will keep existing — the live post itself — right before deleting the staging draft, so `is_already_queued()` has nothing left to "fix." (`includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`, `includes/Publishing/ReviewEndpoints.php`)

## [0.9.20]

### Added
- **WordPress core privacy (GDPR DSAR) integration — Tools → Export/Erase Personal Data can now see and act on this plugin's own data (seventh audit §4a).** Previously the plugin registered no `wp_privacy_personal_data_exporters`, `wp_privacy_personal_data_erasers`, or `wp_add_privacy_policy_content`, so an operator serving a GDPR Art. 15/access or Art. 17/erasure request had no supported way to satisfy it — all of Agnosis's personal data lives in custom tables core's own tools can't see. A new `Core\Privacy` class registers seven exporter/eraser group pairs keyed by the requester's email address: membership application, governance participation (vouches and votes), newsletter subscription, newsletter delivery history, contact messages sent, transactions, and notification preferences.
