Erasure anonymizes rather than hard-deletes wherever a row has continuing referential or statistical value (e.g. a redacted, per-row-unique placeholder email on an application row, rather than breaking its unique-email constraint; a governance vote's own yes/no value is left untouched even though the free-text message beside it is redacted, since a settled community vote isn't the voter's personal data to unilaterally erase). An active (non-terminal) membership application and financial transaction records are deliberately not erased on request — reported back with an explanation instead of silently no-op'ing, since the former belongs to the existing "leave the network" flow and the latter is retained under GDPR's own legal-obligation exemption. Also adds suggested Privacy Policy Guide content describing the third-party AI processors (OpenAI/Anthropic/Stability) and public ActivityPub federation. (`includes/Core/Privacy.php`, `includes/Core/Plugin.php`)
- **Contact-form messages (visitor email + IP + message body) are now automatically pruned instead of being kept forever (seventh audit §4b).** `agnosis_contact_messages` — the only high-volume personal-data table with no retention at all, unlike the queue, log, and unverified-application tables — is now swept daily by a new `ContactForm::prune_old_messages()`, piggybacked onto the existing `agnosis_cleanup_inbox` cron rather than adding a new scheduled event. A new Settings → Email field, "Contact message retention (days)" (`agnosis_contact_message_retention_days`, default 90), controls how long a message row (sent or rejected alike) is kept before outright deletion. Separately, and regardless of that setting, the visitor's raw IP address is cleared on its own fixed 30-day window — it's never read back for rate-limiting (a separate, already short-lived mechanism) or shown anywhere in wp-admin, so there was no reason to retain it for the full message-retention period. (`includes/Artist/ContactForm.php`, `includes/Admin/Settings.php`, `includes/Core/Plugin.php`)
- **Rejected, withdrawn, left, and banned membership applications no longer retain email, biography, statement, and portfolio link forever (seventh audit §4c).** Previously only never-confirmed `unverified` rows had any automatic pruning — a rejected applicant who never became a member had their personal statement stored indefinitely with no automatic retention limit. A new `Admission::anonymize_resolved_applications()`, piggybacked on the existing `agnosis_check_admissions` daily cron alongside `expire_stale_unverified()`, now anonymizes a resolved application's personal fields once `agnosis_application_retention_days` (new Settings → Community field, default 180) has passed since it left `pending` — the row itself (status, dates) is kept for admission history and community-cap accounting. `rejected`/`withdrawn`/`left` rows are fully anonymized, email included; a `banned` row's biography/statement/portfolio are anonymized on the same schedule, but its email is deliberately kept, since it's the only way this site can keep enforcing that ban. The actual redaction is shared with the §4a DSAR eraser via a new `Core\Privacy::anonymize_application_row()` (extracted from `erase_application()`, which now also treats a banned applicant's own erasure request the same way — keeping their email rather than letting them erase their way past an active ban). (`includes/Artist/Admission.php`, `includes/Core/Privacy.php`, `includes/Admin/Settings.php`, `includes/Core/Plugin.php`)
- **The join and contact forms now show a short privacy notice before you submit, instead of no disclosure at all (seventh audit §4d).** The Privacy Policy Guide content §4a already ships only ever surfaces on whatever page an operator separately links to — a visitor filling out either form saw nothing about what happens to what they're about to submit. The Join form now shows a line, right above the Apply button, noting that submitted text/images may be processed by a third-party AI provider and that approved posts are published publicly and federated (irreversibly); the artist contact form shows a shorter line noting the message may pass through an automated content filter before reaching the artist. Both link to the site's configured Privacy Policy page when one is set (`get_privacy_policy_url()`), and degrade to plain text — no dangling link — when it isn't. Also adds a new Settings → AI Providers card, shown only when an AI provider is actually configured, confirming the policy content was added when a Privacy Policy page is set, or warning (with a direct link to Settings → Privacy) when one isn't yet — including a nudge to check that provider's own data processing agreement (DPA). (`includes/Core/Privacy.php`, `includes/Artist/JoinPage.php`, `includes/Artist/ContactFormBlock.php`, `includes/Admin/Settings.php`)

- **AI translation calls are now counted per submission instead of estimated (seventh audit G-2).** `NATIVE-LANGUAGE-PIPELINE.md` §7 estimated the 0.9.19 native-first redesign would drop translation-related AI calls from 3–4 per cross-language submission to roughly 2, but flagged it as an estimate. A new `AI\CallCounter` turns it into a measured number: the one direct translation call `ReviewEndpoints::translate_native_content_to_primary()` makes at approval, and each language Lingua Forge's own fan-out actually translates (via a new listener on `linguaforge_translation_complete`, deliberately excluding the synthetic firing `LinguaForge::sync_native_sibling()` does for its own AI-free native sibling — that's not a real AI call and would otherwise inflate the count), both increment a `_agnosis_ai_translation_calls` post meta counter and write a log line under the existing `ai-calls` context — visible in Settings → Logs with no new UI needed. Deliberately not counted: the description/vision AI call that generates the artwork itself, since §7's estimate is specifically about translation calls, which the redesign left that call unchanged. (`includes/AI/CallCounter.php`, `includes/Publishing/ReviewEndpoints.php`, `includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`, `tests/php/Integration/AI/CallCounterTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Compat/LinguaForgeCompatTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Publishing/ReviewEndpointsNativeLanguagePipelineTest.php`)

### Fixed
- **A staged update no longer leaves a stale native language on the live post when an artist switches back to (or away from) it (seventh audit §2b, a documented `NATIVE-LANGUAGE-PIPELINE.md` Phase 2 follow-up).** `ReviewEndpoints::finalize_publish()`'s staged-update branch only ever copied `_agnosis_native_lang`/`_agnosis_native_medium` from the staging draft onto the live post when the CURRENT submission's own value was non-empty — so an artist who first submitted in, say, Catalan and later resubmitted in the site's primary language never had the stale `'ca'` actively cleared, and the native-language sibling post `Compat\LinguaForge::sync_native_sibling()` had built for them silently stopped being updated and diverged from the primary post forever, with no indication anything had changed. Both meta keys are now handled explicitly: written when the current submission has a native language, deleted outright when it doesn't. When the artist's declared language genuinely *changes* (not just clears back to primary), a new `LinguaForge::trash_orphaned_native_sibling()` also moves the now-abandoned sibling to the trash — recoverable, not force-deleted, since this is a real change the artist made rather than spam cleanup. New coverage: a language-switch test in `PostCreatorMergeRedraftsPublishedTargetTest.php`, and five focused tests for the new trash method in `LinguaForgeCompatTest.php`. (`includes/Publishing/ReviewEndpoints.php`, `includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Publishing/PostCreatorMergeRedraftsPublishedTargetTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Compat/LinguaForgeCompatTest.php`)
- **A throwing listener could silently disable tag/medium translation for every other artist's translated post for the rest of the request (seventh audit §2c).** `LinguaForge::sync_native_sibling()` set a static suppression flag, fired `linguaforge_translation_complete`, then unset the flag — with no guard between the two. If any listener on that action (this class's own, or a third-party integration) threw, the unset line never ran, and the flag stayed stuck `true` for the rest of the request or cron tick, silently skipping tag/medium sync for every OTHER genuinely-AI-translated sibling processed afterward — no error, no log, just quietly wrong tags. The `do_action()` call is now wrapped in `try`/`finally`, guaranteeing the flag resets regardless of what a listener does. New test proves the exception still propagates normally (this method was never meant to swallow errors) while the flag itself is provably reset afterward. (`includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Compat/LinguaForgeCompatTest.php`)
- **ActivityPub's actor/inbox fetches had no guard against a peer directing them at an internal address (seventh audit §3b).** `HttpSignature::fetch_public_key()` fetches the keyId URL carried in an inbound request's own `Signature` header, and `ActivityPub::resolve_inbox()`/`deliver()` fetch and post to a URL taken straight from an inbound Follow activity's `actor` field and the inbox that actor's own document advertises — three peer-controlled URLs, each previously fetched with the plain `wp_remote_get()`/`wp_remote_post()`, with nothing stopping a malicious peer from pointing one at `127.0.0.1`, a `169.254.169.254` cloud metadata endpoint, or any other RFC1918/loopback/link-local/ULA address reachable from the server. All three now use WordPress core's `wp_safe_remote_get()`/`wp_safe_remote_post()`, which reject exactly those ranges via `reject_unsafe_urls`/`wp_http_validate_url()` — re-checked on every redirect hop, IPv4 and IPv6 both, with `WP_ACCESSIBLE_HOSTS` as the operator escape hatch — rather than hand-rolling a narrower custom check. New tests confirm `reject_unsafe_urls` is actually set on the outgoing request at all three call sites. (`includes/Network/HttpSignature.php`, `includes/Network/ActivityPub.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Network/HttpSignatureTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Network/ActivityPubTest.php`)

### Docs
- **README now notes that native-language fidelity only applies to submissions from 0.9.19 onward (seventh audit G-1).** The 0.9.19 native-pipeline redesign (`NATIVE-LANGUAGE-PIPELINE.md`) deliberately doesn't backfill older posts — a native-language sibling built before 0.9.19 is still an ordinary Lingua Forge machine translation of the primary-language post, not a reconstruction of the artist's own words, since that can't be reliably done after the fact. That was a sound call but an undocumented one; the Multilingual feature bullet now says so, so the difference in fidelity between old and new posts doesn't read as a bug. (`README.md`)

## [0.9.19]

### Changed
- **Native-language AI pipeline, Phases 1 and 3 (agnosis-audit/NATIVE-LANGUAGE-PIPELINE.md) — the description AI now writes in the artist's own language instead of translating to primary first, and translation to primary happens once, at approval, instead of two or three times across intake/display/edit.** Previously every non-primary-language artist's submission was translated to the site's primary language BEFORE the description AI ever ran (`SubmissionTranslator::translate()`, one AI call), the resulting primary-language draft was back-translated for display on the review email and approve-confirm page (up to two more calls, cached), and an artist's edit on that form was translated forward again before publishing (another call) — the artist's own words were never what actually got generated or stored; what a non-primary-language artist read and approved was already a translation of an AI description, and what got published was that same chain translated again by Lingua Forge's own fan-out. `Pipeline::process()` no longer pre-translates: it builds the artist's context in their own language (resolved from their WP user locale — new `SubmissionTranslator::resolve_artist_lang()`, now the one shared implementation Pipeline/PostCreator/ReviewConfirm all use) and explicitly instructs the description AI to reply in that language. `PostCreator::create_post()` persists the resolved language as `_agnosis_native_lang` post meta, and the AI's native-language medium pick as `_agnosis_native_medium` (needed later since it won't match the primary-language controlled vocabulary yet). The review email and approve-confirm page no longer back-translate a native-first draft for display — it's already in the artist's language, so showing it costs nothing (`Notification::on_post_drafted()`, `ReviewConfirm::get_display_text()`, both gated on `_agnosis_native_lang`'s presence). `ReviewConfirm::handle_approve_submission()` no longer forward-translates an artist's edit before publishing — it saves whatever the artist typed, in their own language, exactly as submitted. All of that content — original or edited — is translated to primary exactly once, in `ReviewEndpoints::finalize_publish()` (the single point every approval, staged or not, already converges on), via one batched `SubmissionTranslator::translate_fields()` call covering excerpt, body, medium, and tags together; the medium is re-validated against the controlled vocabulary at that point (moved from intake, where it would have silently never matched), and `_agnosis_translated_title` — the AI-generated display title `Compat\LinguaForge`'s dual-title system uses for artwork — is regenerated here too, replacing the not-yet-meaningful native-language copy PostCreator seeds it with at intake. `post_title` itself is untouched throughout — it has always stayed the artist's own verbatim words at rest, for every post type, and continues to. Net effect for a non-primary-language artist: roughly 3–4 translation calls per submission down to 1, and the artist's own native-language page (once Phase 4 lands) will finally reflect their actual generated words instead of a round-tripped approximation. (`includes/AI/Pipeline.php`, `includes/AI/SubmissionTranslator.php`, `includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`, `includes/Publishing/ReviewEndpoints.php`, `includes/Publishing/ReviewConfirm.php`, `includes/Publishing/Notification.php`)
- **The native-language pipeline change above initially had no Phase 2 (preserve the native result) — the primary-language translation in `finalize_publish()` overwrote `post_excerpt`/`post_content` with nothing keeping a copy of the native-language version it replaced.** Caught before Phase 4 (native sibling creation) was ever started, which is the first thing that would have needed that data and found nothing there. `ReviewEndpoints::translate_native_content_to_primary()` now also returns the pre-translation excerpt/body, and `finalize_publish()` (both branches) persists them — `_agnosis_native_excerpt`/`_agnosis_native_body` — onto whichever post actually survives (the live post itself for a first-time publish, the staged update's target for a staged one), captured at the moment of approval rather than intake so an artist's edit on the confirm form is what's preserved, not a stale pre-edit snapshot. The staged branch also now keeps `_agnosis_native_lang`/`_agnosis_native_medium` fresh on the target post (previously only ever written on the now-deleted staging draft). No separate native-title meta was needed — `post_title` was already never translated for any post type. (`includes/Publishing/ReviewEndpoints.php`)
- **Native-language AI pipeline, Phase 4 — the artist's own native-language page now actually exists and reflects what they wrote, and Lingua Forge's own AI fan-out no longer wastes a call re-translating back into the language the content already started in.** Phases 1–3 fixed what got generated and what got published in the primary language, but said nothing about the artist's own language: prior to this, a non-primary-language artist's native words (now preserved as `_agnosis_native_excerpt`/`_agnosis_native_body`/`_agnosis_native_tags` per Phase 2) were captured and then never used — Lingua Forge's fan-out would still generate that artist's own-language sibling by AI-translating the primary-language post, producing a translation of a translation instead of showing the artist their real words back. A new `Compat\LinguaForge::sync_native_sibling( int $primary_post_id )`, called at the end of `ReviewEndpoints::finalize_publish()` for both the direct-publish and staged-update branches, creates or updates that native-language sibling post directly from the preserved native content — no AI call, zero marginal cost — replicating Lingua Forge's own internal `TranslationTrigger::create_translated_post()`/`update_translated_post()` recipe (confirmed via source reading, Phase 0) using only its public API: get-or-create the TRID, unhook/insert-or-update/rehook around its own `wp_after_insert_post` handlers exactly as it does internally, write `_lf_trid`/`_lf_lang`, clear its translation cache, assign the post's template, and fire `linguaforge_translation_complete` itself so every other listener on that action still runs as if a real translation had happened. `post_title` is copied verbatim from the primary post on both create and (newly, self-corrected before shipping) every update — it was never translated to begin with, so the sibling's title simply mirrors it forever, including through a `replace@` resubmission that changes it. Firing `linguaforge_translation_complete` synthetically would otherwise trigger Agnosis's own `LinguaForge::sync_translated_terms()` listener a second time for content it just set directly, so a new `self::$suppress_native_sibling_term_sync` flag brackets that one call; tags and medium are instead applied directly from the preserved native meta right after. Separately, `agnosis_post_published` now carries a second argument — the list of languages to exclude from Lingua Forge's own AI fan-out — computed in `finalize_publish()` from the post's `_agnosis_native_lang` (empty when the artist's own language already is primary, i.e. nothing to exclude) and threaded through `LinguaForge::schedule_translations()`/`schedule_fanout()` into the fan-out job itself, so Lingua Forge never spends an AI call re-generating the one language Agnosis just populated for free. (`includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`, `includes/Publishing/ReviewEndpoints.php`)
- **Native-language AI pipeline, Phase 5 — deleted the back-translation machinery Phases 1–3 made permanently unreachable, rather than leaving it as dead weight.** `ReviewConfirm::get_display_text()` used to back-translate a primary-language excerpt/body into the artist's own language for the approve confirm form on demand, caching the result in `_agnosis_review_backtranslation` postmeta (`BACKTRANSLATION_META`) — necessary before Phase 1 existed, since content really was primary-language at rest at that stage; unreachable since, because content is native at rest from intake onward and nothing translates it before this page is ever shown. It now unconditionally returns the post's own excerpt/body, no AI call, no cache; `BACKTRANSLATION_META`, the private `resolve_artist_lang()` wrapper, and the now-unused `SubmissionTranslator` import were deleted from `ReviewConfirm.php` along with it. `Notification::on_post_drafted()` had a matching legacy block (fifth audit §4b — batched title/excerpt/body translation for the review email preview, warming the same cache) that referenced `BACKTRANSLATION_META` directly; analysis showed it was already unreachable for every post-Phase-1 submission regardless of artist locale, so it was removed outright too rather than left holding a reference to a deleted constant. One deliberate, explicitly-decided gap: a review draft created before Phase 1 shipped (2026-07-12) has no `_agnosis_native_lang` and is genuinely primary-language at rest, and its review-link token can still be valid for up to 7 days — a non-primary-language artist opening one of those old emails within that window now sees primary-language text on the confirm page instead of a back-translation. Accepted rather than engineered around: it self-resolves as old tokens expire, and the alternative was keeping AI-translation code alive solely to cover a shrinking, one-time transition window. `tests/php/Integration/Publishing/NotificationEmailTest.php`'s four tests covering the deleted `Notification.php` block (two of which referenced `ReviewConfirm::BACKTRANSLATION_META` directly, which would have fataled on the now-undefined constant) were replaced with two tests asserting the new invariant: `on_post_drafted()` never translates and never writes the old cache meta key, regardless of artist locale. (`includes/Publishing/ReviewConfirm.php`, `includes/Publishing/Notification.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Publishing/NotificationEmailTest.php`)
- **Text-only biography/pure@ submissions (poetry, prose, any purely-written work) were silently rejected before ever reaching the queue — a blanket, transport-level rule that predates every post-type-specific handling downstream.** `Email\Parser::parse_imap_message()`/`parse_webhook_payload()` both returned `null` unconditionally whenever a message carried zero attachments, regardless of destination address — a policy applied before routing or post-type resolution ever runs. Everything downstream was already fine with this: `PostCreator::handle()` has always tolerated an attachment-less biography/event submission (`$results = []; // Biography/event emails may have no attachments.`), and `remove@`/`promote@` never touch attachments at all — only the Parser gate ever stood in the way. Both methods now reject only when there's genuinely nothing usable — no attachment AND no real text (reusing the existing `clean_text()` signature-stripping/sanitizing helper for that emptiness check) — which, as a direct consequence, also unblocks event@/remove@/promote@ text-only submissions, none of which needed an attachment in the first place. `agnosis_artwork`'s own new-submission path is unaffected: PostCreator's existing "empty artwork submission" guard (no attachment, no text) still rejects that case identically. A pure@ (`agnosis_artwork`, zero-AI, artist's-own-words-verbatim) submission is the one case that still needs *some* visual for the gallery, so a new `Publishing\TextPosterGenerator` renders one from the artist's own words when no photo was sent: the "edge-to-edge overflow poster" design (confirmed with the site owner) sizes each of the submission's own lines to span the canvas width, stacks their vertical centers evenly across the frame, and lets a long submission degrade gracefully into overlap — later lines increasingly stack on each other, so only isolated words/phrases stay legible near the top, with no text ever truncated or redacted (beyond a sane 40-line processing cap for pathologically long input) — concealment is purely a side effect of scale and layout, never content omission. Styled to match the site's own dark brand (`#0d0d12` background, `#ededf0` text, matching `agnosis-theme`'s `theme.json` palette) using a plugin-owned copy of Plus Jakarta Sans SemiBold (SIL OFL 1.1, `assets/fonts/plus-jakarta-sans/`) rather than reading the theme repo's font files at runtime — a plugin's core functionality shouldn't depend on a specific theme being active. `PostCreator::handle()` calls it for pure@ + no attachment + real text, injecting the generated PNG as a synthetic attachment (same shape Parser itself produces) before the existing attachment-loading section, so the rest of the pipeline (`Pipeline::process_raw()`, gallery merge) treats it exactly like a normally-submitted photo; Imagick is a soft dependency here exactly as it already is in `AI\MediaAdapter` — unavailable/failed generation falls back to publishing text-only rather than blocking the submission. New coverage: `ParserTest` for both transports' relaxed gate (text-only accepted, still-empty still rejected); `TextPosterGeneratorTest` covering the line-splitting/subject-fallback/blank-line-filtering/MAX_LINES-cap logic directly (no Imagick needed) plus `generate()`'s Imagick-availability branches, forced deterministically via a new namespace-scoped `extension_loaded()` override in `Stubs/publishing_namespace_stubs.php` (same technique `Unit/AI/MediaAdapterTest` already uses) — `dev/bootstrap.php`'s conditional fake `Imagick` class gained matching `ImagickDraw`/`queryFontMetrics()`/`annotateImage()` support so this runs identically whether or not the real extension is installed on the machine running the suite. (`includes/Email/Parser.php`, `includes/Publishing/TextPosterGenerator.php`, `includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`, `assets/fonts/plus-jakarta-sans/`, `tests/php/Unit/Email/ParserTest.php`, `tests/php/Unit/Publishing/TextPosterGeneratorTest.php`, `tests/php/Unit/Publishing/Stubs/publishing_namespace_stubs.php`, `dev/bootstrap.php`)
- **Biography artists had no way to point visitors to their social presence — the approve form only ever captured one link (portfolio), and nothing rendered it anywhere but a trailing embed inside the body text.** The biography approve form (`ReviewConfirm.php`) now also collects up to three optional social links alongside the existing portfolio field — plain URL inputs, no platform picker, since the platform is auto-detected from the URL itself at render time rather than stored. A new `Publishing\SocialLinks::detect_service()` matches a URL's host (with subdomain matching, same convention `EmbedPolicy::is_trusted_host()` already uses) against a list of common platforms (Instagram, Facebook, X, Bandcamp, YouTube, SoundCloud, WhatsApp, and others), falling back to a generic link icon for anything unrecognized — nothing an artist submits is ever dropped, unlike the portfolio field's `EmbedPolicy`-gated embed (these are plain outbound links, not embedded remote content, so that fetch/AI trust check doesn't apply here). `SocialLinks::render_icon_row()` builds `core/social-links`/`core/social-link` block markup procedurally (the same "construct block markup as a string" technique `PostCreator` already uses for images/embeds/galleries) and renders it through `do_blocks()`, so the icon row uses WordPress's own real Social Icons block — its actual icon set and default styling — rather than a bespoke one. Displaying it required a genuinely per-post-dynamic element inside an otherwise-static FSE template, the same problem the event date/location/address fields already solved: a new `agnosis/biography-social-links` block, registered in `Artist\Profile::register_blocks()` alongside those, with a `render_callback` reading the biography's own postmeta at render time (portfolio link included in the same row — it's just as much an outbound "find me elsewhere" link as the three social ones, only pre-existing) — placed in `agnosis-theme`'s `single-agnosis_biography.html`, beneath the sidebar portrait. The three social fields are also reachable post-publish via `Artist\ContentEditor`'s existing REST field-edit endpoint (`EDITABLE_FIELDS`, `esc_url_raw` sanitized, `http(s)://`-format validated) — same "backend-capable now, no on-page click-to-edit affordance yet" state `event_timezone` has had since 2026-07-10; portfolio_url deliberately stays approval-form-only, unchanged, since it has different (embed-vetting) semantics. Separately, closed a duplicate-hero-image bug found while reading the biography template for this feature: both `single-agnosis_biography.html` and `single-agnosis_event.html` render `wp:post-featured-image` above `wp:post-content`, but `PostCreator::build_post_content()` was *also* prepending that same lone photo as a leading `wp:image` block into the content — visible twice on every biography and event page with a single photo. `build_post_content()` now skips that leading block specifically when the post type is biography/event AND the image about to be skipped is provably the exact attachment `pick_thumbnail_id()` would select as the featured image — checked directly, not merely inferred from "there's only one image", since a lone photo submitted alongside a video (whose poster frame wins the featured-image slot instead) is a different attachment entirely and must still get its own content block or it would vanish from the post altogether. A genuine multi-image gallery (more than one photo) is untouched — the featured image only ever covers one of those, so the rest still need to render somewhere. Artwork's template has no featured-image block at all (the gallery block is the page's actual content there), so it was never affected. (`includes/Publishing/SocialLinks.php`, `includes/Publishing/ReviewConfirm.php`, `includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`, `includes/Artist/Profile.php`, `includes/Artist/ContentEditor.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Publishing/SocialLinksTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Publishing/ReviewConfirmSocialLinksTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Publishing/PostCreatorDuplicateHeroImageTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Artist/ContentEditorTest.php`)
- **Artists had no way for a site visitor to actually get in touch with them — every existing link on a biography page (portfolio, the new social icons) only pointed outward.** A third breadcrumb icon (`agnosis/breadcrumb-icon-link`'s `type=contact` variant) now opens a popover contact form (mirroring `Newsletter\PopoverBlock`/`SignupBlock`'s native-`popover="auto"`, no-custom-JS-for-show/hide shape) letting a visitor message the artist in whatever language they're writing in — the popover/form UI itself renders in the visitor's current site locale via standard WP i18n, same as everything else on the page. A new `Artist\ContactForm` REST endpoint (`POST /agnosis/v1/contact/{artist_id}`) verifies Cloudflare Turnstile first (`Core\Turnstile`, opt-in exactly as elsewhere), rate-limits by IP and by sender email (`Core\RateLimiter`), then runs the message through a new `Pipeline::classify_text()` — `classify_link()`'s sibling, same `<untrusted_message>` prompt-fencing hardening, minus the fetch step — against the site's existing admin-configured disallowed-content categories (`Publishing\EmbedPolicy::disallowed_categories()`, widened to `public static` and reused directly rather than duplicated) plus an always-on spam/solicitation category. Unlike `EmbedPolicy`'s fail-closed contract, an inconclusive AI response is treated as ALLOW here — the cost of silently dropping a genuine visitor's one-shot message is judged higher than an occasional unfiltered one reaching an artist's inbox. Every submission is stored — sent or rejected alike — in a new `agnosis_contact_messages` table, reviewable on a new "Contact Messages" admin page (`Admin\ContactMessagesPage`, mirroring `InboxPage`'s filter/pagination shape); a rejected message is silently dropped from the artist's perspective and the REST response is byte-for-byte identical to an accepted one's, so the response itself can never become a spam-testing oracle. An accepted message is translated into the artist's own language (`SubmissionTranslator::resolve_artist_lang()` + `translate_fields()`, the same pair `Notification`/`ReviewConfirm` already use) before being emailed — the email's `Reply-To` header carries the visitor's own address (no prior precedent for that header in this codebase; a direct extension of the existing `Bcc:`-array convention), so the artist can just hit reply, and this plugin never learns or stores the artist's real address beyond what WP core already has. An artist can turn the form off entirely via a new `_agnosis_contact_optout` toggle on the existing tokenized notification-preferences page (`Artist\NotificationPreferences`, mirroring its `mute_broadcasts` checkbox exactly) — checked both before the trigger icon renders at all and again server-side in `ContactForm::submit()`, so a direct POST to an opted-out artist gets the same 404 as one to a nonexistent artist, never a distinguishable 403. (`includes/Artist/ContactForm.php`, `includes/Artist/ContactFormBlock.php`, `includes/Artist/NotificationPreferences.php`, `includes/Admin/ContactMessagesPage.php`, `includes/AI/Pipeline.php`, `includes/Publishing/EmbedPolicy.php`, `includes/Network/SubdomainNavigation.php`, `includes/Core/Activator.php`, `includes/Core/Plugin.php`, `blocks/contact-form/`, `blocks/breadcrumb-icon-link/`, `tests/php/Integration/Artist/ContactFormTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Artist/NotificationPreferencesTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Network/SubdomainNavigationContactIconTest.php`, `tests/php/Unit/AI/PipelineTest.php`)
- **Native-language AI pipeline, Phase 6 — test coverage for Phases 1–5, which shipped with none.** A grep across `tests/` before this phase turned up zero references to `_agnosis_native_lang` or any related meta key — the whole redesign had been verified by lint and manual code-reading only. Five new areas of coverage, closing that gap: (1) AI-call-count assertions — `ReviewEndpoints::approve()` for a non-primary-language artist now provably makes exactly one batched translation call end to end, zero when the artist's language already matches primary (new `ReviewEndpointsNativeLanguagePipelineTest.php`); (2) `Compat\LinguaForge::sync_native_sibling()` fidelity — the sibling's stored excerpt/body match the preserved native text byte for byte with zero AI calls, on both the create path and the update/re-sync-title path (new tests in `LinguaForgeCompatTest.php`); (3) the medium-term hallucination guard re-verified at its new home — approval-time validation of the AI's *translated* medium value, not intake-time validation of an untranslatable native string; (4) `schedule_fanout()`'s `$exclude_langs` traced all the way from `finalize_publish()` through the scheduled cron event to `request_translations()`'s actual queueing decision, both at the unit-integration level and end-to-end through a real `approve()` call; (5) staging + native-language pipeline exercised together for the first time — every existing "true staging" test predates this redesign and never set an artist locale, so `_agnosis_native_lang` was always `''` and every Phase 3/4 code path in `finalize_publish()`'s staged branch had silently gone untested (confirmed safe by inspection, not assumption); a new test in `PostCreatorMergeRedraftsPublishedTargetTest.php` proves a non-primary-language artist's staged update translates once and the translated result — not the staging draft's own native text — lands on the surviving live post. Required extending the shared Lingua Forge test doubles: `linguaforge_get_trid()`/`linguaforge_set_trid()`/`linguaforge_clear_translation_cache()`/`linguaforge_mark_translation_synced()` stubs, backed by new static state on `FakeLinguaForge`, alongside the `linguaforge_get_translations()`/`linguaforge_source_language()` pair already there. PHPUnit itself was not run (stays with the maintainer, per this session's standing arrangement) — every file is `php -l`/phpcs clean, and each scenario was traced against the actual production code rather than guessed. (`tests/php/Integration/Support/FakeLinguaForge.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Support/linguaforge-function-stubs.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Compat/LinguaForgeCompatTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Publishing/ReviewEndpointsNativeLanguagePipelineTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Publishing/PostCreatorMergeRedraftsPublishedTargetTest.php`)

## [0.9.18] — 2026-07-11

### Added
- **Inbox admin table: Endpoint column (patch 18).** The queue table showed which post a submission became, but not which of the ten intake addresses (artwork, photo, pure, biography, event, replace, remove, promote, goodbye, community) actually routed it there — an operator debugging "why did this become a biography draft" had to reconstruct that from the subject line or the resulting CPT. A new public static `PostCreator::resolve_endpoint_label()` mirrors `resolve_post_type()`'s own address-first, subject-indicator-fallback resolution exactly, but returns a display label instead of the five-tuple used to build the post — computed straight from a queue row's `raw_email` JSON with no Pipeline/Admission dependency, so it works identically for `failed` rows that never reached `create_post()`. `InboxPage` renders it in a new column between Subject and Files; goodbye@/community@/bounce alias rows (whose `raw_email` never carries a normal submission shape) are labelled from their existing `skip_reason` prefix instead. (`includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`, `includes/Admin/InboxPage.php`)

### Fixed
- **The 8 default `agnosis_medium` terms never appeared on a site that was already active before that taxonomy shipped (patch 18).** `Activator::seed_medium_terms()` is idempotent and its own docblock has always said "safe to call on every activation or upgrade," but it was only ever wired into `activate()` — never into `maybe_upgrade()`, the version-gated path (`agnosis_db_version` vs `AGNOSIS_VERSION`, checked on every `plugins_loaded`) that actually runs on an existing install when the plugin updates. `activate()` never re-runs on such a site, so the 8 defaults (Oil Painting, Watercolour, Drawing & Illustration, Photography, Digital Art, Sculpture, Printmaking, Mixed Media) silently never got created. `seed_medium_terms()` is now also called from `maybe_upgrade()`'s idempotent-provisioning block. (`includes/Core/Activator.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Core/ActivatorTest.php`)
- **`PostCreator::build_image_block()` threw `TypeError: Argument #1 ($id) must be of type int` for a biography submitted with a photo, and a biography could accumulate more than one image across resubmissions (patch 18).** Root cause: `Artist\ApplicationBiography` auto-creates an artist's first `agnosis_biography` draft straight from their admission application (bio text + portfolio link) via a bare `wp_insert_post()` that never wrote `_agnosis_gallery_ids` meta_input. When that artist later emailed a photo to bio@, `find_singleton_post()` correctly matched that auto-created post as the merge target, but `merge_gallery()` read `get_post_meta( $id, '_agnosis_gallery_ids', true )` — which returns `''` (an empty string) for a meta key that was never set at all — and blindly `(array)`-cast it; PHP wraps a scalar as a one-element array on that cast (`(array) '' === ['']`), not `[]`. That stray `''` survived `array_merge()`/`array_unique()` into the gallery, into `build_post_content()`'s `$image_ids`, and finally into `build_image_block( int $id )`, throwing under this file's `strict_types=1`. `merge_gallery()` now validates `is_array()` before trusting the meta instead of casting blindly. Separately, confirmed as an intentional product rule: a biography carries at most one image. `merge_gallery()` now takes the post type and, for `agnosis_biography`, a new photo replaces whatever was there instead of accumulating alongside it across resubmissions, a single email with several attachments keeps only the first, and a gallery that already accumulated more than one image before this fix self-heals to one on the next resubmission (with or without a new photo). (`includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Publishing/PostCreatorGalleryAudioSkipTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Publishing/PostCreatorMergeMissSuggestionTest.php`)
- **An update to an already-published biography (or a `replace@`/event resend onto an already-published post) minted a review token that could never actually be approved — every click landed on "Link expired or already used" regardless of how fresh the email was (patch 18, "true staging").** `create_post()` generates-or-reuses a review token and `handle()` unconditionally fires the "please review" email on every merge, published target or not — but `create_post()` also had `$post_data['post_status'] = get_post_status( $existing_id ) ?: 'draft'; // preserve publish state`, which kept an already-published merge target at `publish` instead of `draft`. `ReviewEndpoints::approve()`/`reject()` both hard-require `'draft' === $post->post_status` before touching a post at all (409 `agnosis_not_draft` otherwise), and `ReviewConfirm.php` redirects ANY REST error from that dispatch to the exact same generic `?agnosis_result=error` page a genuinely invalid/expired token produces — so a perfectly valid, freshly-minted token was indistinguishable, from the artist's side, from a broken link. This is the common case for biography specifically: `Artist\ApplicationBiography` auto-creates and the artist typically approves it once at admission (which deletes the token), so the very next bio@ update always hit this. A first fix forced the merge target itself back to `draft` — which made the token redeemable, but meant already-published content could sit offline for as long as the review-link expiry window (default 7 days) while the artist got around to approving, which is worse than the original bug for anyone who doesn't click through right away. The actual fix: an update to already-published content no longer touches that post at all. `create_post()` now detects a published merge target and redirects to inserting a genuinely separate draft post instead, tagged `_agnosis_pending_update_for` with the live post's ID (`find_singleton_post()` also checks for an already-pending staging draft first, so a second resubmission before the first is approved merges into that same draft rather than creating a competing one). The live post is never written to, never unpublished, and never touched in any way while the update is pending. A new `ReviewEndpoints::finalize_publish()` is what `approve()` now calls: for an ordinary (non-staged) draft it publishes exactly as before; for a staged update it copies the staging draft's title/excerpt/content and associated meta onto the live post, leaves the live post's `publish` status alone (never toggled), and deletes the staging draft — deliberately not re-firing `agnosis_post_published` (no re-broadcast/re-translate for an edit to already-live content, the same distinction `Artist\ContentEditor`'s own direct-edit flow already draws). `reject()` on a staged update force-deletes the staging draft outright rather than trashing it — there's no live version of that content to protect, since the live post was never touched. `merge_gallery()`'s "existing gallery" source also had to be corrected for this redirect: it must read the live post's gallery, not the (now always-empty) staging draft's, or a text-only update with no new photo would wipe the existing published one out from under the artist the moment it's approved. A merge into a target that's still a draft (e.g. an `Artist\ApplicationBiography`-created bio the artist has never approved even once) is unaffected by any of this — no live post exists yet to protect, so it updates in place exactly as before. `finalize_publish()`'s tag copy also guarded `wp_get_post_tags()`'s return against `WP_Error` (never `empty()`, so it would previously have been passed straight into `wp_set_post_tags()`'s `array|string` parameter on a lookup failure). `replace@`'s and `[Event]`'s own exact-title-match branches go through this same published-target redirect (they always did — the safety net was written to cover them from the start, see `create_post()`'s own comment), so their existing tests are updated for the new expected outcome (a tagged staging draft, not an in-place update). (`includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`, `includes/Publishing/ReviewEndpoints.php`, `includes/Publishing/ReviewConfirm.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Publishing/PostCreatorMergeRedraftsPublishedTargetTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Publishing/PostCreatorMergeMissSuggestionTest.php`)

## [0.9.17]

### Added
- **Artist notification preferences: mute community broadcasts, vote-email digest mode (security audit §5b/§4a).** An artist could opt out of the newsletter (`_agnosis_newsletter_optout`) but had no dial at all for community broadcasts or application-vote emails — on an active node (daily applications, chatty broadcasts) the realistic exit was the spam button, the single worst outcome for the shared sending domain's reputation. Two new independent per-artist preferences, both readable/writable from a new tokenized, unauthenticated front end (`Artist\NotificationPreferences`, `?agnosis_prefs=1&artist=…&token=…` — a stateless, long-lived HMAC token in the same family as `AdmissionNotification::vote_url()`, following this plugin's "no login required" convention rather than `ContentEditor`'s logged-in front end): `_agnosis_broadcast_optout` mutes community broadcasts entirely (honored by `CommunityBroadcast::broadcast()`'s recipient query, same OR/NOT-EXISTS meta_query shape as `Newsletter\Scheduler::artist_recipients()`), and `_agnosis_vote_email_mode` switches application-vote emails from instant (the default, one email per application) to a once-daily digest — deliberately no "off" option for votes, since voting is a membership duty per the audit. `AdmissionNotification::on_application_received()` now excludes digest-mode artists from its immediate per-artist vote email loop (its admin-oversight summary email also now reports how many were notified immediately vs. deferred to their next digest); a new `Artist\VoteDigest` class, run by a new daily `agnosis_vote_digest` cron, sends each digest-mode artist a single email listing every still-open application they haven't yet voted on — re-derived fresh each run (`agnosis_applications.status = 'pending'` minus any non-revoked row in `agnosis_application_vouches`) rather than tracked as a delta/queue, so it's self-healing by construction. A "manage notification preferences" link (`Core\EmailFooter::preferences_html()`/`preferences_plain_text()`) now appears in vote, broadcast, and welcome emails; the admin Members dashboard shows a muted-broadcasts / digest-mode badge next to each artist, alongside the existing bounce badge. (`includes/Artist/NotificationPreferences.php`, `includes/Artist/VoteDigest.php`, `includes/Artist/CommunityBroadcast.php`, `includes/Artist/AdmissionNotification.php`, `includes/Core/EmailFooter.php`, `includes/Core/Activator.php`, `includes/Core/Plugin.php`, `includes/Admin/Settings.php`)
- **`replace@`/event-update miss no longer creates a silent duplicate (security audit §2a).** A `replace@` or `[Event]`-update email whose subject didn't exactly match one of the artist's existing titles still created a brand-new post — correctly so, since replace is destructive and is never auto-merged on a fuzzy guess — but that new post's review email read exactly like an ordinary new-artwork draft, so an artist who actually meant to update "Sunset Over the Harbor" only discovered the duplicate later. Both miss paths in `PostCreator::handle()` now also consult `gather_title_context()` — the same fuzzy AI "did you mean" comparison §2c already built for `remove@`/`promote@` — and, when it finds a plausible candidate among the artist's other posts (event misses scoped to the artist's other events only, never artwork), the new post is tagged with `_agnosis_merge_miss_suggestion` (JSON `{type, title}`, same always-written/empty-clears-stale shape as `_agnosis_dropped_links`). `Notification::build_email()` renders it as a new amber notice in the review email: "This was published as a new post — if you meant to replace/update X, resend with that exact title." Costs the same one AI call the `remove@` path already budgets; no new plumbing, no change to which post gets created. (`includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`, `includes/Publishing/Notification.php`)
- **Per-email reapplication cooldown + server-side length caps on application fields (security audit §4b/§3b).** `Admission::apply()` let a `withdrawn`/`rejected`/`left` application reapply with no per-email limit beyond the existing 5/min/IP endpoint rate — the same address could cycle apply → confirm → community vote blast → withdraw → apply again in minutes. A new `RateLimiter::check_sender( 'admission_apply_email', $email, 1, WEEK_IN_SECONDS )` guard (the same per-sender-throttle class the intake mailbox already uses) now applies specifically on that reapplication branch, making one lap of the cycle cost a week — scoped narrowly so a brand-new address or a resend of a still-unconfirmed application (governed by the existing, much shorter §3a resend cooldown) is never affected. Separately, `bio`/`statement`/`display_name` were sanitized but uncapped, and the community vote email embeds all three for every recipient — new REST `validate_callback`s on `/admission/apply` now cap `display_name` at 100 characters and `bio`/`statement` at 5,000 each (`Admission::MAX_DISPLAY_NAME_LENGTH`/`MAX_BIO_LENGTH`/`MAX_STATEMENT_LENGTH`), mirrored as `maxlength` attributes on the join form. (`includes/Artist/Admission.php`, `includes/Artist/JoinPage.php`)
- **IMAP UID cursor now detects a UIDVALIDITY change and resets itself (reliability audit §5d).** `agnosis_imap_last_uid` (the cursor `Inbox::process_messages()` uses to ask the server for only new mail via `UID N+1:*`) previously survived a mailbox rebuild, provider migration, or folder recreation — events that, per RFC 3501, can and do make the server reissue UIDs starting from 1 again. Once that happened, every new message had a UID below the now-stale cursor, `UID N+1:*` matched nothing ever again, and the failure was completely silent — no error, cron kept running, and from the outside it looked exactly like "artists stopped emailing." A new `Inbox::check_uidvalidity()`, called at the top of `process_messages()` before the cursor is read, now compares the folder's current UIDVALIDITY (via `getStatus()`) against a newly persisted `agnosis_imap_uidvalidity` option; on a mismatch it logs loudly and resets `agnosis_imap_last_uid` to 0 so the very same poll rescans the date-bounded retention window instead of waiting for a human to notice. A failed STATUS read or a server that omits UIDVALIDITY entirely is treated as "nothing to compare" rather than failing the poll — this is a diagnostic add-on to the cursor, never a prerequisite for it working. (`includes/Email/Inbox.php`)
- **Inbox admin table: status/reason filter, real pagination, and spam-flood aggregation (ops audit §4c).** The table was a flat, unpaginated `LIMIT 100` with no way to narrow it down — a weekend of dictionary spam (every unregistered-sender message becomes its own `failed` queue row, correctly, so the state machine never re-fetches the same UID) could push every real event off the single page entirely, with no filter or next-page link to find them again. `InboxPage` now has a status dropdown and a reason dropdown (keyed off `Inbox::SKIP_REASONS`, made `public` specifically so the two classes share one source of truth for the reason text instead of duplicating it), real Previous/Next pagination (50 rows/page, replacing the old flat cap), and — cheaper than listing every spam row individually — the default (no reason chosen) view now excludes `unregistered_sender` rows entirely, showing one collapsed "N messages from unregistered senders — View them" summary line instead; choosing that reason explicitly still shows every one of them. All filtering/pagination is GET-based (bookmarkable, no nonce needed — read-only, same as any WP list table's own filters). (`includes/Admin/InboxPage.php`, `includes/Email/Inbox.php`)
- **Deliverability health card on Settings → Email Inbox (security audit §5c).** The plugin let an operator configure the community/transactional and newsletter From identities but never checked whether the site could actually send legitimately as them — on ordinary hosting (PHP `mail()`, no SMTP plugin), mail from an address whose domain doesn't match the site's own, or from a domain with no SPF/DMARC record at all, is increasingly likely to land in spam or be rejected outright by large mailbox providers, with nothing in Settings ever warning about it. A new read-only diagnostic card (new `Admin\Deliverability` class) reports, per configured From identity: whether its domain matches the site's own domain, and whether that domain publishes an SPF and a DMARC TXT record at all (correctness/alignment is out of scope — a plugin can't know a shared host's outbound IP without an actual delivered send); it also flags whether a known SMTP-sending plugin (WP Mail SMTP, Post SMTP, FluentSMTP, and others) is active, and offers the same one-click "send a test to my address" pattern the newsletter dashboard already has, using the community identity's own headers. Nothing here changes sending behavior, headers, or configuration — diagnostic only. (`includes/Admin/Deliverability.php`, `includes/Admin/Settings.php`, `includes/Core/Plugin.php`)

- **"Bot Protection" warning card on Settings → General when Cloudflare Turnstile is not configured (security/ops audit §4a, layer (2)).** The join application form (and newsletter signup) are always publicly reachable by design — this plugin has no "close the join page" mode, the whole model is community vouching, not a gatekeeper — and until now, an operator who never filled in the two Turnstile key fields had no indication anywhere that the form was running on IP rate-limiting alone (a fixed 5-submissions-per-minute-per-IP cap, trivially worked around by a distributed bot). A new read-only card, next to the two Turnstile fields on Settings → General, shows a plain confirmation once both keys are set, or an amber warning explaining exactly what's currently protecting the form and what adding Turnstile keys would change — nothing is configured automatically, this only makes the existing state visible. Layer (3) of this same finding (a global daily application cap) remains open. (`includes/Admin/Settings.php`)
- **Event timezone `<select>`, community-broadcast empty-body bounce, and a newsletter "Retry Failed" button (audit §2b, §2c, §5e).** The event review form's Timezone field was a free `<input type="text">` (e.g. "Europe/Madrid") validated server-side against `DateTimeZone::listIdentifiers()` but silently discarded — leaving the previous value in place — whenever what the artist typed ("CET", "GMT+2", "Madrid") wasn't a real identifier, with no indication anything didn't stick; it's now a real `<select>` grouped by region (new `ReviewConfirm::timezone_options_html()`), so only a valid identifier can ever be submitted. This conversion covers the one existing free-text timezone UI (the approve-form event fields); `Artist\ContentEditor`'s own `event_timezone` field has no visual editing affordance at all yet, so there was nothing there to convert — out of scope for this fix, not an oversight. Separately, a community broadcast whose subject and body both came back empty (typically an HTML-only email with no plain-text part) was previously just dropped with no signal to the sender that nothing went out; `CommunityBroadcast::send_empty_bounce()` now emails them back explaining why and suggesting a plain-text resend, wired into both the IMAP (`Email/Inbox.php`) and webhook (`Email/Webhook.php`) community-empty paths. Finally, the newsletter dashboard's issue rows now show a "Failed recipients" count with a "Retry Failed" button per newsletter type — previously a recipient that exhausted `QueueProcessor::MAX_ATTEMPTS` (e.g. during a temporary SMTP outage) had no resend affordance short of a direct database edit; the button resets that type's most recent issue's failed rows back to `pending` (new `QueueProcessor::retry_failed()`, `Scheduler::latest_issue_id()`/`failed_count_for_latest_issue()`) so the next cron tick picks them back up. (`includes/Publishing/ReviewConfirm.php`, `includes/Artist/CommunityBroadcast.php`, `includes/Email/Inbox.php`, `includes/Email/Webhook.php`, `includes/Newsletter/Scheduler.php`, `includes/Newsletter/QueueProcessor.php`, `includes/Admin/Settings.php`, `includes/Core/Plugin.php`)

### Fixed
- **Webhook rate-limit ordering and bucket split; webhook attachment MIME sniffing brought in line with the IMAP path (security audit §3c, §3e).** `Webhook::verify_signature()` previously rate-limited (a single shared `email_inbound` bucket, 60/60s, keyed by IP) BEFORE checking the HMAC signature — on a host where a misconfigured reverse proxy or certain CDN setups rewrite every request to one shared `REMOTE_ADDR`, that bucket becomes effectively global, so an unauthenticated flood of unsigned garbage could starve the ESP's own legitimate signed traffic in the same window. The signature is now matched first (new private `match_signature()`), and the matched/unmatched outcomes use two separate buckets: a tight 10/60s bucket for anything that fails to verify, and a generous 300/60s bucket — never a practical constraint on real traffic — for anything that does. Separately, `Parser::parse_webhook_payload()` previously trusted `$_FILES[...]['type']` outright (entirely sender-declared, no byte-level check at all) where the IMAP path always fileinfo-sniffs the actual bytes first, falling back to the declared type only when the sniff doesn't recognize anything on the allow-list; the webhook path now applies that exact same rule via a new `sniff_mime_from_path()` helper, so both intake transports share one acceptance rule as the audit recommended. (`includes/Email/Webhook.php`, `includes/Email/Parser.php`, `tests/php/Unit/Email/WebhookSignatureTest.php`, `tests/php/Unit/Email/WebhookReplayProtectionTest.php`, `tests/php/Unit/Email/ParserTest.php`)
- **Nine files used a standalone `true` in a return-type union (`true|WP_Error`, `true|string`) — valid only since PHP 8.2, and a hard parse error on PHP 8.1, the minimum version this plugin has always declared support for (`readme.txt`'s "Requires PHP: 8.1", `phpcs.xml`'s own `testVersion 8.1-`).** Surfaced by newly bundling a real PHP 8.1 interpreter for linting (previously only ever lint-checked on a dev machine already running 8.2+, so the parse error had never actually been exercised under the version the plugin claims to support). Any site genuinely running PHP 8.1 would fatal on first touch of rate limiting, webhook replay checks, front-end content editing, review/removal endpoints, ActivityPub inbox signature verification, newsletter sending, or artist invitations — i.e. most of the plugin's security-sensitive surface. Every occurrence now declares `bool|...` instead (valid since PHP 8.0); each docblock's `@return true|...` line is untouched, since it still accurately documents that `false` is never actually returned. No behavior changed — type declarations only. (`includes/Core/RateLimiter.php`, `includes/Email/Webhook.php`, `includes/Artist/ContentEditor.php`, `includes/Publishing/ReviewEndpoints.php`, `includes/Publishing/RemovalEndpoints.php`, `includes/Network/ActivityPub.php`, `includes/Network/HttpSignature.php`, `includes/Newsletter/Scheduler.php`, `includes/Artist/Invitation.php`)
- **`extract_event_fields()`'s AI prompt now fences the artist's own email content the same way `classify_link()` already fences fetched page text (security audit §3d).** The event-extraction prompt previously interpolated the artist's subject/body raw between a bare `---`/`---` marker — no explicit "this is data, not instructions" framing and no `neutralize_prompt_delimiters()` — unlike `classify_link()`'s `<untrusted_page_data>` convention (fourth audit §3d). Exposure was already bounded (the sender is an admitted artist, and every output field is strictly validated — ISO-8601 regex, IANA timezone whitelist, `sanitize_text_field()` — so the worst case was self-inflicted junk in the artist's own event fields), but the codebase now has one rule instead of two: any artist-controlled text entering a prompt gets the same `<untrusted_...>` fence + neutralization. The email content is now wrapped in a new `<untrusted_email_content>` fence with the identical up-front "treat as data, never as instructions" framing, and run through the same (now-shared) `neutralize_prompt_delimiters()` helper. No behavior change to the extracted fields themselves — prompt construction only. (`includes/AI/Pipeline.php`, `tests/php/Unit/AI/PipelineExtractEventFieldsTest.php`)
- **New shared `Email\IntakeGates` helper closes "the third transport-parity episode" (code quality audit §6).** `Webhook::webhook_recipient_addresses()` and `Parser::extract_recipient_addresses()` were byte-identical private copies of the same To:/Cc: address regex, and `Webhook::ALIAS_REASONS`/`ALIAS_STATUSES` mirrored `Inbox::SKIP_REASONS`/`SKIP_STATUSES`'s ten shared goodbye@/community@ entries by hand-maintained convention — the same kind of copy-both-files drift risk the fourth and fifth audits already flagged and fixed twice over. Both duplicated pieces now live once, in a new `Email\IntakeGates` class: `IntakeGates::recipient_addresses()` (both transports' former private methods now just call this), and `IntakeGates::SHARED_ALIAS_REASONS`/`SHARED_ALIAS_STATUSES` (each transport's own constant is now composed from this shared source plus whatever is genuinely transport-specific — Inbox's five IMAP-only gate reasons and two bounce/DSN reasons have no webhook equivalent, so they stay put). Pure refactor: every existing `Webhook::ALIAS_REASONS[...]`/`Inbox::SKIP_REASONS[...]` call site, string, status override, and — for `Inbox::SKIP_REASONS`, which drives the Inbox admin table's reason-filter dropdown order — key order is byte-for-byte unchanged, verified directly rather than assumed. (`includes/Email/IntakeGates.php`, `includes/Email/Webhook.php`, `includes/Email/Parser.php`, `includes/Email/Inbox.php`, `tests/php/Unit/Email/IntakeGatesTest.php`)
- **`agnosis_imap_cleanup_days` default drift, `RateLimiter` docblock/dead-code cleanup, and an undated changelog heading (code quality audit §5e/§6) — the last three outstanding audit nits.** `Settings`/`Activator` both documented and seeded a 7-day default for Inbox retention, but `Inbox::poll()`'s no-cursor scan window, `cleanup_imap()`, and `cleanup_queue()` all silently fell back to 30 days whenever the option row was missing (`cleanup()`'s own docblock said 30 too, even though its code already correctly read 7) — a fresh install missing that row would clean up on a different schedule than Settings documents. All four now fall back to 7, matching Settings/Activator; a new regression test seeds a queue row aged between the two numbers (10 days, with the option deliberately unset) and confirms it's pruned, which would have failed before this fix. Separately, `RateLimiter`'s class docblock called its algorithm a "sliding"/"rolling" window; it's actually a fixed window (`transient_key()`'s `floor(time()/window)` bucketing), which does mean a request burst straddling a window boundary can let up to ~2x the configured limit through — now documented accurately rather than switched to a heavier implementation, since at this plugin's actual traffic that's an acceptable tradeoff. A `wp_cache_incr()` call in both `check()` and `check_sender()`, meant as an object-cache fast path, targeted the wrong cache group and was immediately overwritten by the very next line's `set_transient()` regardless — genuinely dead code, removed (confirmed behaviorally equivalent: the request-counting/blocking sequence is unchanged). Finally, `CHANGELOG.md`'s one undated release heading, `## [0.9.12]`, now reads `## [0.9.12] — 2026-07-09` — the actual commit date, not a guess. (`includes/Email/Inbox.php`, `includes/Core/RateLimiter.php`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `tests/php/Integration/Email/InboxCleanupDebugPruneTest.php`)

## [0.9.16]

### Fixed
- **Join application: double opt-in (security audit §3a/§4a).** `Admission::apply()` previously wrote an application row for any address that passed `is_email()` and immediately fired `agnosis_artist_applied` — sending an acknowledgment to that address (backscatter to a victim for a forged email) and blasting a "please vote" email carrying the applicant's own bio/portfolio/statement to every admitted artist and admin (a phishing/spam lane borrowing the site's own reputation). `apply()` now parks the row as `'unverified'` with a single-use `confirm_token` and sends only a short "confirm your application" email (new `AdmissionNotification::on_application_unverified()`, hooked on a new `agnosis_application_unverified` action); `agnosis_artist_applied` (and `agnosis_artist_waitlisted`, re-checking `CommunityCap` at confirmation time rather than trusting whatever it was at apply() time) now only fires from the new `Admission::confirm_application( $token )`, reached via a new `AdmissionConfirm` class (`?agnosis_admission=1&action=confirm&token=…`, `template_redirect`-based, mirroring `VouchConfirm`/`SubscriptionConfirm`'s GET-interstitial-then-POST pattern so a mail-security scanner's link prefetch can never confirm an application by itself). Resend-cooldown and enumeration-safety logic (a resubmission for a still-unverified address within 5 minutes neither rotates the token nor resends the email) is lifted from `Newsletter\Subscriber::subscribe()`, and a new `Admission::expire_stale_unverified()` prunes abandoned unconfirmed rows older than 14 days, piggybacked on the existing daily `agnosis_check_admissions` cron alongside `check_expired_applications()` — same shape as `Subscriber::expire_stale_pending()`. Schema: `agnosis_applications` gains a `confirm_token` column (`UNIQUE`) and a `'unverified'` status ENUM value (both added via `dbDelta`-unreachable `ALTER TABLE` in `Activator::maybe_upgrade()`, same as the earlier `'banned'`/`'waitlisted'` extensions). The join form's frontend copy and the admin's Pending Applications table both updated to reflect the new "check your email to confirm" step — a plain count of unverified applications is shown on the admin dashboard so an operator fielding "I applied but nothing happened" isn't left guessing. (`includes/Artist/Admission.php`, `includes/Artist/AdmissionNotification.php`, `includes/Artist/AdmissionConfirm.php`, `includes/Core/Activator.php`, `includes/Core/Plugin.php`, `includes/Artist/JoinPage.php`, `blocks/join/frontend.js`, `includes/Admin/Settings.php`)
- **Bounce/complaint handling + suppression (security audit §5a).** A hard bounce or spam complaint for mail this plugin sent previously came back nowhere: `wp_mail()` returning `true` only means a message was handed to the transport, and neither a dead newsletter address nor an artist whose inbox had died was ever flagged — a dead subscriber was mailed every issue forever, and an artist silently stopped receiving review links with no operator-visible sign anything was wrong. A new shared `Email\BounceHandler::record( $email, $type, $source )` is now the single sink for both intake transports: it flips a matching newsletter subscriber (pending or confirmed) to a new `'bounced'` status via `Newsletter\Subscriber::suppress()` — permanently excluded from `confirmed_recipients()`, so no future issue is ever sent there again — and, independently, increments a `_agnosis_bounce_count` user-meta counter (plus `_agnosis_bounce_last_at`) for a matching admitted artist, surfaced as a `⚠ N bounce(s)` badge on the admin Members dashboard. Two intake paths feed it: a new `POST /agnosis/v1/email/events` webhook route (sibling to the existing `/email/inbound`, same `verify_signature()` HMAC/replay protection) parses Postmark's single-object, Mailgun's flat-or-nested `event-data`, and SendGrid's raw-JSON-array event shapes, filtering for hard bounces/spam complaints only — a soft/transient bounce never suppresses anything; and `Inbox::process_messages()` now recognizes a bounce/complaint DSN arriving in the IMAP mailbox itself (RFC 3462 `multipart/report` Content-Type or the de-facto `X-Failed-Recipients` header), checked before the SPF/DKIM auth gate since a DSN's From is the receiving server's own mailer-daemon and would otherwise always fail it, extracting the failed address from `X-Failed-Recipients` first and falling back to the RFC 3464 `Final-Recipient: rfc822;` line in the message body. Schema: `agnosis_newsletter_subscribers` gains a `bounced_at` column and a `'bounced'` status ENUM value (`ALTER TABLE` in `Activator::maybe_upgrade()`, same pattern as the join-application migration above). (`includes/Email/BounceHandler.php`, `includes/Email/Webhook.php`, `includes/Email/Inbox.php`, `includes/Newsletter/Subscriber.php`, `includes/Core/Activator.php`, `includes/Admin/Settings.php`)

## [0.9.15] — 2026-07-10

### Added
- **The event approve confirm form (`ReviewConfirm`) now exposes Date, Hour, Location, Timezone, and Address as individually editable fields before publishing**, instead of only the AI-written description text. Date and Hour are two separate inputs matching how an artist actually thinks about an event, combined back into the existing single `_agnosis_event_date` meta on save (e.g. "2026-08-15T19:00") — every existing reader of that meta (`render_event_date()`, `order_events_archive()`, `ContentEditor`'s post-publish event_date field) is unaffected. Timezone and Address are new fields entirely: `AI\Pipeline::extract_event_fields()` now also extracts them from the artist's email (new `_agnosis_event_timezone`/`_agnosis_event_address` meta), a new `agnosis/event-address` block renders the address on the single event template (paired with `agnosis-theme` 0.5.6), and `render_event_date()` appends the timezone after the formatted date/time when set. Invalid input (an unparseable date, an unrecognised timezone identifier) is silently ignored on approve rather than blocking publication — both remain correctable afterwards via `Artist\ContentEditor`'s existing post-publish correction, which also gained `event_address`/`event_timezone` fields. (`includes/AI/Pipeline.php`, `includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`, `includes/Artist/Profile.php`, `includes/Artist/ContentEditor.php`, `includes/Publishing/ReviewConfirm.php`)
- **The biography approve confirm form now has an editable "Portfolio link" field**, so a misspelled or otherwise-rejected portfolio URL from the join application can be corrected before publishing, not just after. Correcting it re-runs `EmbedPolicy::is_allowed()` against the new URL and rebuilds the `wp:embed` block accordingly. As a side effect, this also fixes a latent bug where editing ANY part of a biography draft's body on the approve form silently dropped an already-approved portfolio embed entirely — `ReviewEndpoints::save()`'s content rebuild only ever preserved leading image/gallery blocks, never a trailing `wp:embed`. The embed is now always re-synced on approval (cheaply, without re-running `EmbedPolicy` unless the URL actually changed), regardless of what else was edited. (`includes/Publishing/ReviewConfirm.php`, `includes/Artist/ApplicationBiography.php`)

### Fixed
- **Any link that didn't clear `EmbedPolicy` — a join application's portfolio URL, or a link an artist mentioned in an artwork/biography/event email — was dropped with nothing beyond a log line, for every content type, not just biography.** `EmbedPolicy::is_allowed()` gained a companion `last_reason()` (non-breaking — every existing `is_allowed()` call site is untouched) that explains WHY a given link was rejected (not on the trusted-platform list with AI review off, the page couldn't be safely fetched, AI review was inconclusive, or AI review flagged the content). Both drafting paths now record every dropped link plus that reason in the same shape — a new `_agnosis_dropped_links` post meta (JSON array of `{url, reason}`), written by `PostCreator::build_external_link_embeds()` for artwork/biography/event email submissions and by `ApplicationBiography::on_artist_admitted()` for a join application's portfolio field. `Notification::build_email()` now reads this one meta key regardless of post type, listing every dropped link with its specific reason in the review email — superseding the biography-only notice from earlier in this same version, which only ever explained biography's portfolio field and never gave a reason. Biography's approve-form correction (above) also keeps this meta in sync when the artist fixes the link. (`includes/Publishing/EmbedPolicy.php`, `includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`, `includes/Artist/ApplicationBiography.php`, `includes/Publishing/Notification.php`, `includes/Publishing/ReviewConfirm.php`)
- **The "new application, please vote" email sent to every existing artist was the one remaining plain-text email in the plugin**, unstyled next to the acknowledgment/welcome/review emails that already used the shared branded HTML template. `AdmissionNotification::send_vote_email()` now builds its body via a new `build_vote_email_body()` (same `EmailBranding` header, 600px card, and styled Yes/No buttons as `build_acknowledgment_body()`/`build_welcome_body()` in the same file) and sends with `html_headers()` instead of `text_headers()`, using `EmailFooter::html()`/`edit_reminder_html()` in place of their plain-text counterparts. Same content as before (bio/portfolio/statement, vote links, footer, edit reminder) — styling only. (`includes/Artist/AdmissionNotification.php`)
- **The artist-breadcrumb's "Biography"/"Events" links could overflow or wrap awkwardly on mobile, next to the artist's name, in languages whose translations of those words are long.** Both links are now icon-only — a book icon for Biography, a calendar icon for Events — a fixed width regardless of locale. The translated word moves to the link's `aria-label` (screen readers) and `title` (hover tooltip) instead of visible text, and the "|" separator between them is gone entirely, replaced by consistent spacing that works whether one or both links are present. Paired with theme-side icon styling (`agnosis-theme` 0.5.7). (`includes/Network/SubdomainNavigation.php`, `blocks/artist-breadcrumb/block.json`)
- **The Community announcement address (`agnosis_email_community`) was missing from the "here's every address you can use" quick-reference card that appears in every work-related notification email** — an artist reading any of those emails had no way of finding out that address existed unless they'd dug through Settings themselves. `EmailFooter::address_options()` now includes it alongside Artwork/Biography/Events/Replace/Remove/Promote/Photo-only/Pure, so it now shows up everywhere that list already does (welcome, acknowledgment, and every review/admission email built on `EmailFooter::html()`/`plain_text()`). The "goodbye" self-removal address remains deliberately excluded — that's a departure action, not something you'd send mail to as part of participating. (`includes/Core/EmailFooter.php`)
- **The Promote address's description ("mark an artwork as featured in your gallery") was ambiguous about which gallery it affects.** An artist's own subdomain already shows every one of their published pieces — promote@ actually decides which single piece represents them in the shared, cross-artist gallery on the main site (`blocks/gallery-overview`'s per-artist featured-post lookup), confirmed still working exactly as originally specified: a per-artist budget that scales inversely with the total number of active artists (more artists → fewer slots each, down to one), a promoted piece filling that artist's slot first, and their most recent piece filling the rest. The address description (Settings → Email, the shared "every address" reference card, and the welcome email's alias list) now says "the shared community gallery on the main site" explicitly, instead of the ambiguous "your gallery." No behavior changed — wording only. (`includes/Core/EmailFooter.php`, `includes/Admin/Settings.php`, `includes/Artist/AdmissionNotification.php`)
- **The footer's newsletter-subscribe bell and the Twitter/Facebook/Pinterest icons next to it rendered too small by default.** `Newsletter\PopoverBlock`'s trigger icon is now 26×26 (was 18×18) and its close-panel icon 20×20 (was 14×14); the shared `.lf-icon-btn` box both sit in grew from 2.25rem to 3rem to match. Paired with a theme-side change (`agnosis-theme` 0.5.8): the footer's Social Icons block now explicitly sets `"has-large-icon-size"` instead of relying on the (smaller) unstyled default, so it stays visually flush with the bigger bell button next to it. (`includes/Newsletter/PopoverBlock.php`, `blocks/newsletter-popover/frontend.css`)
- **`agnosis/artist-breadcrumb`'s Biography/Events icons (added earlier in this version) had no editor controls at all — size, glyph, and color were all hardcoded.** The block now exposes `biographyIcon`/`eventsIcon` (a couple of Feather-style variants each — book/person for Biography, calendar/pin for Events), `iconSize` (a Range control, 12–32px), and `iconColor` (a Color Palette control, independent of the block's own text-color support — left unset, icons keep inheriting `currentColor` from that support exactly as before) as ordinary per-instance block attributes, editable from the block's own Inspector panel, same "vanilla JS icon picker" convention `Newsletter\PopoverBlock` already established. Also fixed a real bug this surfaced: `agnosis-theme`'s own CSS (`.agnosis-artist-breadcrumb__links a svg { width: 1.1em; height: 1.1em; }`) was silently overriding whatever size the plugin wrote into the `<svg>`'s own `width`/`height` attributes — any CSS `width`/`height` beats an HTML attribute regardless of specificity — so the new size control would have been a no-op without a matching theme-side fix (`agnosis-theme` 0.5.9). (`blocks/artist-breadcrumb/block.json`, `blocks/artist-breadcrumb/editor.js`, `includes/Network/SubdomainNavigation.php`)
- **Added an "Icon vertical align" control to the same Inspector panel above.** Icon-only links have no text baseline of their own, so `.agnosis-artist-breadcrumb`'s `align-items: baseline` could sit the Biography/Events icons visibly high or low against the artist name's text baseline once `iconSize` is changed from its default — especially at the larger end of its 12–32px range. New `iconVerticalAlign` attribute (Baseline / Top / Middle / Bottom) resolves through a fixed server-side whitelist to a real `align-self` value on `.agnosis-artist-breadcrumb__links` (never the raw attribute value written into `style="..."` directly), defaulting to `baseline` — i.e. unchanged behaviour until an editor explicitly picks something else. (`blocks/artist-breadcrumb/block.json`, `blocks/artist-breadcrumb/editor.js`, `includes/Network/SubdomainNavigation.php`)
- **Added two new, real-WP-block-shaped alternatives to the single `agnosis/artist-breadcrumb` block above: `agnosis/artist-name-link` and `agnosis/breadcrumb-icon-link`.** Every custom Inspector control the two bullets above just added (icon size, icon color, icon vertical align) exists only because `artist-breadcrumb` renders the name and both icon links as one opaque block — there's no way for a Group block's own native layout controls (justify content, vertical alignment) or a block's own Color/Typography *supports* to reach inside it. These two new blocks are meant to sit inside an ordinary `core/group` instead (`agnosis-theme` 0.5.10's bundled header now does exactly this): `agnosis/artist-name-link` is just the name, `agnosis/breadcrumb-icon-link` is one icon link per instance (a `type` attribute — 'biography' or 'events' — picks which, mirroring `core/social-link`'s single-block-type-plus-attribute shape, surfaced as two named "Biography Icon"/"Events Icon" inserter variations). Both use ordinary Color (Text) and Typography (Font Size) block supports — the icon SVG is sized in `1em` rather than a fixed pixel width, so the standard Font Size control directly controls it, and `stroke="currentColor"` means the standard Text Color control directly recolors it.
