- **External link embedding — the settings-driven, AI-reviewed replacement for `PostCreator`'s old hardcoded platform allowlist.** New `Publishing\EmbedPolicy` centralises the trust decision for every external link Agnosis can turn into a `wp:embed` block — artist-submitted links in artwork/biography/event emails, and (per the point above) the portfolio URL from an admission application. Two tiers:
  - **Trusted platforms (fast path, no AI, no network request)** — the same curated list PostCreator used to hardcode (YouTube, Vimeo, SoundCloud, Bandcamp, …) is now a Settings field (**Behaviour → Trusted embed platforms**), one host per line, still additionally filterable via the existing `agnosis_embed_host_allowlist` filter. A link matching one of these (or a subdomain) embeds immediately, exactly as before.
  - **AI review (opt-in via new setting, off by default)** — a link to any other host is no longer simply discarded. When **Behaviour → "Let artists submit other links too (AI-reviewed)"** is enabled, `EmbedPolicy` safely fetches the destination page (`wp_safe_remote_get()`, which validates the URL against private/internal/loopback targets — the same SSRF protection WordPress core itself relies on for outbound requests), extracts its title/meta description/text, and asks the site's already-configured AI provider (reusing `AI\Pipeline`'s description-provider credentials from Settings → AI Providers — no new provider setup needed) to judge it against admin-chosen disallowed categories: pornographic/sexually-explicit content (on by default), commercial/promotional sites, gambling sites, and a free-text field for anything else in plain language ("hate speech", "phishing pages", etc.). Fails closed at every step — feature disabled, fetch failure, empty AI response, unparseable AI response — except when AI review is on but no category is actually configured to block, which approves (nothing to check the link against). Existing installs are unaffected on upgrade: the new AI-review setting defaults off, so out of the box only the (now-editable) trusted list embeds, identical to pre-0.9.8 behaviour. (`includes/Publishing/EmbedPolicy.php` NEW, `includes/AI/Pipeline.php`, `includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`, `includes/Artist/ApplicationBiography.php`, `includes/Admin/Settings.php`)
  - **Community trust bypass (opt-in via new setting, off by default)** — an admin who considers community-vouched admission itself sufficient vetting can turn on **Behaviour → "Trust all admitted artists (skip link review entirely)"** to skip both tiers above completely: any link an artist submits embeds immediately, with no allowlist check, no page fetch, and no AI call. This is a deliberate, explicit opt-in — off by default — since it removes every other safeguard in `EmbedPolicy` at once. (`includes/Publishing/EmbedPolicy.php`, `includes/Admin/Settings.php`)
- **"Reset to default" button for Settings textareas that ship with substantial built-in copy** — the System prompt, Artist prompt template, Enhancement instructions, Trusted embed platforms, and Invitation intro fields previously had no way back to their original text once overwritten: whatever the admin typed simply replaced it, for good. Each of these is now flagged `resettable` in `Settings::field_definitions()`; `render_field()` renders a "Reset to default" button beneath the textarea carrying the built-in default in a `data-default` attribute, and a small inline script (`reset_default_js()`) repopulates the field client-side on click (after a confirm prompt) — nothing is saved until the admin clicks the page's own Save Changes button, so the reset can still be reviewed or backed out of first. (`includes/Admin/Settings.php`)
- **AI prompts now explicitly ignore mail-client footers and unrelated text** — an artist's raw email (subject and body) is fed to the AI largely as-is for artwork description, biography/event polishing, and biography merging; nothing previously told the AI to disregard a "Sent from my iPhone" footer, an email signature block, or other boilerplate a mail app appends. Added the same instruction to all three touchpoints: `PromptConfig::default_system_prompt()` (artwork description — a new bullet alongside the existing "never invent biographical details" guidance), `Pipeline::polish()` (biography/event spelling-and-grammar pass), and `Pipeline::merge_biography()` (biography-update merging). Admins who have already customised their System prompt away from the built-in default will want to add this instruction themselves, or use the new Reset to default button above to restore the (now updated) built-in version. (`includes/AI/PromptConfig.php`, `includes/AI/Pipeline.php`)
- **AI-drafted newsletter intros, proposed ahead of an issue actually sending (default: 24 hours; both configurable).** The "Artist newsletter intro" and "Public newsletter intro" fields previously had to be hand-written every cycle or left blank. `Scheduler::prepare()`'s existing daily tick now also checks, for each enabled newsletter, whether its next issue is due within the configured lead window (`next_due_at()` / `propose_intro_if_due()`); if so — and only if the admin hasn't already written something for this cycle — it builds a structured summary of what's new since the last issue (new artwork/events with their AI-generated excerpt, tags, and medium, plus new members and open community votes for the artist newsletter — `Digest::build_intro_context()`), asks the site's configured AI provider to draft a short intro from it (`Pipeline::generate_newsletter_intro()`, same "never invent facts not given" discipline as `classify_link()`/`merge_biography()`), saves the draft into the same intro option the admin edits by hand, and emails the admin the proposal with a link back to Settings → Newsletter. Nothing is forced through: the admin can rewrite or clear the field before the real send, same as always, and a proposal is only ever generated once per cycle — editing it doesn't trigger a second draft on the next daily tick. Skips entirely for a newsletter that has never sent before (no established cadence to look ahead of) or when there's nothing new to summarise. Two new Settings → Newsletter fields control it: **"Auto-draft newsletter intros"** (`agnosis_newsletter_intro_proposal_enabled`, on by default — turn off to never auto-draft, ever) and **"Draft intro this many hours ahead"** (`agnosis_newsletter_intro_proposal_lead_hours`, default 24). (`includes/Newsletter/Scheduler.php`, `includes/Newsletter/Digest.php`, `includes/AI/Pipeline.php`, `includes/Admin/Settings.php`)

Confirmed while investigating this feature: biography and event email submissions already turn artist-submitted links into `wp:embed` blocks exactly the same way artwork submissions do — `PostCreator::build_post_content()` calls `build_external_link_embeds()` unconditionally, regardless of post type, so no separate fix was needed there.

### Tests
- **Added `tests/php/Integration/Publishing/EmbedPolicyTest.php`** — trusted-host matching (option-configurable, filter-extensible, subdomain matching, lookalike-host rejection), AI review on/off behaviour, fetch-failure/inconclusive-response fail-closed paths (via `pre_http_request` mocking — no real network access in tests), the "no categories configured" approve-by-default edge case, that extracted page title/custom category text actually reaches the classifier, and the community-trust bypass (embeds unconditionally with no network/AI access when enabled, off by default, still requires a parseable host).
- **Added `tests/php/Integration/Admin/SettingsResettableFieldsTest.php`** — confirms the five expected fields are flagged `resettable` with a non-empty default, that an ordinary textarea with no meaningful default (`agnosis_embed_block_custom`) is not, and that `render_field()` actually emits (or correctly omits) the reset button and its `data-target`/`data-default` attributes via `ReflectionMethod` (same pattern `SettingsNewsletterLocaleTest` already uses for this class).
- **Added `tests/php/Unit/AI/PromptConfigTest::test_default_system_prompt_instructs_ignoring_mail_footers()`** and equivalent tests in `PipelinePolishTest` and `PipelineMergeBiographyTest` — confirm the new mail-footer instruction is present in all three prompts and actually reaches the AI provider call.
- **Added `tests/php/Unit/AI/PipelineGenerateNewsletterIntroTest.php`** — short-circuits (no provider call) when the digest context is entirely empty, the drafted text reaches the provider prompt alongside the site name and per-item facts (excerpt/tags/medium), the "never invent facts" instruction is present, artist vs. public framing differs, new members or open votes alone are enough to generate even with zero artworks/events, and provider failure returns `''`.
- **Added `Digest::build_intro_context()` coverage to `tests/php/Integration/Newsletter/DigestTest.php`** — title/excerpt/tags/medium extraction for artwork, that events carry no medium terms, that only the artist-type context includes new members/open votes, and the empty case.
- **Added `tests/php/Integration/Newsletter/SchedulerIntroProposalTest.php`** — the full `propose_intro_if_due()` behaviour via `prepare()`, using an injectable `Pipeline` stub (`Scheduler`'s constructor now optionally accepts one, same DI pattern as `PostCreator`/`EmbedPolicy`): drafts and saves the intro plus emails the admin (captured via `pre_wp_mail`, same pattern as `SchedulerSendTestTest`) when the next issue falls inside the lead window, does nothing when the next issue is far off or the newsletter has never sent, never overwrites an intro the admin already wrote, does not re-propose or re-email a second time within the same cycle (and an admin's edit in between survives), stays silent when the AI has nothing to summarise or the provider fails, is skipped entirely for a disabled newsletter, that the artist/public proposals are independent of each other, that `agnosis_newsletter_intro_proposal_enabled` (on by default) fully suppresses the feature when turned off, and that `agnosis_newsletter_intro_proposal_lead_hours` (default 24) correctly widens or narrows which issues fall inside the window.
- **Updated `tests/php/Integration/Publishing/PostCreatorExternalLinkEmbedTest.php`** — added two tests confirming `PostCreator` actually wires up to `EmbedPolicy`'s AI-review path end-to-end (approve and reject), on top of its existing trusted-host coverage which continues to pass unchanged (AI review defaults off).
- **Updated `tests/php/Integration/Artist/ApplicationBiographyTest.php`** — several tests from the initial `ApplicationBiography` test suite asserted the portfolio URL embeds unconditionally regardless of host; that behaviour changed with this redesign (see above), so those tests were rewritten to reflect the real, current behaviour: a trusted-platform portfolio URL still embeds by default, a non-trusted one does not unless AI review is enabled and approves it.

### Fixed
- **"Node label" lived under the General tab even though it's purely network-facing** (how this node introduces itself to peer nodes) — moved to the Network tab, alongside ActivityPub federation and the node public key. Same option (`agnosis_node_label`), same stored value; only its tab and settings-form group changed. (`includes/Admin/Settings.php`)
- **`ApplicationBiography::on_artist_admitted()` never checked that `$user_id` actually resolved to a real WP user before creating a post** — found while writing its test suite. Its sibling listener on the same action, `AdmissionNotification::on_artist_admitted()`, already guards on `get_userdata( $user_id )` before sending the welcome email; this one didn't, so a stale or invalid ID would still create a biography draft, orphaned under a `post_author` with no matching account (`wp_insert_post()` doesn't validate this itself). Now returns early in that case, same as its sibling. (`includes/Artist/ApplicationBiography.php`)

### Tests
- **Added `tests/php/Integration/Artist/ApplicationBiographyTest.php`** — the feature above shipped with no test coverage at all; this closes that gap. Covers: draft creation from bio + statement + portfolio URL, content ordering (bio before statement), creation from a portfolio URL alone with no bio/statement text, every skip condition (nothing on the application, missing application row, non-existent user ID, an already-existing biography), `_agnosis_artist_prompt`/`_agnosis_review_token`/`_agnosis_review_expiry` meta correctness for review-pipeline and future bio-merge compatibility, and that `agnosis_post_drafted` actually fires a real review email via `Publishing\Notification`. One end-to-end test drives a full `Admission::apply()` → `vouch()` cycle through the REST API to confirm `Plugin.php` really wires the listener up, rather than only testing the class in isolation. (The portfolio URL's embed trust — allowlist vs. AI review — was reworked after this was first written; see the `EmbedPolicy` entry above and its own updated coverage.)

## [0.9.7] — 2026-07-08

### Fixed
- **The `goodbye@` self-removal workflow had three separate bugs, all visible on the same Inbox admin row: no sender email shown, a red "Failed" badge on a request that actually succeeded, and — worst of all — cases where the row claimed "self-removal confirmation sent" while no email was ever sent.** All three traced back to `Inbox::mark_no_artwork()` and `Inbox::handle_goodbye_email()`:
  - **No sender address shown ("Cal Talaia &lt;—&gt;")** — `mark_no_artwork()` always stored `raw_email` as the literal string `'{}'` for every intake-gate skip, including goodbye requests, even though the sender's address was known at the call site. `InboxPage::render()`'s From column reads `$data['from']` out of that same JSON, so it always fell back to an em dash. `mark_no_artwork()` now accepts the sender's email and stores it as `{"from": "..."}` when known, so the admin table can actually display it. (`includes/Email/Inbox.php`)
  - **Successful goodbye requests showed a red "Failed" badge** — `mark_no_artwork()` hardcoded `status = 'failed'` for every skip reason, including `goodbye_handled`, which represents a successful outcome (the confirmation email was sent), not an error. The `agnosis_queue.status` column is a MySQL ENUM (`pending`/`processing`/`published`/`failed`) with no neutral "handled, not an artwork" value to use instead — extended it to add `'skipped'`, applied via the same `SHOW COLUMNS` + `ALTER TABLE MODIFY COLUMN` migration idiom already used for `agnosis_applications.status`, since dbDelta cannot modify ENUMs. `goodbye_handled` now records `status = 'skipped'`, which `InboxPage::render_status_badge()` renders as a neutral gray "Skipped" badge instead of red "Failed". `Inbox::cleanup_queue()`'s retention prune now also covers `'skipped'` rows, so they don't accumulate indefinitely the way they would have under the old `('published','failed')` list. (`includes/Core/Activator.php`, `includes/Email/Inbox.php`, `includes/Admin/InboxPage.php`)
  - **"Confirmation sent" shown even when nothing was sent** — `Inbox::handle_goodbye_email()` called `Departure::initiate_removal_for_user()`, which returns `false` when the sender has no active (`admitted`/`banned`) membership row — a real, distinct case from `is_admitted_artist()`'s WP-role check just above it, and one that sends no email at all. The old code logged that correctly but then recorded the row with reason `goodbye_handled` regardless of the return value, so the Inbox table's Error column claimed success either way. The `false` branch now records a new, distinct `goodbye_no_membership` reason ("no active membership found for this sender") and keeps `status = 'failed'`, since nothing happened here to relabel as a success. (`includes/Email/Inbox.php`)
  - **Related, found while extending the same ENUM**: `Publishing\PostCreator::handle()` already called `$this->mark( $queue_id, 'skipped' )` when an artist's admission changed between enqueue and processing — but `'skipped'` was never a valid value for this column, so that write silently failed under strict SQL mode (or was coerced to an empty string otherwise), leaving the row's status un-updated. The same ENUM extension above fixes this call site too, with no code change needed in `PostCreator.php`.

## [0.9.6] — 2026-07-08

### Changed
- **New "Community" tab in Settings, consolidating everything about who's in the community and how they get there** — previously scattered across Network (admission vote threshold/minimum/window, join-redirect URL, community size cap and its co-signer/vote-window settings, removal-vote nomination threshold/window, plus the Pending Applications and Members dashboards) and Newsletter (the Invitation intro field and the Invite an Artist card), none of which have anything to do with federation or with sending newsletter issues. All of it — settings fields, the Pending Applications dashboard, the Members dashboard, and the Invite an Artist card — now lives together under Community. The Network tab keeps only the two genuinely network-related settings (ActivityPub toggle, node public key); Newsletter keeps only the newsletter-issue settings and dashboard. Every admin-post handler that redirects back into a tab (admit/reject/suspend/delete/open-vote/send-invitation/send-test-invitation) now redirects to Community instead of Network or Newsletter. Setting values themselves are untouched — same option names, same defaults, same underlying business logic — this only regroups where they're edited. (`includes/Admin/Settings.php`)
- **Community tab split into "Members" and "Rules" sub-tabs** — the Pending Applications and Members dashboards are both unbounded lists (every application, every admitted/banned artist), and used to render directly above the Rules settings form on the same page; a growing community would make that an endless scroll before ever reaching the settings fields. New `render_community_tab()` renders a standard WP `.subsubsub` sub-navigation and shows exactly one or the other, never both: **Members** (Pending Applications, Members, Invite an Artist — the existing `render_tab_tools( 'community' )` branch, unchanged) is first and is the default landing view; **Rules** holds the settings form (admission thresholds, community cap, removal-vote settings, invitation intro). Every admin-post handler that previously redirected to `tab=community` now also passes `subtab=members`, landing back on the dashboard the action was taken from. (`includes/Admin/Settings.php`)

## [0.9.5] — 2026-07-08

### Added
- **New `pure@` work-submission address** — a stricter sibling of `photo@`. Where `photo@` still runs the full AI description pass (title, excerpt, body, tags, alt text) and only skips image *enhancement*, `pure@` skips AI entirely: no vision call, no enhancement, no translation-derived rewriting of any kind. The artwork post is built directly from what the artist sent — `post_title`/`_agnosis_artist_prompt` from the email subject/body (as before), and now the post's visible content and `_agnosis_translated_title` too, both taken verbatim from the artist's own text rather than an AI-generated description. New `AI\Pipeline::process_raw()` mirrors `process()`'s per-attachment result shape (so `merge_gallery()`/`build_post_content()`/`write_post_meta()` need no special-casing) but only ever calls `MediaAdapter::adapt()` — format normalisation (HEIC→JPEG, PDF rasterisation), never a creative or descriptive AI call. Quality-rejection gate is bypassed the same way `photo@` bypasses it (score is never assessed, so it's always 0 — "never reject"). New Settings → Email field (`agnosis_email_pure`) and matching `EmailFooter` entry. (`includes/Admin/Settings.php`, `includes/Core/EmailFooter.php`, `includes/AI/Pipeline.php`, `includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`)
- **New `_agnosis_intake_endpoint` post meta on every `agnosis_artwork` post**, recording which address it was originally submitted to (`artwork`, `photo`, or `pure`). Written once at creation, exactly like `_agnosis_original_title` — never overwritten on a later update, including a `replace@` merge. Closes the gap where `replace@` had no way of knowing the original submission bypassed AI: `PostCreator::handle()` now resolves a `replace@` email's merge target *before* running the AI pipeline (previously this happened after — too late to matter), reads the matched post's `_agnosis_intake_endpoint` (read-only; `replace@` still never writes to it), and forces the replacement through the exact same photo/pure/normal processing strategy the artist used on their original submission, rather than always running full AI regardless of how the artwork was first created. (`includes/Publishing/PostCreator.php`)
- **`_agnosis_intake_endpoint` added to `Compat\LinguaForge::NEUTRAL_META_KEYS`** so it rides along to every translated copy via the existing `linguaforge_translated_post_meta` filter — no new integration code needed, just an allowlist addition. (`includes/Compat/LinguaForge.php`)
- **`pure@` (and, while touching this, the previously-missing `photo@`) added to the welcome/admitted email's "how to share your work" address list and subject-line-convention notes** — `AdmissionNotification::configured_aliases()` had never been updated when `photo@` shipped, so a newly admitted artist never actually learned that address existed unless they'd read the docs; `pure@` would have had the same gap. Both now appear in the address table and the `[Photo]`/`[Pure]` fallback-indicator notes, correctly translated into the artist's own language — `on_artist_admitted()` already wraps the whole email in `switch_to_locale()`/`restore_current_locale()`, and every new string is wrapped in `__()`/`esc_html_e()` accordingly. (The work-submission footer shown on every other artist-facing email already covered both, via `EmailFooter::address_options()`.) Note: since these are brand-new strings, a `wp i18n make-pot` / Loco re-scan is needed before they show up as translatable in any existing language pack. (`includes/Artist/AdmissionNotification.php`)

## [0.9.4] — 2026-07-08

### Fixed
- **An artist's removal request (`remove@`, confirmed via the token link in the removal email) only ever trashed the primary-language post — every Lingua Forge translation of that artwork or event stayed live and publicly visible, with no signal to the artist or an admin that anything was left behind.** `Publishing\RemovalEndpoints::confirm()` called a bare `wp_trash_post( $post_id )` on the single post ID from the request; nothing in the endpoint knew or cared that the post might be the primary member of a TRID translation group. Now uses Lingua Forge's `linguaforge_trash_translation_group()` (LF 2.5.4+ — added specifically to solve this) via a new `trash_post_and_translations()` helper, which trashes every post in the group in one call, the same cascade engine wp-admin's own row/bulk "Trash" actions use. `$check_caps` is deliberately left at its default `false`: this is a signed-token REST request that frequently has no logged-in WP session at all, and the artist's authorization was already established by `verify_token()` before this runs — same convention `linguaforge_trigger_translation()`/`linguaforge_queue_translation()` already use elsewhere in this integration. Falls back to a plain `wp_trash_post()` of just the primary post when Lingua Forge isn't active. Covered by 2 new integration tests (via a dedicated LF function stub) proving the cascade is called with `check_caps=false` and that a cascade reporting nothing trashed still surfaces the existing 500 error. (`includes/Publishing/RemovalEndpoints.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Publishing/RemovalEndpointsIntegrationTest.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Publishing/Stubs/lf_trash_cascade_stub.php` NEW)
- **An artist's self-departure ("goodbye") could silently leave already-trashed content behind, despite the confirmation email's explicit "this action is permanent and cannot be undone."** `Departure::delete_artist_content()` queried with `'post_status' => 'any'` — a well-documented WP_Query behavior where `'any'` silently excludes `trash` (along with `auto-draft`/`inherit`). So a post the same artist had individually removed via `remove@` shortly before departing — still inside WordPress's default 30-day trash retention, along with any of its Lingua Forge translations left trashed by that same cascade — was skipped entirely: not deleted, sitting recoverable until WordPress's own trash-empty cron eventually ran. `'post_status'` is now an explicit list (`publish`, `future`, `draft`, `pending`, `private`, `trash`) rather than `'any'`, so a departure genuinely removes everything regardless of its state at the moment of confirmation. The other five `'post_status' => 'any'` queries elsewhere in the codebase (`PostCreator`'s duplicate/singleton merge-target lookups, `InboxPage`'s admin log display) were audited and left unchanged — excluding trash is the *correct* behavior there, since a new submission accidentally merging into content the artist already trashed would be a worse bug. New regression test trashes a post first, then confirms departure still permanently deletes it. (`includes/Artist/Departure.php`, `tests/php/Integration/Artist/DepartureTest.php`)

## [0.9.3] — 2026-07-07

### Fixed
- **The work-submission address footer's labels and one-line explanations (Artwork, Biography, Events, Replace, Remove, Promote, Photo-only) were never actually translatable, despite `EmailFooter`'s own docblock calling them "Translatable"** — `ADDRESS_OPTIONS` was a PHP class `const`, and constant expressions must be compile-time-evaluable, so the `__()` calls this needed could never appear inside it; every label and description was plain hardcoded English regardless of the `switch_to_locale()` every calling notification email correctly wraps around it. Every other string in these emails switches locale correctly (confirmed via a full audit of the artist-facing email pipeline); this was the one exception, invisible unless you compared the fully-localized surrounding email against this one untranslated block at the bottom. `address_options()` is now a method, evaluated fresh on each call so it reflects whichever locale is active when the caller builds its footer, with every label and description wrapped in `__( ..., 'agnosis' )`. (`includes/Core/EmailFooter.php`) Note: since these strings were never wrapped in `__()` before, they were never extracted into the `.pot` file either — a `wp i18n make-pot` / Loco re-scan is needed before they show up as translatable strings to actually translate.
- **The vote-confirmation pages reached by clicking a link in an admission-vote or removal-vote email (`VouchConfirm`, `RemovalVoteConfirm`) never switched to the voter's own language**, even though the email that linked to them was already correctly localized (`AdmissionNotification::send_vote_email()`, `DepartureNotification`'s removal-vote notice). A voter reading a fully-Spanish vote request email would land on an English confirmation page after clicking through. Both classes now resolve the voter's `locale` user meta and `switch_to_locale()` before rendering any of their `wp_die()`-based pages (confirm interstitial, success, and error), mirroring the pattern every other recipient-facing notification in the plugin already uses. (`includes/Artist/VouchConfirm.php`, `includes/Artist/RemovalVoteConfirm.php`)

### Changed
- **Increased font sizes further across every outbound email template and its matching vote/subscription confirmation pages** (Notification's four emails, Invitation, AdmissionNotification, the newsletter Mailer/Digest/Subscription templates, and the Vouch/Removal/Review/Subscription confirm pages) — roughly +2px across the board (body text 14→16px/16→18px, footers 12→14px/13→15px, headings 22→24px, etc.), on top of the 0.9.1 pass which only covered `Publishing\Notification`. 134 declarations across 13 files; relative hierarchy (headings vs. body vs. fine print) preserved throughout. (`includes/Publishing/Notification.php`, `includes/Artist/Invitation.php`, `includes/Artist/AdmissionNotification.php`, `includes/Artist/VouchConfirm.php`, `includes/Artist/RemovalVoteConfirm.php`, `includes/Publishing/ReviewConfirm.php`, `includes/Newsletter/Mailer.php`, `includes/Newsletter/Digest.php`, `includes/Newsletter/Subscription.php`, `includes/Newsletter/SubscriptionConfirm.php`, `includes/Newsletter/Archive.php`, `includes/Core/EmailBranding.php`, `includes/Core/EmailFooter.php`)

## [0.9.2] — 2026-07-07

### Fixed
- **An artist's own subdomain (`artistx.agnosis.art`) showed every artist's work on its homepage, not just that artist's own** — `blocks/gallery-overview/render.php` builds its artwork pool from a `SELECT DISTINCT post_author ...` query across every artist site-wide by design (it's the cross-artist portal-directory block, reused as the subdomain homepage), and never checked whether it was being rendered on an artist subdomain. It now checks `SubdomainRouter::is_artist_subdomain()` first and, when true, sets the artist pool to just `[ SubdomainRouter::current_artist_id() ]`, bypassing the sitewide discovery query and its 5-minute cache entirely — the existing per-artist pool-building/pagination logic already handles a single-artist pool correctly with no further changes.
- **The "More works" panel on a single artwork page showed other artists' work too** — a second, independent manifestation of the same bug class. `agnosis-theme`'s `single-agnosis_artwork.html` template has a non-inheriting Query Loop block (`inherit:false`, `author:""`) meant to show more of the same artist's own work; unscoped, it queried every artist's artwork sitewide instead. Fixed in the plugin rather than the theme (per this project's existing "Agnosis-platform behavior lives in the plugin" convention) via new `Artist\Profile::scope_more_works_query()`, hooked to WordPress core's `query_loop_block_query_vars` filter: on a singular `agnosis_artwork` page, an `agnosis_artwork` Query Loop with no explicit author gets the current artwork's author set and the current artwork excluded from its own "more works" list. Registered in `Core\Plugin`.
- **Genuinely attached photos (JPG/PNG) were rejected as "no valid image attachments" on the artwork intake address** — traced to webklex/php-imap's `Attachment::getMimeType()`, which never reads the email's own declared `Content-Type` header; it re-sniffs the type purely from decoded binary via PHP's `finfo` extension, and a decoding hiccup or unusual encoder could make that sniff return something unexpected. `Email\Parser` now falls back to the attachment's declared `Content-Type` header when the sniffed MIME type isn't in the allowlist, and logs the sniffed/declared/disposition values either way so a still-rejected attachment is diagnosable from Settings → Logs on the next occurrence.
- **A submission with no usable attachment could still produce an empty, untitled `agnosis_artwork` post** — root-caused to `Inbox::is_already_queued()` auto-retrying *every* `'failed'` queue row indiscriminately, including intake-gate skips (`mark_no_artwork()`: unregistered sender, not admitted, throttled, no valid attachment) that store a placeholder `raw_email = '{}'` with nothing real to retry. Resetting one of those rows to `'pending'` sent it through `PostCreator::handle()` with no attachments and no text, which then published anyway. `is_already_queued()` now only resets a `'failed'` row when its stored `raw_email` actually contains attachments or a description; a placeholder skip is left alone. `PostCreator::handle()` also gained an independent defensive backstop: an `agnosis_artwork` submission that reaches it with zero attachments and no description is now rejected outright rather than published empty, regardless of how it got there.

## [0.9.1] — 2026-07-07

### Fixed
- **The actual root cause behind "no valid image, audio, or video attachment found" on genuinely, correctly attached photos, found using the new debug tooling below**: `Inbox::query_messages()` deliberately builds its IMAP query with `fetchBody(false)` — headers only on the initial listing, so the cheap gates (admitted sender, throttle, auth) can reject a message before paying for a full body fetch. webklex's `Message` does not lazily fetch the body on its own, though: `getAttachments()`/`getTextBody()`/`getStructure()` simply return whatever was populated when the message object was built, and nothing in the pipeline ever explicitly triggered a follow-up fetch — so every IMAP submission's attachments and text body came back empty regardless of what the message actually contained. A first attempt at fixing this guarded a `Message::parseBody()` call on `null === getStructure()`, but this webklex version's query path (`Query::populate()`) always constructs a `Structure` object up front — even from an empty raw body when the body wasn't fetched — so `getStructure()` is never actually null here; that guard silently never fired, confirmed via a body-fetch diagnostic log line showing the structure was already non-null (just empty) before `parseBody()` was ever attempted. The real signal that the body was never fetched is a `Structure` with zero parts — even the simplest single-part email always produces at least one `Part` once real content has been parsed, so zero parts only happens when there was no real content behind it. `Email\Parser::parse_imap_message()` now checks for that instead (`null === $structure || empty( $structure->parts )`) before calling `parseBody()`. The declared-Content-Type fallback added earlier in this same file remains in place as a real safety net, but could never have mattered on its own — until this fix, no attachment was ever reached for it to fall back on.
- **The work-submission address footer (`EmailFooter::html()`/`plain_text()`) was nearly unreadable and gave no indication of what each address actually did** — a single inline line at 11px, `color:#ccc`/`#bbb` against a white background, with just a label and address (e.g. "Replace: replace@example.art") and no explanation of what sending mail there accomplishes. `ADDRESS_OPTIONS` now pairs each address with a one-line description; `html()` renders each address on its own line (label, `mailto:` link, description underneath) at 13px with real contrast (`#555`/`#888` text, `#7c6af7` links) instead of one low-contrast inline row; `plain_text()` gained the same descriptions, one address per line. The four email templates in `Publishing\Notification` that render `EmailFooter::html()` no longer wrap it in the old low-contrast `<p>` — the block is now self-styled and placed directly in the footer, set off with a top border. Also took the opportunity to scale up body text across all four templates (roughly 15–19px depending on role, up from 13–17px; the artwork title heading is now 26px, up from 22px) since it read too small throughout, not just in the footer.
- **Dates rendered by any `core/post-date` block (artwork, biography, event pages, the newsletter archive, anywhere else one is used) never actually adapted their structure to the current language** — the theme hardcodes a `date()`-style format (e.g. `j F Y`), and WordPress only translates the month/day NAME tokens within that fixed pattern, never the surrounding word order or connector words a given language actually needs (Portuguese/Spanish "de", German's trailing period, Russian's genitive month case). Reported 2026-07-07: a Russian artwork page showed a structurally English-shaped date. New `Agnosis\Core\DateFormatter`, hooked to WordPress's `render_block_core/post-date` filter (applies to every rendered `core/post-date` block site-wide, confirmed against WordPress core's own `render_block_{$this->name}` filter tag), swaps in a genuinely locale-native long date via PHP's `IntlDateFormatter` (CLDR-backed — correct for any locale with zero per-language maintenance) when the `intl` extension is available, falling back to WordPress's own `date_i18n()`/`date_format` option otherwise — the same soft-dependency pattern already used for Imagick elsewhere in this plugin. Only the human-visible date text is replaced; the block's own wrapper classes/styles and an "isLink" `<a>` wrapper, if present, are preserved exactly as WordPress rendered them.
- **The translated artwork subtitle (the AI-generated site-language title shown under the artist's own-language title on the single artwork page) was nearly invisible** — `Artist\Profile::render_artwork_title()` colored it with `var(--wp--preset--color--secondary)`, which `agnosis-theme`'s `theme.json` defines as a ~6%-opacity background wash, not a text color; against the dark header this rendered as barely-there dark-on-dark. The theme's own established pattern for legible-but-muted text over that same dark header (post-date block, breadcrumb, pagination) is full-strength `--foreground`/`--primary` at reduced opacity, not a separate low-alpha color token — `render_artwork_title()` now uses `var(--wp--preset--color--foreground)` at 0.75 opacity (higher than the 0.4–0.5 used for incidental chrome like breadcrumbs, since this is actual translated content) and bumped the font-size one step (`small` → `medium`).
- **The review email's body preview was never back-translated into the artist's own language** — only the AI-generated site title and excerpt were (`Notification::on_post_drafted()`), leaving the actual body text in the site's primary language regardless of the artist's locale. A Spanish-speaking artist reviewing a submission on an English-primary site saw a Spanish title/excerpt but an English body preview, with no way to actually read what they were about to approve. `on_post_drafted()` now back-translates the same trimmed preview `build_email()` shows (not the full body, to keep this one short AI call) via the existing `SubmissionTranslator`, using the same "only when the artist's locale differs from the site's" gate the title/excerpt back-translation already uses.

### Added
- **Centralised debug-file workflow for the email intake pipeline**, following the same shape as Lingua Forge's `TranslationDebug` — needed after the fix above still left a genuine JPG/PNG rejected as "no valid image, audio, or video attachment found" with no visible trace of why. New `Agnosis\Core\Debug`: resolves on/off via `AGNOSIS_DEBUG` constant → `agnosis_debug_enabled` option → off, writes timestamped `.txt` dumps to `wp-content/agnosis-debug/` (filterable via `agnosis_debug_dir`, `.htaccess`-guarded like the uploads-adjacent debug directories elsewhere in this project's ecosystem), and exposes file-count/clear helpers. New "Debug logging" checkbox and Debug Files panel (directory, file count, Clear Debug Files button) added to Settings → General.
- **Deep tracing wired through every stage of email intake** so a rejected or lost submission is fully diagnosable from the debug directory without reproducing it live: `Email\Parser::parse_imap_message()` now dumps the message's raw MIME part tree straight from webklex's own structure parser (type/subtype/disposition/filename/name/`isAttachment()` per part) *and* a full per-attachment trace of `getAttachments()`'s own filtering (sniffed vs. declared MIME, disposition, size, accept/reject reason) — the two together show whether a missing attachment was dropped by webklex's own `Part::isAttachment()` filtering (before this class ever sees it) or by this class's MIME allowlist/size cap. `AI\MediaAdapter::adapt()` dumps its input/output attachment lists (including anything dropped for an unmatched MIME type). `Publishing\PostCreator::handle()` dumps the decoded queue-row submission shape (post type, attachment count/filenames/mimes, description length) on entry. `Email\Inbox`'s "no valid attachments" skip also writes a companion pointer file so the matching `parser-attachments-*` dump for that UID is easy to find in a directory listing.

## [0.9.0] — 2026-07-07

### Fixed
- **Submitting the join form with a non-default language (e.g. Spanish) silently fell back to English everywhere** — the acknowledgment email went out untranslated and the WP user created on admission got the site's default locale instead of the artist's own. Root cause: the join form's `<form novalidate>` plus zero client-side validation meant `language` could reach the server empty, and `Admission::apply()` accepted or blanked it rather than rejecting. `language` is now a hard-required REST arg (`'required' => true`) and `apply()` returns 400 `agnosis_language_required` for an empty or unrecognized value; `JoinPage`/`blocks/join/frontend.js` gained matching client-side validation (`languageRequired` message, `firstInvalidField()` checks display_name/email/language before submit) so the same problem can no longer originate from the one form that feeds this whole pipeline.
- **The Inbox admin page could mislabel a legitimate, registered artist's submission as "unregistered sender"**, and separately show a false "not admitted" rejection for an artist who plainly was admitted — both traced to `Inbox::mark_no_artwork()` discarding the sender's `artist_id` and collapsing every skip reason (unregistered, not-admitted, throttled, auth-failed, no-attachments, goodbye variants) into one generic message. `mark_no_artwork()` now takes and persists the real `artist_id` plus a specific `$reason` (new `SKIP_REASONS` map), threaded through every call site, so the admin log always reflects what actually happened.
- **A multi-image gallery submission's quality gate only ever evaluated the first photo** — a second or third image with a low quality score in the same email was silently kept (or, worse, a bad first image rejected the whole submission even when the other photos were fine). `PostCreator::apply_quality_gate()` now scores every image independently: images below the threshold are dropped individually and logged; the whole submission is only rejected when every image fails.
- **The application-received and application-declined emails showed a footer of work-submission addresses** (artwork@, bio@, replace@, etc.) that don't apply yet — the recipient hasn't been admitted and has no way to use them. Both emails no longer include that footer; it still appears, correctly, on every email sent to an existing artist.

### Added
- **Configurable "what happens next" page after a successful join-form submission.** New Settings → Network field, "After applying, send artists to" (`agnosis_join_success_url`) — when set, a successful application redirects the artist to that page instead of just showing an inline confirmation message; blank keeps the previous inline-only behavior.
- **Artists are now notified by email when a submission is silently dropped for having no usable file** — previously both failure modes (a photo pasted/inlined instead of properly attached, and every attachment failing to convert into something the pipeline can use) left the artist with no idea their email never went anywhere. New `agnosis_submission_no_attachment` action, fired from `Inbox` and from `PostCreator::handle()`, and a new `Notification::on_submission_no_attachment()` email explaining both possible causes and how to resend correctly.
- **HEIC/HEIF support — the default photo format on modern iPhones.** Previously silently rejected at intake. `Email\Parser` now allowlists `image/heic`, `image/heif`, and their `-sequence` (burst/Live Photo) variants; new `MediaAdapter::adapt_heic()` converts to JPEG via Imagick (primary frame only for a sequence) before anything reaches the AI vision pipeline, which doesn't accept HEIC/HEIF natively. Degrades gracefully — via the same `extension_loaded('imagick')` guard already used for PDF rasterization — when Imagick isn't installed, or when it is but its ImageMagick build lacks the `libheif` delegate (a common partial-install case); either way the artist gets the same "couldn't process your photo" notification above rather than a silent drop.
- **The application-received acknowledgment and welcome/admitted emails are now styled HTML**, matching every other outgoing email's branded card layout (`EmailBranding::header_html()`, consistent header/body/footer chrome) instead of plain text.

### Changed
- **The welcome email no longer leads with a password-reset link as the main call to action.** Working with Agnosis — submitting, editing, or removing work — is entirely email-based and needs no WordPress login at all. The email now mentions password recovery only as a low-key, opt-in note at the very end, pointing at WordPress's own self-service "Forgot your password?" flow (`wp_lostpassword_url()`) for artists who want the optional online features (like previewing a submission before it publishes) — rather than baking in a single-use, pre-generated reset-key link that implied logging in was part of the normal flow.
- **Artwork submission authentication clarified**: an inbound submission is identified purely by matching the message's From address against an admitted artist's WordPress account email (`get_user_by( 'email', ... )`) — there is no token, signature, or secret in the loop. Optional SPF/DKIM verification (Settings → Email, `agnosis_require_email_auth`) and per-sender throttling (`RateLimiter::check_sender()`) sit in front of that match as opt-in hardening against a spoofed From header, but neither is required by default. Documented as part of this session's review of the intake flow; no code change was required, since this was already the intended design.

## [0.8.2] — 2026-07-06

### Fixed
- **A second, independent cause of the "Sending…" freeze fixed in 0.8.1, found while verifying that fix on a live site: the `agnosis_send_newsletter_queue` cron event itself was not scheduled at all** (`wp cron event run agnosis_send_newsletter_queue` failed with "Invalid cron event") — so the queue had never been processed even once, let alone reconciled. The only code path that registers this event, `schedule_events()`, previously ran only from `activate()` or a version-bump-gated `maybe_upgrade()` — so if it's ever lost for a reason unrelated to a version bump (a host's cron-table cleanup, a manual `wp cron event delete`, a migration between servers), nothing would notice or recover until the next plugin update. New `Activator::ensure_newsletter_cron_scheduled()` is called unconditionally from the Newsletter dashboard on every page view, so a missing cron event self-heals the same way a stuck status now does.

## [0.8.1] — 2026-07-06

### Fixed
- **A newsletter issue could get stuck showing "Sending…" (Send Now disabled) forever, even well past the next scheduled cron tick.** `QueueProcessor::process()`'s per-recipient send loop had no exception handling — if `send_one()` threw for any single recipient (a bad locale render, a branding/image error building that particular email, etc.), the uncaught error killed the entire cron tick before reaching `reconcile_sending_issues()`, which runs once per tick after the loop. That meant *every* currently-"sending" issue, not just the one that errored, silently stopped being reconciled — indefinitely, since the exact same failure recurred on every subsequent tick before ever reaching the reconcile step. `send_one()` is now wrapped in a try/catch per recipient: a failure is logged and that row is retried/eventually marked terminally 'failed' exactly as a normal `wp_mail()` failure already was, and reconciliation always runs regardless of what happened to any individual recipient.
- **The Newsletter Status dashboard (Settings → Newsletter) now self-heals a stuck "Sending…" status the moment an admin views the page**, instead of only reflecting reality on WP-Cron's next tick. On a low-traffic install with no real system cron wired to `wp-cron.php`, that tick may not happen again for a long time. `QueueProcessor::reconcile_sending_issues()` is now public and called at the top of `render_newsletter_dashboard()` — cheap (a few `COUNT` queries), a no-op when nothing is actually "sending".

## [0.8.0] — 2026-07-06

### Added
- **Front-end correction for artists — Phase 1 of the third audit's §7 feasibility evaluation.** Admitted artists can now correct post content on the three CPTs, the artwork excerpt, and an event's location/date directly on the published page — no intake email, no dashboard, no forms. New `Artist\ContentEditor`: `POST /agnosis/v1/content/{id}/text` (`{ field, value }`). Authorization mirrors `ReviewEndpoints`'s existing pattern: logged in, `Admission::is_admitted_artist()`, `post_author === get_current_user_id()` (admins bypass via `manage_options`), post type in an allowlist, status `publish`. A conditionally-enqueued overlay script (`blocks/content-editor/frontend.js`) appears only on a singular page the current viewer may edit — decorating `[data-agnosis-edit-field]` regions (written by new `the_content`/`the_excerpt` filters and by `Profile`'s event render callbacks) with a pencil affordance, `contentEditable`, and a floating Save/Cancel pair.
- **Front-end correction is restricted to the artist's own declared language — never a free language switcher** (audit §7c, reassessed 2026-07-06 after re-checking Lingua Forge's actual translation direction — see that day's audit update for the full reasoning). An artist may only edit the post version whose `_lf_lang` matches their own WP user `locale` (already captured at admission, `Admission::apply()`/`iso_to_wp_locale()` — no new field needed). On save: the edit is persisted verbatim to that post; if it isn't the primary-language post, the edit is translated into the primary language via Agnosis's own `AI\SubmissionTranslator` (the same tool `build_title_translations()` already uses for primary → other title translations — deliberately not Lingua Forge's `linguaforge_trigger_translation()`/`ChunkTranslation`, which operate on the whole post and would re-translate fields the artist didn't touch) and written directly to the linked primary post (found via `linguaforge_get_translations()`); the primary post is then fanned out to every other configured language via the existing debounced dispatch, **excluding the artist's own source language**, which already holds their exact words and must not be re-derived by a double round-trip. `Compat\LinguaForge` gained a static `schedule_fanout( $post_id, $exclude_langs = [] )` (self-contained — doesn't require the single live `LinguaForge` instance) and `locale_to_lang()` is now public.
- **Biography edits also update `_agnosis_artist_prompt`** (using the primary-language text when the edit originated in a non-primary language), so the next emailed bio update AI-merges against the corrected text instead of resurrecting whatever the correction just fixed.
- **`'revisions'` added to the `agnosis_artwork`, `agnosis_biography`, and `agnosis_event` CPTs' `supports` array** — every front-end correction becomes a WordPress revision automatically (via `wp_update_post()`), giving admins free undo and an audit trail with no extra code (audit §7c "safety rails").
- Corrections are rate-limited to 30 saves per artist per hour (`RateLimiter::check_sender()`, reused rather than reinvented) and logged via `Logger`.
- **Front-end photo substitution — Phase 2 of the same feasibility evaluation.** Admitted artists can replace the featured image (biography/event) or a specific gallery image (artwork) with a direct upload: `POST /agnosis/v1/content/{id}/photo`, multipart `{ file, attachment_id? }`. Reuses the exact same authorization as Phase 1 (`ContentEditor::check_access()` — own post, own language, admin bypass, rate limit) and the exact same media-library conventions the AI pipeline already uses: `Publishing\PostCreator::upload_media()` (now public) runs the upload through the real `wp_handle_sideload()`/MIME-sniffing path, no new upload code duplicated. Deliberately skips the AI pipeline entirely — no enhancement, no quality gate; a direct replacement is the artist's deliberate choice, the same `photo_only` semantics `PostCreator` already encodes for `photo@` submissions.
- **The replaced photo is never deleted.** It's marked as the new attachment's `_agnosis_original_attachment_id` and flagged `_agnosis_is_original` — the identical provenance-meta pair the AI-enhancement path already uses for its pre-enhancement sidecar — so it stays recoverable for a future "restore original photo" one-click (Phase 3).
- **Photo replacement propagates to every language version of the post synchronously, with no AI call and no deferred dispatch.** Images are language-neutral (audit §7c), so `_thumbnail_id`/`_agnosis_gallery_ids` are copied directly to every post in the same `linguaforge_get_translations()` group the moment the upload completes, rather than going through the text-edit translate-then-fan-out pipeline.
- The overlay decorates the featured image on all three CPTs via a new `post_thumbnail_html` filter (covers both classic and FSE/core `post-featured-image`-block themes uniformly); clicking the pencil opens a native file picker and uploads immediately. Artwork gallery images beyond the featured one are reachable via the same endpoint's `attachment_id` param, but the overlay doesn't yet decorate them individually — left as a fast-follow.
- **Artwork title editing with dual-title handling — Phase 3 of the same feasibility evaluation.** `title` (→ `post_title`) added to the editable-field allowlist for artwork and biography. Artwork's `post_title` is the artist's own words and, by design (`Compat\LinguaForge::hold_artist_title()`), must stay byte-identical on every language version — never translated, the same as a photo. So a title edit runs through a new `ContentEditor::propagate_title()` instead of the normal translate-then-fan-out path: the literal new title is copied verbatim and synchronously to every sibling post in the `linguaforge_get_translations()` group (no AI call, exactly like the photo swap), while the *separate* AI-translated display title (`_agnosis_translated_title`, the subtitle `agnosis/artwork-title` renders) is regenerated independently — translated into the primary language via `AI\SubmissionTranslator` and stored on the primary post, then the *existing* deferred dispatch (`LinguaForge::schedule_fanout()`, unchanged) rebuilds `_agnosis_title_i18n` and refreshes each sibling's own display title the next time it's (re)translated — no new Lingua Forge hook needed. Biography's title has no dual-title system (LF already translates it normally) and reuses the Phase 1 content-style propagation unchanged. `Profile::render_artwork_title()` and a new `the_title` filter (`ContentEditor::decorate_title()`, scoped to the singular main-query post) expose the pencil affordance on the artist's own title; empty titles are rejected (400).
- **"Restore original photo" one-click — the other half of Phase 3.** `POST /agnosis/v1/content/{id}/photo/restore` swaps the current attachment back to whichever one it recorded as its `_agnosis_original_attachment_id` when it was replaced (Phase 2) — no upload, a pure re-pointing via the existing `swap_photo_everywhere()`. The provenance pointer is reversed rather than deleted, so a second restore call undoes the first: nothing Phase 2 already preserved is ever thrown away by this action either. The overlay shows a "Restore earlier photo" action on any photo with a recorded original.
- An optional, explicit "refresh the AI description for the new photo?" action (audit §7c — never automatic) remains deferred: it would need to run through `AI\Pipeline::process()`'s full submission shape (subject/body translation, MediaAdapter routing), which is a heavier integration than a same-cycle fast-follow warranted. Decorating individual artwork gallery images beyond the featured one (the REST endpoints already accept any `attachment_id` in the gallery) is also still a fast-follow, not part of this release.
- **Newsletter archive / "view in browser" — third audit's §8 roadmap item.** Every sent public issue already stores its fully-rendered HTML in `agnosis_newsletter_issues`, so a public archive was nearly free to add. New `Newsletter\Archive` registers two front-end routes with no new CPT/table: `GET /newsletter/` (paginated index, newest first) and `GET /newsletter/{id}/` (a single issue's permalink). Both are `newsletter_type = 'public' AND status = 'sent'` only — an artist-type issue (open community votes, new-member names; see `Digest::build_artist()`) 404s exactly like a nonexistent one, the same as any other issue ID that doesn't match that filter. The single-issue view best-effort matches the visitor's current `get_locale()` against the issue's per-locale `locale_content` map, falling back to the issue's base (default-locale) render — the same fallback `QueueProcessor` already uses for a recipient. Both routes render via `wp_die()`, not a raw echo+exit, matching the convention every other "render a page and stop" flow in this plugin already follows (`SubscriptionConfirm`/`VouchConfirm`/`ReviewConfirm`) — chosen specifically so Archive stays testable via the `wp_die_handler` filter.
- `Mailer::build_email()`'s branded card markup was split into a new `Mailer::build_body()` fragment (no doctype/head/body) so Archive's single-issue page can reuse the exact same visual design while still going through `wp_die()` for its own document wrapper. Every sent email also gained a small "Having trouble viewing this email? View it online." banner linking to `Archive::issue_permalink()` — public issues only, never artist ones — and the footer now shows "Subscribe to get these by email" instead of a broken "Unsubscribe" link when there's no recipient to unsubscribe (the archive page reusing the same markup with `$unsubscribe_url = null`).
- The newsletter signup block now shows a "See past issues" link to the archive once `Scheduler::last_sent_at('public')` confirms at least one issue has ever gone out.
- Existing installs pick up the new `/newsletter/` rewrite rules automatically: `Activator::maybe_upgrade()` now defers a one-time `flush_rewrite_rules()` to `init` (same pattern already used there for `create_managed_pages()`), so no manual permalink resave is needed after upgrading.
- **Locale coverage metric — third audit's §8 roadmap item.** The Newsletter dashboard's Public row now shows a "By language" breakdown of confirmed subscribers (e.g. "Spanish (12), French (5), Unknown (2)") — a cheap signal for which Lingua Forge languages actually earn their AI translation spend, now that §3c (the signup block's missing `language` param) has been fixed since 0.4.3 and `locale` is reliably captured at signup. New `Subscriber::counts_by_locale()` (confirmed-only, `GROUP BY locale`) backs it; `Admin\Settings::locale_label()` resolves a WP locale to a human-readable name via Lingua Forge's own `linguaforge_language_label()` when LF is active (guarded by `function_exists()`, same convention as the rest of `Compat\LinguaForge`), falling back to the raw locale code otherwise. A subscriber with no recorded locale is labelled "Unknown" rather than dropped, so the breakdown always sums to the existing confirmed-subscriber total.
- **Newsletter signup gained the same language selector the join form already has.** The `agnosis/newsletter-signup` block now renders a `<select name="language">` sourced from the same `AI\SubmissionTranslator::language_names()` list `Artist\JoinPage` uses, giving visitors an explicit way to pick their language instead of the block's previous entirely-invisible auto-detect. Deliberately looser than the join form's version: not `required`, no disabled placeholder — `frontend.js` pre-selects whatever `document.documentElement.lang` reports for the current page (the same signal the old auto-detect used) and the visitor can change it before submitting. A wrong or blank choice here is low-stakes and self-correcting (worst case, a digest renders in the site's default-locale fallback until noticed), unlike the join form's language choice, which an artist must confirm explicitly since Lingua Forge may not actually support it. `Newsletter\Subscription`'s REST endpoint gained the same defensive whitelist re-check `Admission::apply()` already has for its own language param — a submitted code outside `language_names()` is silently dropped rather than trusted.
- **Vision-input images are now downscaled before being sent to the AI for description**, a pure cost/latency optimisation: vision-API token cost scales with resolution, and describing a piece of art needs nowhere near the pixel count of the actual published photo. New setting **AI → "Vision image max width (px)"** (`agnosis_ai_vision_max_width_px`, default 800, set to 0 to disable) controls the target width; new `MediaAdapter::maybe_downscale_for_vision()` resizes proportionally with Imagick (never upscales; falls back to sending the original image unmodified if Imagick is unavailable, the source is already narrower than the configured max, or the image data is unreadable) and is called from `Anthropic::describe()` and `OpenAI::describe()` immediately before base64-encoding the request body. Deliberately **not** wired into `MediaAdapter::adapt()`/`adapt_pdf()`/`adapt_video()` themselves — the attachment data those methods return is reused downstream for AI image enhancement and as the actual published artwork/video-poster file, so downscaling it there would have silently shrunk published images instead of just the copy sent for description. Covers all three image-to-vision routes uniformly (plain image attachments, rasterised PDF pages, extracted video poster frames), since all three already converge on `ProviderInterface::describe()`.
- **Artist-facing emails now mention front-end correction (§7's "your work, your corner" idea, scoped down from the original newsletter-personalization proposal in the audit's §8 roadmap once we established there's no dedicated per-artist newsletter to hang it on — see that day's audit discussion).** New `EmailFooter::edit_reminder_plain_text( $artist_id )` / `edit_reminder_html( $artist_id )` sit alongside the existing work-address summary in the same shared class, but are gated per-recipient rather than shown unconditionally: a private `has_published_work()` checks `count_user_posts()` across all three CPTs and returns `''` until that specific artist has at least one published artwork, biography, or event, since the pencil-edit overlay (Phase 1, above) has nothing to decorate before then. Wired into `Notification`'s pre-publish review, removal-confirmation, and photo-quality-rejected emails (artist_id threaded through each `build_*_email()` for the gate), `AdmissionNotification`'s per-artist admission-vote email, `DepartureNotification`'s reinstatement and removal-vote emails, and `CommunityCapNotification`'s vote-opened email. Deliberately **not** added to the suspension email — `Departure::apply_ban()` actually removes the `agnosis_artist` role for the ban's duration, which is the same capability `ContentEditor::check_access()` requires, so the reminder would be false for exactly as long as that email applies; it reappears in the reinstatement email once access is restored. Also skipped: the welcome/admission email and pre-admission applicant emails (nothing published yet, almost by definition) and the BCC'd community-expiry notice (one shared body across many recipients, no single artist to gate on).
- **Password recovery for artists — gap found while reviewing the login/admission flow.** `SubmissionsPage`'s themed inline login form (`wp_login_form()`) never included a "Lost your password?" link — a WordPress core omission for that function, unlike the full `wp-login.php` page — and it was the *only* login surface anywhere in the plugin or theme, so an artist who forgot their password had no discoverable way back in short of already knowing the unlinked `wp-login.php?action=lostpassword` URL exists. Added a "Forgot your password?" link (`wp_lostpassword_url()`) beneath the inline form. Also added new `Core\LoginBranding`, hooked alongside `FrontendAccess`: since "Lost your password?"/"Reset password" necessarily leave the themed front-end page and land on stock `wp-login.php`, it replaces the WordPress logo/link with the site's own (reusing the configured email logo, `agnosis_email_logo_id`, when set) and restyles the submit button and links to match the rest of the site rather than leaving the one unbranded screen in the whole flow.
- **"Invite an Artist" — a new, deliberately simple way to invite a prospective artist by email, independent of the newsletter system.** New `Artist\Invitation`, a small card on Settings → Newsletter below the existing Newsletter Status dashboard: an admin enters one email address, picks a language, and sends immediately — no list, no queue, no recipient tracking (mirrors `Scheduler::send_test()`'s "fire and forget" shape rather than the newsletter's DB-backed audience/queue). Includes its own "Send Test" (identical content, `[TEST]`-prefixed subject, same convention as the newsletter dashboard's test sends). The email body is a standing, admin-editable intro (new **Invitation intro** setting, pre-populated with starter copy describing what Agnosis is and how artists work with it — unlike the newsletter's one-shot intro fields, this one isn't cleared after sending) followed by a fixed "Apply to join" button linking to the real `/join/` page (resolved from `agnosis_join_page_id`, the page `Activator::create_join_page()` recorded, with a same-slug fallback). Language selection works like the newsletter's own admin-intro localisation: the chosen language switches the template's own locale (`switch_to_locale()`, picking up a matching `.mo` when one exists) and the free-text intro itself is machine-translated via the site's configured AI provider when the target isn't the site's source language — falling back to the untranslated original when no provider is configured, the same graceful degradation used everywhere else this pattern appears.

## [0.7.3] — 2026-07-05

### Fixed
- **Artist-subdomain links dropped the visitor's current language.** `SubdomainRouter::url_for_artist()` and `SubdomainNavigation::portal_home_url()` always built bare source-language URLs (`https://slug.base`), regardless of the page the visitor was actually on. On a translated page (e.g. `ourartist.agnosis.art/fr/...`), this meant the artist-name breadcrumb link and the "back to Agnosis" Site Logo/Site Title link both dropped the visitor back to the English root instead of staying on `/fr/`. Added `Compat\LinguaForge::current_lang_path_prefix()` — resolves the current request's language from LF's `LF_LANG` constant (via `linguaforge_source_language()` for the source-language comparison) and returns a joinable `/xx` path segment, or `''` when Lingua Forge isn't active or the current language already is the source language. Wired into both URL builders; as a side effect this also fixes the same latent bug in `gallery-overview/render.php`'s artist links, since they share `url_for_artist()`.

## [0.7.2] — 2026-07-05

### Fixed
- **Gallery-overview block's pagination could disagree with what it actually rendered, on sites using "Your latest posts" as the homepage.** The block built its artist/artwork pool via raw SQL and per-artist `get_posts()` calls with no language filtering of its own, computing `$agnosis_max_pages` from that unfiltered pool — while Lingua Forge's `handle_secondary_pre_get_posts()` hook silently language-filtered only the final by-ID fetch. Translated posts counted toward the page total but never rendered. Fixed by explicitly filtering all three `get_posts()` calls (featured artwork, extra/remaining, final by-ID fetch) in `blocks/gallery-overview/render.php` by `_lf_lang` against the current request's `LF_LANG` constant, gated on `Compat\LinguaForge::is_active()`, so pagination math and rendered content are now always computed from the same pool. The distinct-authors discovery query is deliberately left unfiltered by language — it only determines which artists have any published artwork at all, so no artist is dropped from a language's pool for lack of translations yet.

## [0.7.1] — 2026-07-05

### Fixed
- **Email logo could render far smaller than configured.** `Core\EmailBranding::header_html()` requested the logo at WordPress's `'large'` size — a 1024×1024 *bounding box* WordPress never upscales past. For a wide banner-style logo, the generated `'large'` file could already be shorter than the configured display height before the `max-height` CSS cap even applied, silently undercutting it. Switched to `'full'`, the attachment's actual native resolution, so the cap always has real headroom to work from.
- **Newsletter subscription-confirmation email (`Newsletter\Subscription.php`) predated `EmailBranding` entirely.** It was missed when the shared email-branding system landed in 0.6.4 and still hardcoded its own plain-text "✦ Site Name" header, old purple color, old padding. Now calls `EmailBranding::header_html()` like every other outgoing email and matches the rest of this changelog entry's changes.

### Changed
- **Email logo height raised to 150px** (was 40px) so a full banner-style logo (wordmark + tagline baked into the image, not just an icon) actually fits, instead of being compressed to the point of illegibility.
- **Email header background changed from purple to the same dark colour used on the website** (`#0d0d12`, the theme's own "Background" palette colour) — across all five outgoing HTML email templates (submission review, removal confirmation, rejection notice, subscription confirmation, newsletter digest). Buttons, links, and border accents elsewhere in these emails are unaffected — only the header bar itself changed, via a new `$header_bg` variable kept separate from the existing `$accent` used for interactive elements.
- **Logo now sits on its own white panel inside the header**, fixed at 552px — the same width as the email body content below (600px card − 24px padding each side) — so it lines up edge-to-edge with the content beneath it. Needed because the newly-created logo file has a white background baked in rather than a transparent one, which didn't render cleanly against the new dark header.
- **Reduced left/right padding from 40px to 24px** in every header, body, and footer cell across all five templates, giving the content more usable width within the same 600px email card.

## [0.7.0] — 2026-07-05

### Added
- **Genuine sound and video submission support.** Previously "supported" only in name — the intake `Email\Parser` MIME allowlist blocked all audio/video before anything else could run, and even the description code that did exist would have discarded the actual video file. Now: `Parser::ALLOWED_MIME` accepts 8 audio and 6 video MIME types with type-appropriate size caps (20MB image / 50MB audio / 150MB video); `AI\MediaAdapter::adapt_video()` extracts a poster frame via ffmpeg when available (never drops the original video if it isn't); `AI\Pipeline::process_video_single()` describes the poster frame with the same vision call used for images, falling back to a text-only description from the artist's message when no frame is available; `Publishing\PostCreator` uploads the real audio/video binary through the same Media Library path as images and publishes it with native `core/audio`/`core/video` blocks (zero theme support required), using a video's poster frame as the post's featured thumbnail. Quality-rejection and AI enhancement never apply to audio/video — both are always published as submitted, described only, never altered.
- **Artist Guide: new "Sound and video" section** explaining that audio/video attachments are sent the same way as images, how AI describes them, and that the file itself is always published untouched.
- **External links become `wp:embed` blocks.** When an artist's message contains a link — typically a video too large to email — to an allowlisted platform (YouTube, Vimeo, Dailymotion, SoundCloud, Bandcamp, Archive.org), `PostCreator::build_external_link_embeds()` appends it as a native embed block at the bottom of the post. Deliberately allowlist-only, not a content classifier: this pipeline has no way to inspect what a linked page actually shows, so "reject commercial/adult sites" is achieved structurally by only ever trusting a short, maintained list of known platforms rather than trying to detect what to exclude. Extensible via the `agnosis_embed_host_allowlist` filter. Capped at 3 embeds per submission.

## [0.6.4] — 2026-07-05

### Added
- **Email logo setting.** New `Agnosis\Core\EmailBranding::header_html()` renders the header of every outgoing HTML email — the three `Publishing\Notification` templates (submission ready to review, removal confirmation, quality-rejection) and both `Newsletter\Mailer` digests (artist + public). Settings → General gains an "Email logo" media-library picker (`agnosis_email_logo_id`, new `media` field type in `Admin\Settings`, backed by `wp.media()`); when set, the logo replaces the plain "✦ Site Name" text wordmark everywhere at once, capped at 40px tall regardless of the image's own dimensions. Falls back to the text wordmark when nothing is configured, so this is a no-op until an operator picks an image.
- **Work-emails footer on artist-facing notifications.** New `Agnosis\Core\EmailFooter` builds a one-line summary of every configured work-submission address (Settings → Email: artwork, biography, events, replace, remove, promote, photo-only) with real `mailto:` links in the HTML templates. Wired into `Publishing\Notification`'s three templates, `Artist\AdmissionNotification` (application acknowledgment, expiry notices, vote-request emails), `Artist\DepartureNotification` (ban/reinstatement notices, community removal-vote emails), and `Artist\CommunityCapNotification` (cap-vote emails) — everywhere except the goodbye/self-removal confirmation email and anything Newsletter-related, and except the welcome email (which already lists every alias address in full). Skips addresses that are blank or invalid, and disappears entirely when nothing is configured.
- **Artist Guide: photo-only lane isn't just for photographers.** Added a paragraph clarifying that any artist, in any medium, can send through the photo address (or `[Photo]` indicator) whenever they don't want AI touching the image representing their piece — verified against `PostCreator::resolve_indicator()`, which treats `photo_only` purely as a routing flag independent of what the artwork actually is.

### Fixed
- **Artist Guide wrongly implied someone other than the artist reviews and approves a submission.** "You will receive an email when your piece is reviewed and published" read as if a third party makes the publish decision — in reality the artist themselves gets the review email with Approve/Discard links (`Publishing\Notification::on_post_drafted()`) and is the only one who decides. Corrected to say so explicitly.

## [0.6.3] — 2026-07-05

### Added
- **`agnosis/newsletter-popover` block — the subscribe trigger + popover chrome, now plugin-owned.** Previously this lived as theme markup (`agnosis-theme`'s `wp:html` trigger button, an anchored `wp:group` panel, and a `render_block_core/group` filter that added `popover="auto"` by regex). Moved here as `Agnosis\Newsletter\PopoverBlock`: a single self-contained dynamic block renders the trigger button, the native-Popover panel, and an `agnosis/newsletter-signup` form inside it (via `render_block()`, same as any other block would), and writes `popover="auto"` directly rather than patching it in after the fact. Any theme gets a working subscribe popover from one `<!-- wp:agnosis/newsletter-popover /-->`, with no CSS or PHP to reimplement. No-ops (renders nothing) when the public newsletter is disabled, same as `newsletter-signup` itself. Requires `agnosis-theme` 0.5.4+.
- **Trigger icon is now a block option instead of hardcoded markup.** `agnosis/newsletter-popover`'s Inspector panel gets a "Trigger icon" dropdown — Bell (default), Envelope, Star, or Lightning bolt — stored as the block's `icon` attribute and rendered server-side from a small fixed icon map (`PopoverBlock::ICONS`). Lets an operator pick something that won't visually blend into whatever sits next to it (e.g. Social Share icons) without editing CSS or the theme.

## [0.6.2] — 2026-07-05

### Changed
- **"Log in to view your submissions" form restyled and gained optional Turnstile protection.** `SubmissionsPage::render_login_form()` previously emitted `wp_login_form()` completely unstyled — labels and inputs sat inline, undersized. Added scoped CSS: username/password stack label-above-input on their own lines, inputs are full-width with larger padding/font-size, matching the Join/Subscribe forms' look.

### Added
- **Turnstile on the login form, scoped so it can't affect any other login on the site.** Since `wp_login_form()` posts straight to `wp-login.php` (WordPress core's own handler, not a plugin REST endpoint), the widget is injected via the `login_form_bottom` filter — added immediately before the call and removed immediately after — alongside a hidden `agnosis_login_source` marker. A new `authenticate` filter (priority 30, after WP's own credential check) only enforces verification when that marker is present, so wp-admin login, REST/XML-RPC auth, and any other login path are completely unaffected regardless of whether Turnstile is configured. No-op entirely until both Turnstile keys are set (Settings → General), same as the Join and Subscribe forms.

## [0.6.1] — 2026-07-05

### Fixed
- **Join form's "Auto-detect (browser language)" option removed — it could silently promise support for a language this site doesn't actually have.** Selecting it left the language blank, and `Admission::apply()` guessed a code from the visitor's `Accept-Language` header with no check against what Lingua Forge is actually configured for — an artist could end up "recorded" in a language nobody translates into. The dropdown now opens on a disabled "Select your language" placeholder and is `required`, so an artist must explicitly pick one of the languages this instance genuinely supports. `Admission::apply()` no longer guesses from the browser header at all, and defensively discards any submitted `language` not found in `SubmissionTranslator::language_names()` (a direct API call bypassing the form can't sneak one in either).

## [0.6.0] — 2026-07-05

### Changed
- **Join form's language list — and translation eligibility — now sourced entirely from Lingua Forge.** `SubmissionTranslator::language_names()` no longer maintains its own curated 28-language constant; it reads `linguaforge_languages()` / `linguaforge_language_label()` directly, so however many languages Lingua Forge is configured for on this site (Settings → Language Router) is exactly how many options the Join form offers — 3 configured means 3, 50 means 50. `resolve_language_name()` (used by the AI translation call and by back-translated notification emails) now reuses the same source, so the dropdown, the translation pipeline, and back-translation all agree on what's supported instead of three separately-maintained lists that could drift apart. Falls back to just the site's own locale when Lingua Forge isn't active. Still filterable via `agnosis_translation_languages`.

## [0.5.4] — 2026-07-04

### Added
- **Cloudflare Turnstile on the public Subscribe and Join forms.** New `Agnosis\Core\Turnstile` helper (widget markup, script loading, `siteverify` check) plus two Settings → General fields (site key, secret key).
