Opt-in by configuration — until both keys are set, `is_enabled()` is false and neither form's markup, assets, or REST validation change at all. Once configured, `agnosis/newsletter-signup` (0.3.1) and `agnosis/join` (0.2.1) render the widget before their submit button, and `/newsletter/subscribe` / `/admission/apply` reject the request server-side if the token is missing or fails verification. Both blocks' frontend.js read Cloudflare's auto-inserted `cf-turnstile-response` field and reset the widget on any error, since tokens are single-use.

## [0.5.3] — 2026-07-04

### Changed
- **`agnosis/artist-breadcrumb` name now links to the artist's own subdomain home.** `SubdomainNavigation::render_block()` wraps the artist's display name in an `<a href="...">` pointing at `SubdomainRouter::url_for_artist()`, so the breadcrumb doubles as a way back to the artist's home from any other page on their subdomain (an artwork, biography, or event single), not just an identifying label.

## [0.5.2] — 2026-07-04

### Added
- **Font weight and font family supports on `agnosis/artist-breadcrumb`.** `block.json`'s `typography` supports gains `fontWeight` and `fontFamily`, alongside the existing `fontSize` — both editable from the block's own Typography inspector panel, picking from the theme's defined font families.

### Changed
- **`agnosis/artist-breadcrumb` now renders a `<div>` instead of a `<p>`.** `SubdomainNavigation::render_block()`'s output tag changed; the `.agnosis-artist-breadcrumb` class (and any per-instance color/typography attributes) are unaffected, since they target the class/wrapper attributes rather than the tag itself.

## [0.5.1] — 2026-07-04

### Added
- **Styling options on `agnosis/artist-breadcrumb`.** `block.json` now declares `color` (text + background) and `typography` (font size) supports, so the block's own Color/Typography inspector panels are available in the Site Editor — no code change needed to restyle it per instance. `SubdomainNavigation::render_block()` applies whatever's picked via `get_block_wrapper_attributes()` on the wrapper `<p>`; anything left unset falls back to the theme's own `.agnosis-artist-breadcrumb` CSS, unchanged from 0.5.0.

## [0.5.0] — 2026-07-04

### Added
- **`agnosis/artist-breadcrumb` block.** A small dynamic block (`blocks/artist-breadcrumb/`, registered by the new `Agnosis\Network\SubdomainNavigation`) that renders `<p class="agnosis-artist-breadcrumb">` with the current artist's display name on an artist subdomain, and nothing at all on the main site. Reintroduces — outside the site title, as its own explicit element — the artist identification that `option_blogname` used to carry before 0.4.3 removed that filter. Any theme can drop the block in wherever it wants the artist identified, rather than reimplementing subdomain-detection itself; agnosis-theme (0.5.0) uses it directly below the header.

### Changed
- **Site Logo/Site Title portal-link fix moved from agnosis-theme into the plugin.** The `render_block_core/site-logo`/`render_block_core/site-title` filters that point those links at the main Agnosis domain on an artist subdomain (added to agnosis-theme in 0.4.1) are now `Agnosis\Network\SubdomainNavigation::link_to_portal()`, registered here instead. This was Agnosis-platform behaviour tied to `SubdomainRouter`, not anything specific to that theme's markup — any theme using core's Site Logo/Site Title blocks now gets the fix automatically, without needing its own copy of this logic.

## [0.4.3] — 2026-07-04

### Changed
- **Artist subdomains no longer replace the visible site title with the artist's name.** `SubdomainRouter` filtered `option_blogname` since 0.1.9 so `wp:site-title` showed the artist rather than "Agnosis" — in practice this left the header with no visible Agnosis branding at all and, combined with `wp:site-title`/`wp:site-logo` both linking to `home_url()` (which `rewrite_home()` already points at the artist subdomain), no way to navigate back to the main portal from an artist's page. The `option_blogname` filter is removed; `document_title_parts`/`wp_title` (the HTML `<title>`, used for the browser tab/SEO) still show the artist's name and are unaffected. The actual "no way back" problem is fixed on the theme side: agnosis-theme's `functions.php` now points the Site Logo and Site Title links at the main Agnosis domain (`agnosis_base_domain` option) instead of `home_url()` whenever `SubdomainRouter::is_artist_subdomain()` is true.

### Fixed
- **Email action links executed on a plain GET — corporate mail-security scanners could trigger them.** Every one-click link in the platform (`ReviewConfirm` review approve/reject/remove, `VouchConfirm` admission votes, `SubscriptionConfirm` newsletter confirm/unsubscribe for both the public list and artists) mutated state the instant its URL was fetched, at `template_redirect`. Link-scanning mail security layers (Outlook SafeLinks/ATP, Mimecast, Proofpoint, and similar) prefetch GET links in incoming email to scan them — which is indistinguishable, server-side, from the recipient actually clicking. A prefetch alone could consume a single-use review token (the artist's real click then shows "link expired or already used"), silently approve/reject/remove artwork, cast a community admission vote on the artist's behalf, or confirm/unsubscribe a newsletter recipient who never opened the email client. Fixed by splitting every one of these shims into two phases: a GET now only renders a themed confirm page naming the action, with a single POST button; the token travels in that form as a hidden field (never in the form's `action` URL, so it is not logged a second time), and the action itself — REST dispatch, vote recording, or subscriber status change — only runs once that POST arrives. Scanners issue GETs and never submit forms, so prefetching a link is now inert. `VouchConfirm` and `SubscriptionConfirm` also had their response pages moved from raw `echo`+`exit` onto `wp_die()` (matching `ReviewConfirm`'s existing pattern), which incidentally closes a testing gap noted in both suites and lets the whole GET/POST split be verified end-to-end; `VouchConfirm`'s error page also now correctly returns HTTP 400 (previously always 200), consistent with the other two shims.
- **The public newsletter signup block never sent the visitor's language, so per-locale rendering never applied to public subscribers.** `Subscription::register_routes()` has accepted a `language` param since 0.4.0 and correctly maps it to a WP locale via `Admission::iso_to_wp_locale()`, but the signup block's `frontend.js` only ever sent `{ email }` — there was no language field, and no other source for the value. Every public-list subscriber therefore had `locale = NULL`, silently resolving to the site default locale at send time and leaving 0.4.1's per-locale digest/intro rendering exercised only by the artist audience in practice. Fixed by having `frontend.js` send `document.documentElement.lang` (the primary subtag, lower-cased — `"es-ES"` becomes `"es"`, the same split-on-hyphen normalization `Admission::apply()` already applies to its `Accept-Language` fallback) as `language` in the subscribe payload. WordPress and Lingua Forge already set `<html lang="…">` per language version of a page, so a visitor subscribing from `/es/` or an `es` subdomain now gets the right locale for free, with no new form field and no server-side change.
- **The community removal-vote email link was completely dead — no handler was ever registered for it.** `DepartureNotification::removal_vote_url()` has generated `?agnosis_removal_vote=1&rid=…&vid=…&vote=…&token=…` links in removal-vote notification emails since the removal-vote feature shipped, but no `template_redirect` handler ever consumed that query string, and there was no other UI to cast a removal vote at all — every link 404'd (or rendered the homepage), silently disenfranchising the entire community on every removal vote. Fixed by adding `RemovalVoteConfirm`, a new email-link shim mirroring `VouchConfirm`'s stateless-HMAC-token pattern and its GET/POST split from day one (a GET renders a themed confirm page; the vote is only recorded on POST). `Departure::cast_vote()` was refactored to delegate to a new shared `record_vote_on_request()` method so the REST endpoint and the email-link shim share one validation path, the same relationship `Admission::record_vote()` already has with `VouchConfirm`.
- **A failed newsletter send was given up on after a single `wp_mail()` failure, with no retry.** `QueueProcessor::process()` marked a queue row `failed` the instant `wp_mail()` returned `false` — a transient SMTP hiccup or a momentary host outbound-rate-limit rejection permanently dropped that recipient from the issue, with no second chance and no visible distinction from a genuinely bad address. Fixed with a bounded retry: `agnosis_newsletter_queue` gains an `attempts` column, and a failed send now stays `pending` (so the next 5-minute cron tick retries it) until three attempts have failed, at which point it is marked terminally `failed` and `resolved_at` records the final-failure time. Existing installs get the column via a guarded `ALTER TABLE` in `Activator::maybe_upgrade()`.
- **No RFC 8058 one-click unsubscribe.** Newsletter mail set `List-Unsubscribe:` but not the paired `List-Unsubscribe-Post: List-Unsubscribe=One-Click` header, and the unsubscribe URL only handled GET — falling short of the RFC 8058 one-click flow that Gmail/Yahoo bulk-sender rules require above ~5k messages/day and that also feeds Gmail/Outlook's built-in "Unsubscribe" affordance and spam-folder placement at any scale. Fixed by adding the `List-Unsubscribe-Post` header to every send, and giving `SubscriptionConfirm` a third path alongside its existing GET-confirm/POST-act split (§2a): a bare POST whose body is the RFC 8058-mandated literal `List-Unsubscribe=One-Click` is recognized (it can only ever come from a mail client's own automated request, never from prefetch-vulnerable GET scanning) and acted on immediately, with no confirm page — reading action/type/token/uid from the URL's query string, since that's where a header-triggered request puts them rather than in the POST body. The *visible* body unsubscribe link a human clicks is untouched and still gets the §2a confirm-button page.
- **The newsletter subscribe endpoint let anyone probe whether an email address was on the list.** `Subscriber::subscribe()` returned a distinguishable `WP_Error` (HTTP 409) for an already-confirmed address versus a 201 for anything else, so a caller could enumerate subscribers by status code alone. Fixed by making every outcome — new, still-pending, or already-confirmed — return the same success shape and the same 201 response; only whether a confirmation email goes out differs (skipped entirely when already confirmed, since there's nothing left to confirm), and that's invisible to the caller.
- **Pending subscribers and their tokens never expired, and every resubmission resent a confirmation email.** A bot hitting the signup form (still bounded by the existing 5/IP/5min rate limit) could accumulate `pending` rows forever, each triggering its own confirmation email, with no cleanup. Fixed with two independent pieces of hygiene: (1) `Subscriber::expire_stale_pending()` deletes abandoned `pending` rows older than 14 days — piggybacked on the existing daily `agnosis_prepare_newsletters` cron (`Scheduler::prepare()`) rather than a new scheduled event — and never touches `confirmed`/`unsubscribed` rows; (2) resubscribing a still-pending address within a 5-minute cooldown now leaves the row and its token completely untouched (no fresh token, no repeat email) instead of resending every time, while a resubmission past the cooldown still resends normally with a fresh token. Both the age check and the cooldown check are done in SQL against MySQL's own `NOW()` rather than PHP's clock, so there's no timezone-mixing risk of the kind fixed separately below (§3e).
- **Newsletter scheduling mixed three different clocks.** `Scheduler::since_window()`'s never-sent-before fallback used `gmdate()` (true UTC) while every other path returns `sent_at` (a WP site-local wall-clock string, from `current_time('mysql')`) — so on a site with a non-zero UTC offset, the very first digest's content window was shifted against `post_date` (also site-local), and `is_due()`'s bare `strtotime($last_sent)` silently substituted PHP's own ini `date.timezone` for the site's actual configured WordPress timezone when converting back to a Unix epoch, double-converting the offset against `time()`. Fixed by keeping every scheduling timestamp on the one clock the rest of the pipeline (`post_date`, `resolved_at`) already uses — site-local — and using WP core's own `get_gmt_from_date()` (DST-correct, via `wp_timezone()`) for the one place an actual Unix-epoch comparison is needed (`is_due()`), instead of a bare `strtotime()`.
- **Four small hygiene nits.** The newsletter signup block's email `<label>` had no `for`/`id` association with its input, so screen readers had no programmatic link between them — fixed with a matching `id`/`for` pair. `agnosis_newsletter_queue`'s `sent_at` column was renamed to `resolved_at` — it was stamped on a terminal failure just as often as a real send, and the old name was misleading; existing installs get the rename via a guarded `ALTER TABLE`. `agnosis_newsletter_subscribers.email` was shortened from `VARCHAR(255)` to `VARCHAR(191)` — its `UNIQUE` index under `utf8mb4` exceeded the 767-byte limit on older MariaDB/MyISAM configurations; 191 (WordPress core's own long-standing convention for indexed email columns) stays safely under it everywhere. The `SubscriptionConfirm::render_page()` hardcoded-`lang="en"` nit turned out to already be resolved as an incidental side effect of the §2a `wp_die()` conversion earlier in this release — no further change was needed there.

## [0.4.2] — 2026-07-02

### Fixed
- **A newsletter issue could get stuck in `sending` forever when every recipient's send failed.** `QueueProcessor::process()` previously only re-checked (and possibly marked `sent`) issues that had at least one row transition to `sent` in that batch (`$sent_per_issue`). If every recipient's `wp_mail()` call failed — e.g. a single-artist newsletter hitting a temporary mail delivery problem — none of its rows ever reached `sent`, so the issue was never reconciled; and since its rows were already `failed` (not `pending`), no future cron tick would ever look at it again either. The admin dashboard showed that newsletter as "Sending…" indefinitely, with "Send Now" disabled (`has_issue_in_flight()` blocks a second send while one is "in flight"). Fixed by having `process()` reconcile **every** currently-`sending` issue each tick via a new `reconcile_sending_issues()` pass, regardless of whether that batch touched it or whether there's anything left to send — self-healing any issue already stuck this way, not just preventing new ones.

## [0.4.1] — 2026-07-01

### Fixed
- **Newsletters are now actually localized.** Previously `Scheduler::prepare_type()` rendered `digest_html` and `intro` exactly once per issue, in whatever locale the daily cron process happened to run in, and stored that as static HTML reused for every recipient regardless of language; `QueueProcessor`'s per-recipient `switch_to_locale()` call only localized a handful of wrapper strings (subject prefix, header title, footer tagline) and only for artists — public subscribers' captured `locale` was written to the DB at signup but never read again. Fixed with a proper per-locale render:
  - `Scheduler::prepare_type()` now groups recipients (artists via user meta `locale`; public subscribers via `agnosis_newsletter_subscribers.locale`, now actually selected by `Subscriber::confirmed_recipients()`) by their resolved locale, rendering the digest and intro once per distinct locale rather than once per issue or once per recipient. Content is stored as a JSON map (`agnosis_newsletter_issues.locale_content`) alongside the existing `intro`/`digest_html` columns, which now hold the site-default-locale entry as the base/fallback render.
  - `agnosis_newsletter_queue` gains a `locale` column, resolved once at fan-out time so `QueueProcessor::send_one()` no longer needs a per-recipient meta lookup, and now switches locale (and looks up that locale's content in the map) for every recipient type, not just artists.
  - `Digest::build_public()`/`build_artist()` take an optional Lingua Forge language code. When given, each listed post links to its translated title/page via `linguaforge_get_translations()`, falling back to the primary-language post whenever no translation exists yet for that recipient's language.
  - `Digest::recent_posts()` now also scopes its `WP_Query` to the site's primary Lingua Forge language (or posts with no `_lf_lang` meta at all, for pre-LF content) — a secondary bug this surfaced: on a multi-language site the digest was previously listing the same artwork once per translated duplicate post, since each translation is its own `agnosis_artwork` post and nothing scoped the query by language outside of normal frontend requests.
  - The admin-written intro (free text, not a translated WP post) is machine-translated per locale via the existing `SubmissionTranslator` (same AI provider used for artwork descriptions) when one is configured; without a configured provider, the intro is sent as-written to every locale rather than blocking the send.

## [0.4.0] — 2026-07-01

### Added
- **Newsletter system.** Two separate, self-hosted newsletters, both sent via a batch-queued WP-Cron pipeline (`agnosis_newsletter_queue`) to avoid host mail-rate-limit/timeout issues:
  - **Artist newsletter** — every admitted artist is auto-enrolled; opt-out is per-user (`_agnosis_newsletter_optout` user meta) rather than a separate subscription flow, since artists are already known members.
  - **Public newsletter** — double opt-in subscription (`agnosis_newsletter_subscribers` table), driven by a new `POST /agnosis/v1/newsletter/subscribe` REST endpoint (rate-limited via the existing `RateLimiter`) and a new `agnosis/newsletter-signup` block for pages. Confirm/unsubscribe links are handled by a token-based `template_redirect` shim (`SubscriptionConfirm`), following the same no-login-required pattern as `VouchConfirm`/`ReviewConfirm`.
  - Each issue combines an **auto-generated digest** (`Digest::build_artist()` / `build_public()` — new artworks, events, admissions, open votes, pulled via `WP_Query`/direct queries over the configured window) with an **optional admin-written intro**, composed into the final email by `Mailer::build_email()`.
  - Frequency is independently configurable per newsletter (`agnosis_newsletter_{artist,public}_frequency_days`, default 30), checked daily by `Scheduler::prepare()` and fanned out to the queue table; `QueueProcessor` drains the queue in configurable batches (`agnosis_newsletter_batch_size`, default 20) on a 5-minute cron tick.
  - A dedicated **From: address** for newsletter mail (`agnosis_newsletter_from_name` / `agnosis_newsletter_from_email`) is now configurable separately from the site's `admin_email`, falling back to the site name/admin email when unset (`Mailer::sender_header()`).
  - A **"Send Test"** action (`Scheduler::send_test()`) sends a one-off preview of the next issue (current draft intro + recent activity) to a single address, clearly marked `[TEST]` with a non-functional unsubscribe link — it does not touch the queue, the schedule, or any subscriber, so it's safe to run repeatedly.
  - New **Settings → Newsletter** tab (`render_newsletter_dashboard()`): per-newsletter enable toggle, frequency, intro text, sender identity, subscriber/artist stats with a configurable low-subscriber-count warning threshold (`agnosis_newsletter_subscriber_warn_threshold`, default 250 — the point at which self-hosting was assessed as no longer being the better option vs. an ESP), and manual "Send Now" / "Send Test" forms.
  - Three new tables (`agnosis_newsletter_subscribers`, `agnosis_newsletter_issues`, `agnosis_newsletter_queue`), two new cron hooks (`agnosis_prepare_newsletters` daily, `agnosis_send_newsletter_queue` every five minutes), and full `uninstall.php` teardown (tables, cron hooks, and the `_agnosis_newsletter_optout` user meta).
  - ESP integration (e.g. Brevo/Mailchimp) was evaluated for scale beyond a few hundred subscribers but deliberately deferred — this release is self-hosted only, with a manual switch-over to an ESP left as a future decision once real subscriber counts are known.

### Changed
- **Default "About" and "Artist Guide" pages rewritten.** The original copy (from 0.3.0) didn't address the questions artists most often have: what AI is actually allowed to do to their work (image quality enhancement only — never altering or replacing the artwork itself), how the dual-title system works, and that a submission can be multiple images treated as one series. Both pages now cover this plus the fuller set of ways to work with Agnosis. Removed a redundant `<h1>` from both pages' content — the FSE theme's `page.html` template already renders `wp:post-title`, so keeping it in the content was duplicating the heading.

### Fixed
- **`composer coverage` was silently under-reporting integration coverage** (reported drop from ~45% to 6.45%). The integration test command relied entirely on the wp-env container's `php.ini` state for its pcov configuration, set once by `dev/scripts/setup-coverage.sh`; that script's short-circuit check treated "pcov extension loaded" as sufficient without re-verifying `pcov.directory`, so a stale value (e.g. surviving a container rebuild) silently disabled instrumentation while the Clover report still counted total statements correctly — producing a plausible-looking but wrong low percentage rather than an outright failure. Fixed by passing `-d pcov.enabled=1 -d pcov.directory=...` explicitly on the integration PHPUnit invocation in `dev/composer.json` (mirroring the unit test command, which already did this), and by hardening `setup-coverage.sh` to always re-assert and correct the ini directives rather than trusting that "loaded" implies "correctly configured." Confirmed restored to 50.45% (4122/8170 statements).

## [0.3.0] — 2026-06-30

### Changed
- **Translation kickoff is deferred off the intake request** (`Compat/LinguaForge.php`). Publishing an Agnosis post no longer makes AI calls inline. `agnosis_post_published` now only schedules a single WP-Cron event (`agnosis_dispatch_lf_translations`); the actual work — building per-language artwork titles and requesting the body translations — runs later in `dispatch_translations()`. The body translations now use LF 2.4.0's async `linguaforge_queue_translation()` (Action Scheduler / WP-Cron) when available, falling back to the synchronous trigger on older LF. Together this takes a webhook/IMAP intake from ~2N blocking AI calls down to zero on the intake request. (audit §3f)
- **Dual-title handling scoped to artwork.** `build_title_translations()` and `hold_artist_title()` now apply to `agnosis_artwork` only. Events use LF's normal title translation (an event title is translatable content); biographies likewise — the artist's name is set at application time and is not derived from the biography post title, so it needs no special protection. The §2a image/meta propagation stays scoped to all three CPTs. (audit §3f)

### Added
- **Two out-of-the-box content pages.** On activation Agnosis now creates an **About** page (`/about/`) explaining what the community is and how it works, and an **Artist Guide** help page (`/artist-guide/`) walking an artist through the email-driven workflow (submitting artwork, the photo-only lane, biographies, events, updating/removing, writing in your own language). Both are managed pages (idempotent on re-activation, tagged `_agnosis_managed_page` so `uninstall.php` removes them) authored in plain language; Lingua Forge translates them like any page, so no separate i18n is needed for the copy. (audit §9)
- **Member-governed community size cap.** Each instance has a maximum number of admitted artists (`agnosis_community_max_artists`, default 50; 0 = unlimited), and the community — not a hard-coded number — controls it.
  - *Phase 1 (cap + waitlist):* a new `CommunityCap` gate. When the instance is full, applications join a FIFO **waitlist** (`waitlisted` status) instead of being rejected; the cap gates new admissions only, so existing members are always grandfathered and lowering the cap never removes anyone. The gate is enforced at `apply()` and re-checked at `maybe_admit()` (a pending application that reaches its vouch threshold while full is parked, not admitted). When a member permanently leaves (`agnosis_artist_left` / `agnosis_removal_vote_passed` / `agnosis_artist_deleted_by_admin`), the oldest waitlisted applicant is advanced back into the vouching flow ("open a slot, fill a slot") and admitted at once if it already had enough vouches. Admins may admit over the cap (logged). Configurable in Settings → Network; the join form reports the full/waitlist state.
  - *Phase 2 (community vote):* a new `CommunityCapVote` governance flow mirroring the removal-vote machinery — any artist proposes a new cap (`POST /agnosis/v1/cap/propose`), it opens as a full community vote once it gathers the configured co-signers (`agnosis_cap_proposal_threshold`, default 3), members vote (`/cap/cosign/{id}`, `/cap/vote/{id}`), and the daily `agnosis_check_cap_votes` cron closes the window: a strict majority (> 50 %) of active artists voting yes writes the new cap and advances the waitlist. New tables `agnosis_cap_proposals` + `agnosis_cap_votes`; `CommunityCapNotification` emails members when a vote opens and the admin on resolution. (audit §8) *(A member-facing voting block + one-click email links — mirroring the removal-vote HMAC links — are a noted follow-up; the governance backend and REST API are complete.)*
- **`uninstall.php` — complete teardown on delete.** Deleting the plugin now removes its full infrastructure footprint: the 9 custom tables, every `agnosis_*` option and transient, the `agnosis_artist` role, the managed pages (`/join/`, My Submissions), all scheduled cron events, and the `uploads/agnosis-queue/` working directory. Multisite-aware (runs per site). Deliberately preserves the artists'/operator's content — published artwork/biography/event posts and their media, and WordPress user accounts (removing the role drops only its capabilities). Previously `deactivate()` cleared cron only, so everything else was orphaned on delete. (audit §C-2)
- **Per-language artwork titles across translations** (`Compat/LinguaForge.php`). The dual-title architecture (`post_title` = artist's own-language title; primary/translated title in `_agnosis_translated_title`) now carries correctly to LF translations. (1) `hold_artist_title()` hooks `linguaforge_translation_content` to keep `post_title` as the artist's original on every language version — previously LF translated that non-primary title from the wrong source language. (2) `build_title_translations()` runs at publish (`agnosis_post_published` priority 15) and translates the primary-language title into each enabled LF language via `SubmissionTranslator`, storing a `_agnosis_title_i18n` map. (3) `supply_translated_meta()` / `copy_translated_meta()` write each translation's `_agnosis_translated_title` from that map. Solved entirely with existing LF hooks (`linguaforge_translation_content` + the 2.4.0 `linguaforge_translated_post_meta`) — no new LF API. Graceful no-op when no AI provider is configured. (audit §2d title note)
- **Translated-post image/meta propagation** (`Compat/LinguaForge.php`). Translated `agnosis_artwork` / `agnosis_biography` / `agnosis_event` posts created by Lingua Forge now inherit the source post's images and other language-neutral meta, so they no longer render empty. A curated allowlist (`NEUTRAL_META_KEYS`: `_thumbnail_id`, `_agnosis_gallery_ids`, `_agnosis_original_title`, `_agnosis_event_location`, `_agnosis_event_date`) is copied — deliberately **not** "all `_agnosis_*`", which would leak per-post security tokens (`_agnosis_review_token` / `_agnosis_removal_token`), corrupt duplicate-detection identity (`_agnosis_queue_id`, `_agnosis_image_hash`), and carry language-specific values (`_agnosis_translated_title`, `_agnosis_detected_lang`) onto the wrong-language post. On LF 2.4.0+ the allowlist is supplied via the `linguaforge_translated_post_meta` filter so the post is born complete (no empty-image window); on older LF it falls back to the `linguaforge_translation_complete` action (which also refreshes on re-translation). Image alt text is not copied — translations reuse the same attachment IDs, so it travels with the attachment. (audit §2a)

### Changed
- **No params passed to `linguaforge_trigger_translation()`** (`Compat/LinguaForge.php`). `request_translations()` previously sent `domain` / `priority` / `source` — none of which Lingua Forge reads, so they were silently dropped. They are gone; LF's defaults are exactly what we want. `with_meta_description` is intentionally not set: the translated excerpt LF now produces (LF 2.4.0 writes it at creation) is the artwork's description, so a separate AI-generated meta description would be redundant cost. (audit §2c)

### Fixed
- **`_lf_lang` now tracks LF's primary language, not the WP locale** (`Compat/LinguaForge.php`). `set_language_meta()` reads the `linguaforge_primary_language` option (the language `SubmissionTranslator` normalises submissions to), falling back to `get_locale()`. On a site whose WP locale differs from LF's configured primary, `_lf_lang` was previously mislabeled — telling LF the wrong source language for translation. (audit §2d residual)
- **Removed the dead `_agnosis_detected_lang` read** (`Compat/LinguaForge.php`). `set_language_meta()` previously read `_agnosis_detected_lang` as a first-choice source language, but nothing ever wrote that key — Agnosis normalises content to the primary language at intake rather than detecting a source language. The vestigial read is gone; `_lf_lang` now derives solely from `linguaforge_primary_language` → locale. (audit §C-4 / §3d)
- **`LinguaForgeCompatTest` repaired** — removed dead tests for the `filter_meta_description()` / `register_textdomain()` methods dropped in the 0.2.1 hook rewire, and updated the `filter_og_image()` / `filter_schema_type()` cases to the current signatures (driven through `go_to()` since both read global query state). Added coverage for the meta-propagation allowlist, including the token / identity / language-key exclusions. (24 Compat tests green.)

### Added
- **`agnosis/event-date` block** — server-side-rendered block that reads `_agnosis_event_date` post meta and formats it with WordPress's configured date (and time, when present) format via `date_i18n()`. Emits a `<time datetime="…">` element; returns empty string when no date is set so the block takes no space. The event template now shows the actual event date instead of the post publication date. (§4c)
- **Event date AI extraction** — `Pipeline::extract_event_fields()` now also extracts the event date from the email body (ISO 8601), stored in `_agnosis_event_date` post meta. Non-ISO strings are discarded to prevent AI hallucinations from producing garbage output.

### Added
- **Photo-only intake lane** (`photo@` address + `[Photo]` subject indicator). Photographers and lens-based artists whose photograph is the artwork can submit to a dedicated address that publishes their image exactly as sent — AI enhancement is skipped entirely (no API call, no image mutation), and the quality-rejection gate is bypassed (a deliberately dark, grainy, or low-fi image is an aesthetic choice, not a defect). AI description (title, excerpt, tags, alt text) still runs. Original preservation also added: for standard artwork submissions where enhancement does run, the original binary is now uploaded as a sidecar attachment (`_agnosis_is_original = '1'`) linked via `_agnosis_original_attachment_id` on the enhanced attachment — so the master is always recoverable. (§4f)
- **`Pipeline::process()` `$skip_enhancement` flag** — when `true`, the enhancement provider is not called at all. Used by the photo-only path in `PostCreator`.

### Added
- **`FrontendAccess` class** (`includes/Artist/FrontendAccess.php`) — enforces frontend-only access for the `agnosis_artist` role: redirects artists who land on any `/wp-admin/` URL to the front page (`admin_init`), hides the admin toolbar on the frontend (`show_admin_bar`), and sends artists to the front page instead of the dashboard after login (`login_redirect`). Admins who also hold the artist role are intentionally excluded from all three restrictions. AJAX requests are skipped in the redirect to avoid breaking any `admin-ajax.php` calls. (§2c)

### Added
- **`EmailAuth` helper** (`includes/Email/EmailAuth.php`) — parses `Authentication-Results` headers (RFC 8601) to extract SPF, DKIM, and DMARC verdicts. Includes a Mailgun-specific extractor for the `message-headers` JSON field. `passes()` returns true when at least SPF or DKIM is `pass` — requiring both would over-reject legitimate senders who have only one mechanism configured. (§2a)
- **Per-sender intake throttle** (`RateLimiter::check_sender()`) — rate limit keyed by hashed `From:` address (not IP, since all ESP relay traffic shares the same IP). Both the IMAP and webhook paths enforce a configurable hourly cap per artist (default: 5). Exceeding the limit silently drops the message so ESPs do not retry. (§2a)
- **`Admission::is_admitted_artist()` public static** — centralises the admission role check. Called by `Inbox`, `Webhook`, and (as a defense-in-depth re-assert) `PostCreator` before any AI spend. (§2a)
- **Settings: `agnosis_intake_per_sender_limit`** (Email tab) — per-artist hourly submission cap (default 5, min 1). (§2a)
- **Settings: `agnosis_require_email_auth`** (Email tab) — opt-in SPF/DKIM enforcement via `Authentication-Results`. Off by default; requires SPF/DKIM records to be configured and the ESP to include the header. (§2a)

- **IMAP poll UID cursor + headers-first fetch** (`Inbox::query_messages()`). Each poll now fetches only messages whose IMAP UID is strictly greater than the last processed UID, persisted in `agnosis_imap_last_uid`. First run (cursor = 0) falls back to the configured retention window so no legitimate back-dated mail is skipped. Query is run in UID-sequence mode (`ST_UID`) so the cursor survives mailbox expunges and reconnects. `fetchBody(false)` is set on every query so the initial IMAP FETCH returns only RFC-822 headers; body download is triggered lazily by `parse_imap_message()` and only for senders that clear all cheap gates. The cursor advances to the highest UID seen in each poll — including skipped messages — so it can never regress. (§2b)
- **LinguaForge SEO/OG/schema hooks rewired** (`Compat/LinguaForge.php`). The four previously broken hook registrations (silent no-ops against non-existent LF filters) are now corrected or removed: `linguaforge_og_image` → `linguaforge_seo_og_image` (single string arg, `get_post()` used internally); `linguaforge_schema_type` → `linguaforge_seo_schema_data` (array + type, returns modified array with `@type = VisualArtwork`); `linguaforge_meta_description_post` dropped (LF reads `post_excerpt` natively via `get_og_description()`); `linguaforge_managed_textdomains` dropped (LF has no such system). Admin notice URL corrected (`linguaforge-settings` → `lingua-forge`). (§3b, §3c)

### Fixed
- **Biography and event `post_content` now uses the artist's own written statement, not the AI image description** (`PostCreator::build_post_content`). For `agnosis_biography` and `agnosis_event`, the body is now the (optionally AI-polished) text the artist sent. The AI image description body is reserved for `agnosis_artwork`, where the image *is* the work. Text-only biography/event submissions no longer produce a blank page. (§4b)
- **Biography updates are now AI-merged with existing content** (`Pipeline::merge_biography()`). When an artist sends a biography update and a previous biography already exists, the new information is merged with the existing text rather than replacing it — preserving all prior content and integrating the new update naturally. Artists can send incremental updates ("I just won an award") without resubmitting their full biography. Events are intentionally excluded and continue to replace. Gated by the `agnosis_ai_merge_biography` setting (default on). As a fallback when no existing content is present or the merge call fails, the new submission is used as-is. When a resend produces no text at all, the existing body is preserved unchanged. (§4d)
- **Webhook path now enforces the admitted-sender gate** (`Webhook::handle()`). Previously, any image-bearing message relayed by the ESP was AI-processed and drafted regardless of whether the sender was an admitted artist. The admission check now runs before any DB write or AI call. Returns HTTP 200 to prevent ESP retries. (§2a)
- **IMAP path now checks admission, throttle, and auth from headers before downloading message body** (`Inbox::process_messages()`). The sender's `From:` address is read cheaply; non-admitted senders and throttled senders are skipped without incurring a body download. SPF/DKIM check is also performed at this cheap stage when `agnosis_require_email_auth` is on. (§2a)
- **`PostCreator::handle()` re-asserts admission before AI spend** — defense-in-depth guard catches the edge case where an artist's role is removed between enqueue and cron processing. (§2a)

## [0.2.0] — 2026-06-29

### Added
- **Admission revocation — three independent departure paths (§5h)**

  - **Self-removal** — an artist submits `POST /agnosis/v1/departure/request`. A confirmation email is sent (localised via `switch_to_locale`) with an HMAC-signed link. Clicking the link calls `Departure::confirm_self_removal()`: deletes all `agnosis_artwork`, `agnosis_biography`, and `agnosis_event` posts permanently (bypass trash), removes the `agnosis_artist` role, marks the membership row `status='left'`, and calls `wp_delete_user()`. The admin receives a brief notice; the community is not named.

  - **Admin revocation** — two actions exposed in Settings → Network → Members:
    - **Suspend** — `admin_post_agnosis_ban_artist` sets `status='banned'`, removes the role, and sends a localised suspension email. An optional date picker restricts the ban to a specific day; leaving it blank creates an indefinite ban. A daily cron (`agnosis_check_bans`) automatically reinstates artists whose `banned_until` has passed (role re-granted, status → `admitted`, reinstatement email sent).
    - **Delete** — `admin_post_agnosis_delete_artist` permanently deletes all content and the WP account via `Departure::admin_delete()`. Requires a JS confirmation dialog.

  - **Community vote** — any artist can nominate another via `POST /agnosis/v1/removal/nominate/{id}`. When nominations reach the configurable threshold (default 3, setting `agnosis_removal_nomination_threshold`) **or** an admin triggers `admin_post_agnosis_initiate_removal_vote` directly, the vote opens to the whole community. Each artist receives a personalised email with HMAC-signed yes/no vote links (stateless; tokens verified by `template_redirect`). Artists can change their vote by following the other link before the deadline. A daily cron (`agnosis_check_removal_votes`) resolves expired votes: if >50 % of active members voted yes the artist is removed (same effect as self-removal); otherwise the vote fails and no action is taken. Admin receives an outcome email in both cases.

- **`Departure` class** (`includes/Artist/Departure.php`) — business logic for all three departure paths. Key public API: `request_self_removal()`, `confirm_self_removal()`, `admin_ban()`, `admin_delete()`, `check_expired_bans()`, `nominate()`, `cast_vote()`, `admin_open_removal_vote()`, `check_expired_removal_votes()`, `execute_removal()`, `delete_artist_content()`.

- **`DepartureNotification` class** (`includes/Artist/DepartureNotification.php`) — hooks into actions fired by `Departure` to send all departure-related emails: `agnosis_departure_confirmation_requested`, `agnosis_artist_left`, `agnosis_artist_banned`, `agnosis_artist_reinstated`, `agnosis_removal_vote_opened`, `agnosis_removal_vote_passed`, `agnosis_removal_vote_failed`. Per-recipient locale switching applied throughout.

- **Members dashboard** — Settings → Network now shows an admitted/banned **Members** card below the pending applications table. Each row displays artist name/email, status (Active or Banned with expiry date if applicable), joined date, and action buttons: **Suspend** (with optional expiry date picker), **Delete** (with confirmation dialog), **Open Vote** (admin-bypass community vote). Banned artists only show the Delete button.

- **`agnosis_removal_nomination_threshold` and `agnosis_removal_window_days` settings** (Network tab) — configure how many nominations open a community vote (default 3) and how long the vote stays open (default 7 days).

- **Schema additions** — `agnosis_applications` table extended with `banned_until DATETIME NULL`, `removal_token VARCHAR(64) NULL UNIQUE`. Status ENUM extended to include `banned`. New tables `agnosis_removal_requests` and `agnosis_removal_votes` track community vote state and individual votes. `maybe_upgrade()` guards ensure backward compatibility. Two new daily crons registered on activation: `agnosis_check_bans` and `agnosis_check_removal_votes`.

- **`agnosis/join` block** — dynamic server-side-rendered block that displays the public application form (name, email, bio, portfolio URL, "Why do you want to join?"). Submits via `fetch` to `POST /agnosis/v1/admission/apply`. Shows a success message on acceptance or a server error message on rejection. Admitted artists see a short confirmation instead of the form. Enqueues `frontend.js` and `frontend.css` (no build step — vanilla JS).
- **`/join/` page auto-created on activation** — `Activator::create_join_page()` creates a published page at slug `join` with `<!-- wp:agnosis/join /-->` as content. Idempotent; stored in `agnosis_join_page_id` option.

- **`AdmissionNotification`** — sends personalised emails to admin and every current artist when an application is received, with HMAC-signed yes/no vote links. Artists can change their vote at any time within the voting window. When an application expires without reaching the threshold: applicant is notified the community declined; artists receive a brief closure notice. Newly admitted artists receive a zero-configuration welcome email: password-reset link + a formatted list of all configured alias email addresses (submit, bio, event, replace, remove, promote) so they can start sharing work immediately without any additional documentation. Aliases are only listed when their option is configured — partial setups show only what is available. All email body strings are wrapped in `__()` for `.po`/`.mo` translation. Every outgoing email is now wrapped in `switch_to_locale()` / `restore_current_locale()`: vote emails switch to each artist's WP user locale; expiry and welcome emails switch to the applicant/artist's language.
- **Per-recipient locale switching across all notification emails** — `Publishing\Notification` (`on_post_drafted`, `on_removal_requested`, `on_submission_rejected`) wraps each `wp_mail()` call in `switch_to_locale($artist_locale)` so translated strings are correct for every recipient regardless of the site's default language. In `on_post_drafted`, only the AI-generated `post_excerpt` is back-translated to the artist's language; the artwork title (`post_title`) is intentionally left in the site language — artwork titles are proper nouns and creative decisions by the artist that must not be silently altered. The artist's original submitted title is shown separately in the review email (see `_agnosis_original_title` above).
- **Applicant language capture** — `POST /agnosis/v1/admission/apply` accepts an optional `language` parameter (ISO 639-1 code, e.g. `es`). When omitted, the primary language tag is extracted from the `HTTP_ACCEPT_LANGUAGE` header. The code is stored in `agnosis_applications.language`. On admission, it is mapped to a WP locale (e.g. `es` → `es_ES`) and saved to the user's `locale` meta via `wp_update_user`.
- **Language select on join form** — the `agnosis/join` block now includes a "Language you work in" select field with all 29 languages matching the AI translation map (auto-detect default). The selection is sent as `language` in the application payload.
- **`SubmissionTranslator::translate_text()`** — new public method for back-translating a single string to a given ISO 639-1 target code. Used by `Publishing\Notification::on_post_drafted()` to translate the AI-generated post excerpt back to the artist's language before building the review email. The post title is intentionally not translated — see below.
- **Original artwork title preserved as `_agnosis_original_title` post meta** — the artist's email subject (stripped of any `[Indicator]` prefix, before AI translation rewrites it) is captured in `PostCreator::handle()` and stored once on first post creation. Never overwritten on resends or singleton merges. Used by `Notification::on_post_drafted()` to surface the artist's own words in the review email subject line and as a subtitle beneath the AI-generated site title in the email body.
- **URL slug derived from original submitted title** — `PostCreator::make_slug()` generates the `post_name` from `_agnosis_original_title` rather than the AI-translated `post_title`, so an artist whose subject is "El Jardín Secreto" gets the permalink `…/el-jardin-secreto/` rather than `…/the-secret-garden/`. For non-Latin scripts (CJK, Arabic, Devanagari, Cyrillic, Korean, Thai, etc.) the PHP `intl` extension's `Transliterator` converts to a Latin/ASCII approximation using the ICU rule chain `Any-Latin; Latin-ASCII; Lower()` (e.g. "秘密花園" → `mi-mi-hua-yuan`, "الحديقة السرية" → `alhdy-alsry`). Degrades gracefully on hosts without `intl`: WordPress derives the slug from the translated `post_title` instead.
- **`SubmissionTranslator::from_settings()`** — static factory method that creates a translator from the currently configured AI provider without requiring constructor injection. Returns `null` when no API key is configured so callers degrade gracefully.
- **`VouchConfirm`** — `template_redirect` handler that processes the signed email vote links. Verifies the HMAC token (stateless — no DB write for the token itself), records the vote via `Admission::record_vote()`, and renders a minimal self-contained HTML thank-you or error page without loading the theme.
- **Community voting: yes/no votes, dynamic threshold, 7-day window** — `Admission::vouch()` now accepts a `vote` parameter (`yes` | `no`, default `yes`). Votes are stored with `INSERT … ON DUPLICATE KEY UPDATE` so artists can change their mind. Only positive (`yes`) votes count toward the admission threshold. `calculate_required()` returns `max( ceil( active_artists × percent / 100 ), minimum )` using two new settings (`agnosis_admission_percent` default 10%, `agnosis_admission_minimum` default 3). `check_expired_applications()` runs via daily cron; rejects pending applications older than `agnosis_admission_window_days` (default 7) that have not reached the threshold.
- **Dual-title artwork architecture** — `post_title` is now always the artist's original submitted title (their language, their words — never rewritten by AI). The AI-generated site-language title is stored separately in `_agnosis_translated_title` post meta. `_agnosis_original_title` is retained for backwards compatibility and mirrors `post_title` on first creation. Review emails surface both: the `<h2>` heading shows the original title; a "On the site:" line shows the AI title; a "In your language:" back-translation hint shows the AI title translated back to the artist's locale.
- **`agnosis/artwork-title` block** — server-side-rendered block registered via `Profile::register_blocks()`. Reads `post_title` (original) and `_agnosis_translated_title` meta (AI translation). When the two strings differ, renders an `<hgroup>` with the original as `<h1>` and the translation as a styled `<p>` subtitle. When identical (same-language artist on same-language site), renders a plain `<h1>`. Replaces `wp:post-title` in `single-agnosis_artwork.html`.
- **Applicant acknowledgment email** — when an artist submits an application (`POST /agnosis/v1/admission/apply`), they now immediately receive a confirmation email in their own language via `AdmissionNotification::send_application_acknowledgment()`. The email is localised via `switch_to_locale()` / `restore_current_locale()` using the applicant's submitted language code. Previously applicants received no immediate feedback.
- **HTML email `lang` attribute localised** — all three HTML email templates in `Publishing\Notification` previously hardcoded `<html lang="en">`. A new `html_lang()` helper derives the BCP 47 tag from the current locale (after `switch_to_locale()` has been applied) so the `lang=` attribute matches the actual language of the email content.
- **Language list driven by installed WP language packs** — `JoinPage.php` no longer maintains a hardcoded 29-language array. `SubmissionTranslator::language_names()` (new public static method) reads `get_available_languages()` + the site locale, reduces them to 2-letter ISO codes, and intersects against `LANGUAGE_NAMES` so the join form only offers languages the site actually has localisation files for. Falls back to the full `LANGUAGE_NAMES` constant on a fresh English-only install. Filterable via `agnosis_translation_languages` for operator overrides. No Lingua Forge dependency — plain WP core.
- **Welcome email extended** — the admission welcome email now includes the artist's personal gallery URL (subdomain when `agnosis_base_domain` is configured, falling back to `home_url()` via `SubdomainRouter::url_for_artist()`), a direct link to `/my-submissions/`, and a subject-line convention reference (`[Biography]`, `[Event]`, artwork default). Everything the artist needs in a single email.
- **`agnosis_email_goodbye` alias** — an optional email address (Settings → Email) artists can write to in order to request self-removal without needing access to the website. Sending any email (no attachment required) to this address triggers the same confirmation-email flow as `POST /agnosis/v1/departure/request`: a single-use token link is sent back; clicking it permanently deletes the artist's content and account. Both the IMAP poller (`Inbox`) and the webhook endpoint (`Webhook`) handle the alias; unrecognised or non-artist senders are silently ignored and logged. The goodbye address is listed in the admission welcome email under "To leave the network and delete your account." `Departure::request_self_removal()` refactored to delegate to the new `initiate_removal_for_user(int $user_id): bool` method so both REST and non-REST paths share the same logic.

- **Admin admission dashboard** — Settings → Network now shows a **Pending Applications** card below the configuration fields. The table lists applicant name/email, applied date, a vote progress bar (received/required), bio excerpt, portfolio link, and admin-override **Admit** / **Reject** buttons. Admit (`admin_post_agnosis_admit_application`) bypasses the community threshold: creates the WP user, grants `agnosis_artist`, and fires `agnosis_artist_admitted` so the welcome email is sent. Reject (`admin_post_agnosis_reject_application`) marks the row rejected and fires `agnosis_artist_rejected`. Both actions are nonce-protected, `manage_options`-gated, and redirect back to the Network tab with an inline success or error notice. `Admission::admin_admit()` and `Admission::admin_reject()` are new public methods.

### Fixed
- **LF translation trigger was a silent no-op** — `LinguaForge::request_translations()` was calling `do_action('linguaforge_request_translation', …)`, a hook that does not exist anywhere in Lingua Forge. No translations were ever triggered after artwork publication. Fixed by replacing the `do_action` with direct calls to `linguaforge_trigger_translation(int $post_id, string $target_lang, array $params)` — LF's actual public API in `ai/ai.php` — once per target language, guarded by `function_exists()`.

### Changed
- **Application-first admission flow** — no WP account is created before the community approves. `apply()` is now unauthenticated and stores the application in the new `agnosis_applications` table (email, display_name, bio, portfolio_url, statement). Artists vouch against the application ID via `agnosis_application_vouches`. `maybe_admit()` calls `wp_create_user()` only when the vouch threshold is reached, then grants `agnosis_artist` and fires `agnosis_artist_admitted`. Reapplication is allowed for withdrawn/rejected/left entries by updating the existing row.
- **Membership lifecycle table (`agnosis_applications`)** — tracks every applicant and member with statuses `pending → admitted | rejected | withdrawn | left`. `resolved_at` timestamps every transition. `wp_user_id` is null until admission. Serves as the authoritative membership status table for future leave-community and re-join flows.
- **Pre-admission vouch table (`agnosis_application_vouches`)** — separate from `agnosis_vouches` (post-admission community table). Revocation sets `revoked_at` rather than deleting so the audit trail is preserved.
- **Status endpoint is admin-only** — `GET /agnosis/v1/admission/status/{application_id}` now takes an application ID and requires `manage_options`. Applicants are informed of state changes by email only.
- **Self-vouch guard by email** — previously compared WP user IDs; now compares the vouching artist's `user_email` against the application email, correctly covering the case where the applicant has no WP account yet.

## [0.1.9] — 2026-06-28

### Added
- **`/my-submissions` works on artist subdomains** — `SubdomainRouter::scope_query()` previously applied the `author` filter to every main query, including static page requests. Since the `/my-submissions` page is created by the system (not the artist user) it returned a 404 on any artist subdomain. A guard now skips the author and post_type filters when `pagename` is set or the query already targets `post_type=page`, letting WordPress resolve sitewide pages normally. Session cookies must also carry across subdomains — add `define('COOKIE_DOMAIN', '.agnosis.art');` to `wp-config.php` so artists logged in on the main domain are also authenticated on their subdomain.
- **Inline login form on `/my-submissions`** — unauthenticated visitors no longer see a plain "Please log in" notice or get bounced to `wp-login.php`. `SubmissionsPage` now renders an inline form via `wp_login_form()` with the current page URL as the redirect, so the artist logs in and lands back on their submissions page without ever leaving the frontend.
- **Artist name in subdomain site title** — `SubdomainRouter` now filters `option_blogname` on artist subdomains so the `wp:site-title` block (and anything else reading `get_bloginfo('name')`) displays the artist's display name instead of the main portal site name. Falls back to the nicename slug so the header is never blank. The existing `document_title_parts` and `wp_title` filters (HTML `<title>`) already did this; `option_blogname` closes the gap for the visible header.
- **Multilingual submission translation** — artist emails are automatically translated to the site's primary language before AI processing. The target language is resolved from the Lingua Forge `linguaforge_primary_language` option, with fallback to the WordPress site locale and a final fallback to English. Translation is performed in a single `chat()` call (one round-trip) using a JSON envelope that carries both the email subject and body. If translation fails (empty or non-JSON response) the original text is passed through unchanged — the pipeline always continues. The target language is extensible via the `agnosis_translation_languages` filter. Translation events are logged to Settings → Logs (`pipeline` context). Implemented in new `SubmissionTranslator` class (`includes/AI/SubmissionTranslator.php`); `chat()` max_tokens bumped from 512 → 1024 in OpenAI and Anthropic to accommodate translated email bodies.
- **Media type expansion** — the AI pipeline now handles audio, video, and PDF attachments in addition to images:
  - **PDF portfolios** — each page is rasterised to a JPEG at 150 dpi using the PHP Imagick extension and fed into the normal describe → optionally-enhance image branch. Multi-page PDFs produce one gallery image per page. Falls back gracefully (skips with a logged notice) when Imagick is not installed.
  - **Video stills** — the first frame is extracted via `ffmpeg` and processed as a JPEG through the image branch. Enhancement is applied normally. Falls back gracefully when `ffmpeg` is not in `PATH`.
  - **Audio files** — routed through a new audio branch: (1) transcribed via OpenAI Whisper (`POST /v1/audio/transcriptions`, `whisper-1`); (2) the transcript + artist context is sent to the text model (`chat()`) with a structured JSON prompt to produce `title`, `excerpt`, `body`, `tags`, `alt_text`, and `medium`; (3) no image is uploaded to the Media Library — `PostCreator::merge_gallery()` skips `upload_image()` for `media_type === 'audio'` results. Providers without audio support (`Anthropic`, `WordPressAI`) return an empty transcript and fall back to describing from artist text alone.
  - **`MediaAdapter`** — new `includes/AI/MediaAdapter.php` class with a single static `adapt(array $attachments): array` method. Sits in front of the pipeline loop; expands each attachment into zero or more normalised entries with a `media_type` field (`'image'` or `'audio'`). Unsupported MIME types are logged and dropped.
  - **`ProviderInterface`** extended with `transcribe(string $audio_data, string $mime_type): string` and `supports_audio(): bool`; existing providers updated.
- **Automatic quality rejection gate** — when the primary image's quality score is at or below the configurable rejection threshold (default: 3 / 10), the submission is rejected automatically: the queue row is marked `failed`, no draft post is created, and the artist receives a friendly HTML email explaining the specific photographic issue and how to fix it. Issue labels from the vision AI (e.g. "too dark", "motion blur", "glare") are mapped to plain-language advice with concrete tips ("Try photographing near a large window in daylight…"). The email also includes four universal photography tips. Artists are invited to resubmit — the entire flow is automated with no admin action required. Configurable via Settings → AI Providers: **Rejection threshold** (set to 0 to disable). Covered by `QualityRejectionTest` (5 assertions: score at threshold rejects, score below threshold rejects, score above threshold proceeds, score 0 skips gate, threshold 0 disables gate entirely). — when the primary image's quality score is at or below the configurable rejection threshold (default: 3 / 10), the submission is rejected automatically: the queue row is marked `failed`, no draft post is created, and the artist receives a friendly HTML email explaining the specific photographic issue and how to fix it. Issue labels from the vision AI (e.g. "too dark", "motion blur", "glare") are mapped to plain-language advice with concrete tips ("Try photographing near a large window in daylight…"). The email also includes four universal photography tips. Artists are invited to resubmit — the entire flow is automated with no admin action required. Configurable via Settings → AI Providers: **Rejection threshold** (set to 0 to disable). Covered by `QualityRejectionTest` (5 assertions: score at threshold rejects, score below threshold rejects, score above threshold proceeds, score 0 skips gate, threshold 0 disables gate entirely).
- **`Pipeline::extract_event_fields()`** — lightweight chat pass that runs after the polish step for `agnosis_event` submissions; sends body + subject to the text model and returns a JSON object with a `location` key; strips markdown fences from the response; short-circuits (returns `['location' => '']`) when body and subject are both blank. No admin entry required — location is fully automated.
- **`_agnosis_event_location` post meta** — stored on every `agnosis_event` post via `meta_input` during `PostCreator::create_post()`; populated from `Pipeline::extract_event_fields()` and falls back to an empty string when the AI finds no location in the email.
- **`agnosis/event-location` block** — server-side-rendered block registered in `Profile::register_blocks()`; uses `postId` context from the query loop; reads `_agnosis_event_location` meta and renders a styled `<p class="agnosis-event-location">` (small, bold, uppercase, letter-spaced); returns an empty string when meta is unset so events without a location leave no visual gap.
- **`agnosis_email_promote` setting** (Email tab) — configurable promote@ address (e.g. `promote@agnosis.art`); description explains the workflow: artist sends an email with the exact artwork title as subject to explicitly feature that artwork in their gallery overview.
- **`PostCreator::handle_promotion_request()`** — handles the `agnosis_promote` pseudo-type; finds the sending artist's published artwork by exact title match; calls `set_featured()` if found; logs a warning and exits silently when subject is empty or no match is found.
- **`PostCreator::set_featured()`** — sets `_agnosis_featured = '1'` on the target artwork and demotes all other published artworks by the same artist to `'0'`; drafts and other artists are not affected. Kept in the publishing layer (not `GalleryOverview`, which is a display class) because featuring is a workflow decision.

### Fixed
- **`CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` removed from `dbDelta()` calls** — `dbDelta()` handles the "table already exists" case itself by diffing the schema against the current table; the `IF NOT EXISTS` clause caused it to short-circuit before performing that comparison, silently skipping new columns on existing tables. All five `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` statements in `Activator::create_tables()` are now plain `CREATE TABLE`. The pre-existing manual `ALTER TABLE` guards in `maybe_upgrade()` (`post_id`, `revoked_at`) are retained for backward compatibility with installs created before this fix.

### Changed
- **Auto-promotion on approval removed** — `ReviewEndpoints::approve()` and `save(publish=true)` no longer set `_agnosis_featured`; the entire `promote_featured()` method has been deleted. Featuring is now always explicit — the artist sends an email to the promote@ alias with the artwork title as subject.
- **Theme 0.1.5** — `single-agnosis_biography.html` rebuilt with a two-column layout (left 38%: featured image at 3/4 aspect, 4 px border-radius; right 62%: title + spacer + content; columns stack on mobile; separator + author/year footer preserved); `single-agnosis_event.html` updated to group the post date and `wp:agnosis/event-location` block together with reduced block gap.

### Fixed
- **`ReviewEndpoints::reject()` incorrect action arg count** — `do_action('agnosis_submission_rejected', $post_id)` was passing only 1 argument; hooks registered with `accepted_args=4` received `$post_id` in the `$score` parameter position instead of `$author_id`. Fixed to pass all four expected args: `$post_id, (int) $post->post_author, 0, []`.
- **`render.php` unescaped `$agnosis_thumb_id`** — attachment ID in `class="wp-image-{id}"` was emitted raw; wrapped with `absint()`.
- **Minimum WordPress version bumped to 6.6** — `wp_interactivity_state()` and `wp_enqueue_script_module()` were both introduced in WP 6.5; declaring 6.4 as minimum caused Plugin Check errors. Updated plugin header, `AGNOSIS_MIN_WP` constant, and `readme.txt`.

### Tests
- **`MediaAdapterTest`** (new, 12 tests) — unit tests for `MediaAdapter::adapt()`: empty input; `image/jpeg` and `image/png` passthrough with `media_type='image'` and key preservation; multiple images; `audio/mpeg`, `audio/wav`, `audio/ogg` passthrough with `media_type='audio'`; `application/zip`, empty MIME, and `text/plain` dropped; PDF returns empty when Imagick unavailable (skipped if Imagick present); video returns empty when ffmpeg absent (skipped if ffmpeg present); mixed batch drops unknown and preserves image + audio in order.
- **`PipelineAudioBranchTest`** (new, 9 tests) — unit tests for `Pipeline::process_audio_single()` via reflection: `transcribe()` called when `supports_audio()=true`; `transcribe()` not called when `supports_audio()=false`; transcript included in `chat()` prompt; artist context included in prompt; valid JSON maps to all correct result fields; markdown fences stripped; empty `chat()` response → failure result; invalid JSON → failure result; empty transcript + no artist context → failure without calling `chat()`.
- **`PostCreatorGalleryAudioSkipTest`** (new, 4 tests) — integration tests for `PostCreator::merge_gallery()` audio skip: single audio result produces empty gallery; multiple audio results produce empty gallery; failed audio result also skipped; mixed batch with audio does not crash.
- **`ReviewEndpointsIntegrationTest`** — replaced the 5 now-invalid auto-promotion tests with 2 regression guards: `test_approve_does_not_set_featured_meta` and `test_save_with_publish_does_not_set_featured_meta`; both assert that `_agnosis_featured` is NOT `'1'` after approval, catching any accidental re-introduction of auto-promotion.
- **`PipelineExtractEventFieldsTest`** (new, 8 tests) — unit tests for `Pipeline::extract_event_fields()`: returns location from valid JSON; includes subject in prompt; returns empty when no location found; strips markdown fences; returns empty on invalid JSON; returns empty when provider returns empty string; does not call provider on empty submission; does not call provider when body and subject are both blank.
- **`PostCreatorPromotionIntegrationTest`** (new, 9 tests) — integration tests for `PostCreator::set_featured()` (marks post featured, demotes previous artwork by same artist, does not affect other artists, does not demote drafts) and `PostCreator::handle_promotion_request()` (features by title, no-op when title has no match, no-op on empty subject, does not match drafts, does not match other artist's artworks); both private methods exercised via reflection.
- **`ProfileEventLocationBlockTest`** (new, 4 tests) — integration tests for `Profile::render_event_location()`: renders HTML with class and text when meta is set; returns empty string when meta is absent; returns empty string when meta is blank/whitespace; HTML-escapes the location value.
- **`SubmissionTranslatorTest`** (new, 11 tests) — unit tests for `SubmissionTranslator`: `resolve_target_language()` returns LF option when set; falls back to first two chars of WP locale when LF option is empty; falls back to `'en'` when both are empty; `translate()` short-circuits (no chat call) when subject and body are both empty; short-circuits when the resolved language code is not in the map; valid JSON response updates subject and description; body-only submission updates only description; subject-only submission updates only subject; target language name appears in the chat prompt; markdown fences stripped from response; empty or non-JSON chat response preserves the original submission unchanged; `agnosis_translation_languages` filter can add a custom language code that is then used in the prompt. Namespace-scoped stubs (`ai_namespace_stubs.php`) override `get_option()`, `get_locale()`, and `apply_filters()` in `Agnosis\AI` so tests control all external inputs via static properties without affecting Pipeline or MediaAdapter tests.

## [0.1.8] — 2026-06-28

### Security
- **Token generation** — review and removal tokens now use `bin2hex(random_bytes(32))` (256-bit CSPRNG) instead of `wp_hash()` (HMAC-MD5 over predictable inputs). Tokens cannot be reconstructed from artist ID, timestamp, or site secrets. Extracted into `PostCreator::generate_token()` and covered by `TokenGenerationTest` (format, uniqueness, `hash_equals` compatibility).
- **REST endpoint permission gates** — `ReviewEndpoints` (`PUT /review/{id}`, `POST /review/{id}/approve`, `POST /review/{id}/reject`) and `RemovalEndpoints` (`POST /removal/{id}/confirm`) previously used `'permission_callback' => '__return_true'`, relying entirely on the internal `check_access()` / `verify_token()` logic. Added `check_permission()` to each class as an explicit outer gate: returns `true` when a token param is present or the user is logged in, `WP_Error(401)` otherwise.
- **Token URL shim** — email action links (approve, reject, remove) previously linked directly to REST endpoints with `?token=` in the query string; tokens appeared in server access logs, browser history, and Referer headers. Added `ReviewConfirm` class, registered on `template_redirect`: email links now point to `/?agnosis_review=1&id={id}&action={action}&token={token}`. The shim calls `rest_do_request()` with the token in the POST body (no logged REST URL) and immediately redirects to `/?agnosis_result={action}` — a clean URL. Browser history and Referer headers never contain the token.
- **ActivityPub inbox HTTP Signature verification** — `POST /activitypub/inbox` previously accepted any payload from any IP. Added `HttpSignature` class implementing Fediverse-compatible HTTP Signature verification: parses `keyId`/`headers`/`signature` from the `Signature` header; enforces a ±12 h Date freshness window; verifies the `Digest: SHA-256=…` body hash when present; fetches `publicKey.publicKeyPem` from the sender's actor document (cached 24 h per keyId); reconstructs the signing string and verifies RSA-SHA256 via `openssl_verify()`. Wired as `verify_inbox_signature()` permission callback on the inbox route — a spoofed or unsigned Follow/Announce is rejected with 401/403 before `inbox()` runs.

### Security (continued)
- **Admission status endpoint now requires authentication** — `GET /agnosis/v1/admission/status/{id}` previously returned `is_artist`, `has_applied`, and vouch counts for any WP user ID without authentication, allowing enumeration of the entire artist/applicant roster. Added `require_logged_in_for_status()` permission callback (returns 401 for anonymous requests) and an ownership guard inside `status()`: a non-admin user requesting a different user's status receives 403. Administrators retain full access. Covered by `AdmissionStatusTest` (7 assertions: 401 anonymous, 403 cross-user, 200 own data, field correctness, admin access to any user, admin field accuracy, artist own status).
- **Per-IP rate limiting on webhook and REST endpoints** — new `Core\RateLimiter` class uses WordPress transients to count requests per action per IP within a rolling time window. The window slot rotates automatically via `floor(time() / $window)` so counters expire without a cleanup cron. Limits: `POST /admission/apply` → 5 req/min (wired in `Admission::require_logged_in()`); `POST /admission/vouch/{id}` → 20 req/min (in `Admission::require_artist()`); `POST /email/inbound` → 60 req/min (in `Webhook::verify_signature()`). Exceeding the limit returns `WP_Error('agnosis_rate_limit', …, ['status' => 429])`. IP detection uses `REMOTE_ADDR` only — not `X-Forwarded-For` — to prevent header spoofing; sites behind a trusted reverse proxy that rewrites `REMOTE_ADDR` (nginx `real_ip_from`, AWS ALB, Cloudflare) work correctly without configuration.

### Changed
- **`WP_Filesystem` used for all filesystem writes** — replaced bare `file_put_contents()` / `file_get_contents()` calls in `PostCreator::upload_image()` and `Email\AttachmentStore` with `WP_Filesystem` (`'direct'` method forced via filter, since FTP/SSH credentials cannot be prompted in cron or admin-post context). Extracted as a private `filesystem()` helper on `PostCreator` and an equivalent static helper on `AttachmentStore`.
- **Attachment binaries moved out of the database** — `Inbox::enqueue()` now writes each image binary to `uploads/agnosis-queue/{uid}/{index}-{filename}` via the new `Email\AttachmentStore` class; `raw_email` JSON stores a `file` path instead of a base64 blob, eliminating 5–10 MB DB payloads per submission. `PostCreator` reads the file and deletes it after a successful media library upload. `AttachmentStore::sweep_orphans()` is called by the daily cleanup cron to remove dirs left by failed rows. The queue directory is protected with `.htaccess` and `index.php` on activation. Rows enqueued before this change (base64 inline) continue to work via a backward-compat branch.
- **Vouch revocation** — added `revoked_at DATETIME NULL DEFAULT NULL` to `agnosis_vouches`; existing installations receive the column via `maybe_upgrade()` on the next page load. `count_vouches()` filters `AND revoked_at IS NULL`. New `Admission::revoke_vouch(int $voucher_id, int $candidate_id): bool` sets `revoked_at` on the matching active row (row preserved for audit history; returns false when not found or already revoked). Covered by `VoucheRevocationTest`.
- **`handle_test_ai()` duplicate HTTP logic extracted** — the identical `wp_remote_post` + error-handling block that was copy-pasted for OpenAI and Anthropic is replaced by a shared private `Settings::ping_provider()` method. Each provider case now passes its specific URL, headers, and body; the error-handling path (transport failure → 429 error message, non-200 → extract `error.message` or fall back to `HTTP {code}`) lives in one place. Adding a fourth provider now costs 5 lines, not 18.
- **Automated queue drain on every poll** — `Inbox::drain_pending()` queries all `pending` rows from `agnosis_queue` (up to 50 per run, staggered 1 s apart) and schedules a `wp_schedule_single_event('agnosis_publish_submission', [$id])` for each. Called at the end of every `poll()` run regardless of IMAP configuration. Covers webhook-sourced rows whose initial single event was missed due to no page load after ingest, and sites running in webhook-only mode. `wp_schedule_single_event` deduplicates identical events already queued so this is safe to call every 5 minutes. Covered by `QueueDrainTest`.
- **`maybe_upgrade()` uses `SHOW COLUMNS` instead of `information_schema`** — both column-existence checks (`post_id` on `agnosis_queue`, `revoked_at` on `agnosis_vouches`) previously queried `information_schema.columns`, which is restricted on managed database providers (PlanetScale, Kinsta DB, etc.). Replaced with `$wpdb->get_results("SHOW COLUMNS FROM {$table} LIKE '{$column}'")`: returns empty on absence, works without elevated DB privileges, and is compatible with all MySQL/MariaDB hosting environments.
- **`upload_size_limit` filter cleanup scoped to own closure** — `PostCreator::upload_image()` was calling `remove_all_filters('upload_size_limit')` after `wp_handle_sideload()`, silently removing any filters added by co-active plugins. Changed to assign the closure to `$size_filter` and call `remove_filter('upload_size_limit', $size_filter)` — surgical removal of only our filter.
- **`no_found_rows` on all ID-only `get_posts()` calls** — added `'no_found_rows' => true` to 8 calls across `PostCreator` (5), `Admin\InboxPage` (2), and `Network\ActivityPub` (1) that fetch IDs and never read `$query->found_posts`. Eliminates the `SELECT COUNT(*)` subquery WP runs unconditionally otherwise; measurable on large post tables.
- **`PostCreator` Pipeline dependency injection** — constructor changed from `__construct()` to `__construct(?Pipeline $pipeline = null)`. Production code passes nothing; tests inject a stub that skips provider resolution and returns canned results without hitting AI endpoints. Covered by `PipelineInjectionTest`.
- **`PostCreator::create_post()` refactored** — reduced from 157 lines to 67 lines by extracting three private helpers: `merge_gallery()` (hash-aware gallery merge and upload), `build_post_content()` (Gutenberg block assembly), and `write_post_meta()` (featured image, tags, medium taxonomy, image hash mirroring, quality meta). No behaviour changes.
- **`Plugin.php` reduced to pure orchestrator** — extracted all business logic out of the bootstrap class. New `Admin\QueueController` takes the five queue admin-post handlers (`poll_now`, `force_reprocess`, `process_queue`, `process_one`, `delete_queue_row`); `handle_test_inbox` moved to `Admin\InboxPage`; `handle_test_ai` and `handle_clear_logs` moved to `Admin\Settings`; `compatibility_notices()` moved to `Compat\LinguaForge`; `ensure_roles()` extracted to new `Core\Roles`; `register_image_sizes()` extracted to new `Core\ImageSizes`. `Plugin.php` is now 145 lines of hook wiring only.
- **Gallery overview — WP Interactivity API lightbox** — replaced the custom `<dialog>`-based lightbox with WordPress core's built-in `core/image` lightbox. Each artwork card is now a `<figure class="wp-block-image wp-lightbox-container">` with the full set of `data-wp-*` directives; `wp_interactivity_state('core/image', [...])` registers per-image metadata (full-resolution `uploadedSrc`, dimensions); `block_core_image_print_lightbox_overlay()` prints the WP overlay once via `wp_footer`; `@wordpress/block-library/image/view` script module is enqueued.
- **Gallery overview — artist label routing** — on the main domain, the artist name links to the artist's subdomain; on an artist subdomain, it links to their biography page (`/biography/{slug}/`), falling back to the subdomain home if no biography exists yet. Uses `SubdomainRouter::is_artist_subdomain()`; memoised per request.

## [0.1.7] — 2026-06-27

### Fixed
- **`agnosis/gallery-overview` block not rendering in FSE template** — block was registered with `"render": "file:./render.php"` in `block.json`, which routes output through WordPress's own `ob_start()/ob_get_clean()` wrapper. Our `render.php` also used `ob_start()/return ob_get_clean()`, creating nested buffering: our inner buffer captured the HTML while WP's outer buffer saw nothing, causing the block to emit an empty string. Fix: removed the `"render"` key from `block.json` and replaced it with a PHP `render_callback` (`GalleryOverview::render_block()`) that owns the `ob_start()/ob_get_clean()` pair and `include`s `render.php` directly. `render.php` now outputs HTML directly; early exits use bare `return`
- **`editor.js` used ES module imports and JSX** — the file required a bundler (webpack/esbuild) to run but no build step existed; WordPress would reject the raw file in the block editor. Rewrote as an IIFE using `window.wp.*` globals (`wp.blocks`, `wp.element`, `wp.blockEditor`, `wp.components`, `wp.i18n`) — identical pattern to the project's other blocks; no build step needed
- **Plugin Check: `InputNotSanitized` on `$_GET`/`$_POST` reads** — `(int)` cast is not on WPCS's recognised sanitisation function list; replaced all affected reads with `absint( wp_unslash( ... ) )` (`queue_id`, `reprocessed`, `enqueued`, `polled` in `InboxPage` and `Plugin`)
- **Plugin Check: `NoCaching` on gallery-overview direct DB query** — `phpcs:ignore` comment was missing `NoCaching`; added alongside the existing `DirectQuery` suppression (result is cached via `wp_cache_set()` immediately after)
